## Phase 7: LLVM Code Generation

- [x] **CI guard — codegen containment invariant.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-17. New `Codegen containment guard` step in the `lint` job of `.github/workflows/ci.yml`. Shape: `grep -rlE '^\s*use\s+inkwell|\b(LLVMValue|LLVMType|BasicValueEnum|BasicTypeEnum)\b' src/ | grep -vE '^src/codegen(\.rs$|/)'`. Allow-set widened from the entry's original `^src/codegen\.rs$` to `^src/codegen(\.rs$|/)` because the codegen module is now `src/codegen.rs` plus `src/codegen/*.rs` (32 files at landing time); the original single-file regex would have rejected every submodule. Optional LLVM-type-substring refinement folded into the same step. Verified locally: 32 inkwell-importing files, all matched by the allow-set; planting `use inkwell::values::BasicValueEnum;` in a throwaway `src/__guard_violator_test.rs` correctly trips the guard. Enforces the architectural invariant from `design.md § Codegen architecture` programmatically — without this, the containment can erode silently through "one-off" imports in future PRs. Cross-reference `CLAUDE.md § Architecture > Codegen containment` and `deferred.md § MLIR Adoption as Codegen Substrate`.

- [x] **Hot-swap codegen flag — `--enable-hot-swap` (P0 architectural commit).** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18 (cumulative across slices 1+2 of phase-7 line 5, validated by [`investigations/hot_swap_indirection_cost.md`](../investigations/hot_swap_indirection_cost.md)). New codegen feature flag, off by default in v1. When enabled, `extern`-public module symbols are emitted via PLT-style indirection (callers invoke through a function pointer table rather than direct `call @foo`); internal calls stay direct. Without this commit at v1 freeze, retrofitting hot-swap for continuous PGO + shared-object reload (post-v1, see [`deferred.md § Continuous PGO with Shared-Object Hot-Swap`](../deferred.md#continuous-pgo-with-shared-object-hot-swap)) means recompiling every binary — the AOT artifact format effectively becomes versioned. Granularity is **module-level, not function-level** — hot-swap operates by reloading whole modules rather than swapping individual functions; `auth.verify` is hot-swapped by reloading `auth`. Sub-items:

  1. [x] **Codegen pass.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-17 (slice 2). `--enable-hot-swap` parses through `parse_build_command`, threads via `Command::Build` / `Command::BuildProject` → `cmd_build` / `cmd_build_project` → `run_multi_file_codegen` → new `compile_to_object_with_hot_swap` entry (with a parallel `compile_to_ir_with_hot_swap` for tests). Codegen state carries `hot_swap_enabled` + `hot_swap_slots` (fn name → slot index) + `hot_swap_fns` (ordered slot/value list). `declare_function` in `src/codegen/functions.rs` registers a slot for every user-defined `pub fn`. Between the decl pass and the body pass, `compile_program` calls `pre_emit_hot_swap_table` to emit `@karac_hotswap_table = [N x ptr] zeroinitializer` so call-site lowering can GEP into it. At call dispatch (`call_dispatch.rs`), pub-fn callees with a slot lower as load-from-table + `build_indirect_call` via the new `build_hot_swap_indirect_call` helper; private callees stay direct. At finalize, `finalize_hot_swap_table` emits an internal-linkage ctor `@__karac_init_hot_swap_table` that stores each declared pub-fn address into its slot, registered in `@llvm.global_ctors` at priority 65535. v1 binaries store direct function addresses so dispatch behavior is unchanged; the indirection exists for post-v1 reload.
  2. [x] **AOT-perf cost benchmark.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. Measured on Apple M5 Pro at [`bench/hot_swap_cost/`](../../bench/hot_swap_cost/): worst-case microbench (tight pub-fn call loop, ~3 ops per call body, N=500M) shows **2 ± 1 %** slowdown; realistic microbench (12-stage hash mix, N=50M) shows **1 ± 2 %** slowdown. Both within the entry's prior "<1% overall" amortized claim; neither approaches the prior "10–20% worst case" upper bound — indirect-call branch prediction (target never varies in v1 binaries) + 8-wide out-of-order issue absorb the load+indirect-call into the existing data-dependency chain. Full method, disassembly, and caveats in [`docs/investigations/hot_swap_indirection_cost.md`](../investigations/hot_swap_indirection_cost.md). **Flag is safe to expose; no fallback to per-symbol opt-in needed.**
  3. [x] **Target gating.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-17 (slice 1). `cmd_build_project` hard-errors when `--enable-hot-swap` is set and the manifest declares `[package].profile = "embedded"` or `"kernel"` — neither has the dynamic-symbol-resolution machinery hot-swap requires. The wasm-target half of the entry's gating defers until a wasm CompileProfile (or `--target=`) lands; no enum variant to gate against today.
  4. [x] **Smoke test.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-17 (slice 2). `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_enable_hot_swap_minimal_pub_fn` compiles a `pub fn answer() -> i64 { 42 }` + `fn main() { println(answer()) }` through `compile_to_object_with_hot_swap(_, true)`, links, runs the binary, and asserts stdout is `42`. Paired with `test_hot_swap_ir_shape` which locks in the IR-level surface: the table global, the init ctor, the `@llvm.global_ctors` entry are present when the flag is on; none of the scaffolding appears when off.

  Graduated from brainstorm v65 (2026-05-09). Spec at [`design.md § Specification Layers > Reported behavior > Profile-guided optimization output and runtime-JIT'd code`](../design.md#specification-layers).

- [x] **`.kara_jit_template` section + version manifest (P0 architectural commit).** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. New binary-format section reserved in v1 for post-v1 runtime monomorphization JIT (see [`deferred.md § Runtime Monomorphization JIT`](../deferred.md#runtime-monomorphization-jit)). v1 reserves the section name and ships an empty, versioned manifest; v2+ fills in actual bitcode emission. Without this commit, retrofitting JIT-template emission means a binary-format break.

  1. [x] **Section reservation.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. `Codegen::emit_jit_template_section` runs at module finalize and adds a global `karac_jit_template_manifest: [4 x i8]` with platform-appropriate section attribute (`__TEXT,__jittmpl` on Apple Mach-O targets due to the 16-char section-name cap; `.kara_jit_template` on ELF/COFF). Verified on a real Mach-O binary: `otool -lv` shows `(__TEXT,__jittmpl)` with the expected 4-byte payload; `nm` reports `_karac_jit_template_manifest`. **Apple segment re-scope (2026-05-25):** the original ship parked the manifest in a fresh `__KARA` segment to pre-reserve segment shape for post-v1 JIT — measurement against kata-88's bench surfaced the 16-KiB-per-binary tax (Mach-O page-aligns segments, so a 4-byte payload in its own segment still costs a whole page; every minimal-runtime kara binary grew from ~33 KiB → ~49 KiB). Re-scoped to `__TEXT,__jittmpl`: the section identifier and JIT-discovery surface are unchanged, the 16 KiB is reclaimed across every binary forever, and post-v1 JIT will add whatever segment shape its *actual* payload needs at the emission site (additive segment additions don't break v1 readers; anyone running post-v1 JIT necessarily has post-v1 karac and is rebuilding sources anyway). `tests/codegen.rs::test_jit_template_section_roundtrip` grew an `otool -l` regression guard asserting absence of `__KARA` segment + presence of `__jittmpl` section in the linked binary.
  2. [x] **Manifest format — opaque-payload, future-proof.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. Layout is `[version: u8, reserved: u8, reserved: u8, reserved: u8]` — 4 bytes total. v1 ships `[0x00, 0x00, 0x00, 0x00]` (version 0 = empty); v2+ readers see version byte = 0 and ignore the rest, or pick any payload shape under version 1+ without breaking v1 readers. **Trivially future-proof.**
  3. [x] **Target gating.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18 (deferred to v2 emission site per the entry's own guidance — "handled at the v2 emission site, not in v1's empty-section commit"). v1 emits the 4-byte marker unconditionally; the marker has zero observable cost on embedded/wasm regardless. The hard-error against `--enable-hot-swap`-style profile incompatibility belongs at v2's bitcode-payload emission site, where it can refuse to populate the section based on profile. v1's empty marker is harmless on every target.
  4. [x] **Binary-format roundtrip test.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. Two tests in `tests/codegen.rs`. `test_jit_template_section_reserved` locks in the IR-level shape (global + initializer + section name + `@llvm.used` pinning) so the codegen request can't silently rot. `test_jit_template_section_roundtrip` builds the object via `compile_to_object`, links it, and confirms `nm` reports the manifest symbol both pre- and post-link (soft-skips when the runtime archive is absent — the IR test is the unconditional safety net). The manifest registers in `@llvm.used` (via the new `used_data_globals` companion to `used_symbols`) so the linker can't strip it under `--gc-sections` / `-dead_strip`.

  **IR ABI stability stance for v1 is (a):** pin runtime + AOT-compiler to the same Kāra version. v1 binaries with embedded JIT templates are not redistributable across Kāra releases. Harder positions — (b) Cranelift CLIF as the embedded format, or (c) Kāra-side stable IR (KIR / typed AST snapshot) — are evaluated at promotion time when 3.3 ships. **This is the operational kill that ended ClangJIT** (the C++ research project that prototyped the same architecture in 2019); v1's stance is "reserve the section; pick the durable answer when consumers exist."

  Graduated from brainstorm v65 (2026-05-09). Spec at [`design.md § Specification Layers > Reported behavior > Profile-guided optimization output and runtime-JIT'd code`](../design.md#specification-layers).

- [x] **Compiler queries — P1.3: Inlining + branch hints.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. New `src/codegen_queries.rs` plain-data analyzer walks the AST after parse and emits two query kinds: `QueryKind::InliningDecision` for non-`#[inline]`/`#[inline(never)]` `pub fn`s called from three-or-more inside-loop call sites whose body is below a 20-statement cap (i.e. small hot helpers where inlining moves the needle), and `QueryKind::BranchHint` for `match` / `if`-`else` sites with notable arm-size skew (heaviest arm ≥ 3 statements AND ≥ 3× the lightest peer). Resolution surface advertised on each query — `[inline, inline(never)]` for the inlining variant and `[likely, unlikely]` for the branch-hint variant — already reserved by phase-8 sub-item 4. `cmd_query queries` in `cli.rs` calls `codegen_queries::analyze(&program)` unconditionally (cheap, single AST walk, no later-phase side-tables needed) and serializes the union into the `{"queries":[…]}` envelope using a new `render_compiler_query` JSON encoder. The analyzer lives outside `src/codegen.rs` deliberately — the heuristics are plain-data AST walks with no LLVM dependency, so keeping it un-gated means `karac query queries` works regardless of whether the LLVM backend is built (uniform tooling surface across feature configurations). **v1 deviations from the entry's natural shape, documented in the module's frontmatter:** (a) match-arm and if-branch attribute placement isn't supported in the parser today, so `#[likely]`/`#[unlikely]` suppression isn't checked yet — the resolution_surface still names those attributes so downstream tools render the correct guidance; (b) `SubItemHash` uses the decision site's byte offset as the per-compile disambiguator (the `def_path.rs` stub returned `ROOT`) — sufficient for v1 query identity but not edit-stable. Per design.md § Compiler Queries, author claims are trusted at v1 — a wrong `#[likely]` produces suboptimal codegen, no worse than today's annotation surface. Tests: ten unit tests in `tests/codegen_queries.rs` (five inlining arms, four branch-hint arms, one clean-program negative); `tests/cli.rs::test_query_queries_populated_envelope_has_inlining_query` locks in the JSON envelope shape end-to-end. Cumulative test counts unchanged on the gates the prior commit ran clean against.

- [x] **G12 — RC creep in AI-generated code**. ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. Validation + monitoring surface for the AI-creep heuristic. Three sub-tasks closed:

  1. **`warn_above_0` default validated.** The `rc_fallback` lint is registered in `STARTER_LINTS` at `src/lints.rs:108` with `default_level: LintLevel::Warn` — meaning every RC fallback Phase 1 produces a Warn-level perf note unless the function opts out. Regression test `tests/rc_fallback.rs::rc_fallback_lint_default_level_is_warn` pins the registry shape; a future refactor that quietly drops the lint to `Allow` (and erases the AI-creep signal G12 is monitoring) trips a test failure.

  2. **`#[allow(rc_fallback)]` visible in code review.** Already recognized by the `#[allow]` machinery at `src/ownership.rs:1114-1129` — the attribute is grep-able verbatim in PR diffs without further compiler work. The existing `allow_rc_fallback_suppresses_notes` test confirms it silences perf notes while leaving the RC entry intact in `rc_values` (so the budget enforcement and `karac query cost-summary` data still flows).

  3. **AI-agent over-suppression monitoring.** `OwnershipCheckResult` now exposes `pub suppressed_rc_fn_keys: HashSet<String>` (previously a `pub(crate)` field on the checker — promoted to the public result). `cost_summary::build` reads it and surfaces two new fields: `RcOpsBreakdown.suppressed: usize` (count of RC sites whose enclosing function carries `#[allow(rc_fallback)]`) and `FunctionCostRow.rc_ops_suppressed: bool` (per-row flag). `karac query cost-summary` JSON now reports `"rc_ops":{"count":N,"rc":…,"arc":…,"suppressed":S}` in totals and `"rc_ops_suppressed":true|false` per function row. A PR-level alert can now compare `suppressed/count` ratios to spot the "100% suppression" anti-pattern at a glance — the load-bearing signal for AI agents that reached for `#[allow]` rather than restructuring for zero-cost ownership. Tests: `tests/rc_fallback.rs::allow_rc_fallback_records_function_key_for_monitoring` (result-surface lock) + `tests/cli.rs::test_query_cost_summary_rc_fallback_suppressed_via_allow_is_surfaced` (CLI envelope lock); the two pre-existing cost-summary tests grew the `"suppressed":0` field in their totals assertions.

  Behavior delta is purely additive to the cost-summary JSON envelope (new fields, no renames or removals) — external tooling that ignores unknown fields stays compatible.

- [x] **RC fallback Phase 1 — trigger 3 (container store + subsequent use).** ✓ DONE (round 12.4, 2026-05-02). Resolved with option (b): retag-at-the-call-site approach. New `MoveKind::ContainerStore` + `RcTrigger::ContainerStoreWithSubsequentUse` variants; `MethodCall` arg-handling in `check_expr_reading` snapshots `Live` arg-rooted bindings before the call (only when the receiver is `mut ref self`) and retags any that flipped to `Moved/Direct` during arg consumption to `Moved/ContainerStore` — sequential `bag.insert("k", w); audit(w);` reroutes from `UseAfterMove` to RC fallback while leaving free-fn calls, `ref self` methods, and `self`-consuming methods on the prior path. Detection requires the typechecker to have resolved the method to a `Type.method` key registered by `collect_method_self_modes`, so trigger 3 fires for user-defined containers today and extends to Vec/Map once stdlib impls become visible to the ownership pass (Phase 7+). 6 new tests in `tests/rc_fallback.rs`. Commit `7f0ab90`.

- [x] **RC fallback Phase 1 — full CFG + dominator-tree dataflow.** ✓ DONE (rounds 12.7–12.22, 12.38, 12.41–12.42; 2026-05-02 → 2026-05-04). New `src/cfg.rs` + `src/dominator.rs` (Cooper–Harvey–Kennedy iterative dominance) + `src/use_classifier.rs` + `src/rc_predicate.rs` together replace the AST-driven branch-merge scheme with the formal `∃C∃U. ¬dom(C,U) ∧ ¬dom(U,C)` check from design.md § Part 4. Triggers 1 / 2 / 3 close via structural CFG fixes (sibling-sink-block lowering for closure bodies in 12.11 and `mut ref self` method-call sink-args in 12.12); par/seq/unsafe/lock/providers transparent forms walk through 12.13; flavor labeling via `ConsumeOrigin` in 12.14 reconstructs the `RcTrigger` without a second AST walk; direct-UAM predicate companion in 12.15 covers the dominance-comparable error case the formal RC predicate excludes. In-place integration (12.16 / 12.17 / 12.21) makes the predicate authoritative for both `rc_values` and `UseAfterMove` errors; the legacy `MoveKind` propagation chain that drove RC routing is removed in 12.42 (ContainerStore / ClosureCapture retags deleted; `MoveKind` enum gone; `ValueState::Moved` collapsed to `{ at: Span }`); once-callable closure bookkeeping migrated from the legacy state machine to the predicate pipeline in 12.20 (detection) and 12.38 (state-machine cleanup); reassignment-resets-state lands as `UseKind::Reassign` in 12.19; loop-of-consume detection in 12.22 covers the in-loop "next iteration" partner the formal predicate cannot model; defer/errdefer cleanup-edge ordering in 12.41 lowers cleanup bodies onto exit edges per design.md § Drop ordering, closing a soundness gap in the legacy state machine. Final test counts: 2293 non-LLVM / 2495 LLVM (with `KARAC_SKIP_ASAN_TESTS=1`). Net `ownership.rs` shrink of 72 lines from 12.42 alone; cumulative ~700 lines of new CFG/dominator/predicate machinery across the umbrella. Cross-reference the Phase 4 checklist entry "OwnershipChecker: implement RC fallback dataflow" — same work; folded in.

  Out of scope and tracked separately:

  - [ ] **RC fallback Phase 1 — closure-body CFGs as nested function analyses.** *(Precision-only refinement — build when a witness program demands it.)* The round-12.11 sibling-sink-block split makes capture-position consumes inside a closure body dominance-incomparable with subsequent outer uses, which is structurally sufficient for the *outer* function's predicate. Running the predicate pipeline recursively on each closure body (treating the body as its own nested function for analysis purposes) would refine intra-body precision but does not correct any predicate decision in the outer function. No false positives or negatives have been observed under the current model. Build this when (a) a real Kāra program surfaces a misclassification that the recursive analysis would resolve, or (b) a downstream tool (e.g. precise per-closure cost reporting) needs the per-body CFG as a first-class artifact.

  - [x] **Closure-capture mode classification migration.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. New `Classification.closure_capture_consumes: HashMap<SpanKey, HashMap<String, Span>>` (cfg.rs) — keyed by closure expression span, maps capture-name → first consume span seen inside that body. Populated by `use_classifier.rs` via a `closure_span_stack` push/pop wrapper around the existing `consume_origin_ctx = ClosureCapture` body walk; the new `record_closure_capture_consume` helper fires on every `Consume` identifier-leaf walked while inside a closure body. `OwnershipChecker` gains a `current_classification: Option<Classification>` field populated once per function in `check_function` via `classify_function_body` and cleared at function exit. Three `ValueState::Moved` consumers in `expr_check.rs` migrated to the classifier-driven lookup: (1) per-name capture mode classification (~line 994 — Own vs Ref/MutRef decision); (2) per-path capture mode classification (~line 1047 — disjoint-capture slice's root-consume signal); (3) K2 enforcement for `ref` / `mut ref` prefixes (~line 1149 — extracts consume span from the classifier map instead of `Moved { at }`). Closure-param shadowing filter added explicitly at the K2 site since the classifier doesn't track scope nesting (the legacy path relied on the state-machine restore). All 6 `test_capture_mode_*` tests + 1078 lib tests + 2495 full-suite tests pass with no behavior delta. `ValueState::Moved`'s only remaining consumer is now `handle_moved_use`'s short-circuit (expr_check.rs:446-453) which prevents cascading-read diagnostics on descendant expressions of an already-moved identifier; full retirement of Moved tracking would require migrating that short-circuit too, tracked as a separate follow-up if any cleanup driver demands it. Behavior delta is purely internal — closure_captures map shape unchanged, K2 diagnostic wording unchanged, RC fallback flavor labels unchanged.

  - [x] **Loop-of-consume reassign-suppression precision.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. `rc_predicate.rs::loop_of_consume_candidates` now matches each Consume against the natural-loop set containing its block and fires iff at least one containing loop has no Reassign of the same binding in its own blocks. Previously the rule unioned every natural loop's blocks into a single `loop_blocks` set, so any in-loop reassign of the binding suppressed loop-of-consume across the whole function — sibling-loop and outer-loop-only rebinds spuriously closed inner-loop back-edges they couldn't actually reach. The legacy-state-machine parity concern noted in round 12.22 is no longer load-bearing (round 12.42 collapsed `ValueState::Moved` and removed the legacy RC routing chain), so the precision improvement ships without a behavior-parity trade-off. Helper renamed `loop_blocks` → `natural_loops` (returns `Vec<HashSet<BlockId>>`, one entry per back-edge); the `in_loop.contains` checks at the witness-emission and suppression sites collapse into a single `loops.iter().any(...)` filter. Two new regression tests in `rc_predicate::tests`: (1) `loop_of_consume_fires_for_sibling_loop_reassign` — sequential sibling loops with consume in L1 and reassign in L2 must fire; (2) `loop_of_consume_fires_when_reassign_is_outside_inner_loop` — nested loops where consume is inner and reassign is outer (before the inner header) must fire because the inner natural loop's blocks don't contain the rebind. The same-loop suppression test (`loop_of_consume_suppressed_by_in_loop_reassign`) continues to pass — the common `consume(x); x = next();` rebind shape still suppresses because both uses share the same natural loop. Full lib + LLVM suite green; no behavior delta on any existing test.

  - [x] **Defer body inner-local consume duplication.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. `CfgBuilder` now alpha-renames inner-local introductions inside each per-exit-site defer/errdefer body lowering. A new `CleanupRenameFrame { suffix, bindings }` stack is pushed in `emit_scope_cleanup` around each `self.lower_block(item.body, ...)` call (both the errdefer pass and the defer pass), with a monotonic `next_cleanup_id` counter minting a `@cuN` suffix per emission. `lower_stmt`'s `Let`, `LetUninit`, and `LetElse` arms now call `note_local_introduced` after the RHS walk so the introduced binding names land in the active cleanup frame (no-op when no frame is active — function-body-level lets are unaffected). `record_use` mangles every recorded binding name through `mangle_binding`, which walks the cleanup-rename stack innermost-first and appends the matching frame's suffix — deepest-introducing frame wins, matching scope shadow semantics for nested defer-in-defer. Outer captures match no frame and keep their bare name, so the formal RC predicate continues to see all cleanup-block reads of an outer capture as one binding (the legitimate defer-body shape per design.md "defer/errdefer may only read outer captures"). Without the renaming, the duplicate inner-local Consume sites across cleanup blocks paired as dominance-incomparable and spuriously fired the formal RC predicate for a binding that has only one live instance per cleanup-site emission. Three new tests cover the surface: (1) `cfg::tests::defer_body_inner_locals_alpha_renamed_per_cleanup_site` pins that the bare name vanishes from UseSites and at least two distinct mangled `local@cuN` names appear; (2) `cfg::tests::defer_body_outer_capture_keeps_bare_name` pins that an outer capture inside a defer body stays unrenamed; (3) `rc_predicate::tests::defer_body_inner_local_does_not_fire_formal_rc` end-to-end verification that the formal RC predicate (under the real classifier with a non-Copy `Data` type) produces no witness for the defer body's inner-local — neither under its bare name nor under any `local@cuN` mangled form. `pattern_bindings` lost its `#[allow(dead_code)]` since it now has a real caller. Full lib + LLVM suite green; no behavior delta on any existing test.

- [x] **`#[rc_budget(max: N)]` module-level enforcement.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. All three sub-items shipped together:
  - (1) Parser — `#![rc_budget(max: N)]` inner-attribute syntax. New `Parser::parse_inner_attributes` consumes the `#! [` prefix at the top of `parse_program` (between module doc comments and item parsing); shares the existing attribute body grammar via a one-line `is_inner: bool` switch on `parse_attribute` to avoid duplication. The new `Program.inner_attrs: Vec<Attribute>` carries them downstream. Unknown inner-attribute names parse without rejection so future module-level attrs (`#![no_std]`, etc.) can ride this surface non-breakingly.
  - (2) Ownership-pass integration — `OwnershipChecker::enforce_rc_budget` runs at the end of `check()` after Phase 1/2 produce the final `rc_values` table (so Phase 2's `Rc → Arc` promotion is folded in before the count). The pass reads `program.inner_attrs`, parses the `max:` named argument, and sums `rc_values.values().map(|m| m.len())`. Bare `#![rc_budget]` (no `max:` arg) is treated as absent for v1.
  - (3) Diagnostic — `E_RC_BUDGET_EXCEEDED` (new `OwnershipErrorKind::RcBudgetExceeded { budget, observed }`). The `suggestion` field lists every contributing `<function>.<binding>` in source-sorted order so the author can pick which to restructure first. CLI error-code map in `cli.rs` covers the new kind.
  Six tests in `tests/ownership.rs` (`rc_budget_*`): under-budget passes, over-budget emits one error with the full contributing list, absent-attr-doesn't-enforce, `max: 0` rejects any RC, bare-attr-no-args ignored, and parser-surface lock-in that the attribute lands on `Program.inner_attrs` with the parsed `max:` argument.

- [x] **RC values: codegen integration.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-08 — substep (2) atomic-RC for `arc_values` (`atomicrmw add` / `atomicrmw sub`, `SeqCst`). Substeps (1) and (3) had landed earlier under the RC fallback Phase 1 umbrella.

- [x] **OwnershipChecker Phase 2: `spawn(closure)` and `Sender.send(closure)` par-region awareness for closure captures.** ✓ Both halves shipped (Sender.send 2026-05-08, spawn 2026-05-18). The Phase 2 `Rc → Arc` walker (`scan_block_for_par_uses` family in `src/ownership.rs`) now recognises every parallel-region escape route, not just `par {}` blocks: round 12.34 (Step 6 of the closure-ownership track) extended the walker to follow closure-binding uses inside `par {}` to their captures via a per-function `closure_bindings` map; the two halves below extended boundary detection to `Sender.send` and `spawn` call shapes, both routed through a unified `inside_parallel_region: bool` flag that the round-12.34 `closure_bindings` plumbing rides unchanged.

  1. [x] **`Sender.send(closure)` half — shipped 2026-05-08.** A closure value flowing through `Sender.send` crosses to whatever task owns the receiver; captures' live range extends into the receiver scope, so any RC-marked capture must be `Arc`. The walker (`scan_*_for_par_uses` family) now recognises `Sender.send(closure)` as a parallel-region boundary, with receiver-type resolution via a new `let_types` map populated from function-parameter `Sender[T]` annotations, explicit `let pat: Sender[T] = …;`, and `let (tx, rx) = Channel.new();` destructure. Cloned-sender shape (`tx.clone().send(h)`) handled. The `Channel` surface was already in v1 (`prelude.rs`); only the walker's boundary detection was missing. See **What landed** close-out below for full implementation, deviations from the slice plan, and the six new tests in `tests/rc_fallback.rs`.

  2. [x] **`spawn(closure)` half — shipped 2026-05-18.** Walker now recognizes `spawn(...)` as a parallel-region boundary symmetric with `tx.send(...)`. New `is_spawn_callee(&Expr) -> bool` predicate in `src/ownership/par_helpers.rs` mirrors `provider_escape::check_spawn_escape`'s recognition surface: bare-identifier callee `spawn` and single-segment path callee `spawn`. The `ExprKind::Call { callee, args }` arm computes `spawn_boundary = is_spawn_callee(callee)` once per call and threads `inside_parallel_region || spawn_boundary` into the args-subtree walks (callee subtree stays under the outer flag — the callee position is just the builtin name and never holds a candidate). With the boundary flipped, three propagation paths fire identically to `par {}` and `tx.send(...)`: (a) **let-bound closure** `let h = || apply(cfg); log(cfg); spawn(h);` — Identifier(h) is seen under the flag, the round-12.34 `closure_bindings` lookup yields h's captures, each RC-marked capture lifts to Arc; (b) **inline-wrapper closure** `spawn(|| h())` — the walker descends the closure body under the flag, Identifier(h) hits the same closure_bindings path; (c) **inline closure with direct capture** — the walker descends and any candidate Identifier inside the body promotes. The previously-noted "v1.1 blocked" framing referred to the *user-runtime* spawn surface, not the syntax: `spawn(...)` already parses as a bare-identifier `Call` and `provider_escape.rs` has been treating it as a soundness-relevant boundary since round 8 — only the Phase 2 promotion side was outstanding. Five tests in `tests/rc_fallback.rs::Phase 2 boundary: spawn(closure)`: (1) `phase2_spawn_closure_promotes_capture_to_arc` (positive let-bound base case), (2) `phase2_spawn_inline_closure_invoking_let_bound_promotes_capture` (closure-descent + closure_bindings path through inline wrapper), (3) `phase2_no_par_no_send_no_spawn_keeps_rc` (negative — locally-invoked closure stays Rc), (4) `phase2_spawn_and_send_consistent_decision` (monotonic property — spawn alongside `tx.send` produces one Arc decision), (5) `phase2_user_spawn_method_does_not_promote` (negative gate — a user `impl Pool { fn spawn(...) }` method goes through the MethodCall arm and is *not* the builtin `spawn` callee). Tests stand in `fn spawn(c: Fn() -> ()) { }` for the v1.1 prelude entry; the walker recognizes the name regardless of resolution target, which means the boundary will trip on any user-declared `spawn` free function — minor over-approximation (false-positive Rc → Arc = perf hit, never unsound), accepted at v1 because the canonical spawn-prelude entry will subsume user shadowing when it lands. Doc updates: module header of `par_helpers.rs` rewritten from "Channel + par-block helpers" to "Channel + spawn + par-block helpers" with the recognition surface listed; the Identifier-arm comment drops the prior "spawn deferred to Phase 6.3 / v1.1 user syntax" sentence in favor of listing spawn as a peer boundary; the comment block at the top of the Sender.send test section rewrites the trailing "deferred to v1.1" sentence to point at the new sibling section. Behavior delta is purely additive — the walker accepts a new call shape; existing par/channel-send classification unchanged.

  **Related v1 work:** the type-rejection-side dual is tracked at the existing Phase 6 entry "Cross-task-safe set + structural Send replacement at task boundaries" (its sites (a) `spawn(closure)` and (d) `Channel.send`), which rejects cross-task-unsafe captures at these boundaries — distinct from this entry's Rc → Arc *promotion* concern but shares the boundary-detection machinery.

- [x] **Par codegen: cancellation and error propagation. ✓ Closed 2026-05-25.** All four slices (1 [1a + 1b], 2, 3, 4 below) shipped. The three design properties from design.md § *Parallel Failure and Cleanup* land in IR: (1) fail-fast — a Result-typed branch writing Err stores `true` into the per-call `AtomicBool` cancel flag (slice 1a), siblings observe at the next mid-branch cancel check; (2) source-order error reporting — `atomicrmw umin` against a parent-allocated `i32` cell keeps the smallest err-branch index, surfaced as the par-block's value (slice 2); (3) completion-wins-at-branch-granularity — no preemption, a branch past its last cancel check runs to natural completion. Slice 4 (the long-blocked one) wired the `defer` / `errdefer` integration on the cancel path: `emit_branch_cancel_check`'s cancel-bb now drains via `emit_scope_cleanup_for_error_path` so errdefer fires on cooperative cancel (matches the interpreter's `ExitPath::Cancelled` semantics); both cleanup sites in `par_blocks.rs` (cancel-bb + branch-end) save/null/restore `branch_cancel_ptr` around the drain to suppress a pre-existing latent compile-time infinite recursion bug (a user defer/errdefer body containing an effectful call would re-enter `emit_branch_cancel_check`, which re-walks `scope_cleanup_actions` and re-encounters the same still-unpopped UserDefer/UserErrDefer). Original entry follows.

  Original entry: The language semantics require (design.md § Parallel Failure and Cleanup): (1) fail-fast — first `Err` cancels siblings via an `AtomicBool` cancel flag checked at compiler-inserted effect boundaries; (2) source-order error reporting — the scope returns the earliest-in-source-order error, not the first-completed one; (3) completion-wins-cancellation — a branch that has already passed its last effect-boundary check when cancel fires completes naturally and its `defer`s run. See also Phase 6.2 roadmap entries "Completion wins cancellation" and "Cascading cooperative cancellation."

  **Current state (audit 2026-05-18).** Substantial scaffolding is already in place — the gap is narrower than "the runtime doesn't honor cancel flags" from the original framing:
  - [x] **Cancel flag plumbing — done.** `karac_par_run` allocates a per-call `AtomicBool` cancel flag inside `ParCall` (`runtime/src/lib.rs:315`); each branch fn's synthesized signature already takes the flag pointer as its second parameter (`emit_par_branch_fn` at `src/codegen/par_blocks.rs:506`).
  - [x] **Fail-fast on PANIC — done.** `execute_task` wraps each branch in `catch_unwind` and stores `true` into `call.cancel` on panic (`runtime/src/lib.rs:413-416`); queued-but-not-started tasks skip on pickup (`runtime/src/lib.rs:388`).
  - [x] **Cooperative cancel checks — done.** Entry-time cancel check at branch start emits a fast-return path (`emit_par_branch_fn` at `src/codegen/par_blocks.rs:544-571`); `emit_branch_cancel_check` emits a mid-branch check before every effect-bearing call site, gated by the `callee_effectful` table so pure callees don't bloat the IR (`src/codegen/par_blocks.rs:857`).
  - [x] **Completion-wins-at-branch-granularity — done.** No preemption; a branch already past its last cancel check runs to natural completion.
  - [x] **Branch-return-slot mechanism — done.** Slice A (let-bindings that flow out to the join expression) shipped 2026-05-09; the env-struct carries `__par_returns` pointing at a parent-allocated return struct that each branch writes into before `ret` (`src/codegen/par_blocks.rs:325-360`). Slice 1a (Result-typed branches) shipped 2026-05-18 (`649ca70`); env-struct now also carries `__par_result_slots` (`src/codegen/par_blocks.rs:357-358, 448-468`) and each Result-tracking branch writes its Result value into its assigned slot before `ret void`. Parent-side load-and-surface of the Result slots is slice 1b below.

  **What remains.** The MVP discards branch return *values* in the Result sense: branches end in `ret void`, no Err payload reaches the parent, and no source-order error selection happens. Closing that gap requires four pieces of work — Result-type threading through ownership/effect pipeline, per-branch Result-slot writes, runtime-side source-order error selection, and defer/errdefer integration on the cancel path (the third blocks the first ship; the fourth waits on slices 1+2 of the **`defer` / `errdefer` codegen** entry below).

  **Slicing (drafted 2026-05-18).** Four-slice tranche. Slice 1 is the foundation (branches CAN return Result); slices 2–3 sharpen the semantics; slice 4 is gated on the **`defer` / `errdefer` codegen** entry below — see that entry's slice 2 close-out note (closes line 92 by inheritance once user defers/errdefers land on `scope_cleanup_actions`).

  - [x] **Slice 1 — Result-slot ABI + codegen + first-Err runtime hook. ✓ Landed across 1a (2026-05-18, `649ca70`) and 1b (2026-05-20).** Detect a par-block branch whose terminal source expression is `Result[T, E]`-typed; synthesize a per-branch Result-slot in a new parent-allocated array threaded through the env-struct; emit a slot-write of the branch's Result value before the branch's `ret void`. When a branch writes Err (tag == 0 per the existing Result lowering convention), codegen also stores `true` into the per-call `AtomicBool` cancel flag — no runtime change needed since the cancel flag pointer is already threaded into the branch fn signature. Sibling branches' existing cooperative-cancel checks fire as a result. Parent loads back the first Err slot and surfaces it as the par-block's value. **"Any Err wins"** in this slice — source-order selection is deferred to slice 2. ABI delta: env-struct grows by one trailing pointer field (`__par_result_slots`) that's null when no branch is Result-typed.

      **Split (2026-05-18):** landed in two commits.
      - [x] **Slice 1a — ABI + slot writes + Err-triggers-cancel (no parent surface). ✓ Landed 2026-05-18** (`649ca70`). New `ResultSlot { binding_name, branch_index, array_index }` in `src/codegen/state.rs`; `compile_par_block` builds the slot list via `branch_result_binding_name` over each branch's let-statements (annotation-only detection per the slice plan — inferred Result types fold in alongside slice 2's typechecker hooks). Env-struct grows by one trailing pointer field (`__par_result_slots`) carrying a `*mut [Result_t_e; N]` allocated parent-side; null when no branch is Result-typed so ABI delta is invisible to plain par-blocks. In `emit_par_branch_fn`, the slot-write is emitted after the branch's `compile_stmt` and before scope cleanup + `ret void`: the just-bound Result value is loaded out of the branch's local alloca, GEP'd into `slots_ptr[array_index]`, and stored. Tag (Result field 0) is compared against `0_i64` (Err per `seed_builtin_enum_layouts`); on equality, a conditional basic-block flow stores `i8 1` through the cancel-flag pointer (the branch fn's second parameter, captured into `self.branch_cancel_ptr`). Sibling branches' next cooperative-cancel check observes the flip. Two tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs`: `test_ir_par_branch_result_typed_let_emits_slot_and_cancel_store` (IR — slot alloca, slot GEPs, set-cancel basic blocks; negative-side plain par-block doesn't allocate the array) and `test_e2e_par_result_typed_branches_run_to_completion` (E2E smoke — post-par `println` fires regardless of which branch errored, confirming the new IR doesn't crash or deadlock). Slice 1b's parent-side Err surface remains.
      - [x] **Slice 1b — Parent-side Err surface. ✓ Landed 2026-05-20** (`fe0a451`). `emit_par_run` widens its return type by one optional pair — `(slots_array_ptr, Result_struct_ty)` — `Some` whenever any branch is Result-typed and `None` otherwise. `compile_par_block` consumes the new tuple element after `karac_par_run` returns: when the option is `Some` *and* the par-block has a join expression, codegen emits a per-slot check-BB chain in branch-index order (`__par_err_check_<i>`), each loading just the Result's tag (field 0) and branching on `tag == 0` (Err) to a per-slot `__par_err_found_<i>` block that loads the full Result and jumps to a shared `__par_block_exit`. The last Ok-path branch falls through to `__par_compile_join`, which compiles the user's join expression normally. All paths phi-merge at `__par_block_exit` (`__par_block_value = phi { i64, i64 }`), so the par-block's value is the first-found Err if any branch errored, else the join expression's value. Skip path: when `result_slots` is empty OR `final_expr` is `None`, the err-walk machinery is suppressed and codegen falls back to slice 1a's behavior (no phi, no per-slot BBs) — slice 1a's existing E2E test still passes because its par-block omits the join expression. The auto-par dispatch site in `src/codegen/stmts.rs` always passes an empty `result_slots` list and now destructures + discards the new tuple element. Three new tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs`: `test_ir_par_block_result_typed_join_emits_err_walk_and_phi` (IR — per-slot check/found labels, compile-join + exit labels, `__par_block_value` phi; negative side that no-join shape doesn't emit them), `test_e2e_par_block_result_ok_only_returns_join_expression` (E2E — Ok-only branches yield join's Ok), `test_e2e_par_block_result_single_err_overrides_join` (E2E — one Err branch overrides join's Ok). All 52 par_codegen tests pass; 5356-test full `--features llvm` suite green.

      Tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs`: positive (Ok-only branches return Ok, slice 1b), single-Err (one branch errs, others complete, slice 1b), cancel-propagation (one Err triggers sibling cancel check, slice 1a). ~150 LoC codegen + ~40 LoC test scaffolding split across the two commits.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — Source-order error reporting. ✓ Landed 2026-05-21.** Replaces slice 1b's N-block tag walk with a single-load + GEP-by-index path: the parent stack-allocates an `i32` initialised to `u32::MAX` (sentinel), and each branch fn does `atomicrmw umin ptr, i32 array_index, monotonic` against that cell from inside the existing is-err arm (right after the cancel-flag store). After `karac_par_run`'s join barrier returns, `compile_par_block` step 7 loads the cell once, compares against the sentinel, and either GEPs into `slots_ptr[loaded_idx]` (when an Err was reported) or evaluates the join expression — a 2-incoming phi (`__par_block_value`) merges them at `__par_block_exit`. Because slot `array_index` is assigned in source-statement order, `umin` keeps the smallest index seen, which is exactly the source-order earliest Err; the design's "ParCall tracks the smallest branch_idx" goal lands as a parent-stack `i32` cell threaded through the env-struct rather than as a `ParCall` field, so the runtime change is zero and the new state follows the same shape as `__par_result_slots`. Env-struct grows by one trailing pointer field (`__par_earliest_err_idx_ptr`); auto-par dispatch site in `src/codegen/stmts.rs` already discards the unused tuple element from slice 1b. Three slice-2 tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs`: `test_ir_par_block_result_typed_join_emits_err_pick_and_phi` (IR — pins `__par_err_check` / `__par_err_found` labels, `atomicrmw umin` instruction, and the absence of slice 1b's per-index labels), `test_e2e_par_block_result_source_order_earliest_branch_wins` (E2E — slow-then-Err branch 0 still wins over fast-Err branch 1 even when branch 1's slot is written first), `test_e2e_par_block_result_later_branch_err_still_surfaces` (E2E — Ok-Ok-Err sanity-checks the umin direction so the cell isn't spuriously read on the Ok-only path). Slice 1b's existing IR test was updated; the two E2E tests from 1b still pass against the new code. 86/86 par_codegen tests pass; full `--features llvm` suite green.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Effect-boundary cancel check granularity audit. ✓ Landed 2026-05-21.** Audit conclusion: **no emission code change required**. All v1 observable effects route through one of two compiler entry points — `compile_call` (`src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs:87`) for free-function / assoc-fn / FFI / closure calls, and `compile_method_call` (`src/codegen/method_call.rs:37`) for method calls — both of which invoke `emit_branch_cancel_check` unconditionally at the top of the function before any specialised dispatch. The three non-call shapes flagged in the slice plan are handled as follows: (a) **direct shared-struct field reads/writes** lower to raw `build_load` / `build_store` IR via `compile_field_access` and `compile_field_store`; v1 effect semantics declare `reads(R)` / `writes(R)` on *functions*, not per-operation, so the cancel check at the call-site that entered the shared-struct method covers the in-method field stores (inside-callee checks are not in scope for v1's "completion-wins-cancellation at branch granularity" policy). (b) **`Channel.send/recv`** are method calls (`tx.send(v)`, `rx.recv()`), routed through `compile_method_call` — the existing method-call cancel-check covers them. (c) **Raw effect-bearing intrinsics** (`karac_*` runtime symbols) are declared as LLVM functions and only invoked via the regular `compile_call` / `compile_method_call` paths from user-facing calls — there is no user syntax that emits a `karac_*` call bypassing those entry points. **Surprise finding:** the `lowering.rs` pass rewrites binary operators (`+ - * / %`, comparisons, bitwise) into `Path` calls like `i64.add(a, b)` after typecheck, so even "arithmetic-only" par-branches trip the cancel-check path. This is the desired behaviour — `i64.add` is in `callee_effectful = false`, so the narrowing elides the check anyway, but the structural call site exists. Three new lock-in tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs`: `test_ir_par_branch_field_access_does_not_add_cancel_check` (pins that interleaved field reads don't add checks beyond the call-site count), `test_ir_par_branch_indexing_does_not_add_cancel_check` (same for `arr[i]`), `test_ir_par_branch_literal_only_no_mid_branch_cancel_check` (corollary — par-branch with only literal bindings emits zero mid-branch checks). All 87 par_codegen tests pass; full `--features llvm` suite green.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — `defer`/`errdefer` on the cancel path. ✓ Landed 2026-05-25.** Two surgical emission changes in `src/codegen/par_blocks.rs` plus two pinning E2E tests. The slice's original "no new emission code" framing was stale: defer-codegen slice 2's split of `emit_scope_cleanup` (normal exit, skips `UserErrDefer`) vs `emit_scope_cleanup_for_error_path` (error exit, drains errdefers in phase 1 then defers + drops in phase 2) meant that `emit_branch_cancel_check`'s existing `emit_scope_cleanup` call silently swallowed errdefers on cooperative cancel. **Fix 1:** switch the cancel-bb's drain to `emit_scope_cleanup_for_error_path` (1 line at `emit_branch_cancel_check`). User defers still fire (phase 2 mirrors the normal-exit drain's defer behaviour); errdefers now fire in phase 1 with `ExitPath::Cancelled` semantics — matches the interpreter's `run_cleanup` shape. **Fix 2:** suppress `branch_cancel_ptr` around BOTH `emit_scope_cleanup*` call sites in par_blocks (the cancel-bb in `emit_branch_cancel_check` + the branch-end in `emit_par_branch_fn`). The original was a pre-existing latent recursion bug: a user defer/errdefer body containing an effectful call (e.g. `defer { println("x"); }`) routes through `compile_call` → `emit_branch_cancel_check`, which re-walks `scope_cleanup_actions` and re-encounters the SAME `UserDefer` / `UserErrDefer` action still in the outer frame (only removed on frame pop) → infinite compile-time recursion. The cleanup IS the cancel-exit / branch-end terminal work; nothing meaningful to re-cancel inside cleanup bodies. Save + null + restore the cancel pointer at both sites; the symmetric pattern matches the per-branch save/restore boundary at `emit_par_branch_fn`'s entry/exit. Slice 4 surfaced the bug because pre-slice-4 no par_codegen test exercised a user defer/errdefer in a par-branch body. **Two pinning tests** in `tests/par_codegen.rs`: `test_e2e_par_branch_defer_fires_on_cooperative_cancel` (`defer { println("def-fired-on-cancel"); }` body fires after sibling Err triggers cancel-flag store via slice 1a; loop sized at 10_000 iters so branch 0 cannot complete before cancel-check fires; sanity-checks `9999` absence from output to prove cancellation actually happened) and `test_e2e_par_branch_errdefer_fires_on_cooperative_cancel` (the discriminating test — errdefer ONLY fires on error paths, and the branch's source-level return is `Ok`-shaped, so `"err-fired-on-cancel"` in output is the unique signal that the cancel-exit is now treated as an error path). Branch 1 uses the slice-1a recognition shape (`let b: Result[i64, i64] = fast_err();` — `PatternKind::Binding` + explicit `Result[...]` annotation per `branch_result_binding_name`); wildcard `let _ = ...` bindings would NOT trigger the cancel-flag store (annotation-only detection). 102/102 par_codegen tests pass (100 prior + 2 new); full `--features llvm` suite green; clippy clean with `--all --all-targets`.

  **Validation criterion (slices 1+2).** A new `examples/par_error_propagation.kara` runs three concurrent branches, one of which returns Err; the program prints the Err value, observably from branch 0 (not branch 1's or branch 2's Err if multiple err). Acceptance: `tests/par_codegen.rs::par_err_propagates_source_order` pins the output.

- [x] **`defer` / `errdefer` codegen. ✓ Closed 2026-05-25.** All five planned slices shipped (1, 1.5, 2, 3, 4 below) — `karac build` and `karac run` now have parity for `defer { ... }`, `errdefer { ... }`, and `errdefer(e) { ... }` on every error-exit path the compiler emits today (`?` propagation, explicit `return Err(...)` / `return None`, function-tail `Err(...)` / `None`). Cleanup is unified on the existing `scope_cleanup_actions` stack — `UserDefer(Block)` and `UserErrDefer { binding, body }` variants interleave with the six compiler-internal cleanup variants (`RcDec` / `FreeVecBuffer` / `FreeMapHandle` / `EnumDrop` / `StructDrop` / `RcDecOption`) in program-order LIFO per design.md § *Drop ordering within a branch*. Normal-exit drain (`emit_scope_cleanup` / `drain_top_frame_with_emit`) skips `UserErrDefer` slots; error-exit drain (`emit_scope_cleanup_for_error_path`) walks each frame innermost-first, draining errdefers LIFO in phase 1 then non-errdefer actions LIFO in phase 2 — mirrors the interpreter's per-scope `run_cleanup` (`src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs:364-408`). 18 codegen tests in `tests/codegen.rs` (4 from slice 1, 4 from slice 1.5, 5 from slice 2, 3 from slice 3, 2 from slice 4) pin every shape the interpreter tests cover for the no-binding form plus the slice-4 binding form. **Validation criterion delta (vs the original spec below):** instead of a single `examples/defer_resource_cleanup.kara` + `defer_matches_interpreter_behaviour` test, the slices ship per-shape E2E tests directly (each one re-runs `compile + link + run`, asserts the byte-exact stdout the interpreter would produce). The combined-example fixture is a documentation artifact, not a coverage gate — the per-shape tests already cover every error-exit / cleanup-interleave permutation. **Known limitations carried as follow-ups** (per slice 4's notes): (a) ~~wider E payloads at the `?` site~~ **closed 2026-05-26**. `compile_function` now records the current function's `Result[T, E]` Err-arm LLVM type into a new `Codegen` field `current_fn_err_payload_ty` (lowered via `llvm_type_for_type_expr`). `compile_question`'s `fail_bb` reads this field and, when `Some`, extracts every payload word the result struct carries (w0/w1/w2 at fields 1/2/3 — synthesising 0 for words past the struct's `count_fields`) and dispatches through the existing `rebuild_value_from_payload_words` helper (`src/codegen/calls.rs`) to reconstruct the source-typed Err value. Coverage: primitives (i8..i64 truncate/zext, bool, char), floats (bitcast), pointers (inttoptr), Vec/String 3-word struct, Slice 2-word struct, and generic user structs field-by-field for ≤3-word payloads. One new test `test_e2e_errdefer_with_binding_sees_wider_e_at_question_propagation` pins the canonical wider-E shape (`Result[i64, String]` with `errdefer(e) { println(e); }` at `boom()?` — `e` binds the live `"kaboom"` String). Residual: payloads wider than 3 words (helper's `[w0, w1, w2]` array bound) still get partial reconstruction — orthogonal to this slice. Explicit-return and tail-Err paths continue to handle wider E for **pure** payload expressions via re-compile per follow-up (b)'s split. (b) ~~Double-evaluation of side-effecting Err arg expressions in return / tail-Err sites~~ **closed 2026-05-26**. `compile_expr`'s `ExprKind::Return(Err(arg))` arm and `compile_function`'s tail-Err emitter now split staging by `Self::is_pure_recompilable(payload_expr)`: pure args (Identifier / Path / literal) re-compile (single-eval-equivalent value, preserves wider-E source-typed binding); impure args extract the i64-coerced payload word from the constructed Err struct's field 1 via `build_extract_value` — single eval, accepts the i64-coerce trade for wider-E impure args (folded into (a)). One new test `test_e2e_errdefer_with_binding_no_double_eval_on_impure_err_arg` pins `make_err()` (impure helper) firing exactly once in `return Err(make_err());` and the binding-form errdefer seeing the staged i64 payload. (c) Panic landing pads — the panic-unwind story isn't in this compiler today (panic=abort-style); slice 2's design called this conditional on the panic story landing first. (d) ~~Par-cancellation slice 4 inheritance~~ **closed** alongside this entry — par-codegen line 92 shipped 2026-05-25, wiring the par-branch cancel-bb to `emit_scope_cleanup_for_error_path` so errdefer fires on cooperative cancel (and closing a pre-existing latent compile-time recursion in defer/errdefer body cleanup emission). Original entry follows.

  Original entry: **Filed 2026-05-21.** Defer/errdefer ship working in the interpreter (unified drop+defer cleanup stack per design.md § Drop ordering within a branch — landed Phase 4 line 103, 2026-05-06) but are **silently no-op'd at the LLVM backend**. `src/codegen/stmts.rs::compile_stmt` does not match `StmtKind::Defer` or `StmtKind::ErrDefer`; both fall through to the catch-all `_ => Ok(())` at line 1658, so a compiled binary observes none of the cleanup the interpreter runs. This is a correctness gap for v1: any user program that relies on `defer` for resource cleanup (file handles, locks, telemetry counters, scope-guard-style instrumentation) has divergent behaviour between `karac run` (interpreter, correct) and `karac build` (compiler, dropped on the floor). The fix is structurally half-built: codegen already has a `scope_cleanup_actions: Vec<CleanupAction>` per-scope stack (`src/codegen/state.rs:156-158`) that compiler-internal cleanup uses today (Vec/String free, Map handle free, RC dec), drained by `emit_scope_cleanup` at every scope exit; user-level defer and errdefer need to be added as new variants of the same stack with the right phase semantics (errdefer fires on error paths only, defer + drops interleave in program-order LIFO).

  **Current state (audit 2026-05-21).**
  - **AST + parser + typechecker:** ✓ done. `Defer { body }` / `ErrDefer { binding: Option<String>, body }` in `src/ast/stmts.rs:51-57`; parsed at `src/parser/stmts.rs:309,342`; typechecker verifies no `?` inside defer block, types the cleanup expr, contributes its effects to the enclosing function (roadmap.md:140, 192).
  - **Interpreter:** ✓ done. Two-phase cleanup with unified drop+defer LIFO stack (`src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs:33-48,56-65,370-408`). Errdefer phase 1 drains on error paths only (line 374); drop+defer phase 2 interleaves in program-order LIFO (line 395). Tests pass: `test_defer_runs_on_scope_exit`, `test_defer_lifo_order`, `test_errdefer_fires_on_err_return`, `test_errdefer_skipped_on_normal_return`, `test_errdefer_with_binding_sees_err_payload`, others in `tests/interpreter.rs`.
  - **Codegen:** **NOT IMPLEMENTED.** Both stmt variants fall through to the `_ => Ok(())` catch-all (`src/codegen/stmts.rs:1658`). No tests in `tests/codegen.rs` exercise compiled-binary defer behaviour.

  **Slicing (drafted 2026-05-21).** Four-slice tranche, mirrors the interpreter's structure so the IR semantics line up directly with the interpreter spec.

  - [x] **Slice 1 — `defer` on normal scope exit. ✓ Landed 2026-05-21.** Added a `UserDefer(Block)` variant to `CleanupAction` in `src/codegen/state.rs`. `compile_stmt` matches `StmtKind::Defer { body }` (before the catch-all `_ => Ok(())` arm) and pushes `UserDefer(body.clone())` onto the top `scope_cleanup_actions` frame. `emit_scope_cleanup` and `drain_top_frame_with_emit` were promoted to `&mut self` and now drain each frame in **reverse push order** (LIFO) — required for user defers per design.md § *Drop ordering within a branch*. The compiler-internal variants (`RcDec`, `FreeVecBuffer`, `FreeMapHandle`, `EnumDrop`, `StructDrop`, `RcDecOption`) each touch independent allocations and commute, so reversing their drain order is a correctness no-op for them. UserDefer dispatch is split out via `emit_cleanup_action_at(frame_idx, action_idx, ...)` which clones the AST Block, drops the `&self.scope_cleanup_actions[..]` borrow, then calls `self.compile_block(&body)` under `&mut self`; the existing `emit_cleanup_action(&self, action, ...)` fast path stays for the compiler-internal arms. Four E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs`: `test_e2e_defer_fires_on_normal_scope_exit`, `test_e2e_defer_lifo_order_within_function`, `test_e2e_defer_fires_on_explicit_early_return`, `test_e2e_defer_with_three_actions_lifo`. **Out of scope for slice 1 — tracked as separate follow-on slice 1.5 below (line 107):** block-scoped dispatch (defer inside a nested block fires at end-of-fn, not end-of-block) and runtime-reachability (defer inside `if false { defer ... }` registers at compile-time and fires at fn exit; interpreter's `test_defer_registers_when_reached_not_at_block_start` shape is therefore not yet matched). 700/700 codegen tests pass; full `--features llvm` suite green.

  - [x] **Slice 1.5 — block-scoped dispatch + runtime-reachability for `defer`. ✓ Landed 2026-05-22.** Added a new `compile_block_with_frame` helper next to `compile_block` in `src/codegen/stmts.rs` — it pushes a `scope_cleanup_actions` frame at entry, calls `compile_block`, then on normal fall-through calls `drain_top_frame_with_emit` (which emits the cleanup IR inside the block's current BB and pops the frame) or, when the body terminated via `return`/`?`-propagation, just pops (the early-exit's `emit_scope_cleanup` already walked the frame). The implementation took the narrower path of giving the new behaviour an opt-in helper rather than retrofitting `compile_block` itself: the original `compile_block` stays in use at the "owns its own frame" call sites (`compile_for_range`, `compile_while`, `compile_loop`, match arms, par-branch worker fns, `compile_function`/`compile_function_body`, and the mono'd-function-body path) so the function-tail `suppress_cleanup_for_tail_return` + `emit_scope_cleanup` ordering in `compile_function` (which is load-bearing for move-aware Vec/String tail returns — the FreeVecBuffer's `cap > 0` runtime check has to be preceded by the zero-cap suppression IR) keeps working unchanged. The new helper is wired at all "naked block" sites: `compile_if`'s then/else arms (`src/codegen/control_flow.rs:407, 422`), `compile_if_let`'s then/else arms (lines 50, 65), `ExprKind::Block`/`ExprKind::Seq` (`src/codegen/exprs.rs:261`), `ExprKind::Unsafe` (line 301), and the `CleanupAction::UserDefer` dispatch in `emit_cleanup_action_at` (`src/codegen/runtime.rs:775`, so a nested `defer` inside a defer body scopes to that body). Because the drain IR is part of the **emitted** then-arm's BB, an `if false { defer ... }` skips the drain instruction at runtime via the conditional jump — runtime-reachability falls out of block-scoping for free, matching the interpreter's `test_defer_registers_when_reached_not_at_block_start`. The `while` body case was already correct in slice 1 (per-iteration frame in `compile_while` already catches body defers); the new test pins the semantic against future regressions. Four E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs`: `test_e2e_defer_in_if_true_fires_at_end_of_arm`, `test_e2e_defer_in_if_false_does_not_fire`, `test_e2e_defer_in_while_body_fires_per_iteration`, `test_e2e_defer_in_nested_block_fires_at_inner_block_exit`. **Out of scope for slice 1.5 — intentionally left for later:** `compile_labeled_block` body (which has its own early-exit semantics via `break label`) and `compile_break`/`compile_continue` paths (today don't walk the cleanup stack at all — pre-existing shape, separate from defer codegen); the cross-cut into compiler-internal cleanups (RcDec/FreeVecBuffer/etc. still land on the legacy outer frame at the loop/match callers) is also untouched here — the slice's goal is matching interpreter defer semantics, not refactoring the existing RAII cleanup graph. 738/738 codegen tests pass (734 prior + 4 new); full `--features llvm` suite green.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — `errdefer` phase-1 on error paths. ✓ Landed 2026-05-25.** Added `UserErrDefer { binding: Option<String>, body: Block }` variant to `CleanupAction` (`src/codegen/state.rs`). `compile_stmt` matches `StmtKind::ErrDefer { binding, body }` and pushes onto the top `scope_cleanup_actions` frame — gated on `binding.is_none()` so the param-less form ships now and the binding form `errdefer(e) { ... }` falls through to the catch-all `_ => Ok(())` arm until slice 4 lifts the gate (mirrors slice 1's deferral of block-scoped defer to slice 1.5). Split the drain into two phases routed by exit path: `emit_scope_cleanup` (normal-exit) and `drain_top_frame_with_emit` (block-scope normal-exit) skip `UserErrDefer` slots so an `errdefer { ... }` declared in a normally-exiting scope never fires; a new `emit_scope_cleanup_for_error_path` walks each frame innermost-first, draining errdefers LIFO in phase 1, then non-errdefer actions LIFO in phase 2 — mirroring the interpreter's per-scope `run_cleanup` shape (`src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs:364-408`). `emit_cleanup_action_at` extended to extract the errdefer body alongside `UserDefer` and route through the same `compile_block_with_frame` path, so a nested `defer` inside an errdefer body scopes to that body (same shape slice 1.5 wired for defer). Error-exit sites: the `?` operator's `fail_bb` (`src/codegen/exprs.rs:570`) now calls `emit_scope_cleanup_for_error_path` after `emit_error_trace_push`; `ExprKind::Return(val)` (`src/codegen/exprs.rs:269`) and the function-tail emitter (`src/codegen/functions.rs:404`) detect syntactic `Err(...)` / `None` shapes via a new `Codegen::is_error_exit_value` helper and route to the same path. Panic landing pads are not wired — the panic-unwind story is not in this compiler today (panic=abort-style), so there's nothing to coordinate with; slice 2's design called this out as conditional on the panic story landing first. Five E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs`: `test_e2e_errdefer_fires_on_explicit_return_err`, `test_e2e_errdefer_skipped_on_normal_return`, `test_e2e_errdefer_fires_on_question_propagation`, `test_e2e_errdefer_phase1_before_defer_lifo`, `test_e2e_errdefer_fires_on_tail_err_expression`. **Closes par-cancellation slice 4 (line 92) by inheritance** for the no-binding form — the par-branch's `emit_scope_cleanup` call site would need to switch to `emit_scope_cleanup_for_error_path` on the cancel-check exit path to actually fire errdefers there; tracked separately as a follow-on rather than bundled here. **Slice 4 prerequisite already met:** the `binding: Option<String>` field is on the variant and threaded through emission; slice 4 only needs to lift the `binding.is_none()` gate in `compile_stmt` and add the bind-payload-then-emit code in `emit_cleanup_action_at`'s errdefer branch. 808/808 codegen tests pass (803 prior + 5 new); full `--features llvm` suite green; clippy clean with `--all --all-targets`.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — LIFO interleave between user `defer` and compiler-internal drops. ✓ Landed 2026-05-25.** Audit + regression pin (no code change to the cleanup-stack machinery). The structural invariant was already established by slice 1: `compile_stmt`'s `StmtKind::Defer` arm (`src/codegen/stmts.rs:1787`) and every compiler-internal cleanup-emitting handler (`track_vec_var` / `track_rc_var` / `track_rc_option_var` / `track_map_handle` / `track_enum_var` / `track_struct_var` at `src/codegen/runtime.rs`) all push onto the SAME frame via `scope_cleanup_actions.last_mut()`, and `emit_scope_cleanup` walks frames innermost-first with `(0..n).rev()` per frame — pure reverse-push LIFO across the unified stack. Design.md's canonical example `let v = Vec.new(); defer foo();` drains `[FreeVec(v), UserDefer(foo)]` as `[UserDefer(foo), FreeVec(v)]` — `foo()` first, then `drop(v)`. Three tests in `tests/codegen.rs` pin the observable consequences against future regression: (1) `test_e2e_defer_lifo_with_let_vec_interleave` — `let mut v: Vec[i64] = Vec.new(); v.push(...); defer { println(f"len={v.len()}"); }` prints `len=3` at scope exit, proving the defer fires while v's buffer is still alive (rules out "all drops then all defers"); (2) `test_e2e_defer_lifo_with_two_let_vecs_interleave` — mirrors the slice description's canonical example shape (`let v; defer A; let w; defer B;`) and observes `wlen=2` then `vlen=1` at scope exit, pinning the cross-action LIFO order between defers and the unified stack; (3) `test_ir_defer_drop_interleave_emission_order` — IR-level pin that distinguishes the unified-LIFO drain from the "all defers then all drops" two-phase alternative (both pass the live-buffer E2E tests, but only unified-LIFO interleaves `mark_a` between two `@free` calls in the emitted main body). Scopes the IR walk to `define i32 @main`'s body and uses `call void @free(ptr %cleanup.data` to skip Vec.push's realloc-time `@free` calls. 811/811 codegen tests pass (808 prior + 3 new); full `--features llvm` suite green; clippy clean with `--all --all-targets`.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — `errdefer(e)` binding form. ✓ Landed 2026-05-25.** Lifted the `binding.is_none()` gate in `compile_stmt`'s `StmtKind::ErrDefer` arm (`src/codegen/stmts.rs:1844`) so binding-form errdefers also land on the unified `scope_cleanup_actions` frame. Binding-form dispatch in `emit_cleanup_action_at` (`src/codegen/runtime.rs:898`): when the action's `binding` is `Some(name)`, allocate an entry-block alloca of the staged payload's LLVM type via `create_entry_alloca`, store the value, save the prior `variables[name]` slot (for restoration), insert a fresh `VarSlot { ptr, ty }` so the body's `compile_expr` reads of `e` resolve, run `compile_block_with_frame`, then restore the prior slot (or remove if there was none — required so the alloca scope ends with this body, not bleeding into later errdefer bodies or re-entries). The payload is staged into a new `Codegen` field `pending_errdefer_payload: Option<BasicValueEnum<'ctx>>` (`src/codegen.rs:528`) immediately before each of the three error-exit sites' `emit_scope_cleanup_for_error_path` call and cleared on return: (1) `compile_question`'s `fail_bb` stages `w0` directly (the i64-wide payload word extracted from the result struct's field 1); (2) `ExprKind::Return(Err(arg))` in `compile_expr` extracts `arg` via the new `Self::err_payload_from_value` helper (mirrors `is_error_exit_value`'s call-shape detection — accepts both `Path([..., "Err"])` and bare `Identifier("Err")` callees) and re-compiles it to get the source-level value; (3) the function-tail `Err(arg)` emitter in `compile_function` does the same. Two E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs` pin the binding-form dispatch: `test_e2e_errdefer_with_binding_on_explicit_return_err` mirrors interpreter `test_errdefer_with_binding_sees_err_payload` (errdefer(e) prints `e` on `return Err(7_i64)`); `test_e2e_errdefer_with_binding_on_question_propagation` pins the `?`-site path (errdefer(e) in the caller binds `e` to the propagated payload from `boom()?`). **Known limitations (out of scope, tracked as follow-ups):** (a) wider E payloads at the `?` site — `compile_question` extracts only `w0` (one i64 word), so `Result[T, String]` and `Result[T, struct]` binding forms at the `?` path see the i64-coerced first word rather than the reconstructed source-level value; the explicit-return and tail-Err paths re-compile the inner Err arg directly so they work for any payload type. (b) Double-evaluation of side-effecting payload expressions in the explicit-return and tail-Err sites — `return Err(expensive())` evaluates `expensive()` once for the return-struct construction and once to stage the binding-form payload. Acceptable for v1's narrow common case (typed `i64` / identifier payloads); revisit when a workload surfaces non-pure Err arg expressions. 813/813 codegen tests pass (811 prior + 2 new); full `--features llvm` suite green; clippy clean with `--all --all-targets`.

  **Validation criterion.** A new `examples/defer_resource_cleanup.kara` opens a file (or simulates it via stdout-instrumented helper), uses `defer` to close on every exit path, uses `errdefer(e)` to log the error before propagation, and `karac run` vs `karac build && ./binary` produce identical stdout. Acceptance: `tests/codegen.rs::defer_matches_interpreter_behaviour` runs both paths and asserts byte-equal stdout.

- [ ] **`errdefer(e)` binding: panic-path payload threading.** **Blocked on the panic-unwind story landing first.** The defer-codegen entry (line 98) closure note carried this as follow-up (c). When `karac` grows real panic landing pads — replacing today's `panic=abort` semantics with a runtime-walked unwind path (or LLVM `landingpad` blocks per the existing `panics` effect roadmap entry) — the `errdefer { ... }` and `errdefer(e) { ... }` blocks registered upstream of the panic site should fire with `e` bound to the panic value (per design.md "observing cancellation — `errdefer(e)` sees `e = Cancelled`" and its sibling rule for panic). Implementation surface (mechanical once unwind ships): (1) at each panic landing pad, route through `emit_scope_cleanup_for_error_path` rather than the abort handler's no-cleanup return; (2) stage the panic value into `pending_errdefer_payload` from whatever shape the landing pad receives (likely an `i8*` payload pointer that the runtime resolves to a typed value); (3) pin the semantics with an E2E test mirroring interpreter `test_errdefer_runs_before_defer_on_panic_path` (filed under Phase 4's defer test family). Filed 2026-05-26. Reopens when the panic-unwind entry lands.

- [ ] **`errdefer(e)` binding: payload reconstruction for >3-word E at the `?` site.** Slice 4 follow-up (a) closed the canonical wider-E case (closed 2026-05-26) by routing `compile_question`'s `fail_bb` through `rebuild_value_from_payload_words(target_ty, w0, w1, w2)` — the helper carries an `[w0, w1, w2]` array and handles every E whose lowered payload fits in ≤3 i64 words (primitives, floats, pointers, Vec/String 3-word struct, Slice 2-word struct, generic user structs field-by-field up to 3 words). Residual: `Result[T, E]` where E lowers to ≥4 i64 words (deeply nested user structs, multi-field aggregates) reconstructs partially — the helper sees only the first 3 words and silently zero-fills the rest into the constructed struct value, so the binding-form errdefer's `e` carries stale-filled tail fields. Implementation surface: widen `rebuild_value_from_payload_words`'s arity (variadic or `&[IntValue]` slice) and have the `?` site extract every available payload word from the result struct (driven by `enum_ty.count_fields() - 1`). The cross-cut into the helper's three existing call sites (`compile_question`'s fail-bb, the `Option/Result.unwrap` path, etc.) needs each updated to compute and pass the full word vector. Filed 2026-05-26. Reopens when a workload pulls — typical user error types are ≤3 words today (primitives, single-arity structs, String).

- [ ] **Par codegen: inferred `Result[T, E]` types in par-block branches trigger cancel-flag store.** Slice 1a's `branch_result_binding_name` recognises a par-block branch as `Result`-typed only when the `let` carries an explicit `Result[T, E]` annotation (`PatternKind::Binding(name)` + `TypeKind::Path` whose segments are `["Result"]`). Annotation-less bindings (`let b = fast_err();` where `fast_err -> Result[T, E]` is inferred) are silently skipped — no slot allocated, no cancel-flag store on Err, sibling branches' cooperative-cancel checks never fire. Slice 1a's own comment flagged this: "annotation-only detection per the slice plan — inferred Result types fold in alongside slice 2's typechecker hooks." Slice 2 (source-order error reporting) shipped 2026-05-21 without addressing it. Implementation surface: thread the typechecker's recorded RHS type into `branch_result_binding_name` (either via a new map on `Program` keyed by stmt span, or by reading from `typed.expr_types` if such a map exists), so an unannotated `let b = result_returning_call();` is treated identically to `let b: Result[T, E] = result_returning_call();`. Filed 2026-05-26. The corresponding pinning tests in `par_codegen.rs` use explicit annotations today (`let b: Result[i64, i64] = fast_err();`) — extending to inferred shapes is the validation. Reopens when a real par-block workload surfaces the annotation-only constraint as friction.

- [ ] **Par codegen: auto-parallelization of non-`par` regions.** *(Moved to Phase 8 — see roadmap.md § Phase 8 > Auto-Concurrency Codegen.)* The current MVP only lowers explicit `par {}` blocks. The concurrency analysis output (`ConcurrencyAnalysis.function_decisions`) identifies parallelizable statement groups *outside* `par` blocks — those are still emitted sequentially. Wire codegen to honor `parallel_groups` on non-`par` blocks: for each group of two or more statements, emit the same `karac_par_run` call path. Needs the concurrency analysis result threaded into `Codegen` (currently not passed to `compile_to_object`). Guard with a codegen-level granularity heuristic (roadmap Phase 6.1 "Task granularity heuristics") to avoid spawning threads for trivial pure statements.

  **Slicing (drafted 2026-05-08).** Two-slice tranche: (1) **plumbing** — thread `ConcurrencyAnalysis` through codegen entry points and into the `Codegen` state, no behavior change; (2) **codegen MVP** — consume the threaded analysis, emit `karac_par_run` for compiler-inferred parallel groups, apply `is_trivial` skip. Slice 2 is the Parallax demo punchline; slice 1 is its prerequisite. Slice 2's plan to be drafted after slice 1 lands. Tracked in `wip-staging.md § Active slate: Phase 8 auto-concurrency codegen`.

- [x] **Auto-par reduction recognition: split Σ / Π / min / max accumulators across threads (P1.x).** **Closed 2026-05-20.** All three design pillars below are checked (validation criterion hit at 10.16× ahead of Rust on kata-7, well above the 4–6× projection; allow-list policy settled at `+ * | & ^` for ints; cost-model interaction closed by slices 3b.5 + 3b.8). All eleven slices in the status block (1, 2, 3a, 3b, 3b.1, 3b.2, 3b.3, 3b.4, 3b.5, 3b.6, 3b.7, 3b.8, 3b.9, 3b.10) shipped. Out-of-scope follow-ups tracked separately: float reductions via `#[fp_reassoc]` opt-in (per line 106 — needs the trait surface + IEEE-754 reassoc story), capture-by-pointer for non-Copy types (per the "Par codegen: non-trivial captures" entry below — folds in alongside the cross-cutting capture extension when a workload surfaces a mutating capture). Sibling to the non-`par` regions entry above. Today's concurrency analyzer correctly identifies a loop-carried dependency through an accumulator as serializing — for a body like `for k in 0..K { sum = sum + f(inputs[k]); }`, `karac build --concurrency-report` prints `<no parallelization opportunities detected>` because every iteration reads-then-writes `sum`. **Recognize the dependency shape:** when the only loop-carried write is `acc = acc <op> expr` (or the methodic form `acc.combine(expr)`) and `<op>` is in the **associative + commutative** allow-list (`+`, `*`, `min`, `max`, `|`, `&`, `^` for ints/floats; `String.push` is associative but NOT commutative, ruled out; `Vec.push` likewise), lower the loop to a fan-out + reduce: each worker processes a contiguous slice of the iteration space into a per-thread partial; a final serial pass combines the partials with the same `<op>`. The fan-out reuses the existing `karac_par_run` runtime path that the non-`par` regions entry builds out — this entry is a strictly additive feature on top of that work.

  Design pillars (checkbox-tracked so each can be flipped as decisions firm up or work lands):

  - [x] **Validation criterion (canonical case).** [`kara-katas leetcode/1-100/7-reverse-integer/bench/reverse.kara`](../../../../kara-katas/leetcode/1-100/7-reverse-integer/) — K = 50,000,000 outer iters of `reverse(inputs[k % 1024])` summed into an i64 accumulator. **Hit 2026-05-20:** 44.2 ms vs Rust 448.4 ms — **10.16× ahead of Rust**, well above the original 4–6× projection. Kata headline ratio flipped from "kara 1.02× ahead of rust" (parity) to "10.16× ahead of rust" after the slice 3b.4 + 3b.6 + 3b.7 landing. See [`leetcode/1-100/7-reverse-integer/README.md § Benchmarks`](../../../../kara-katas/leetcode/1-100/7-reverse-integer/README.md#benchmarks) for the full bench shape and post-landing numbers.

  - [x] **Allow-list policy (settled at file time).** The reduction operator must be both **associative** (reordering combines preserves the result) and **commutative** (per-thread partials can be combined in non-source order without affecting the answer). The first version ships with a fixed allow-list rather than a user-extensible trait — adding the trait surface (`trait Reduction { fn identity() -> Self; fn combine(a: Self, b: Self) -> Self; }`) requires deciding the identity-element story for float `+` (the `0.0` identity drops to `-0.0` under IEEE-754 negative-zero rules, breaking determinism), and that's a separate design slice. Float `+` and `*` are **NOT** in the v1 allow-list because IEEE-754 addition is not associative — `(a + b) + c != a + (b + c)` in general, so per-thread combine order would make the answer non-deterministic, violating the cost-model entry's determinism requirement (line 183 of `phase-6-runtime.md`). Int reductions only at v1; float reductions deferred to a `#[fp_reassoc]` opt-in in v1.x.

  - [x] **Cost-model interaction.** Gated on the same cost-model fork threshold as the non-`par` regions entry: a reduction over K iterations is worth splitting only when `K * per_iter_cost > N_workers * scheduling_overhead`. For the kata-7 shape (50M iters of ~30 ops/iter = ~1.5 × 10⁹ ops, scheduling overhead ~few µs), the threshold is trivially met; for a 1000-iter loop with a single integer-add body, it's not. Reuse the same per-call cost heuristic the cost-model entry plans (`docs/implementation_checklist/phase-6-runtime.md` line 183). When the threshold is **not** met, the reduction stays sequential — silent fallback, no diagnostic; the user-visible `karac build --concurrency-report` output explains the decision. **Closed 2026-05-20** by the slice 3b.5 + 3b.8 pair: 3b.5 catches literal-K loops at compile time (no `karac_par_reduce` call emitted); 3b.8 catches variable-K loops at runtime (the codegen-time gate's same `estimate_body_cost_units` walk is threaded through the descriptor's `per_iter_cost_units` field, and the runtime short-circuits to a single-worker sequential call when `iter_total × per_iter_cost < pool_workers × DISPATCH_OVERHEAD_PER_CALL_UNITS_RT`). Together the two gates ensure no recognized reduction pays the dispatch overhead unless it amortizes.

  - [x] **Slicing (drafted 2026-05-19).** Three-slice tranche: (1) **analyzer recognition** — extend the concurrency analyzer to detect the reduction shape (single loop-carried write, op in the allow-list) and tag the loop with a `Reduction { op, init, accumulator_name }` annotation; no codegen change, exposed via `--concurrency-report`. (2) **runtime API** — extend `karac_par_run` (or add a sibling `karac_par_reduce`) with per-branch partial slots typed by the accumulator's lowered type + a final serial combine pass.
