(3) **codegen lowering** — emit the fan-out/reduce pattern for any loop tagged with a `Reduction` annotation whose cost-model threshold fires. Slice 1 is prerequisite for slices 2 + 3; 2 and 3 can be drafted in parallel but lock at the runtime ABI. **Surfaced 2026-05-19** during the kata-7 perf investigation; the kata's bench harness doubles as the validation case for slice 3.

      **Status tracker (2026-05-19).** Done in this tranche:
      - [x] **Slice 1 — analyzer recognition.** Landed `fd47114`. `LoopReduction { accumulator, op, stmt_index, loop_line }` recognition for op ∈ `+ * | & ^`, both pre-lowered `Binary` and lowered `Call(Path([type, op_method]), [a, b])` shapes, induction-step (`i = i + const_lit`, `i += const_lit`) folded as loop counters. Surfaced in `karac build --concurrency-report` as `reduction { op, accumulator, line }` per recognized loop. 11 new tests in `tests/concurrency.rs`.
      - [x] **Slice 2 — runtime `karac_par_reduce`.** Landed `ae72b22`. Opaque-bytes ABI with caller-provided `init_slot` / `worker_fn` / `combine_fn` function pointers — one runtime symbol covers every (op, type) pair in the allow-list without ABI growth. Identity-element discipline: every slot starts at identity, so 0-iter returns identity and the final combine folds slots in any order. v1 uses `thread::scope` per call. 8 new runtime tests stub the codegen-emitted fns directly so the dispatch path runs without the full compiler.
      - [x] **Slice 3a — codegen wiring + extern + diagnostic.** Landed `37b08a0`. Declares the `karac_par_reduce` extern in the codegen module, threads `loop_reductions` into `Codegen::concurrency_decisions` (already free since `FunctionConcurrency` carries the field), adds `loop_reduction_for_stmt(stmt_index)` lookup helper, and an `eprintln!`-style diagnostic gated on `KARAC_REDUCE_DEBUG=1` that surfaces every recognized reduction at codegen time. New IR-level test in `tests/par_codegen.rs` pins the extern declaration.
      - [x] **Slice 3b — actual lowering (v1, narrow shape).** Landed `e5ce4b3`. New `src/codegen/reduce.rs` module synthesizes per-(op, type) `init_slot` / `worker_fn` / `combine_fn` LLVM functions, builds a stack-allocated `KaracReduceDescriptor`, calls `karac_par_reduce`, and loads `out_slot` back into the accumulator's alloca. v1 narrow shape: `for k in 0..hi { ... }` with `+` op and i64 accumulator. Worker-fn body emission reuses `compile_block` against a rebound `self.variables` (accumulator → worker-local alloca at identity, loop var → worker-local alloca at chunk-start, captures → unpacked from a parent-built env-struct). Early exits reject the lowering. **Measured: 4.1× wall-clock speedup** on a 50M-iter Add-reduction with non-trivial inner work (1.36s → 0.33s), matching the roadmap projection. 3 new tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs`.

      Open follow-ups (each additive, no rework on already-landed slices):
      - [x] **Slice 3b.1 — non-Add ops.** Landed alongside this status update. `emit_reduce_init_fn` and `emit_reduce_combine_fn` are now parameterized by `(op, int_ty)` rather than hardcoded to Add+i64; the (op, type) pair drives both the helper symbol name (`__karac_reduce_<role>_<op>_i<width>`, cached per pair via the LLVM symbol table) and the identity element (`+`/`|`/`^` → 0, `*` → 1, `&` → all-ones via `IntType::const_all_ones()` — correct for signed and unsigned alike under two's-complement). The Add-only early return in `try_emit_reduction_lowering` is removed; all five recognized ops (`+`, `*`, `|`, `&`, `^`) now lower. 9 new tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs`: IR-level (helper symbol presence) + E2E (factorial-18 = 6_402_373_705_728_000 for Mul, OR-fold over [0, 100_000) = 131_071 for multi-worker BitOr, etc.).
      - [x] **Slice 3b.2 — non-i64 accumulator types.** Landed alongside slice 3b.1 (same commit — single coherent (op, type) generalization). The i64-only `acc_slot.ty != i64_t` gate widens to "any of i8/i16/i32/i64" via `BasicTypeEnum::IntType(acc_int_ty)` + `bit_width ∈ {8, 16, 32, 64}` (unsigned widths share the same LLVM int type, so they're covered transparently). `acc_int_ty` is threaded through worker fn synthesis (alloca + identity + final-publish load) and `emit_reduce_call` (slot_size / slot_align computed from bit width; out_slot alloca + load-back match). The runtime ABI keeps i64 start/end worker params; the worker fn truncates them to `acc_int_ty` in its prologue when narrower (gate: end_expr's type must equal acc type — natural outcome of source-level typechecker unification of `acc <op> k`). `iter_total` widening switched from sext to zext so high-bit-set unsigned end values widen correctly. 3 new tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs` for the Add+i32 path (IR pins helper symbols + `start.trunc` / `end.trunc`; E2E verifies Σ correctness through the truncation path). `run_program` updated to thread the full analysis pipeline so reduction E2E tests actually exercise the par_reduce lowering instead of silently validating the sequential fallback's output.
      - [x] **Slice 3b.3 — non-zero `lo` in for-range.** Landed alongside this status update. `LoopShape` gains an `Option<Expr>` `lo_expr` field; `extract_loop_shape` normalizes `None`/`Integer(0)` to `None` (no shift math at all in the common case — the worker's chunk-local index already matches the source-level `k`) and stores any other start as `Some(expr)`. When `lo_expr` is `Some`, `try_emit_reduction_lowering` compiles `lo` in the parent, computes `iter_total = end - lo` (named `iter.total` in IR), and threads `lo_val` through to `emit_reduce_worker_fn` (via a `has_lo: bool` flag) and `emit_reduce_call` (which prepends `lo` to the env-struct at field 0, allocating an env-struct even when no source-level captures exist). The worker fn unpacks `lo` from env field 0 into a plain `IntValue` (no alloca — read twice, never written) and adds it to `raw_start` / `raw_end` after truncation, producing the source-level `start..end` range. While-shape continues to require literal-zero init (unchanged). Const-eval cost gate updated: `const_eval_iter_count(end, lo)` now subtracts when both bounds are literals; variable-lo (or variable-end) bypasses the gate as before. 4 new tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs`: IR pins `iter.total` / `start.shift` / `end.shift` / `__reduce_lo` / `__reduce_env` for the variable-lo path; E2E covers literal-lo multi-worker (Σ from 5 to 100004 = 5_000_450_000), variable-lo single-worker (Σ from 10 to 1009 = 509_500), and Mul reduction over [3, 10) = 181_440 to pin the slice 3b.x corner where lo + non-Add op interact.
      - [x] **Slice 3b.4 — `while` loop shape.** Landed alongside this status update. New `extract_loop_shape` helper in `src/codegen/reduce.rs` returns a canonical `LoopShape { loop_var, end_expr, body }` for either the for-range shape (slice 3b) or the new while shape. The while-shape parser pulls `(loop_var, end_expr)` out of the condition (handles both pre-lowering `Binary { Lt, ... }` and post-lowering `Call(Path([T, "lt"]), ...)`), strips the body's terminal `k = k + 1` / `k += 1` increment so the worker fn synth uses the same back-edge code path as the for-loop case, and verifies the preceding `let mut k: T = 0;` init. 4 new tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs` (IR-level, small-N matches serial, multi-worker, compound-assign increment variant).
      - [x] **Slice 3b.5 — cost-model gate.** Landed alongside this status update. Compile-time gate in `src/codegen/reduce.rs::try_emit_reduction_lowering`: const-evaluates the loop's end-bound to a literal iteration count, walks the body AST for a per-iter cost estimate (CALL_COST_UNITS=10 for function/method calls, 1 unit per arithmetic op, free for leaf literals/identifiers, NESTED_LOOP_MULTIPLIER=16 for inner loops), and skips the lowering when `K * per_iter_cost < REDUCE_DISPATCH_THRESHOLD_UNITS` (= 80,000 unit-iters ≈ 80µs, calibrated from the slice-3b.7 ~10µs dispatch overhead × assumed-N=8). Variable-K loops bypass the gate (the runtime can't see through to const-eval the end expr cheaply at codegen time; in practice variable-K loops like the kata-7 bench's `k_iters = 50M` are large). Sequential fallback is silent — no diagnostic; the user-visible `karac build --concurrency-report` output still names the recognized reduction. 4 new tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs`: K=100 trivial body → no `karac_par_reduce` call (IR); K=100 trivial body → correct Σ sink (E2E); K=100 with method-call body → still gated (cost weight respected); variable-K K=100 → lowers anyway (bypass pin). Kata-7 unchanged at 43.9 ms (variable-K bypass). A dynamic runtime-side gate (carrying the per-iter cost estimate into the descriptor) is a follow-up for the variable-K case.
      - [x] **Slice 3b.6 — kata-7 bench validation.** Landed alongside slice 3b.4. With the while-shape codegen in place, the kata-7 bench's K-iter sum loop lowers to `karac_par_reduce` automatically. Vec-by-value capture is sufficient: the parent's `inputs: Vec[i32]` `{ptr, len, cap}` struct is copied into the env-struct, every worker reads through the shared buffer (safe for read-only access — the body never mutates `inputs`). **Measured headline (M5 Pro, hyperfine warmup 3, 10 runs, `--shell=none`):** kara codegen 45.0 ± 3.1 ms vs Rust 444.0 ± 3.3 ms — **9.87× ahead of Rust**, far above the roadmap's 4–6× projection. CPU utilization 649ms user / 45ms wall ≈ 14× — close to perfect parallelism across the M5 Pro's P+E cores. Sink matches Python's exactly (`-292465958482676`). Capture-by-pointer for non-Copy types remains a separate optimization (today's by-value works because reads are safe; only writes would race). Kata README refresh tracked in a sibling commit.
      - [x] **Slice 3b.7 — pool-sharing for `karac_par_reduce`.** Landed alongside this status update. `Task { func, ctx_addr }` generalized to `Task { run: Box<dyn FnOnce(&AtomicBool) + Send> }` so the same pool dispatches both `karac_par_run`'s 2-arg branch invocations and `karac_par_reduce`'s 5-arg worker invocations. New `dispatch_and_wait(call, tasks)` helper consolidates the queue-push + work-helping wait loop pattern; the wait loop opportunistically executes pool tasks while the per-call `Condvar` blocks, so nested `par_reduce` inside a `par {}` block can't deadlock the pool. Per-call cost drops from ~tens of µs (`thread::scope` spawn) to one `Box` alloc per task (~hundreds of ns total for N=18 workers). **Wall-clock on kata-7 essentially unchanged** (44.2 ms vs the prior 45.0 ms, within σ) because the kata is a one-shot reduction — the pool benefit is per-call dispatch latency, which dominates only when reductions fire repeatedly. **Peak RSS unchanged** (still 1.4 MiB) because both `thread::scope` and the long-lived pool hold N OS-thread stack reservations at peak; the pool just holds them across calls rather than re-reserving per call. RSS reductions live at the pool-sizing layer (separate knob — tracked in the `karac_par_run` follow-up entry below).
      - [x] **Slice 3b.8 — runtime-side dynamic cost gate.** Landed alongside this status update. `KaracReduceDescriptor` gains a trailing `per_iter_cost_units: usize` field (struct shape grows from 7 → 8 fields, `#[repr(C)]` layout pinned by an IR test in `tests/par_codegen.rs`). Codegen always emits the field with the same `estimate_body_cost_units(&shape.body)` walk slice 3b.5 already runs (lifted out of the const-K branch so variable-K loops also carry a meaningful estimate); the body-cost walker bottoms at 1, so `0` is reserved as a "no estimate / always dispatch" sentinel for any hand-built descriptor (today only the runtime tests' `run_reduce` helper, kept for back-compat with the existing dispatch-correctness suite). The runtime gate in `karac_par_reduce` short-circuits to a single-worker sequential call when `iter_total × per_iter_cost_units < pool_workers × DISPATCH_OVERHEAD_PER_CALL_UNITS_RT` (10_000 units ≈ 10 µs, mirrors the codegen-side constant for calibration consistency). Closes the open design pillar on line 108 — together with slice 3b.5, no recognized reduction pays the par_reduce dispatch overhead unless the estimated total work amortizes it across the actual pool worker count. 3 new tests in `runtime/src/lib.rs` exercise the gate by call-count: small-K + real per_iter → 1 worker_fn invocation (sequential); small-K + fat per_iter → N invocations (dispatched); sentinel 0 → N invocations regardless of K (bypass). Per-test AtomicUsize counters flow through the descriptor's `ctx` pointer so cargo-parallel tests don't race on a shared static. **Variable-K kata-7 measurement post-3b.8** stays at the 44 ms baseline (variable-K shape's `iter_total × per_iter` cost is far above the threshold), so the cross-cutting refactor pays no perf tax on the validated headline workload.
      - [x] **Slice 3b.9 — while-shape non-zero literal init.** Landed alongside this status update. Mirror of slice 3b.3 for the while-loop path: `preceding_stmt_inits_to_zero` (bool) → `preceding_stmt_int_literal_init` (returns `Option<Expr>` — the init expression for any int literal). `extract_loop_shape`'s While arm normalizes `Integer(0)` → `lo_expr = None` (current path, no shift math) and any other int literal → `lo_expr = Some(expr)`. All the slice-3b.3 lo-threading machinery (env-struct field 0, worker fn `start.shift` / `end.shift` add, parent `iter.total` sub) is reused unchanged — a single shared shape-extractor + lowering path now handles both for-range `for k in lo..hi` and while `let mut k: T = lo; while k < hi { ...; k += 1; }`. 3 new tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs`: IR pins `__reduce_lo` / `start.shift` / `end.shift` / `__reduce_env` for the non-zero init while-shape; E2E covers small-N (Σ from 3 to 102 = 5_250, gated to sequential by the cost model — still correct) and multi-worker (Σ from 10 to 100_009 = 5_000_950_000).
      - [x] **Slice 3b.10 — while-shape arbitrary init expression.** Landed alongside this status update. Lifts slice 3b.9's int-literal-only gate by reading the init value from the parent's already-initialized k alloca instead of re-evaluating the init expression. `preceding_stmt_int_literal_init` → `preceding_stmt_init` (drops the `matches!(value.kind, ExprKind::Integer(_, _))` gate; returns any RHS). `extract_loop_shape`'s While arm now three-way normalizes: `Integer(0)` → `lo_expr = None`; non-zero int literal → `lo_expr = Some(literal)` (re-compile, free); anything else → `lo_expr = Some(Identifier(loop_var))` (compile_expr loads from k's alloca). Single-evaluation guaranteed regardless of side effects in the init expression, because the let-stmt has already evaluated it once before we reach the while-stmt; the adjacency check (`stmt_index - 1`) means nothing modifies k between let and while. 3 new tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs`: IR pins the lo-threading symbols for the variable-init while-shape; E2E covers multi-worker variable init (Σ from 20 to 100_019 = 5_001_950_000) and a complex `base + offset` init expression (Σ from 37 to 100_036 = 5_003_650_000).

- [x] **Auto-par reduction Min/Max: analyzer recognition + codegen lowering (single combined slice).** **Landed 2026-05-20.** All five planned pieces shipped: (1) `ReductionOp::Min`/`Max` variants + `symbol()` (`"min"`/`"max"`); (2) codegen identity via `signed_int_max`/`signed_int_min` helpers (sign-bit-only / `T::MAX` patterns at any int width); (3) codegen combine via `icmp slt`+`select` for Min, `icmp sgt`+`select` for Max, extracted into a shared `emit_reduce_combine_inst` helper so future op additions only update one match; (4) analyzer direct-call recognition (`reduction_binary_shape` extends to `"min"`/`"max"` method names); (5) analyzer conditional-assign recognition (`conditional_minmax_shape` desugars `if x < acc { acc = x; }` to Min and `if x > acc { acc = x; }` to Max, with cover for both `Stmt::Expr` and `final_expr` positions in the loop body — kata-153's for-range body has the if as `final_expr`, missed by the initial Stmt-only integration). **Load-bearing correctness fix surfaced during this slice:** `emit_reduce_call` previously stored the worker-combined result directly to the parent's accumulator alloca, overwriting the parent's pre-existing value. For Add reductions starting at 0 (= identity) this passed silently; for Min/Max with a non-identity initial value (kata-153 shapes `let mut m = nums[0]; for i in 1..n { if nums[i] < m { m = nums[i]; }}`) it would have dropped `nums[0]` from consideration. Fix: after par_reduce returns, load the parent's existing value, fold with the par_reduce result via the same combine helper, then store back. Generalizes Add correctness too — `let mut sum = 100; for k... sum += k` now correctly produces `100 + sum_of_K` instead of dropping the 100. **Tests:** 7 new in `tests/concurrency.rs` (direct Min/Max + commutative-pair + else-branch reject + cond-unrelated reject + post-lowering Call shape + post-lowering for-range with final_expr-positioned if), 4 new in `tests/par_codegen.rs` (Min IR pins `icmp slt` + `%min` select + `__karac_reduce_init_min_i64`; Max IR pins `icmp sgt` + `%max` select; Min multi-worker E2E over `(i*7+11)%977` → 0; Max multi-worker E2E → 976; initial-value-preserved E2E that bottoms out the fold-the-parent's-value path with `m = -999999` initial). **Validation:** kata-153 `linear_scan`'s `find_min` `if x < m { m = x; }` inner loop now recognized — `karac build --concurrency-report` prints `reduction { op: min, accumulator: m, line: 11 }`; binary grows 49 KiB → 311.9 KiB (par_reduce linked); User-CPU rises 3.5 ms → 11.8 ms (parallel engaging). Wall stays at 4.9 ms because the workload is memory-bandwidth-bound (2M i64 loads per call × K=10 ≈ scan 16 MiB × 10, near the M5 Pro's ~30 GB/s ceiling), not because the parallelism failed — kata-7's compute-bound shape was the one with 9× headroom. No regression. Original entry framing follows.

  Original entry: Surfaced 2026-05-20 during the post-3b.10 kata re-bench sweep. The umbrella entry's allow-list at line 106 lists `min max` alongside `+ * | & ^`, but no implementation slice ever shipped them: `ReductionOp` (concurrency.rs:188) has 5 variants (Add/Mul/BitOr/BitAnd/BitXor), `reduce_identity` (codegen/reduce.rs:987) handles the same 5, and the combine-instruction builder (codegen/reduce.rs:438) emits `int_add` / `int_mul` / `or` / `and` / `xor` only. Slice 1 (line 113) and slice 3b.1 (line 119) both stopped short of Min/Max despite the design pillar. Combined work in one coherent slice: (1) **enum + plumbing** — add `ReductionOp::Min` / `ReductionOp::Max` variants, extend `symbol()` (`"min"` / `"max"` in the report), no `from_bin_op` or `from_compound_op` extension (no BinOp / CompoundOp glyph — recognition is call-form or conditional-only). (2) **codegen identity** — Min identity = `T::MAX` for the acc int type (the recognized loop's body type is signed in source today; codegen uses `IntType::const_int(MAX_for_width, true)` where `MAX_for_width = (1u64 << (bit_width-1)).wrapping_sub(1)` for bit_width ∈ {8,16,32,64}). Max identity = `T::MIN` = `(1u64 << (bit_width-1))` (the sign-bit-only pattern). Unsigned vs signed is not source-level visible at `ReductionOp` today; signed Min/Max identities ship first, with a separate follow-up for unsigned if a workload needs it. (3) **codegen combine** — emit `icmp slt` + `select` for signed Min, `icmp sgt` + `select` for signed Max; no LLVM intrinsic dependency (lowest-common-denominator), and `-O2`'s `InstCombine` lifts the select+icmp idiom to `smin`/`smax` intrinsics so the optimized output matches what a hand-rolled intrinsic call would produce. (4) **analyzer direct-call recognition** — `acc = min(acc, x)` / `acc = i64.min(acc, x)` (mirror of the existing `Call(Path([type, op_method]), [a, b])` recognition in `reduction_binary_shape` with `"min"` / `"max"` method names; commutativity makes `min(x, acc)` accepted symmetrically). (5) **analyzer conditional-assign recognition** — `if x < acc { acc = x; }` desugars to `Min`, `if x > acc { acc = x; }` desugars to `Max`; only fires when the if has no else, the body is exactly one accumulator-assignment statement, and the condition compares the assigned RHS against the accumulator (`<` for Min, `>` for Max). The analyzer's existing per-stmt inner-write check (`classify_loop_body`'s `StmtKind::Expr` arm) currently rejects any `Expr(If { ... })` that writes to an outer-scope name; the conditional-assign path needs to special-case-recognize before the rejection fires. Validation workload: [`kara-katas leetcode/101-200/153-find-minimum-in-rotated-sorted-array/bench/linear_scan.kara`](../../../../kara-katas/leetcode/101-200/153-find-minimum-in-rotated-sorted-array/) — `find_min`'s `if x < m { m = x; }` inner loop is 4.9 ms today single-threaded (N=2M, K=10 outer, binary 49 KiB without `karac_par_reduce` linked); projecting compression to ~0.5–1 ms once analyzer + codegen both engage and the binary grows to ~310 KiB with `karac_par_reduce` linked. Tests land in `tests/concurrency.rs` (recognition shapes, both forms) and `tests/par_codegen.rs` (IR pins `icmp slt` + `select` for signed Min combine + identity = `i64::MAX`; E2E pins multi-worker correctness on a Min-reduction over a Vec). Once shipped, sweep affected kata READMEs per the memory rule on cross-cutting fixes. Cross-refs: lines 100 (closed umbrella — design pillar 106 was aspirational, not implemented), 106 (allow-list), 113 (slice 1 — recognition shape pattern), 119 (slice 3b.1 — codegen op-matrix pattern).

- [x] **Auto-par reduction cost gate: function-call body-cost estimation (path (a) shipped, path (b) deferred).** **Path (a) landed 2026-05-20.** New `CostEstimator` struct in `src/codegen/reduce.rs` builds a free-fn body lookup from `Program.items` at the start of each `try_emit_reduction_lowering` call (via `self.program_snapshot`), then walks the loop body with the same per-expr weights as the prior free-fn estimator but recursively descends into known free-fn callees up to `INLINE_DEPTH_CAP = 3` levels. Past the cap, recursive call graphs (e.g. `a() → b() → a()`), or for any unresolvable callee shape (`MethodCall`, multi-segment `Path`, `OptionalChain`, opaque identifier), falls back to the original `CALL_COST_UNITS = 10`. The estimator's recursion is bounded by depth alone — no visited-set needed — so indirect-recursive call graphs terminate cleanly. **Tests:** 4 new in `tests/par_codegen.rs`: (1) trivial inlined callee `double(x) { x + x }` still gate-blocks at K=100 (callee body cost = 1, doesn't accidentally over-trigger); (2) heavy inlined callee unlocks K=3000 outer that wouldn't pass with `CALL_COST_UNITS` — discriminator pinned at `helper()` body cost ~33 via inlining (16 × inner for-body=2 + let + return) so K=3000 × 35 = 105k crosses the 80k threshold, whereas opaque-cost K=3000 × 12 = 36k blocks; (3) E2E correctness of the inlining-unlocked sink; (4) indirect-recursive callees terminate via depth cap (no hang). **Validation reality vs. original prediction:** the original entry projected kata-121 compressing 14.6 ms → ~2 ms; in practice **kata-121 still measures 14.6 ms single-threaded** after this slice. The inlining IS engaging (max_profit's body cost rises from `CALL_COST_UNITS = 10` to ~160 via inlining: 11 + 1 + 3 + 1 + 144 for the inner `for i in 1..n` with NESTED_LOOP_MULTIPLIER = 16), but K = 10 outer × ~172 per-iter = ~1720 cost units is still well below the 80,000 threshold. The remaining gap is the **`NESTED_LOOP_MULTIPLIER = 16` underestimate**: real-world inner-loop trip counts (kata-121's N = 2_000_000) blow past 16 by 5+ orders of magnitude, but bumping the multiplier without empirical calibration risks over-parallelizing small loops. Two follow-ups to unlock kata-121: **(b) `#[hot]` / `#[cold]` attribute** as an authoritative override when the user knows the call is heavy (deferred per the original priority order), and **NESTED_LOOP_MULTIPLIER tuning** with bench-driven calibration across several katas. Both filed separately when needed — the inlining-aware infrastructure shipped here is the load-bearing piece both follow-ups build on. **Validation that the slice itself shipped correctly:** kata-7 unchanged (variable-K bypasses the gate entirely); kata-153 linear_scan unchanged (Min reduction wall is memory-bandwidth-bound per the Min/Max slice's closeout note); full test suite passes (cargo test --features llvm green across all crates); clippy + fmt clean. Cross-refs: lines 100 (closed umbrella), 108 (cost-model pillar — slice 3b.5 + 3b.8 + this slice all contribute), 123 (slice 3b.5 — the free `estimate_body_cost_units` it introduced is now the inlining-aware `CostEstimator::estimate_body`), 126 (slice 3b.8 — the runtime `per_iter_cost` field now carries the inlining-aware estimate).

  Original entry: Surfaced 2026-05-20 during the same re-bench sweep. Slice 3b.5's compile-time gate (line 123) scores every function or method call as `CALL_COST_UNITS = 10` regardless of body depth, and slice 3b.8 (line 126) carries the same per-iter cost into the descriptor for runtime gating. This bottoms out for outer-reduction patterns shaped `for _ in 0..K { sum = sum + f(big_input); }` — kata-121's K=10 outer scores as `10 * 10 = 100` cost units, well below the `N_workers * 10_000 = 180_000` threshold, so the codegen-time gate rejects the dispatch and emits a sequential loop even though each `f` call is a 2M-iter scan (~1.5 ms of real work per call). Result: kata-121 binary is **49 KiB instead of 311 KiB** (no `karac_par_reduce` linked), wall = 14.6 ms with single-threaded User-CPU 12.7 ms. Same shape costs kata-153 linear_scan a parallelism opportunity on its K=10 outer. Two paths to fix, in priority order: (a) **inlining-aware recursive walk** — when the callee is non-recursive and lives in the same module (or the stdlib), recursively call `estimate_body_cost_units` on its body up to a depth cap (2–3 levels) so a call into a 2M-iter scan scores ~2M units instead of 10; automatic, no user surface needed, covers the common shape. (b) **`#[hot]` / `#[cold]` attributes** as an authoritative override when the user knows the call is heavy/light — cleaner ergonomics, opt-in surface, lands as a follow-up after (a). Validation: kata-121 should compress from 14.6 ms wall → ~2 ms (User-CPU stays ~13 ms, just spread across cores); kata-153 linear_scan from 4.9 ms → ~0.5–1 ms; kata-7 unchanged (variable-K shape already passes the gate). Tests land in `tests/par_codegen.rs` (gate-engagement IR + E2E pinning the new call-cost shape). Cross-refs: lines 100 (closed umbrella), 108 (cost-model pillar), 123 (slice 3b.5), 126 (slice 3b.8).

- [x] **Auto-par reduction memory-bound rejection gate.** **Landed 2026-05-20.** Surfaced by the Min/Max slice's kata-153 measurement: the existing cost gates (3b.5 compile-time + 3b.8 runtime-time) score memory accesses (`Index`, `FieldAccess`) at the same low compute-units weight as a single arithmetic op, so a body that's mostly memory-streaming (`let x = nums[i]; if x < m { m = x; }`) looks compute-parallelizable (~10M units for N=2M >> 180k threshold) when it's actually bandwidth-bound — splitting the work across workers doesn't reduce wall, but does pay dispatch overhead. Measured cost on kata-153 before this gate: User-CPU rose 3.5 ms → 11.8 ms (~3.4× more CPU for zero wall benefit), binary grew 49 → 311.9 KiB (+262 KiB to link the runtime). New `body_is_memory_bound` helper + `MemoryBoundDetector` walk in `src/codegen/reduce.rs`: fires when the body has at least one Index/FieldAccess AND no substantial function/method call. "Substantial" excludes lowered primitive-op `Call(Path([type, op_method]), [a, b])` shapes (`add`/`sub`/`mul`/`div`/`rem`/`neg`/`eq`/`ne`/`lt`/`le`/`gt`/`ge`/`bitor`/`bitand`/`bitxor`/`shl`/`shr`/`min`/`max`) — these are intrinsic operator dispatches, not real callees, and ignoring them is load-bearing because every body has at least one comparison post-lowering. Also excludes trivial accessor MethodCalls (`len`/`is_empty`/`as_slice`/`as_str`/`as_bytes`) — shape-queries on the collection don't add real compute. Gate fires *before* the cost-model gates so the per-iter estimate isn't wasted on a loop we'll reject. **Tests:** 2 new in `tests/par_codegen.rs`: (1) memory-bound `find_min` shape skips par_reduce (validates kata-153's specific pattern); (2) Index + substantial Call body bypasses the gate (pins that has-call escapes the rejection — kata-7's `sum + reverse(inputs[k])` shape). **Validation:** kata-153 User-CPU back to 3.6 ms (baseline restored); binary back to 49 KiB (baseline restored); wall 5.2 ms (parity, within noise). kata-7 unchanged — User=645ms ≈ 15× wall (parallel still engaging), binary 319 KiB (par_reduce still linked) — confirms compute-bound workloads with substantial calls bypass the gate correctly. **Trade-off:** false-negative bias — a body with a heavy Call + heavy Index (e.g. `f(big_index_chain)` where the index chain dominates) gets parallelized even though it's bandwidth-bound. Accepting that direction is the safer call: missing a parallelism win on a hybrid workload is recoverable (smarter detector can land later), but over-parallelizing memory-bound work pays cost every run. Cross-refs: lines 100 (closed umbrella), 108 (cost-model pillar — now includes a memory-bandwidth dimension), 134 (cost-gate fn-call body-cost — sibling cost-estimator improvement).

- [x] **Auto-par reduction analyzer: nested-binary chain recognizer extension.** **Landed 2026-05-20.** Surfaced during the post-Min/Max kata survey: `sum = sum + r[0] + r[1]` (kata-5 outer + a natural user-code shape) parses left-associatively as `Binary(+, Binary(+, sum, r[0]), r[1])`. The prior `reduction_binary_shape` only checked the outer Binary's direct operands for the acc identifier — neither child matched, so the chain fell through to "rejected." This entry extends recognition to any chain of the same allow-list op where acc appears exactly once across the leaf positions (by commutativity, any such chain can be reordered to `acc + (others-combined)` — the standard fan-out + combine model handles it). New `count_acc_in_chain` helper walks the chain through both pre-lowering Binary nodes and post-lowering Call shapes (`Call(Path([T, op_method]), [a, b])`) uniformly via `op_method_for_bin_op` / `bin_op_for_op_method` mapping helpers. Recognition fires when the count is exactly 1 — count=0 means acc isn't in the chain (not a reduction step), count≥2 means acc compounds with itself (`sum + sum + a` = `2*sum + a`, not a valid identity-element fan-out). **Tests:** 6 new in `tests/concurrency.rs`: chain of 2 (kata-5 shape), chain of 4 (arbitrary depth), acc in middle (commutative reorder), mixed-op rejection (`sum + a * b` — outer direct match works, walker doesn't over-traverse), double-acc rejection, post-lowering Call chain recognition. **Expected kata wall impact: zero** — kata-5 outer K=10 still hits the cost gate (and the inlined longest_palindrome body is memory-streaming so memory-bound gate would catch it anyway). Slice ships analyzer capability for future workloads; recognizer no longer rejects a natural user shape. Cross-refs: lines 100 (closed umbrella), 113 (slice 1 — recognition shape this extends).

- [x] **Auto-par reduction analyzer: conditional accumulator-update recognition.** **Landed 2026-05-20** (`3294e50`). Surfaced benching `kara-katas/leetcode/65-valid-number/bench/valid.kara`: outer loop body `let r = is_number(...); if r { sum = sum + 1i64; }` ran single-threaded (User 62.5 ms ≈ wall 64.3 ms, no parallelism) because the slice-1 matcher recognized `acc = acc + EXPR` but rejected the `if cond { acc = acc + DELTA }` shape, even though the two forms are semantically equivalent for associative+commutative ops with a known identity: `if cond { acc = acc + delta }  ≡  acc = acc + (if cond { delta } else { 0 })`. New `conditional_acc_update_shape` method in `src/concurrency.rs` recognizes the if-wrapped form for both `StmtKind::Assign` and `StmtKind::CompoundAssign` inner stmts, with three soundness guards: (1) else branch absent OR an empty block (non-empty else taints the contribution shape; reserved for a future two-arm slice — see follow-on below); (2) then-block is exactly one statement of the recognized update shape; (3) condition does NOT read the accumulator (`if sum > threshold { sum = sum + 1 }` is order-dependent — each iteration's decision depends on prior workers' partials; reject). Wired into both the `StmtKind::Expr` arm and the `final_expr` branch of `classify_loop_body` so trailing-no-semicolon shapes are caught the same way `conditional_minmax_shape` already was. **Tests:** 7 new in `tests/concurrency.rs` covering accept paths (Add via Assign, Add via CompoundAssign, with empty-else, Mul accumulator) and reject paths (cond reads acc, non-empty else, multi-stmt then-block); renamed pre-existing `test_reduction_rejects_nested_inner_write` → `test_reduction_recognized_for_nested_conditional_acc_update` since that test's body shape is now what the new matcher accepts. **Validation:** re-running kata 65's bench dropped wall 64.3 → 8.9 ms (7.2× speedup from the single analyzer extension), User-CPU 62.5 → 67.1 ms (1.0× → 7.5× — auto-par engaging across cores), kara/rust ratio flipped from 1.15× slower to **6.21× faster**. Cross-refs: lines 100 (closed umbrella), 113 (slice 1 — recognition shape this extends), 140 (sibling chain-recognizer extension, same date).

- [x] **Auto-par reduction analyzer: two-arm conditional accumulator-update.** **Landed 2026-05-20.** Extension to the 1-arm conditional-acc-update slice (line 142). The 1-arm matcher recognized `if cond { acc = acc + delta; }` and the trivially-equivalent empty-else form but rejected `if cond { acc = acc + delta_a; } else { acc = acc + delta_b; }` — both arms write the accumulator, both add-shaped, both contributions order-independent under associative+commutative `+`. This extension lifts the rejection: when both arms are single-statement updates targeting the same accumulator with the same op, the shape is recognized as a reduction. Semantically equivalent to `acc = acc + (if cond { delta_a } else { delta_b })`, so the same fan-out + combine model handles it. **Implementation.** Refactored `conditional_acc_update_shape` in `src/concurrency.rs` to factor the per-arm classification into two shared free helpers: `single_stmt_as_acc_update` (classifies a single `Stmt` as Assign/CompoundAssign accumulator update via the existing `reduction_binary_shape` / `ReductionOp::from_compound_op` machinery) and `single_stmt_block_as_acc_update` (the block wrapper requiring exactly one stmt + no trailing expr). The if-stmt walker calls `single_stmt_block_as_acc_update` on the then-block, then dispatches on the else-branch: absent or empty → 1-arm shape; single-update with matching (acc, op) → 2-arm shape; anything else → reject. Delta expressions remain acc-free by construction since `reduction_binary_shape` requires acc to appear exactly once on each arm's RHS. The condition-doesn't-read-acc guard is unchanged. **Tests:** 5 new in `tests/concurrency.rs` (`test_reduction_recognized_for_two_arm_acc_update_same_op` with literal deltas, `test_reduction_recognized_for_two_arm_acc_update_compound` with CompoundAssign in both arms, `test_reduction_recognized_for_two_arm_acc_update_with_variable_deltas` with non-literal expressions, `test_reduction_rejects_two_arm_acc_update_with_different_accumulators`, `test_reduction_rejects_two_arm_acc_update_with_mixed_ops`); the pre-existing `test_reduction_rejects_conditional_acc_update_with_nonempty_else` was flipped to `test_reduction_recognized_for_two_arm_acc_update_same_op` since that test's body shape is now exactly what this slice recognizes. 2 new in `tests/par_codegen.rs` covering the end-to-end pipeline through codegen + runtime + sink-correctness (assign-form: hit=+3 / miss=+1 → 166668 over K=100k with i%3==0 trigger; compound-assign-form same workload). All 65 concurrency tests + 89 par_codegen tests pass; fmt + clippy clean. **Workload impact:** any "tally with two outcomes" shape — `if hit { right += 1 } else { right += 0 }`-style code where both branches contribute to the same accumulator with potentially different deltas. Cross-refs: lines 100 (closed umbrella), 142 (1-arm slice this extends), 140 (sibling chain-recognizer extension, same date).

- [x] **Auto-par reduction analyzer: collect-style `if cond { acc.push(x) }` reduction.** Different reduction kind from the conditional-acc-update slice — this is a Vec/String/Buffer accumulator that *collects* per-iter contributions rather than scalar-folding them. Today every `acc.push(x)` write to an outer-scope name fails the simple-reduction recognizer (it isn't `acc = acc <op> EXPR` shape). Lowering: each worker collects into a private partial `Vec[T]` slot, then a final serial concat (`extend` / `append` chain) builds the parent's full result. **Important:** the final result is order-dependent (concat order = worker order, not call order), so this is **only** sound when the user's algorithm tolerates any ordering — that's true for "set of accepted values" use cases (counting matches with their values, building a worklist of candidates) but **not** for "preserve input order" (which is a different reduction primitive — needs reorderable partials). **Design call (2026-05-20):** the order-not-preserved property requires explicit user opt-in via the new `#[par_unordered]` attribute on the loop. Auto-firing without opt-in was rejected — silent semantic surprises in user code are not acceptable, and the project's `no workarounds — fix the compiler` discipline supports surfacing the choice in the source rather than hiding it. Slice scope: (1) **Phase 1 — `#[par_unordered]` attribute parser surface.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-20. AST: `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` field added to `ExprKind::While`/`WhileLet`/`For`/`Loop`. Parser: new `Token::Pound` arm in `parse_primary` recognises `#[par_unordered]` (the only attribute name accepted at Phase 1) before a `while`/`for`/`loop` keyword; non-loop expressions after the attribute block are rejected with a focused diagnostic; unknown attribute names on loops are also rejected. Six new tests in `tests/parser.rs` cover the three loop kinds + the regression that un-attributed loops still parse + the two reject diagnostics. No behaviour change yet — the analyzer (Phase 2) and codegen (Phase 3) don't consume the new attribute field, so `#[par_unordered]` is currently a no-op annotation. Labeled-loop targets (`#[par_unordered] my_label: while ...`) are deferred to a follow-up slice — the unlabeled case is the one Phase 2 will recognise. (2) **Phase 2 — analyzer recognition gated on the attribute.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-20. `ReductionOp::Collect` variant added to the public enum with `symbol() = "collect"`; codegen `try_emit_reduction_lowering` early-returns `Ok(None)` on `ReductionOp::Collect` so Phase 3's heap-Vec lowering can land later without affecting the int-only ops (`reduce_op_short_name`, `reduce_identity`, `emit_reduce_combine_inst` all have explicit `Collect => unreachable!()` arms for exhaustiveness). Analyzer-side: `classify_loop_body` now accepts an `attributes: &[Attribute]` parameter (threaded through `recognize_reductions`); when `#[par_unordered]` is present, two new shape matchers fire: free `collect_push_shape` recognises `acc.push(EXPR)` (single-arg `push` method call on a bare-identifier receiver), and `conditional_collect_shape` recognises `if cond { acc.push(EXPR); }` (with the optional empty-else variant). Both shapes appear in both `StmtKind::Expr` and `final_expr` positions; `let_introduced` guards skip body-local accumulators. Mixed Collect+scalar reductions in the same loop are rejected by the existing single-accumulator contract. 7 new analyzer tests in `tests/concurrency.rs` cover positive recognition (bare push, conditional push, empty-else), gating (bare and conditional push without attribute fall through to no-reduction), and rejection (body-local acc, mixed Collect+Add). Behaviour validation: `karac check --concurrency-report` on a `#[par_unordered] while ... { if cond { results.push(k); } }` workload reports `reduction { op: collect, accumulator: results }` and the codegen path falls through to sequential, producing the correct sink (no parallel speedup yet — Phase 3 lands the lowering). (3) **Phase 3 — codegen.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-21. Implementation route diverged from the originally-filed plan: the existing `karac_par_reduce` runtime FFI (slot_size + init/worker/combine fn pointers) is type-generic over slot width, so **no `runtime/src/lib.rs` changes were required**; all Phase 3 work lives in `src/codegen/reduce.rs`. `try_emit_reduction_lowering`'s Collect early-return now dispatches to a new `try_emit_collect_reduction_lowering` method that mirrors the scalar shape-extraction path but uses the Vec-struct (24-byte `{ptr, len, cap}`) slot ABI. Three Collect-specific codegen helpers: (a) `emit_reduce_collect_init_fn(elem_int_ty)` writes the empty-Vec literal `{null, 0, 0}` into the slot — cached by element-type bit width so multiple sites share one definition; (b) `emit_reduce_collect_combine_fn(elem_int_ty)` extends `src` into `dst` (malloc a fresh `(dst.len + src.len) * elem_size` buffer, memcpy dst's elements first then src's, free both old buffers, zero src so the slot's subsequent cleanup is a no-op) — same per-elem-type caching; (c) `emit_reduce_collect_worker_fn` allocas a local Vec accumulator, registers it under the source-level acc name in `self.variables` + `self.vec_elem_types` so the body's `acc.push(EXPR)` dispatches through the existing `compile_vec_method` push path, runs the loop body, and copies the final Vec struct into the slot at exit (no cleanup registration — buffer ownership transfers to the slot). The post-call fold in `emit_reduce_collect_call` reuses `combine_fn` to extend `out_slot`'s Vec into the parent's accumulator, so pre-existing items in the parent's `acc` (e.g. `let mut acc = Vec.new(); acc.push(-1); #[par_unordered] for ...`) are preserved at the head of the final dst. **Cost gates.** `#[par_unordered]` is an explicit user opt-in to parallel dispatch, so the Collect path skips the memory-bound gate and emits `per_iter_cost_units = 0` (runtime sentinel for "always dispatch"); second-guessing the user's attribute would surprise them. Phase-3 supported element types: `Vec[i8]` … `Vec[i64]` (the scalar reduce path's int-width gate, reused). Non-int element types (String, nested-Vec, struct) fall back to sequential codegen; broader element-type support is a follow-up. **Tests:** 5 new in `tests/par_codegen.rs` — three sink-correctness e2e (bare `acc.push(k)` produces length 1000 + sum 499500 over `0..1000`; conditional `if k%3==0 { hits.push(k); }` produces 334 + 166833; parent-initial items at head of final dst with length 102 + sum 4947 after `acc.push(-1); acc.push(-2); #[par_unordered] for k in 0..100`); one IR pin asserting `karac_par_reduce` call + `__karac_reduce_init_collect_i64` + `__karac_reduce_combine_collect_i64` + `__karac_reduce_worker_collect_<N>` symbols are present in IR; one regression guard that an un-attributed `for k in 0..K { results.push(k); }` does NOT emit the Collect helpers (sequential fallthrough preserved). All gates green: 89 par_codegen tests pass, 65 concurrency tests pass, full `cargo test --features llvm` zero regressions, fmt + clippy `--all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` clean. See follow-on entry below for Phase 4 (demonstration kata). Cross-refs: lines 100 (closed umbrella), 142 (1-arm sibling), 144 (2-arm sibling), 141 (chain recognizer).

- [x] **Auto-par reduction: collect-style combine_fn — amortized-doubling rewrite (Phase 3.1).** Landed 2026-05-21. Follow-on to Phase 3 (line 146). Surfaced by the post-Phase-3 microbench: K=1B `is_candidate` filter into `Vec[i64]` ran in 1.34s sequentially vs 1.43s parallel (`#[par_unordered]`) — parallel was *slower* despite using 2× the CPU. Diagnosis: the Phase-3 combine_fn did fresh `malloc(dst.len + src.len)` + 2× memcpy + 2× free per combine. With N workers each producing ~9M-element partials, the N sequential combines do O(N²) memcpy traffic (~12 GB at K=1B). The combine work alone dominated the parallel filter work. **Implementation.** combine_fn rewritten in `src/codegen/reduce.rs::emit_reduce_collect_combine_fn` from a single "malloc-and-merge" path to a four-path dispatch: (1) `new_len == 0` → early return (both empty). (2) `dst.cap == 0` (first combine into an empty out_slot) → adopt src's `{data, cap}` wholesale; no alloc, no memcpy — first combine becomes O(1). (3) `dst.cap >= new_len` (existing buffer fits) → memcpy src into dst's tail, free src.data, update dst.len. dst's data + cap untouched. (4) Otherwise → `new_cap = max(new_len, 2 × dst.cap)` (Vec.push-style amortized-doubling growth), malloc one new buffer, memcpy both sides, free both old buffers. Across N combines total memcpy traffic drops to O(total_elements) — same as the runtime cost of just constructing the final Vec sequentially. **Microbench validation.** Same K=1B is_candidate workload: SEQ 1.48s wall (1.03s user, 81% CPU) → PAR 0.60s wall (1.41s user, 339% CPU) — **2.45× speedup**, 3.4 cores active. K=2B: SEQ 2.50s → PAR 0.99s — **2.52× speedup**, 4.1 cores active. Sink correctness preserved across both K's (165039065 hits / sum 80550662197839 at 1B; 330078125 hits / sum 161101318359375 at 2B). **Tests.** All 5 Phase-3 Collect tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs` continue to pass (sink-correctness + IR pin + regression guard). Full `cargo test --features llvm` zero regressions; fmt + clippy `--all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` clean. Cross-refs: line 146 (Phase 3 codegen this optimizes), line 100 (closed umbrella).

- [x] **Auto-par reduction: collect-style demonstration kata.** Landed 2026-05-21 as `kara-katas/leetcode/201-300/204-count-primes/` (commit `ee2eb55`). Kata picked: **LeetCode #204 Count Primes** with the natural extension "list all primes under N" — workload walks `[0, n)` calling `is_prime(k)` (trial division up to √k), pushes matching k into `Vec[i64]`. Why this shape beats #71/#1071: it returns integers (not Strings), so it fits the Phase-3 element-type gate without needing the Vec[String] broader-element-types follow-up; and `is_prime(k)` is compute-heavy (up to ~3162 mod ops at N=10^7) so parallelism wins decisively over memory-streaming workloads. **Sink:** `(count, sum) = (664579, 3203324994356)` at N=10^7, matches OEIS A006988 / A000720 cross-checks. **Benchmark numbers** (Apple M5 Pro 6P+12E cores; hyperfine 10 runs after 3 warmups). Seven rows after Go was added (kara-katas commit `e52b622`): rust+rayon 36.7 ms ± 1.1 ms (~15 cores), kara par 48.2 ms ± 3.3 ms (~11 cores), go par 50.4 ms ± 1.2 ms (~10 cores), go seq 456.0 ms ± 2.5 ms, kara seq 509.8 ms ± 4.4 ms, c seq 511.3 ms ± 4.6 ms, rust seq 512.5 ms ± 8.3 ms. **Two fair-comparison lanes**, both kept because each surfaces real karac signals: (1) **Per-core compiler quality** (kata's primary purpose, like kata-7/8/65): kara seq 510 ms vs rust seq 513 ms vs c seq 511 ms — all within **0.5%**, three-way parity. Go is the outlier at 456 ms (11% faster — likely better inlining + slice-growth heuristic; speculative, would need `llvm-mca` / `perf stat -e instructions` to localize). The kata's compiler-quality answer: Kāra hasn't traded codegen quality for higher-level features at the per-core level; there's a real per-core optimization opportunity surfaced by the Go gap that's worth investigating but doesn't undermine the C/Rust parity finding. (2) **Built-in/library parallelism**: kara `#[par_unordered]` 48.2 ms vs rust `rayon` 36.7 ms vs go goroutines 50.4 ms — Kāra is 1.31× behind rayon and slightly ahead of Go's goroutine runtime. Brand-new auto-par lands within 31% of a mature work-stealing library + ~5% ahead of Go's mature goroutine runtime on first iteration. All three spend similar user-CPU; rayon distributes load across ~15 cores via per-worker-deque work-stealing, karac and Go across ~10-11 (karac uses a single global queue + Condvar — the v1 MVP per `runtime/src/lib.rs § Pool`). The codegen path (Phase 3 + 3.1) is competitive with rayon at the worker-fn / merge level; the runtime scheduler is the remaining gap to rayon — tracked at line 163 ("real work-stealing scheduler") as the codegen-adjacent optimization target this comparison empirically validates. **Cross-lane wall-time ratios (e.g. "auto-par Kāra vs single-threaded Rust") are explicitly NOT a headline** — they conflate parallel dispatch with single-core codegen and would silently let a parallel win hide any per-core regression. Same shape as the user-CPU-vs-wall-clock confusion that surfaced earlier in drafting the bench; the kata README's `caveats` section calls this out so future readers don't get pulled into it. **Codegen gap landed during impl:** `Vec.len()` / `Vec.is_empty()` on a non-Identifier receiver (e.g. `list_primes_under(n).len()`) wasn't handled by `compile_method_call` and panicked; fixed in karac commit `e313154` with a focused direct-field-extract path for the two element-type-agnostic read-only methods. Two new e2e tests in `tests/codegen.rs` pin the fix using the LC #204 anchor values. Cross-refs: line 146 (Phase 3 codegen the kata exercises), line 148 (Phase 3.1 combine that made the speedup real), `kara-katas/leetcode/201-300/204-count-primes/README.md § Benchmarks` (the kata's bench numbers).

- [ ] **Auto-par reduction: collect-style — broader element-type support.** Phase 3 ships `Vec[i8]` … `Vec[i64]` (the scalar reduce path's int-width gate, reused). Non-int element types fall back to sequential codegen. Three follow-up extensions, each its own future slice: (a) **`Vec[String]`** — the per-elem-type combine_fn would need to deep-copy String elements during extend (each String's `{ptr, len, cap}` data buffer must be re-allocated, not moved, since multiple workers may have produced overlapping byte sequences). (b) **`Vec[Vec[T]]` / nested Vec** — same deep-copy concern as String, recursively. (c) **`Vec[struct S]`** — bit-copy is sound when `S` is all primitives, deep-copy needed when any field is Vec/String. Gate via the same `llvm_ty_is_vec_struct` / inner-field check the cleanup machinery in `state.rs::CleanupAction::FreeVecBuffer` uses. Defer until a kata workload demands it.

- [x] **Auto-par `karac_par_run` (find_parallel_groups): per-stmt cost gate.** Landed 2026-05-23 at karac-rust `1a26792` via path (b) — codegen-time gate with two thresholds (sum < `PAR_RUN_DISPATCH_THRESHOLD_UNITS` = 500 AND min_per_branch >= `PAR_RUN_VISIBILITY_THRESHOLD_UNITS` = 50, both must clear). The visibility threshold is the load-bearing discriminator that distinguishes "estimator confident the work is small" (kata-2: each branch ≈ 211 units, estimator sees the loop) from "estimator blind to real work" (parallax: each branch ≈ 10 units, only sees method-call shell). Original-entry context follows for archeology; the validation criterion (kata-2 binary 311.9 → 49.0 KiB, wall 507.6 → 465.9 ms, peak RSS 1.6 → 1.1 MiB) was met. Known limitation: when slice 155's `CostEstimator` is extended to trace into impl method bodies (separate slice — needs typechecker-resolved receiver type), the visibility threshold can be lowered or removed entirely.

  **Original entry (preserved for archeology):** Surfaced 2026-05-23 by the kata-2 (add-two-numbers) bench re-run during the kata 1-4 BENCH.md-protocol sweep. The `is_trivial` gate in `src/concurrency.rs::find_parallel_groups` (line 1191) classifies a parallel group as trivial when `all_pure || non_constant_count <= 1`. Kata 2's `main` prologue contains a 2-stmt par group `let b = make_nines(n); let l1 = from_array(a.as_slice());` — both are non-pure (allocates + panics) and both are non-constant, so `is_trivial = false` and `karac_par_run` dispatches. Per-branch work at the kata's n=100 is ~10μs (one Vec push-loop + one linked-list build); `karac_par_run`'s ~7 ms dispatch overhead doesn't amortize. Measured impact: default-build kara binary is **319,352 B (311.9 KiB)** vs `KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0` build at **50,184 B (49.0 KiB)** — +263 KiB par-machinery linked for zero wall-time benefit (517.2 ± 11.0 ms vs 509.9 ± 6.9 ms — within σ on the 500 ms range), plus 0.4 MiB peak RSS for the par-pool init that's never used. This is the same wasteful-activation shape kata 91 had pre-`1f3f498`, but the `stmt_is_constant_init` ByteLit fix doesn't apply — both kata-2 prologue calls are real work, not misclassified constants.

  **Why a blanket size-2 trivial-gate doesn't ship.** Existing tests at `tests/concurrency.rs:660-665` (`test_pure_independent_effectful_calls_are_real_parallelism`) and `tests/concurrency.rs:691-694` (`test_cost_model_let_with_effectful_rhs_counts_as_work`) explicitly assert 2-effectful-stmt groups must be non-trivial. The design intent is that "two independent calls on different resources" can in principle parallelize; the kata 2 finding is that the *cost gate* for the par_run path isn't catching small-per-branch shapes — the analyzer is doing its job correctly, the gate downstream isn't.

  **Proposed fix paths (each its own slice).** (a) **Runtime cost gate for `karac_par_run`** mirroring slice 3b.8's design for `karac_par_reduce` (see line 147): codegen carries a `per_branch_cost_units` estimate in the `KaracBranch` struct, the runtime short-circuits to in-caller-thread sequential execution when `sum_branch_costs < pool_workers × DISPATCH_OVERHEAD_PER_CALL_UNITS_RT` (≈ 10_000 units = ~10 µs, mirrors the par_reduce calibration). Preserves the codegen-time analyzer behavior (par group is still identified, reflected in `--concurrency-report`); just elides the dispatch when the math doesn't pay. Doesn't reduce binary size (par_run symbol stays linked) — eliminates only the wall-time overhead. (b) **Per-stmt compile-time cost estimator** in `find_parallel_groups` analogous to slice 3b.5's `estimate_body_cost_units` walk: count CALL_COST_UNITS for function/method calls, descend into known free-fn callees up to INLINE_DEPTH_CAP per slice's "function-call body-cost estimation" entry above (line 155), and route to trivial when `non_constant_count >= 2 && sum_stmt_costs < threshold`. Tighter than (a) (eliminates par_run emission entirely + binary stays lean), but the existing tests' "must not be marked trivial" assertions need to flex to "marked trivial when costs are small" — a behavioral semantics shift, not just a heuristic tweak. Most aligned with the slice-155 cost-estimator infrastructure already in tree.

  **Validation criterion.** Kata-2's bench binary drops from 311.9 KiB to ≤50 KiB (matching the `KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0` build); kara wall stays at ≤510 ms or improves; peak RSS drops 1.6 → 1.2 MiB (matching C/Rust parity — the par-pool init ballast disappears). Re-run kata 91, kata 7 (reverse-integer, the canonical par_reduce validation), kata 65 (valid-number, the conditional-acc validation), kata 153 (find-min, the memory-bound rejection validation), and kata 204 (count-primes, the collect-style validation) to confirm no regressions on existing par/auto-par paths.

  **Cross-refs.** Line 117 (umbrella — par codegen for non-`par` regions); `src/concurrency.rs:1184-1191` (the `is_trivial` gate); `runtime/src/lib.rs:478` (`karac_par_run` FFI surface — would gain `per_branch_cost_units` in path (a)); line 144 (slice 3b.5 — `estimate_body_cost_units` walk this slice would extend to par_run); line 147 (slice 3b.8 — the runtime cost-gate pattern path (a) mirrors); line 155 (inlining-aware `CostEstimator` infrastructure path (b) builds on); `kara-katas/leetcode/1-100/2-add-two-numbers/README.md § Runtime — seq lane`'s auto-par observation paragraph (kata-side evidence); `kara-katas/BENCH.md § Implicit auto-par` (the discipline that surfaced the empirical detection).

- [x] **Compiler-assisted migration diagnostic: `shared struct` accessed from multiple concurrent tasks. ✓ Landed 2026-05-26 (prose-diagnostic v1).** Detection + prose error shipped this slice; the JSON `fix_diff` envelope is deferred as a separate follow-up (filed below) because no sibling diagnostic exists yet to mirror the envelope from — design.md spells out an `E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT` analog that hasn't been built either, and locking a JSON shape from one side would force rework when the sibling lands. **Detection** lives in a new `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs` module hooked off `OwnershipChecker::check()` after the RC-budget pass. For each function body it builds a `binding_name → (shared_type_name, def_span)` table from parameters (head type via `type_expr_head_name`, gated on `is_shared_type`) and let-introduced bindings (joining each leaf pattern's span against `typecheck_result.pattern_binding_types`, then gated on `is_shared_type` for both struct and enum cases). It then walks for `ExprKind::Par(block)` and per-branch (each top-level `block.stmts[i]`) collects the set of shared-binding names referenced anywhere in the branch subtree — Identifier shapes plus the obvious nesting (FieldAccess receiver, MethodCall receiver, Call arg, Binary/Unary operands, If/While/For/Match/Loop/Lock/Block/LabeledBlock/Tuple/Cast/Range/Return/Break sub-trees). Any shared binding appearing in ≥2 distinct branches → one `OwnershipError` at the second-branch use site with the first-branch use threaded as `consume_span` (we keep the existing dual-span shape rather than growing the error struct). The new `OwnershipErrorKind::ConcurrentSharedStruct { type_name, binding }` flows through `src/cli.rs`'s diagnostic-code map as `"E_CONCURRENT_SHARED_STRUCT"`. **Suggestion text** spells out the four-step migration from design.md verbatim (rename `shared struct` → `par struct`, wrap each bare `mut` field in `Mutex[T]`, insert `lock field { ... }` blocks at every write site within `par` regions, surface Rc→Arc clone semantics at call sites) and points at the future `karac migrate shared-to-par <Type>` tool for the preemptive workspace rewrite. **Soundness — "sole-ownership move into exactly one branch is not an error"**: design.md is explicit that a single-branch use is fine. The detector preserves this by requiring `branches_using_binding.len() > 1` before firing; a `par { use_a(c); other_work(7); }` passes through cleanly (test 2 below pins this). **Tests** (5 new in `tests/ownership.rs`, ownership 245 → 250): `test_concurrent_shared_struct_fires_on_two_branch_use` — canonical case (two `par`-branch calls take `c: Counter` where `Counter` is `shared struct`); validates the `type_name`/`binding` payload + message naming + suggestion text contents (`par struct Counter`, `Mutex`); `test_concurrent_shared_struct_silent_when_only_one_branch_uses` — sole-branch usage stays clean (the rule's accept side); `test_concurrent_shared_struct_does_not_fire_on_plain_struct` — kind-selector lock: plain `struct Counter` may trip `UseAfterMove` or other diagnostics but never `ConcurrentSharedStruct`; `test_concurrent_shared_struct_fires_via_field_access` — pins that field-access shapes (`root.val` in branch A AND B) also fire (we don't accept only "binding passed to fn" forms); `test_concurrent_shared_enum_fires` — sibling enum case (shared enum follows the same rule, via `EnumInfo.is_shared`). All gates green (fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` — every prior test-binary's pass count unchanged, 250 / 250 ownership tests pass). **What this slice does NOT cover (carry forward as their own `[ ]` entries below):** the JSON `fix_diff` envelope; closure-captured shared bindings (a closure inside a branch that captures the shared binding, then is dispatched to a sibling branch — the binding flows in indirectly and the v1 detector doesn't see it); `spawn(...)` boundaries beyond `par {}`; the sibling `E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT` for plain structs. Cross-refs: design.md § Compiler-assisted migration from `shared struct` to `par struct` (the spec we matched); design.md § Rc vs Arc — Two-Phase Algorithm "Rule for `shared struct`" (the detection condition); `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs` (the new pass); `src/ownership.rs::OwnershipErrorKind::ConcurrentSharedStruct` (the diagnostic kind); `src/cli.rs::E_CONCURRENT_SHARED_STRUCT` map entry.

- [x] **`E_CONCURRENT_SHARED_STRUCT` + `E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT`: JSON `fix_diff` envelope. ✓ Landed 2026-05-26 (mut-field Mutex-wrap edits; keyword rename + lock-block insertion deferred).** Combined slice with the plain-struct sibling (entry below) — both diagnostics co-designed one envelope so the JSON shape locks together instead of one side forcing rework on the other. **Envelope shape**: sidecar `OwnershipCheckResult.error_fix_diffs: HashMap<SpanKey, Vec<TextEdit>>` keyed by the diagnostic's primary span (the second-branch use). Rendered to JSON in `src/cli.rs` as `"fix_diff":[{"offset":…,"length":…,"text":…},…]` spliced into the diagnostic envelope's `extra_json` slot, peer to the existing `"replacement":{…}` single-edit form (mutually exclusive in v1 — these new kinds emit `replacement: None`, so either-or is sufficient; when a future kind needs both, the cli site combines them as `"replacement":{…},"fix_diff":[…]`). **Picked the sidecar over a new field on `OwnershipError`** because the 17 existing construction sites across `ownership/{rc_promote,expr_check,borrow,block_stmt,closure_escape}.rs` would all need touching otherwise, for a feature only two kinds use — the per-emit fix_diffs are looked up via `SpanKey::from_span(&err.span)` join. **Edit shape**: for every `mut field: T` in the matching `StructDef`, emit two pure-insertion `TextEdit`s — `{offset: ty.span.offset, length: 0, text: "Mutex["}` and `{offset: ty.span.offset + ty.span.length, length: 0, text: "]"}` — derivable from `StructField.ty.span` without needing any source-text access. Immutable fields generate nothing. **What's deferred (sibling follow-up filed below)**: the **keyword rename** (`shared struct`/`struct` → `par struct`) and the **`mut ` keyword stripping** need precise keyword spans on `StructDef`, which the parser doesn't capture today; **lock-block insertion at write sites** needs a per-fn-body walk over mutating field-accesses inside par regions. Both stay in the diagnostic's suggestion prose as the user's manual review step. The fourth design point — Rc→Arc clone-semantics callouts at call sites — is a note rather than an edit (no source-level rewrite; the clone semantics change automatically once the type becomes `par struct`), already covered by the suggestion text. **Tests** (4 new: 3 in `tests/ownership.rs` for the data shape, 2 in `tests/cli.rs` for the JSON wire format): `test_concurrent_struct_fix_diff_wraps_each_mut_field` — shared struct with 2 mut fields produces 4 edits (2 prefix + 2 suffix), all pure insertions; `test_concurrent_plain_struct_fix_diff_wraps_each_mut_field` — sibling case for the plain kind; `test_concurrent_struct_fix_diff_empty_when_no_mut_fields` — shared struct with no mut fields produces empty/absent fix_diff; `test_json_concurrent_shared_struct_carries_fix_diff_array` — JSON output contains the `"fix_diff":[…]` array with `"text":"Mutex["` and `"text":"]"`; `test_json_concurrent_plain_struct_carries_fix_diff_array` — JSON output for the plain kind. All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm`). Cross-refs: `src/ownership.rs::OwnershipCheckResult.error_fix_diffs` (the sidecar map); `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::build_fix_diff_edits` (the per-`mut`-field edit builder); `src/cli.rs` (the `"fix_diff":[…]` JSON renderer).

- [x] **`E_CONCURRENT_*_STRUCT`: keyword rename + `mut ` strip edits. ✓ Landed 2026-05-26 (L201a).** Closes the keyword-rewrite half of the original L201 entry. **Parser surface**: extended `StructDef` with `struct_keyword_span: Span` (always present, covers `struct`) and `kind_keyword_span: Option<Span>` (Some(span over `shared`) iff is_shared, None for plain `struct`); extended `StructField` with `mut_keyword_span: Option<Span>` (Some iff is_mut) and `name_span: Span` (always present, covers the identifier). The `Token::Shared` arm in `src/parser/items.rs::parse_item_body` captures `current_span()` before advancing past the keyword and threads it into `parse_struct_def`'s new `kind_keyword_span` parameter; `parse_struct_def` captures `current_span()` before `expect(&Token::Struct)?` for `struct_keyword_span`. `parse_struct_fields` (and the second copy in `src/parser/generics.rs::parse_struct_body`, which handles invariant-aware bodies) replace `eat(&Token::Mut)` with a check-current-span-then-advance pattern to capture `mut_keyword_span`, and grab `current_span()` before `expect_identifier()?` for `name_span`. The synthetic prelude `stub_struct` carries the item's full span as a benign placeholder for both new fields — never consulted in practice because stubs don't appear in user `par` blocks. **`build_fix_diff_edits` extension**: now takes `BindingKind` (so it can pick the right keyword edit) and emits three edit families per affected `StructDef`: (1) keyword rewrite — `Shared` replaces the `shared` token with `par` (`{offset: kind.offset, length: kind.length, replacement: "par"}`); `Plain` inserts `par ` before the `struct` token (`{offset: struct.offset, length: 0, replacement: "par "}`); (2) `mut ` strip per mut field — deletion from `mut_keyword_span.offset` to `name_span.offset`, so trailing whitespace (tabs, multiple spaces, embedded comments) is consumed without re-scanning source text; (3) `Mutex[T]` wrap per mut field — pre-existing pure-insertion edits from the L197 slice, unchanged. Edits emit in source order; consumer applies back-to-front per standard `karac fix` discipline. **Suggestion text** updated for both kinds: previously "fix_diff covers the per-field Mutex wraps; the keyword rewrite and `mut ` stripping are left as the human review step", now "fix_diff covers steps 1 and 2 (keyword rewrite, `mut ` stripping, and per-field Mutex wrap); steps 3 and 4 [lock-block insertion + clone-semantics callout] remain the human review step". **Tests** (3 new in `tests/ownership.rs`, ownership 260 → 263; 3 existing edit-count tests updated to match the new totals): `test_l201a_shared_keyword_rename_targets_shared_token` — byte-precise pin at `src.find("shared")` with length 6; `test_l201a_plain_keyword_insert_targets_struct_token` — pure-insertion at `src.find("struct")`; `test_l201a_mut_strip_covers_mut_and_trailing_whitespace` — strip-range from `src.find("mut count")` to `src.find("count: i64")`, validates the whitespace-consuming property. The pre-existing `test_concurrent_struct_fix_diff_wraps_each_mut_field` now expects 7 edits (1 rename + 2 strips + 2 mut × 2 wraps); `test_concurrent_plain_struct_fix_diff_wraps_each_mut_field` expects 4 (1 insert + 1 strip + 1 mut × 2 wraps); `test_concurrent_struct_fix_diff_keyword_rename_only_when_no_mut_fields` (renamed from `_empty_when_no_mut_fields`) now expects exactly 1 (the keyword rename, even with no mut fields). All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm` across 40+ test binaries; zero failures, zero regressions). Cross-refs: `src/ast/items.rs::StructDef` / `StructField` (the new span fields); `src/parser/items.rs::parse_struct_def` + `parse_struct_fields` (parser capture sites); `src/parser/generics.rs::parse_struct_body` (the invariant-aware copy); `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::build_fix_diff_edits` (the extended edit emitter); `src/prelude.rs::stub_struct` (the synthetic-stub placeholder).

- [x] **`E_CONCURRENT_*_STRUCT`: lock-block insertion at par-internal write sites. ✓ Landed 2026-05-26 (L201b).** Closes the second half of the original L201 entry. Per-diagnostic, walks the `par_body` (the par block at which the diagnostic fired) and emits two pure-insertion edits per matching write site: `lock <field> {\n    ` at the write's start and `\n}` at the write's end, derivable from AST spans alone (Kara's `lock` syntax takes a bare identifier, not an expression, so no source-text reconstruction is needed for the receiver). **Detection scope** (v1): receiver is `Identifier(binding_name).<field>` — simple binding-rooted field access of the diagnosed binding only (chained projections `c.nested.field`, index access `arr[0].field`, and receivers on temporaries fall outside v1); write shape is `StmtKind::Assign` or `StmtKind::CompoundAssign` (mutating method calls like `c.field.push(x)` require per-method mutability classification and are a separate follow-up); field is a `mut` field of the matching `StructDef`; containment is "any nesting depth inside the par block" — the walker descends into nested `if` / `while` / `for` / `match` / `block` / inner `par` / `lock` / `loop` / try/seq/unsafe/labeled-block constructs to catch writes buried in branches. **Edit anchoring**: `target.span.offset` (start) to `value.span.offset + value.span.length` (end). The parser sets `stmt.span` to the target's span only (see `src/parser/stmts.rs` Assign / CompoundAssign arms), so the value's end span — not `stmt.span.offset + stmt.span.length` — is the right end-anchor. The trailing `;` falls outside the wrap and becomes the lock-statement's own terminator (`lock f { ... };` is a valid lock-expression-statement form). **Integration**: `build_lock_block_edits_for_binding(par_body, binding_name, type_name, program_items)` is a new helper invoked at the diagnostic-emit site in `detect_par_block_conflicts`, and its output is appended to the keyword-rewrite + mut-strip + Mutex-wrap edits from L201a. Empty when the struct has no `mut` fields, no matching writes exist, or the struct definition isn't found in `program_items`. **Tests** (4 new in `tests/ownership.rs`, ownership 263 → 267): `test_l201b_lock_block_wraps_assign_in_par_branch` — canonical case (`par { c.count = 7; ... }`) with byte-precise offset pins; `test_l201b_lock_block_skips_immutable_field_writes` — struct with only immutable fields produces no lock-block edits; `test_l201b_lock_block_wraps_nested_assign_inside_par_if` — recursive-walk pin (assign inside an `if` body inside a par branch still gets wrapped); `test_l201b_lock_block_wraps_compound_assign` — `c.count += 1` covered by the same path. All existing concurrent_* tests pass unchanged (their fixtures contain no writes to mut fields, so they emit 0 lock-block edits). All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm` across 40+ test binaries; zero failures, zero regressions). **Out of scope (filed as follow-ups, below)**: (1) mutating method-call writes (`c.field.push(x)` and similar); (2) program-wide write detection in functions called from par contexts (not just textually inside the par body) — would need inter-procedural reachability analysis; (3) receivers beyond simple `Identifier(name)` (chained projection, index access, deref). Cross-refs: `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::build_lock_block_edits_for_binding` + `collect_lock_block_writes_in_*` + `matched_self_field_access` + `emit_lock_wrap_around` (the new helpers); `src/parser/stmts.rs` (where `stmt.span = target.span` is established); design.md § Compiler-assisted migration from `shared struct` to `par struct` (step 3 of the four-step spec).

- [x] **`E_CONCURRENT_*_STRUCT`: mutating method-call lock wraps. ✓ Landed 2026-05-26 (L205).** Closes the third half of the original L201 entry. Extends the L201b walker so statement-position `c.field.push(x)` / `c.field.clear()` / etc. — any mutating method call on a `binding.<mut_field>` receiver — receives the same lock-wrap edit family as the L201b `Assign` / `CompoundAssign` cases. **Mutability classifier** (`MethodMutClassifier` in `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs`): bundles `typecheck_result.method_callee_types` (per-call-site canonical `Type.method` key, populated by the typechecker's `infer_method_call`) with `OwnershipChecker.method_self_modes` (user impl receiver modes, populated by `collect_method_self_modes` at construction). For each `MethodCall` span, looks up the callee key, then consults `method_self_modes` first for user-impl methods (`SelfParam::MutRef` → mutating) and falls back to `stdlib_method_self_borrow_kind` for built-ins (`Vec.push` / `Map.insert` / `String.push_str` / etc. → `BorrowKind::MutRef`). Conservative default: missing-key (typecheck resolution failure or non-`mut ref self` receiver) is "not mutating", no wrap emitted. **Detection scope** (additive over L201b): receiver shape is `Identifier(binding_name).<mut_field>` (the same gate `matched_self_field_access` already checked); write site is a `MethodCall` in `StmtKind::Expr` position (method calls embedded in RHS expressions are NOT wrapped — wrapping mid-expression would require splitting the enclosing statement; the surrounding stmt is handled instead); the classifier confirms `mut ref self`. **Parser surface change**: added `args_close_span: Span` to `ExprKind::MethodCall`. The parser sets `Expr.span` for a `MethodCall` to `lhs.span.clone()` (the receiver's first identifier only), so previous code couldn't anchor the wrap end at the call's closing `)`. The new field captures the `)` token (`tokens[pos-1].span` after `expect(&Token::RightParen)?`), and the wrap emitter uses `args_close_span.offset + args_close_span.length` for `wrap_end`. The trailing `;` falls outside the wrap, becoming the lock-statement's terminator (same shape as L201b assigns). Only 2 construction sites: `src/parser/exprs.rs` (real source) and `src/lowering.rs::rewrite_path_call_to_method_call` (synthetic; placeholder span — never reaches user-source edit emission). All other consumers use `MethodCall { object, args, .. }` rest pattern; 2 destructure sites without rest pattern (`src/formatter/exprs.rs`, `src/typechecker/exprs.rs`) updated to ignore the new field. **Threading**: `&MethodMutClassifier` flows through `scan_block_for_par_conflicts` → `scan_stmt_for_par_conflicts` → `scan_expr_for_par_conflicts` → `detect_par_block_conflicts` → `build_lock_block_edits_for_binding` → `collect_lock_block_writes_in_*`. Four functions cross the clippy `too_many_arguments` threshold; annotated with `#[allow(clippy::too_many_arguments)]` per existing precedent in this codebase (9 other call sites). **Tests** (4 new in `tests/ownership.rs`, ownership 267 → 271): `test_l205_lock_block_wraps_stdlib_vec_push` — canonical `c.items.push(7)` with byte-precise offset pins for receiver-start prefix and `)`-end suffix; `test_l205_lock_block_wraps_user_mut_ref_self_method` — user impl `mut ref self` method on a field whose type is a user struct (`c.tracker.bump()` where `Tracker.bump` is `mut ref self`); `test_l205_lock_block_skips_immutable_method` — `c.items.len()` is `Vec.len` → `BorrowKind::ImmRef`, classifier returns false, no wrap; `test_l205_lock_block_wraps_method_call_nested_in_par_if` — recursive walker pin (`if true { c.items.push(7); }` inside par branch). All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm` across all test binaries; zero failures, zero regressions across the 1249-test parser + 565-test resolver + 823-test codegen suites). Cross-refs: `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::MethodMutClassifier::is_mutating` (the new classifier); `src/ast/exprs.rs::ExprKind::MethodCall.args_close_span` (the new parser-captured field); `src/parser/exprs.rs:135` (the capture site); `src/ownership.rs::collect_method_self_modes` + `::stdlib_method_self_borrow_kind` (the classifier sources). **Out of scope (carried to the remaining `[ ]` L207 entry below)**: chained-projection receivers (`c.nested.field.push(x)`), index-access receivers (`arr[0].push(x)`), receivers on temporaries (`f().push(x)`); also program-wide write detection in functions called from par contexts (not textually inside the par body) — would need inter-procedural reachability analysis.

- [x] **`E_CONCURRENT_*_STRUCT`: write detection beyond simple `Identifier(name).field` receivers. ✓ Landed 2026-05-26 (L207).** Closes the fourth half of the original L201 entry. Generalized `matched_self_field_access` from the v1 single-step gate (`FieldAccess { Identifier(binding), field }`) to a place-expression walker that supports multi-step projection chains. **Accepts**: `c.field` (v1 baseline), `c.field.subfield`, `c.field.subfield.subsubfield…` (any depth of field projections), `c.field[0]` / `c.field[0..3]` (field followed by index or range), `c.field.0` (field followed by tuple index), and all of the above as receivers of mutating method calls (`c.field.subfield.push(x)`, `c.field[0].clear()`). **Lock target**: the **first** field projection on the binding (the outermost-on-binding field). For `c.nested.val = 7`, lock = `nested`; for `c.items[0] = 7`, lock = `items`. The sub-field's mut-ness is the typechecker's concern (immutable-sub-field writes are rejected at typecheck); the lock target's mut-ness is the gate this slice enforces. **Rejects (preserved as out-of-scope follow-ups; not filed as separate entries — they require fundamentally different lock semantics, not walker widening)**: (1) **Index-first chains** (`c[0].field`, `arr[0].field`) — `c[0]` is an *element* of the Vec/Array binding, not the binding itself; `lock <field> { ... }` doesn't model element-level locking. The natural mapping would be either a per-element lock (`lock items[0] { ... }`, which isn't a Kara syntax form) or migrating the element type to `par struct` (which is a separate user-facing decision). (2) **Receivers on temporaries** (`f().field = x`, `c.method().field = x`) — no binding to associate with the diagnostic; temporary writes by definition can't outlive the statement, so the par-conflict diagnosis doesn't fire on them in the first place. **Implementation**: new free-standing `resolve_place_chain` helper mirrors `OwnershipChecker::place_expr_root` (same projection shapes — `FieldAccess` / `Index` / `TupleIndex`) but doesn't depend on `slice_binding_sources` (that resolution is for slice-borrow tracking, not write detection). Returns `Option<PlaceExpr>` with `root` and `projections`. `matched_self_field_access` then checks `place.root == binding_name && place.projections.first()` is a `Field` in `mut_fields`. Reused `PlaceExpr` and `Projection` types from `src/ownership.rs` (already `pub`); no new types added. **Tests** (4 new in `tests/ownership.rs`, ownership 271 → 275): `test_l207_lock_block_wraps_chained_field_projection_assign` — `c.nested.val = 7` locks the outer field `nested` (chained-field write through binding `c`); `test_l207_lock_block_wraps_chained_field_method_call` — `c.nested.bump()` via user-impl `mut ref self` method on a deep field chain; `test_l207_lock_block_wraps_field_followed_by_index` — `c.items[0] = 7` (Field-then-Index projection chain) locks the field `items`; `test_l207_lock_block_skips_index_first_chain` — `c.items[0]` read inside par fires the diagnostic but emits no `lock ` edit (negative case, since the read is the immediate test target and Index-first chains are out of scope). All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm`; zero failures, zero regressions across the entire suite). Cross-refs: `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::matched_self_field_access` (the generalized gate) + `::resolve_place_chain` (the new walker); `src/ownership.rs::PlaceExpr` + `::Projection` (reused types); `src/ownership/borrow.rs::OwnershipChecker::place_expr_root` (the borrow-tracker analog this mirrors). **Note**: this closes the L197 family of par-conflict diagnostics.
