The seven `[x]` entries (L197 detection, L199 fix-diff envelope, L201a keyword rewrite + mut-strip, L201b assign lock wraps, L203 closure captures, L205 method-call wraps, L207 receiver generalization) together produce machine-applicable migration edits covering the canonical shapes — keyword rewrite, per-field Mutex wrapping, per-write lock blocks across all four supported receiver/write shapes.

- [x] **`E_CONCURRENT_*_STRUCT`: closure-captured shared/plain bindings. ✓ Landed 2026-05-26.** Mirrors the round-12.34 step-6 `closure_bindings` mechanism from `src/ownership/par_helpers.rs` into `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs` so closures dispatched into sibling branches with tracked-binding captures count as per-branch uses. **Two code paths**: (1) **Let-bound closures** — a forward pre-walk over each function body builds `closure_bindings: HashMap<String, Vec<String>>` from every `let pat = closure_expr;` form, joining the leaf-binding names against `closure_captures[closure.span]`'s capture-name list. During the per-branch identifier-collection walk, every `Identifier(name)` is expanded through `closure_bindings` (cycle-safe via visited set, transitive over chained closures) and each expanded name that resolves to a tracked binding is recorded at the identifier's span. (2) **Inline closures** — `ExprKind::Closure { .. }` arms look up `OwnershipChecker.closure_captures` at the closure's `SpanKey` directly; each captured tracked-binding name is recorded at the closure expression's span. The closure body is NOT recursively walked — `closure_captures` is the authoritative set of outer names referenced (filtered through the body's own bindings/shadowing), so a textual recurse would risk double-counting locals or shadowed names. **Threading shape**: `closure_captures: &ClosureCaptures` (immutable borrow of the ownership checker's field) plus `closure_bindings: &ClosureBindings` (per-function, built once per Function/ImplBlock item) flow through `scan_block_for_par_conflicts` → `scan_stmt_for_par_conflicts` → `scan_expr_for_par_conflicts` → `detect_par_block_conflicts` → `collect_identifier_uses_*`. The single helper `expand_through_closure_bindings(name, closure_bindings)` returns every transitively reachable capture; `Identifier` and `Closure` arms both invoke it so chained-closure flows (closure A captures closure B which captures `c`) resolve correctly. **Tests** (4 new in `tests/ownership.rs`, ownership 256 → 260): `test_concurrent_shared_struct_fires_via_let_bound_closure` — `let f = || use_a(c); let g = || use_b(c); par { spawn(f); spawn(g); }` exercises the closure_bindings path (`Identifier(f)` and `Identifier(g)` in sibling branches each expand to `[c]`); `test_concurrent_shared_struct_fires_via_inline_closure` — `par { spawn(|| use_a(c)); spawn(|| use_b(c)); }` exercises the inline `closure_captures` lookup path; `test_concurrent_shared_struct_silent_when_only_one_branch_closure_captures` — sole-branch closure use stays silent (validates the accept side via the let-bound path with `f(); other_work(7);`); `test_concurrent_plain_struct_fires_via_inline_closure` — sibling plain-struct case via inline closures (BindingKind discriminator routes plain to `E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT`). **One existing test surfaced a real race**: `step6_closure_created_inside_par_still_promotes_capture` (in `tests/rc_fallback.rs`) had `par { let h = || apply(cfg); h(); }` — two statements at top of par → two branches → branch 0 captures `cfg` via the closure literal and branch 1 expands `Identifier(h)` through `closure_bindings` to record `cfg`, correctly flagging the race. The test was written before this detection existed; updated to collapse the two stmts into one branch via a block expression (`par { { let h = ...; h(); } }`), preserving the test's intent (Arc promotion via the round-12.34 walker) without the unrelated branch-count race. All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm` across 30 test binaries; zero failures, zero regressions). Cross-refs: `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::expand_through_closure_bindings` + `build_closure_bindings` (the new helpers); `src/ownership/par_helpers.rs::scan_block_for_par_uses` (the round-12.34 reference implementation this mirrors); `src/ownership.rs::OwnershipChecker.closure_captures` (the read-only capture map this consumes).

- [x] **`E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT`: plain-struct sibling diagnostic. ✓ Landed 2026-05-26 (combined slice with JSON envelope above).** Companion to `E_CONCURRENT_SHARED_STRUCT`: detects plain (non-shared) `struct` bindings referenced from two or more concurrent branches of a `par {}` block. Implementation extended `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs` to unify both detection paths: new `BindingKind` discriminator (`Shared`/`Plain`) carried in a `TrackedBinding` struct; new `OwnershipChecker::classify_binding_type` returns `Some(Shared)` for `shared struct`/`shared enum`, `Some(Plain)` for non-shared `struct`, `None` for plain enums and unions (no migration target spec'd in design.md). Plain enums fall through deliberately — they don't have `mut` fields to wrap, so the `par struct` migration shape doesn't apply. Single walk catches both diagnostic flavors via one pass over each function body. **Suggestion text** for the plain kind says `rename `struct Foo` to `par struct Foo`` (insert `par ` keyword, vs the shared case's `shared` → `par` replacement). **New `OwnershipErrorKind::ConcurrentPlainStruct { type_name, binding }`** flows through `src/cli.rs`'s diagnostic-code map as `"E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT"`. **Soundness preserved across both kinds**: sole-branch use stays silent; the kind-selector locks so the wrong diagnostic doesn't over-fire (plain struct → only PlainStruct fires; shared struct → only SharedStruct fires; sibling tests pin both directions). **Tests** (6 new in `tests/ownership.rs`, ownership 250 → 256): `test_concurrent_plain_struct_fires_on_two_branch_use` — canonical two-branch case (plain `struct Counter`); validates message, suggestion text (`rename `struct Counter` to `par struct Counter``, `Mutex`), and the kind variant; `test_concurrent_plain_struct_silent_when_only_one_branch_uses` — sole-branch accept side; `test_concurrent_plain_struct_does_not_fire_on_shared_struct` — kind-selector lock mirror of the existing shared-struct sibling test. The original `test_concurrent_shared_struct_does_not_fire_on_plain_struct` from the first slice keeps its meaning: plain struct still does NOT fire SharedStruct (the new PlainStruct kind fires instead). All gates green. Cross-refs: design.md § Compiler-assisted migration from plain `struct` to `par struct` (the spec); `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::BindingKind` + `::classify_binding_type` (the discriminator); `src/ownership.rs::OwnershipErrorKind::ConcurrentPlainStruct` (the new diagnostic kind); `src/cli.rs::E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT` map entry.

- [x] **Definition-site perf note: `shared struct` with mut fields (Tier 2, `--perf-report`).** ✓ Landed 2026-05-08. When a `shared struct` definition contains one or more bare `mut` fields, emit a perf note in the Tier 2 summary report (surfaced via `karac build --perf-report`): *"`shared struct Foo` has mut fields; if a future caller needs concurrent access, the migration to `par struct` is structural — consider defining as `par struct` from the start."* **Off by default** — definition-site notes are predictive (fire before any cost is paid), so they belong in Tier 2 rather than the always-emitted Tier 1 inline stream. Not coupled to `--strict` (which is for correctness lints, not perf hints). Implementation: add a check in the type-checker pass that walks `StructDef` items, conditional on `kind == Shared` and at least one field carrying `mut`; emits a `PerfNote` with code `perf[shared-struct-mut-field]` into the perf-report aggregator. See design.md § Compiler-assisted migration from `shared struct` to `par struct` and § Performance Diagnostics.

- [x] **`karac migrate shared-to-par <Type>` tool: CLI surface + type-definition rewrite. ✓ Landed 2026-05-26 (L215a).** Foundation slice of the preemptive `shared struct` → `par struct` migration tool. Covers the first half of the original L215 entry: CLI surface, type-definition rewrite, dry-run / `--apply` mode, workspace dirty-check guard. Consumer-rewrite (the cross-file walk that rewrites every read/write of bindings of the migrated type into `lock self.field { ... }` blocks) is carried as the L215b follow-up below; the Atomic[T] heuristic is L215c. **CLI surface**: new `Command::Migrate { type_name, apply, force, file }` variant with parser `parse_migrate_command` (under `karac migrate shared-to-par <Type> <file.kara> [--apply] [--force]`). Subcommand-shape: the migration kind (`shared-to-par`) is a positional argument rather than a flag so future kinds (`plain-to-par`, etc.) extend the same dispatcher. Dry-run is the default — printing each edit's offset / original / replacement in source order — and `--apply` writes the rewrite back. `--force` bypasses the workspace guard (`git status --porcelain` shell-out; opportunistic — absence of git or running outside a repo is treated as "clean", not an error, so the guard never spuriously rejects). **Type-definition rewrite** reuses `crate::ownership::build_fix_diff_edits` directly (now `pub(crate)` along with `BindingKind`, re-exported through `src/ownership.rs`). The same edit emitter the `E_CONCURRENT_SHARED_STRUCT` fix-diff path uses — keyword rename (`shared` → `par`), `mut ` strip per mut field, `Mutex[T]` wrap per mut field — invoked preemptively against the parsed source rather than against a fired diagnostic. **What's intentionally NOT in this slice** (matches design.md § Compiler-assisted migration "manual at the review step" clause): consumer-site `lock` blocks aren't auto-emitted — the L215b follow-up needs a workspace-wide binding-type discovery pass that doesn't exist yet, so v1 produces a starting-point diff and the human reviewer hand-completes the consumer migrations. Per-file mode only (single positional `<file.kara>`); project-mode discovery is gated on L215b because it has no behavioral advantage today. **Tests** (7 new in `tests/cli.rs`, integration count 266 → 273): `test_migrate_dry_run_prints_diff_for_shared_struct` (canonical dry-run shape — pins keyword rewrite + Mutex wrap in stdout, asserts disk is unchanged); `test_migrate_apply_rewrites_file` (canonical apply — pins post-rewrite text contains `par struct Counter` + `count: Mutex[i64]` + absence of stale `shared struct` / `mut count`); `test_migrate_rejects_missing_type` (hard error when `<Type>` doesn't exist in the file); `test_migrate_rejects_non_shared_struct` (hard error when the named struct is plain — the tool is `shared-to-par` only); `test_migrate_unknown_kind_rejected` (subcommand-shape gate — unknown migration kind fails fast at parse); `test_migrate_multiple_mut_fields_all_wrapped` (multi-field invariant — every mut field gets wrapped, non-mut fields stay untouched, the load-bearing L201a property); `test_migrate_help_lists_kind_and_flags` (per-subcommand help page renders with `--apply` / `--force` / `shared-to-par`). All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm` across 50 test binaries — zero failures, zero regressions). Cross-refs: `src/cli.rs::cmd_migrate` + `::workspace_has_uncommitted_changes` (the new helpers); `src/cli/args.rs::parse_migrate_command` (the parser); `src/cli/help.rs` `"migrate"` arm (per-subcommand help); `src/ownership.rs` (the `build_fix_diff_edits` + `BindingKind` re-exports); `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::build_fix_diff_edits` (the shared edit emitter, unchanged behavior — only visibility was widened from `fn` to `pub(crate)`).

- [x] **`karac migrate shared-to-par <Type>`: consumer-site write-rewrite, single-file, type-annotated bindings (L215b1). ✓ Landed 2026-05-26.** First slice of the original L215b entry. Walks every top-level function body (and impl-block method body) in the migrating file's parsed AST, discovers bindings of the migrating type — both function parameters (`fn f(c: Counter)` / `fn f(c: ref Counter)` / `fn f(c: mut ref Counter)`) and `let` declarations with explicit type annotations (`let c: Counter = ...`) — and runs the existing par-body write walker on each function body for every matching binding. Edits whose offset falls inside any `par { ... }` body are dropped post-collection — those sites stay with `karac fix`'s `E_CONCURRENT_SHARED_STRUCT` path. **What this slice covers**: assign + compound-assign writes against discovered bindings. The existing `collect_lock_block_writes_in_block` walker is reused unchanged — the new code is purely the binding-discovery layer that feeds it. `MethodMutClassifier` is supplied empty (migrate runs parse-only, no typecheck data) so mutating method-call wraps silently no-op; lifts when L215b's full-pipeline integration lands (see L215b2 below). The type-match helper `type_expr_is_single_segment_named` strips `ref` / `mut ref` modifiers before comparing the inner path, so all three borrow forms route through the same wrap. **Wrap shape**: this slice reuses the existing walker's `lock <field-shorthand> { ... }` emission — design.md line 8522's `lock self.field { ... }` form (with inner `c.field` → `self.field` rewrite) is deferred to L215b2 because it changes the wrap emitter's contract. Per the "always **manual at the review step**" clause of design.md § Compiler-assisted migration, the v1 output is a starting-point diff the reviewer hand-completes — the wrap-shape mismatch is one of the documented hand-review steps. **Tests** (7 new in `tests/cli.rs`, integration count 273 → 280): `test_migrate_wraps_assign_writes_against_typed_let_binding` (canonical `let c: Counter; c.count = 5` case — pins lock-wrap insertion); `test_migrate_wraps_writes_through_ref_parameter` (the common real-world shape — `fn bump(c: ref Counter)` + `fn reset(c: mut ref Counter)`, both wrapped); `test_migrate_skips_writes_inside_par_block` (par-internal sites NOT wrapped — exact-count pin of 6 edits: 4 type-def + 2 consumer for the single outside-par assign); `test_migrate_wraps_compound_assign` (`c.count += 1` covered via the existing CompoundAssign arm); `test_migrate_skips_writes_to_non_mut_fields` (only mut fields get wrapped, mirroring the L201a type-def invariant); `test_migrate_ignores_bindings_of_other_types` (mixed-type let block — only the Counter binding's write gets wrapped); `test_migrate_dry_run_lists_consumer_edits_in_addition_to_typedef` (dry-run output shape — both type-def and consumer edits appear). All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm` across all test binaries — zero failures, zero regressions). **Files**: `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::build_consumer_rewrite_edits_in_program` (the new entry point) + `::visit_each_function` / `::visit_fn_bodies` / `::collect_typed_bindings_in_*` / `::collect_par_body_spans_in_*` / `::type_expr_is_single_segment_named` (helpers); `src/ownership.rs` (re-export of the new function alongside existing `build_fix_diff_edits` / `BindingKind`); `src/cli.rs::cmd_migrate` (wires consumer edits after the type-def pass; dedup + sort-descending pipeline shared with `cmd_fix`); dry-run + apply messages updated to reflect consumer-rewrite coverage. Cross-refs: `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::collect_lock_block_writes_in_block` (the existing L207 walker reused unchanged); design.md § Compiler-assisted migration (the spec). Closes the foundational chunk of the original L215b entry; the three follow-ups below (L215b2 read-site + self.field shape, L215b3 typechecker-resolved bindings, L215b4 project-mode walk) remain open.

- [x] **`karac migrate shared-to-par <Type>`: read-site rewriting + `lock self.field` wrap shape (L215b2). ✓ Landed 2026-05-27.** Second slice of the original L215b entry. Two coupled changes that align the migrate output with design.md § Compiler-assisted migration line 8522 — *"bare reads/writes become `lock self.field { ... }` for `Mutex[T]` fields"*. (1) **Wrap shape**: parameterized the existing `emit_lock_wrap_around` with a new `WrapShape` enum (`Shorthand` / `SelfPrefix`). `karac fix` keeps `Shorthand` (par-body method context — `self` implicit, field-name resolves); `karac migrate shared-to-par` switches to `SelfPrefix` (emits `lock self.<field> { ... }` AND emits per-occurrence binding-root rewrite edits `<binding>` → `self` for every `Identifier(<binding>)` at the object position of a `FieldAccess` inside the wrap body, via the new `collect_binding_root_rewrites_in_expr` helper). Output compiles cleanly when the surrounding context already has `self` in scope (impl methods); in free functions taking the binding by `ref` / `mut ref`, the wrap references `self` which isn't in scope and the reviewer hand-completes the refactor — design.md's "always **manual at the review step**" clause documents this as expected behavior. (2) **Read-site rewriting**: new walker family `collect_lock_block_reads_in_*` finds every `FieldAccess { Identifier(<binding>), <mut_field> }` in rvalue position and emits a single replacement edit replacing the full `<binding>.<field>` span with `lock self.<field> { self.<field> }`. Skip rules prevent double-wrapping: (a) Assign / CompoundAssign whose target's binding root matches `<binding>` — both target and value RHS are subsumed by the write-wrap; (b) statement-position MethodCall whose receiver's binding root matches `<binding>` — receivers like `c.field.push(x)` are left untouched so a future write-wrap (when typecheck-supplied classifier lands per L215b3) doesn't produce nested `lock self.field { ... }.push(x)` shapes. Mutating method-call writes still no-op in v1 (empty classifier from parse-only pipeline). **FieldAccess span quirk**: parser sets `FieldAccess.span = lhs.span.clone()` (`src/parser/exprs.rs:149`), so the outer span only covers the object identifier; the read walker computes the replacement extent as `object.span.length + 1 + field.len()` — works for the canonical no-whitespace-around-dot Kāra formatting, and whitespace edge cases land a slightly-wrong edit that the reviewer hand-completes. **Edit-emission ordering**: binding-root rewrites are emitted BEFORE the wrap-prefix insertion so the stable sort by `Reverse(offset)` preserves them in the correct apply order at the same offset (length>0 replacement applied before length==0 insertion, otherwise the insertion would land before the wrap-prefix text and the replacement would consume the inserted bytes instead of the original binding identifier). **Tests** (4 new in `tests/cli.rs`, integration count 280 → 284 — note 5 existing L215b1 tests also updated for the new wrap shape): `test_migrate_wraps_read_site` (canonical `let x: i64 = c.count;` → `let x: i64 = lock self.count { self.count };`); `test_migrate_read_wrap_skips_assign_targets` (`c.count = c.count + 1` produces exactly one `lock self.count` wrap — no nested wrap for the value-side read; both `c`s get binding-rewritten to `self`); `test_migrate_wraps_read_inside_if_condition` (read inside an if-condition gets wrapped — exercises the non-trivial AST descent); `test_migrate_skips_reads_inside_par_block` (par-internal reads are filtered out just like writes — the par-span post-filter applies uniformly). All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm` across 50 test binaries — zero failures, zero regressions). **Files**: `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs` (new `WrapShape` enum + parameterized `emit_lock_wrap_around` + threaded shape through `collect_lock_block_writes_in_*` chain + new `collect_binding_root_rewrites_in_expr` helper + new `collect_lock_block_reads_in_*` chain); `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::build_consumer_rewrite_edits_in_program` (switched to `WrapShape::SelfPrefix`, added read walker call); `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::build_lock_block_edits_for_binding` (passes `WrapShape::Shorthand` explicitly to preserve `karac fix` behavior). Cross-refs: design.md line 8522 (the wrap-shape spec); design.md § Compiler-assisted migration "always manual at the review step" clause (the rationale for shipping non-compilable output in non-method contexts); `src/parser/exprs.rs:149` (the FieldAccess-span limitation worked around by the read walker's length computation). Closes the second of three follow-up slices for the original L215b entry; L215b3 (typechecker-resolved bindings) and L215b4 (project-mode walk) remain open.

- [x] **`karac migrate shared-to-par <Type>`: typechecker-resolved binding discovery (L215b3). ✓ Landed 2026-05-27.** Third slice of the original L215b entry. Two coupled changes: (1) widen consumer-binding discovery to inferred-type bindings (`let c = make_counter()`) by routing `cmd_migrate` through `Pipeline::resolve()` + `Pipeline::typecheck()` and consulting `TypeCheckResult.pattern_binding_types`; (2) lift the L215b1/b2 mutating-method-call no-op by populating `MethodMutClassifier` with real `method_callee_types` data — `c.field.push(x)` now wraps as `lock self.field { self.field.push(x) }` (with `c` → `self` binding-root rewrite) when the file typechecks. **Mitigation chosen**: option (a) — graceful degradation. `cmd_migrate` always runs resolve + typecheck; the `pipeline.typed.as_ref().map(...)` consumer passes a `ConsumerRewriteTypeCtx` when typecheck data is available and `None` otherwise. On `None`, the consumer-rewrite walker falls back to L215b1/b2's parse-only behavior (annotated bindings + no mutating-method-call wraps). Even when typecheck reports errors, the partial `pattern_binding_types` map carries data for the bindings that did typecheck, so the rewrite covers strictly more cases than parse-only — matches design.md § Compiler-assisted migration "always **manual at the review step**" clause. **Binding-discovery shape**: the typecheck-aware path is additive over the L215b1 parse-only path. Function parameters and `let` bindings get checked against both `type_expr_is_single_segment_named(ty)` (catches `ref` / `mut ref` annotations the typechecker doesn't record in `pattern_binding_types` because the outer `Type::Ref` doesn't match the `Named` / `Shared` insertion arms of `bind_pattern_types`) AND `pattern_binding_types[span] == type_name` (catches inferred bindings). The walker dedups via `bindings.sort(); bindings.dedup()` after collection — annotated bindings naturally trigger both paths, but the dedup discipline prevents duplicate emission. `LetUninit` stays on the parse-only check because its type is recorded in `expr_types[name_span]` not `pattern_binding_types`, and it always carries an explicit annotation. **Classifier lift**: `MethodMutClassifier { method_callee_types, method_self_modes }` is built with real data when typecheck succeeded — `method_callee_types` from `TypeCheckResult`, `method_self_modes` derived locally via a new private `collect_method_self_modes_in_items` helper (mirrors the existing `collect_method_self_modes(&Program)` but takes `&[Item]` so the consumer-rewrite path doesn't need a `&Program` reference). When typecheck didn't run to completion, an empty `method_callee_types` map keeps `is_mutating` returning `false` and the L207 walker silently no-ops on method calls — same behavior as L215b1/b2. **API**: new `pub(crate) struct ConsumerRewriteTypeCtx<'a>` re-exported from `src/ownership.rs` alongside `BindingKind` and `build_fix_diff_edits`. `build_consumer_rewrite_edits_in_program` signature gains a third `Option<ConsumerRewriteTypeCtx<'_>>` parameter; the threaded ctx propagates through `collect_typed_bindings_in_*` via a new `pattern_binding_matches_type` helper (returns `false` for `None` ctx → typecheck-aware path is silent, parse-only path still fires). **Tests** (4 new in `tests/cli.rs`, integration count 284 → 288): `test_migrate_discovers_inferred_let_binding` — canonical `let c = make_counter()` discovery + wrap (without L215b3 this would emit only the 4 type-def edits and silently miss the consumer write); `test_migrate_wraps_mutating_method_call_with_typecheck_data` — `q.items.push(42)` wraps as `lock self.items { self.items.push(42) }`; `test_migrate_typecheck_failure_falls_back_to_annotated_only` — `let _ = undefined_function()` triggers a resolve error, but the annotated `let c: Counter` write still wraps via the parse-only fallback; `test_migrate_discovers_inferred_binding_alongside_annotated` — mixed shape with one annotated + one inferred binding emits exactly two wraps with no double-emission from the dedup discipline. All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm` across all test binaries — zero failures, zero regressions; included a standalone `chore: cargo fmt cleanup` commit for pre-existing reflow drift in `tests/typechecker.rs`). **Files**: `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs` (new `ConsumerRewriteTypeCtx<'_>` + new private `collect_method_self_modes_in_items` + threaded `type_ctx: Option<&ConsumerRewriteTypeCtx<'_>>` through the `collect_typed_bindings_in_*` chain + new `pattern_binding_matches_type` helper); `src/ownership.rs` (re-export of `ConsumerRewriteTypeCtx`); `src/cli.rs::cmd_migrate` (switched from `crate::parse(&source)` to `Pipeline::new(...).resolve().typecheck()`, builds the ctx from `pipeline.typed.as_ref().map(...)`, threads through to the consumer-rewrite call; dry-run + apply footers updated to reflect the lifted scope — now reads "consumer-site lock-block wraps cover assign / compound-assign writes, reads, and mutating method calls against bindings of `<Type>` in this file — including type-inferred bindings when the file typechecks. Cross-file walks remain a hand-review step — see L215b4 follow-up"). Closes the third of three follow-up slices for the original L215b entry; only L215b4 (project-mode cross-file walk) remains open. Cross-refs: `src/typechecker.rs::TypeCheckResult::pattern_binding_types` (the inferred-binding source); `src/typechecker.rs::TypeCheckResult::method_callee_types` (the classifier source); `src/cli.rs::Pipeline` (the parse+resolve+typecheck wrapper now also used by `cmd_migrate`); `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::MethodMutClassifier` (lifted from empty-stub to real-data); `src/typechecker/patterns.rs::bind_pattern_types` (the insertion site that pattern_binding_types comes from — explains the `ref` / `mut ref` annotation gap the parse-only fallback handles).

- [x] **`karac migrate shared-to-par <Type>`: project-mode (cross-file) walk (L215b4). ✓ Landed 2026-05-27.** Fourth and final slice of the original L215b entry. When the user omits `<file.kara>`, `cmd_migrate` discovers the project root via `manifest::discover_project_root` (walks up from CWD looking for `kara.toml`), enumerates every module under `src/` via `walker::walk_project(WalkerOpts::default())`, and runs the L215b1/b2/b3 discovery + rewrite pipeline against each. Single-file mode (explicit `<file.kara>` argument) preserves its prior behavior unchanged — the user can still target one file when needed. **Two-stage walk**: stage 1 parses + resolves + typechecks every walked module, locates the file containing `shared struct <Type>`, and extracts its mut-field set via the new `crate::ownership::collect_struct_mut_field_names` entry point. Exactly one walked file must contain the definition — zero (no candidate) and >1 (ambiguous) are hard errors with explicit diagnostics. Wrong-kind (plain `struct <Type>` instead of `shared struct <Type>`) is also a hard error. Stage 2 iterates the prepared parses again and computes per-file edits — the def-file gets both type-def + consumer edits, every other file gets consumer edits only. **Key API lift**: the existing `build_consumer_rewrite_edits_in_program` collected mut-fields locally via `collect_mut_field_names(type_name, program_items)`, which silently no-ops on consumer-only files (their items don't define the struct). New sibling entry `build_consumer_rewrite_edits_with_mut_fields` takes the def-file's mut-field set as a parameter so consumer-only modules participate. The original entry is preserved (delegates to the new one with locally-collected fields) — single-file mode and existing `karac fix` callers keep their behavior. **Workspace dirty-check** in project mode runs from the project root (passing `&root.to_string_lossy()` to `workspace_has_uncommitted_changes`) instead of a single file's parent — captures uncommitted changes anywhere in the project, not just the migration file's directory. **Output shape**: project mode prints a top-level "would apply N migration edit(s) across F file(s) for `<Type>`:" header, then per-file edit blocks (same shape as single-file mode), then a unified dry-run footer. The single-file dry-run footer is preserved untouched for backward compatibility with existing L215a/b1/b2/b3 tests. Apply mode prints "applied N migration edit(s) to <file>" once per affected file. **Refactor**: `cmd_migrate` is now a 3-line dispatcher that picks between `cmd_migrate_single_file` (the prior body, preserved verbatim modulo the helper extraction) and `cmd_migrate_project` (the new two-stage walk). A new `FileMigrationOutcome` enum + `FileMigrationPlan` struct + `compute_migration_edits_for_file` helper extract the parse-error-handling + outcome-routing logic so single-file mode stays small. Project mode doesn't go through the helper — it inlines the parse + struct-lookup so it can cache the `Pipeline` snapshots between the def-discovery pass and the rewrite pass. **Tests** (6 new in `tests/cli.rs`, integration count 288 → 294): `test_migrate_project_mode_walks_modules` — canonical 2-file setup (counter.kara has the def, main.kara consumes via `fn bump(c: ref Counter) { c.count = 1; }`); pins "across 2 file(s)" header, keyword rename in counter.kara, lock-wrap in main.kara; `test_migrate_project_mode_apply_rewrites_all_files` — `--apply --force` writes both files; pins post-rewrite content of both; `test_migrate_project_mode_errors_when_struct_missing` — empty src/main.kara, no Counter; errors with "no `shared struct Counter`"; `test_migrate_project_mode_no_kara_toml_errors` — runs from a /tmp dir with no manifest; errors with kara.toml mention; `test_migrate_project_mode_errors_when_struct_in_multiple_files` — duplicate defs in src/a.kara + src/b.kara; errors with "multiple"; `test_migrate_single_file_mode_unchanged_with_explicit_path` — regression guard that explicit `<file>` short-circuits project-mode (no project-mode header in output). All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm` across all 50 test binaries — zero failures, zero regressions). **Files**: `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs` (extracted `build_consumer_rewrite_edits_with_mut_fields` from the existing entry + new `collect_struct_mut_field_names` public surface); `src/ownership.rs` (re-export of the two new functions alongside the existing surface); `src/cli.rs::cmd_migrate` / `cmd_migrate_single_file` / `cmd_migrate_project` / `compute_migration_edits_for_file` / `emit_migration_for_file` / `FileMigrationPlan` / `FileMigrationOutcome` (the refactor + project-mode dispatcher); `src/cli/args.rs::parse_migrate_command` (docstring updated to document the now-optional file argument); `src/cli/help.rs` (updated `migrate` subcommand summary + per-subcommand help to describe the project-mode default); `tests/cli.rs` (6 new tests). **Closes L215b family**: L215a (type-def rewrite) + L215b1 (annotated-binding write wraps) + L215b2 (read-site wraps + `lock self.field` shape) + L215b3 (typechecker-resolved inferred bindings) + L215b4 (cross-file walk) — `karac migrate shared-to-par <Type>` is now a complete first-class migration tool. The remaining L215c (Atomic[T] heuristic) was previously gated on L215b4 in the design — that gate clears now; L215c can proceed when prioritized. Cross-refs: `src/walker.rs::walk_project` (the project enumerator); `src/manifest.rs::discover_project_root` (the project-root detector — walks up from CWD looking for `kara.toml`); `src/cli.rs::Pipeline` (per-file parse+resolve+typecheck, reused unchanged); `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::collect_mut_field_names` (the field-set source the new entry exposes); design.md § Compiler-assisted migration (the spec).

- [x] **`karac migrate shared-to-par <Type>`: Atomic[T] heuristic (L215c). ✓ Landed 2026-05-27 (type-def half; consumer-rewrite for Atomic-classified fields tracked as L215c-cons follow-up).** Third sub-piece of the original L215 entry. Adds the type-definition half of the Atomic heuristic via a new opt-in `--atomic` flag (project-mode only). When set, each mut field is classified as `Atomic[T]` iff (a) its declared type is in the lock-free Copy-eligible set (`i32`, `i64`, `u32`, `u64`, `usize`, `isize`, `bool`) AND (b) every observed write across the workspace is a bare `=` assignment — no compound assign (`+=` etc.), no mutating method call. Atomic-classified fields' type-def slot becomes `Atomic[T]`; other mut fields stay `Mutex[T]`. Without `--atomic`, the L215a–b4 default (all-Mutex) applies — the flag is strictly opt-in so v1 behavior is preserved. **Why opt-in rather than default**: design.md spec calls for Atomic-classified consumer sites to emit `.store(v, Ordering)` / `.load(Ordering)` instead of `lock` blocks. This MVP ships the type-def half only — Atomic-classified consumer sites stay as bare `=` / read forms in the migrated output (reviewer hand-converts per "manual at the review step"). Making this the default would produce non-compilable consumer code if the reviewer doesn't hand-convert; gating on `--atomic` keeps the v1 default safe while making the heuristic available for early adopters. The follow-up slice (L215c-cons) lifts the consumer-rewrite half — `--atomic` then graduates to default with `--no-atomic` as the opt-out posture. **Single-file gate**: `--atomic` is documented as project-mode only and silently ignored in single-file mode (the classifier needs workspace visibility — single-file can't tell if a bare `=` is the only observed write across the project). **API**: new `FieldWrapKind` enum (`Mutex` | `Atomic`) + new `build_fix_diff_edits_with_field_kinds` entry that consults a per-field classifier (absent entries default to Mutex). The existing `build_fix_diff_edits` delegates to the new entry with an empty map — L215a–b4 callers + `karac fix` keep their behavior unchanged. New `is_atomic_eligible_type(TypeExpr)` predicate + new public `classify_field_wrap_kinds` workspace-aware classifier + new `ProjectMigrationFile<'a>` carrier struct bundling per-file `program_items` + `type_ctx`. New focused walker chain `collect_atomic_disqualifying_writes_in_*` (block/stmt/expr) detects the disqualifying shapes (CompoundAssign, mutating MethodCall) without piggybacking on the existing wrap-emitter walker. **Project-mode integration**: `cmd_migrate_project` adds a Stage 1b between def-discovery (Stage 1) and per-file rewrite (Stage 2) that calls `classify_field_wrap_kinds` only when `--atomic` is set; otherwise the field-kinds map stays empty and all fields get Mutex. The consumer-rewrite walker receives a `mutex_only_fields` subset (mut_fields minus Atomic-classified) so Atomic-classified sites stay un-wrapped. Dry-run + apply footers carry a note when any field was Atomic-classified, pointing the reviewer at the hand-conversion to `.store()` / `.load()`. **Tests** (5 new in `tests/cli.rs`, integration count 294 → 299): `test_migrate_l215c_atomic_when_only_bare_assigns` — canonical case: bare `=` writes only → `Atomic[i64]`, no consumer lock-wrap; `test_migrate_l215c_mutex_when_compound_assign` — `+=` disqualifies → `Mutex[i64]` with consumer wrap; `test_migrate_l215c_mutex_when_non_eligible_type` — `Vec[i64]` field type ineligible → `Mutex[Vec[i64]]`; `test_migrate_l215c_single_file_always_mutex` — pins that single-file mode never emits Atomic even when writes are bare; `test_migrate_l215c_mixed_fields_atomic_and_mutex` — two i64 fields, one bare-=, one `+=` → one Atomic, one Mutex with consumer wrap. All 33 migrate tests pass (28 prior + 5 new). All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm` across all 50 test binaries, zero failures, zero regressions). **Files**: `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs` (new `FieldWrapKind` enum + `build_fix_diff_edits_with_field_kinds` extracted from `build_fix_diff_edits` + `is_atomic_eligible_type` predicate + `collect_atomic_disqualifying_writes_in_*` walker chain + `classify_field_wrap_kinds` workspace-aware classifier + `ProjectMigrationFile<'a>` carrier struct); `src/ownership.rs` (re-exports of the 5 new public surfaces); `src/cli.rs` (added `atomic: bool` field to `Command::Migrate`; `cmd_migrate` + `cmd_migrate_project` thread the flag; Stage 1b in project-mode dispatches the classifier when `atomic` is set; dry-run / apply footers report the Atomic-classified field count); `src/cli/args.rs::parse_migrate_command` (`--atomic` flag parsing); `src/cli/help.rs` (per-subcommand help documents the flag). **Cross-refs**: design.md § Compiler-assisted migration (the spec, including the consumer-rewrite half that L215c-cons will complete); `runtime/stdlib/atomic.kara` (the Atomic[T] surface — currently a bare `struct Atomic[T] { }` with method dispatch hardcoded in codegen; L215c-cons will need to learn the runtime's actual `Atomic.load/store/compare_exchange` method names + Ordering enum surface); `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::MethodMutClassifier` (the existing classifier reused for the disqualifying-method-call detection); `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::matched_self_field_access` (reused for the disqualifying-write target match).

- [x] **`karac migrate shared-to-par <Type>`: consumer-rewrite for Atomic-classified fields (L215c-cons). ✓ Landed 2026-05-27.** Closes the consumer half of the Atomic migration story. Before this slice, `--atomic` rewrote the type def (`mut count: i64` → `count: Atomic[i64]`) but left consumer sites bare (`c.count = 1`, `c.count`) for the reviewer to hand-convert; now the same flag auto-rewrites those sites to canonical Atomic call forms. **What landed**: (1) `build_consumer_rewrite_edits_with_mut_fields` gains a 5th `atomic_fields: &HashSet<String>` parameter threaded through every walker (`collect_lock_block_writes_in_block/_in_stmt/_in_expr` + `collect_lock_block_reads_in_block/_in_stmt/_in_expr`); at each emission site the walker dispatches by `atomic_fields.contains(field)` — Mutex → existing lock-wrap, Atomic → new `.store(...)` / `.load(...)` rewrite. (2) Two new emitters in `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs`: `emit_atomic_store_around(target_full_end, value_start, value_end)` produces the two-edit rewrite ` = ` → `.store(` + insert `, MemoryOrdering.Release)` after the value; `emit_atomic_load_after(end)` inserts `.load(MemoryOrdering.Acquire)` after the field-access span. Bare assigns are restricted to the single-step `Identifier(<binding>).<atomic_field> = <value>` shape; multi-step chains can't legally apply to an `Atomic[T]` field (Atomic has no user subfields) and fall through with no edit. (3) CompoundAssign and mutating method-call sites defensively skip when the field is in `atomic_fields` — the classifier already disqualifies fields with either shape from Atomic, so a hit here indicates a classifier/walker mismatch and emitting no edit (rather than a wrong-shape rewrite) keeps the source review-visible. (4) `cli::cmd_migrate_project` swaps the prior `mutex_only_fields` exclusion for `atomic_fields` + full `mut_fields`: the walker now sees every classified field and the dispatch happens at the emission site. (5) Footer messages updated to reflect auto-rewriting instead of hand-conversion instruction. **Sub-item resolutions** (mapped from the original 4-step plan): sub-step (1) — both emit-sites shipped (writes ↔ `.store`, reads ↔ `.load`). sub-step (2) — confirmed the runtime call shape: `<binding>.load(MemoryOrdering.Acquire)` / `<binding>.store(<value>, MemoryOrdering.Release)` via the interpreter tests at `tests/interpreter.rs:3294-3318`. **Important correction to the original entry**: it asserted "method dispatch hardcoded in codegen" — that's true for the interpreter (`src/interpreter/eval_call.rs:474+` recognizes `MemoryOrdering` variant patterns), but the codegen side (`src/codegen/method_call.rs`) has NO Atomic dispatch today. The migration tool emits source-level text edits that compile under the interpreter immediately and become compilable under codegen once the codegen-side dispatch lands. The migrated source is canonical Kāra in both cases — the gap is a missing v1 feature (per [roadmap.md:950](../roadmap.md): `Atomic[T]` `load(ord)` / `store(val, ord)` is in v1 scope, tracked as the new follow-up entry below), not a tool bug. sub-step (3) — 5 new tests in `tests/cli.rs` (`test_migrate_l215c_cons_atomic_read_rewrites_to_load`, `test_migrate_l215c_cons_atomic_apply_produces_compilable_shape`, `test_migrate_l215c_cons_atomic_read_in_complex_expression`, `test_migrate_l215c_cons_mixed_atomic_and_mutex_rewrites_apply`, `test_migrate_l215c_cons_atomic_without_flag_keeps_mutex_path`); the two pre-existing L215c tests (`test_migrate_l215c_atomic_when_only_bare_assigns`, `test_migrate_l215c_mixed_fields_atomic_and_mutex`) have updated comments + positive assertions for the new `.store(` rewrite. sub-step (4) — `--atomic` default-flip is **deferred**: making default-on today would produce code that doesn't compile under codegen (Atomic.load/store dispatch missing from `src/codegen/method_call.rs`), regressing the safe-by-default behavior. The flip stays gated on the codegen-side slice below. **Files**: `src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs` (atomic_fields threading + two emitter helpers + Assign branch split + CompoundAssign defensive arm); `src/ownership.rs` (re-export of the updated entry is unchanged — the signature widened but the public surface is identical from the cli side); `src/cli.rs` (cmd_migrate_project: `mutex_only_fields` → `atomic_fields` flip + footer message refresh); `tests/cli.rs` (5 new tests + 2 updated). All gates green (fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm`). **Cross-refs**: `tests/interpreter.rs:3294-3318` (the call shape this slice emits — `MemoryOrdering.Acquire/Release`, validates the rewrite against the live interpreter dispatch); the new codegen-side tracker entry directly below this one (the blocker for the `--atomic` default-flip); design.md § Compiler-assisted migration (the spec this slice completes for the Atomic[T] family of fields).

- [x] **Atomic.load / store / new method dispatch in codegen (int-typed `Atomic[T]`). ✓ Landed 2026-05-27.** Closes the codegen-side gap left by L215c-cons. `Atomic[T]` for power-of-two-byte integer `T` (i8/i16/i32/i64/i128/usize/isize/u8/u16/u32/u64) now compiles end-to-end through karac's LLVM backend, matching the interpreter's behavior. The migration tool's `--atomic` flag now emits code that compiles under both backends for int-typed fields. **What landed**: (1) **Transparent struct layout** — `Atomic[T]` lowers via a new arm in `llvm_type_for_type_expr` (`src/codegen/types_lowering.rs`) that extracts the single generic arg and delegates to its LLVM type. No struct wrapper, no header — the storage IS the inner primitive. This matches the LLVM atomic ABI (atomic load/store operate on integer pointers directly). The baked `struct Atomic[T] { }` in `runtime/stdlib/atomic.kara` isn't fed into codegen's struct-declaration pass (same as Vec/VecDeque baked stubs), so no per-name struct_types registration was needed. (2) **`Atomic.new(v)` arm** in `compile_assoc_call` (`src/codegen/assoc_call.rs`) — forwards `v` directly; the let-binding stores the value into a primitive-typed alloca. Mirrors the `Vec.new` arm pattern. (3) **`is_atomic_receiver` + `compile_atomic_method` + `resolve_atomic_storage` + `parse_memory_ordering`** new helpers in `compile_method_call` (`src/codegen/method_call.rs`) — gated dispatch arm runs before the user impl-block lookup. Both receiver shapes work: (a) Identifier `a.load(ord)` for top-level `let a = Atomic.new(v)` bindings (var_type_names registered via a new `is_atomic_new_call` recognizer in the let-stmt handler), and (b) FieldAccess `c.count.load(ord)` for struct fields whose declared type is `Atomic[T]` (the shape `karac migrate --atomic` emits). The FieldAccess path threads through the existing `try_compile_field_receiver_method` mint-a-synth-binding flow; the missing piece was registering the synth binding's `var_type_names = "Atomic"` — added an Atomic arm at the top of `register_var_from_type_expr` (in `types_lowering.rs`) so the synth binding is recognized on the recursive dispatch. (4) **`MemoryOrdering.X` → `inkwell::AtomicOrdering` mapping**: `Relaxed → Monotonic`, `Acquire → Acquire`, `Release → Release`, `AcqRel → AcquireRelease`, `SeqCst → SequentiallyConsistent` — pattern-matches the qualified-variant literal at the call site (no runtime enum value). Mirrors the interpreter's recognizer at `src/interpreter/eval_call.rs:474+`. Invalid combinations (Release-on-Load, Acquire-on-Store, AcqRel-on-either) are rejected at codegen with a clear diagnostic — LLVM would reject them at the verifier anyway; surfacing earlier with a named ordering keeps the error legible. (5) **Alignment** — `set_alignment` is called with `ceil(bit_width / 8)` (e.g. i64 → 8, i32 → 4); LLVM's atomic load/store requires alignment ≥ the type's size, and the cleared variants of int sizes all naturally meet this. **Atomic[bool] explicitly deferred**: rejected with a diagnostic naming the deferral. LLVM doesn't accept `load atomic i1` directly — bool support would require widening the slot to `i8` plus zext/trunc wrappers around .load/.store. The L215c classifier still admits `bool` fields for Atomic classification, so users who migrate a `bool` field with `--atomic` see this clear codegen error today; the slice is filed below. **Tests** (6 new in `tests/codegen.rs` under "Atomic[T] codegen" section, codegen test count grew by 6): E2E — `test_e2e_atomic_new_and_load_seqcst` (interpreter parity), `test_e2e_atomic_store_then_load_relaxed`, `test_e2e_atomic_release_store_acquire_load` (the migration tool's canonical pair), `test_e2e_atomic_field_load_store_struct_field` (FieldAccess shape — the form the migrate tool emits); IR-shape — `test_ir_atomic_load_emits_load_atomic_seq_cst` and `test_ir_atomic_store_emits_store_atomic_release` (regression pins on the `atomic` marker + ordering keyword in the emitted IR). Full `cargo test --features llvm` clean (one pre-existing par-cancel timing-flake passes on retry). **Files**: `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs` (Atomic arm in `llvm_type_for_type_expr`, Atomic arm in `register_var_from_type_expr`, new `is_atomic_new_call` recognizer); `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` (`Atomic.new(v)` arm); `src/codegen/stmts.rs` (let-stmt Atomic RHS recognizer sets `var_type_names = "Atomic"`); `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (the `atomic_alignment_for` free helper, `is_atomic_receiver` / `compile_atomic_method` / `resolve_atomic_storage` / `parse_memory_ordering` methods, dispatch arm before user impl-block lookup); `tests/codegen.rs` (6 new tests). **`--atomic` default-flip status**: int-typed migrations now compile under codegen, so for int-only `shared struct`s the migrated source is a strict improvement. The default-flip stays gated on Atomic[bool] codegen (filed below) — making `--atomic` default-on with `bool` fields still admitted by the L215c classifier would produce a clear codegen error rather than a runtime miscompile, but is still a regression from today's no-error opt-in posture. Two paths to clear the gate, either is fine: (a) add `Atomic[bool]` codegen (widen to i8 at the slot, zext/trunc at load/store); (b) drop `bool` from the L215c classifier's eligible set. Cross-refs: `runtime/stdlib/atomic.kara` (the type-shape carrier — unchanged); `runtime/stdlib/memory_ordering.kara` (the `MemoryOrdering` enum — unchanged); `tests/interpreter.rs:3294-3318` (the call shape this slice mirrors at codegen); `src/interpreter/eval_call.rs:474+` (the `MemoryOrdering` qualified-variant pattern matcher this slice mirrors); `roadmap.md:950` (v1 scope statement, now satisfied for int types); `deferred.md:279-283` (the split rationale); the L215c-cons entry above (the migration tool's consumer-rewrite that emits the canonical call shape this slice compiles).

- [x] **`Atomic[bool]` codegen. ✓ Landed 2026-05-27.** Closes the last blocker for the `karac migrate --atomic` default-flip. `Atomic[bool]` now compiles end-to-end via i8 slot-widening — the cheaper classifier-narrowing alternative was passed over because Atomic flags are a foundational systems primitive (shutdown sentinels, initialization gates), production-shaped not kata-shaped. **What landed**: (1) **Slot widening at type lowering**: a new `is_bool_type_expr` / `is_atomic_bool_type_expr` pair in `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs`; the existing Atomic arm in `llvm_type_for_type_expr` returns `i8` (not `i1`) when the inner type's last path segment is `bool`. Struct fields of type `Atomic[bool]` therefore lay out at a single byte and satisfy LLVM's "atomic memory access' size must be byte-sized" verifier rule. (2) **`Atomic.new(v)` widening**: the `Atomic.new` arm in `compile_assoc_call` (`src/codegen/assoc_call.rs`) inspects the compiled value — if it's `i1`, it `zext`s to `i8` before returning so downstream let-binding / struct-field stores get a width-matching value. (3) **Per-receiver `inner_is_bool` tracking**: a new `atomic_var_inner_is_bool: HashSet<String>` field on `Codegen` (`src/codegen.rs`) records top-level `let` bindings whose Atomic inner is bool; populated at let-stmt time via two paths — explicit annotation `let a: Atomic[bool] = ...` (using `is_atomic_bool_type_expr`) and inferred `let a = Atomic.new(<bool literal>)` (matching `ExprKind::Bool` in the first arg). The struct-field receiver path consults `struct_field_type_exprs` directly at the FieldAccess site, which always carries the full annotation. (4) **Synth-binding pickup**: the FieldAccess flow mints a synth `__field_elem_N` binding through `try_compile_field_receiver_method` and registers it via `register_var_from_type_expr`. The Atomic arm there now also writes `atomic_var_inner_is_bool` when the field's TypeExpr is `Atomic[bool]`, so the recursive dispatch's Identifier-path lookup hits. The synth's cleanup site in `calls.rs` removes the new entry alongside the others. (5) **`compile_atomic_method` widening boundary** (`src/codegen/method_call.rs`): `resolve_atomic_storage` now returns a 3-tuple `(ptr, elem_ty, inner_is_bool)`; the load arm `trunc i8 → i1` when `inner_is_bool`; the store arm `zext i1 → i8` when `inner_is_bool` and the incoming value is `i1`. The original bool-rejection diagnostic was lifted (updated to say "or `bool` (widened to i8)"). **Tests** (7 new in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new "Atomic[bool] codegen" subsection, codegen test count 696 → 703): E2E — `test_e2e_atomic_bool_new_and_load_seqcst`, `test_e2e_atomic_bool_store_then_load_relaxed`, `test_e2e_atomic_bool_release_store_acquire_load` (migration-tool canonical pair on bool), `test_e2e_atomic_bool_annotated_let` (the explicit-annotation detection path), `test_e2e_atomic_bool_field_load_store_struct_field` (FieldAccess path — the `karac migrate --atomic` output shape); IR-shape — `test_ir_atomic_bool_load_emits_load_atomic_i8` (pins `load atomic i8` + `trunc i8 ... to i1`) and `test_ir_atomic_bool_store_emits_store_atomic_i8_with_zext` (pins `store atomic i8` + `zext i1 ... to i8`; uses a `let flag = true` to defeat constant folding that would otherwise collapse the zext). All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm`, zero regressions across all test binaries). **Files**: `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs` (new free helpers `is_bool_type_expr` + `is_atomic_bool_type_expr`; Atomic arm in `llvm_type_for_type_expr` widens to i8 for bool inner; `register_var_from_type_expr` also writes `atomic_var_inner_is_bool` for the synth-binding case); `src/codegen.rs` (new `atomic_var_inner_is_bool` field + init); `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` (Atomic.new arm zexts i1 → i8); `src/codegen/stmts.rs` (let-stmt registration writes `atomic_var_inner_is_bool` on annotation-or-literal match); `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (`compile_atomic_method` + `resolve_atomic_storage` thread `inner_is_bool` and wrap with zext/trunc at the i1↔i8 boundary; updated rejection diagnostic); `src/codegen/calls.rs` (synth-binding cleanup removes the new entry); `tests/codegen.rs` (7 new tests under "Atomic[bool] codegen"). **Default-flip status**: with bool now compiling under both backends, the L215c classifier's full eligible set (i32/i64/u32/u64/usize/isize/bool) is supported end-to-end. The `karac migrate --atomic` default-flip is now technically unblocked — filed as its own follow-up entry below since it's a UX decision (flag default + the `--no-atomic` opt-out) rather than a codegen change. Cross-refs: `runtime/stdlib/atomic.kara` (the type-shape carrier — unchanged); `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs::is_atomic_bool_type_expr` (the single point of truth for the bool-inner classification, reused at both populating sites); the L215c entry above (the migration tool's classifier that admits bool fields); the int-Atomic codegen entry above (the slice this completes the surface for).

- [x] **`karac migrate --atomic` default-flip (`--no-atomic` becomes the opt-out). ✓ Landed 2026-05-28.** With the int-Atomic and `Atomic[bool]` codegen slices above shipped, `--atomic` is no longer behind a codegen gap — every type the L215c classifier admits (`i32`/`i64`/`u32`/`u64`/`usize`/`isize`/`bool`) compiles end-to-end through karac's LLVM backend. Project-mode now runs the Atomic[T] heuristic by default; `--no-atomic` is the explicit opt-out. **What landed**: (1) **Surface flip** — `src/cli/args.rs::parse_migrate_command` defaults `atomic = true` and adds a `"--no-atomic" => atomic = false` arm. `--atomic` is still accepted as an explicit (now redundant) opt-in so every existing `--atomic` invocation — including the L215c/L215c-cons test corpus — keeps working unchanged. (2) **Help** — `src/cli/help.rs` migrate block rewritten: USAGE shows `[--no-atomic]`, DETAILS documents the default-on heuristic + the per-wrapper consumer rewrite (`Mutex[T]` → `lock self.field { ... }`, `Atomic[T]` → `.store(v, MemoryOrdering.Release)` / `.load(MemoryOrdering.Acquire)`), OPTIONS replaces the `--atomic` entry with a `--no-atomic` entry, and the last EXAMPLE switched to `--no-atomic --apply`. The stale "reviewer hand-converts" line (pre-L215c-cons) was corrected to the auto-rewrite shape. (3) **Doc comments** — `Command::Migrate.atomic` field doc + the Stage 1b comment in `cmd_migrate_project` (`src/cli.rs`) updated from "opt-in via `--atomic`" to "on by default; `--no-atomic` clears it". **Default-on semantics preserved**: still project-mode only (the workspace-wide "every write is bare `=`" classifier needs cross-file visibility); single-file mode's `atomic` is always false and keeps emitting all-Mutex (`cmd_migrate` routes single-file through `cmd_migrate_single_file`, which never threads the flag). **Tests** (`tests/cli.rs`, migrate count 38 → 39): three project-mode tests that asserted the Mutex shape on an eligible-typed bare-`=` field now pass `--no-atomic` to pin that shape — `test_migrate_project_mode_walks_modules`, `test_migrate_project_mode_apply_rewrites_all_files`, and `test_migrate_l215c_cons_atomic_without_flag_keeps_mutex_path` (renamed → `test_migrate_l215c_cons_no_atomic_flag_keeps_mutex_path`, comments flipped from "without --atomic" to "with --no-atomic"). New `test_migrate_default_atomic_when_only_bare_assigns` pins the flip directly: no flag → `Atomic[i64]` type-def + `.store(` consumer rewrite + no `Mutex[`/no `lock self.count {`. `test_migrate_help_lists_kind_and_flags` gained a `--no-atomic` assertion. The L215c/L215c-cons tests (all pass `--atomic` explicitly) and the single-file tests (`test_migrate_l215c_single_file_always_mutex`, `test_migrate_single_file_mode_unchanged_with_explicit_path`) are unchanged and still green — confirming the explicit-opt-in and single-file-always-Mutex paths survive the flip. All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm`; the lone `test_e2e_par_branch_defer_fires_on_cooperative_cancel` failure is the pre-existing par-cancel timing flake, passes on retry — unrelated to this CLI-only change). **Files**: `src/cli/args.rs` (default + `--no-atomic` arm + doc), `src/cli.rs` (field doc + Stage 1b comment), `src/cli/help.rs` (migrate help block), `tests/cli.rs` (3 tests get `--no-atomic`, 1 renamed, 1 new, 1 help assertion). **Cross-refs**: the int-Atomic codegen entry + the `Atomic[bool]` codegen entry above (the two slices that closed the codegen gap and unblocked this flip); the L215c entry (the classifier whose eligible set the flip now applies by default); the L215c-cons entry (the consumer-rewrite that makes default-on produce compilable `.store`/`.load` shapes); `feedback_ship_vs_bookkeep` (the rationale for shipping rather than carrying the deferral).

- [x] **Par codegen: non-trivial captures (L227). ✓ Landed 2026-05-27.** Closes the latent miscompile risk where `compile_par_block`'s by-value-through-env capture path would race the parent's owning reference for `shared struct` / `shared enum` captures. **Three coupled changes**, threading a new ownership-pass classification through to the codegen branch prologue: (1) **`ParCaptureMode` enum + `OwnershipCheckResult::par_capture_modes` field** (src/ownership.rs) — keyed by the par-body `SpanKey`, values list each captured name with `Copy` (default) or `SharedRc` (shared struct/enum). (2) **`classify_par_capture_modes` walker** (new src/ownership/par_capture_classify.rs, the 8th module under `src/ownership/`) — runs as a final pass in `OwnershipChecker::check` after `check_concurrent_shared_struct`, walks every fn body + impl method for `ExprKind::Par(body)`, gathers captures using a free-function mirror of `Codegen::refs_in_block` (shape-for-shape so the two walkers can't disagree), classifies via `TypeCheckResult::struct_info[name].is_shared` / `enum_info[name].is_shared`, and writes per-par-block entries keyed by `body.span` (matches the lookup site in `emit_par_run`'s thread-through). **Side effect**: SharedRc captures are also pushed into `self.arc_values[fn_key]` so `is_arc_binding` returns true for the binding on both sides of the par boundary — without that, the parent's scope-exit dec would dispatch through non-atomic `emit_rc_dec` while the branch's dec dispatches through atomic `emit_arc_dec`, racing on a shared refcount. (3) **Codegen consumption** (src/codegen.rs + src/codegen/par_blocks.rs) — `Codegen.par_capture_modes` field populated in `load_rc_fallback`; `emit_par_run` resolves the per-block modes once at the entry and threads `Option<&[(String, ParCaptureMode)]>` into `emit_par_branch_fn`; the branch's capture-unpack loop, immediately after `build_store(alloca, field_val)`, looks up the mode and (for `SharedRc`) emits `emit_arc_inc(heap_type, field_ptr)` + `track_rc_var(name, alloca, heap_type)` so the branch-exit `emit_scope_cleanup` balances the inc with an atomic dec. **What this enables**: the spec's "sole-ownership move into exactly one branch is not an error" case (per `concurrent_shared.rs` docstring) now lowers correctly — a single-branch capture that flows into a function consuming the reference no longer races the parent's owning reference. The multi-branch shared case stays an `E_CONCURRENT_SHARED_STRUCT` compile error upstream of codegen. **Sub-items (2) and (3) from the original entry**: ref captures are correct as-shipped — the existing by-value-through-env path faithfully forwards an alloca-of-pointer storage (e.g. a `ref T` parameter's slot), so branch reads/writes through the pointer reach the caller's memory without extra plumbing; move-captures of non-shared owned heap types (Vec, String, plain owned struct) remain a documented latent miscompile risk for v1 — the existing concurrent-shared diagnostic family covers the most dangerous shape (multi-branch shared writes), and a dedicated `E_PAR_MOVE_CAPTURE_UNSUPPORTED` slice can land alongside `Vec`/`String` par-block use-case work without re-touching the L227 surface. **Tests**: 3 in `tests/par_codegen.rs` — IR positive (`test_ir_l227_shared_capture_emits_atomic_rc_inc_in_branch` — asserts `atomicrmw add` appears inside the `__par_branch_*` fn IR for a shared-struct capture), IR negative (`test_ir_l227_primitive_capture_no_atomic_rc_inc` — guards against over-eager classification firing on `i64` captures), E2E lifecycle (`test_e2e_l227_shared_capture_single_branch_lifecycle_ok` — par-runs to completion, asserts the branch's field read + the parent's post-par field read both observe the value, pinning the refcount-stays-positive invariant). **Plumbing nit**: `tests/par_codegen.rs::run_program` + `ir_for_with_pipeline` previously passed `None` for ownership; both now thread `karac::ownershipcheck(...)` through `compile_to_object` / `compile_to_ir` so codegen sees the new classification. Sanity-checked across the full 6226-test suite — no regressions. **Cross-refs**: src/ownership.rs:54-66 (ParCaptureMode definition); src/ownership.rs:579-595 (OwnershipCheckResult field); src/ownership/par_capture_classify.rs (the walker); src/codegen.rs:780-790 (Codegen field); src/codegen/par_blocks.rs L227 marker in `emit_par_run` + `emit_par_branch_fn` capture-unpack loop. **Follow-up tracked separately**: dedicated `E_PAR_MOVE_CAPTURE_UNSUPPORTED` diagnostic for owned-heap (non-shared) captures into par blocks — its own future slice when a workload surfaces the shape.

- [x] **Par codegen: return values.** `compile_par_block` currently returns unit regardless of the block's final expression. Slice 2's auto-par lowering (landed `8bc3bab` 2026-05-08) introduced a `group_defines_binding_used_outside` gate that drops any inferred parallel group whose let-bindings are read after the group — the conservative wall around the missing return-slot mechanism. Lifting that gate is the load-bearing codegen unblock for the **full Parallax demo**: today `let profile = fetch_profile(...); let orders = fetch_orders(...); ... build_dashboard(profile, orders, ...)` lowers sequentially because the group-defines-binding-used-outside gate refuses to fan out; after this entry, the same source auto-parallelizes through `karac_par_run` and the join site reads the values back from per-branch slots. Coordinated with the cancellation work above (line 114) — both extend the same runtime ABI; cancellation lands separately and the slot-write happens after the cancel-check at end of branch.

- [x] **Run LLVM mid-end optimization passes on Kāra-generated IR.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-10 (commit `280ce2d`). `apply_optimization_passes` helper wires `module.run_passes("default<O2>", &target_machine, options)` into `compile_to_object_with_options` between IR construction and emit. Env-var routing (`KARAC_OPT_LEVEL=0|1|2|3`) keeps the target-machine `OptimizationLevel` and the mid-end pipeline string in sync via `backend_optimization_level()`. Disasm of `_busy_loop` post-fix shows LLVM's `LoopIdiomRecognize` recognized the body as the triangular-number sum and replaced N iterations with the closed-form `n(n-1)/2`; `fetch_*` callers had their `let _` results DCE'd. 92× throughput jump (1,054 → 97,172 rps) on the Parallax bench at the moment, but the bench was no-work-eaten by the optimization (later fixed in G1 / `5ef2ea6`). Deferred follow-ups remain for PGO, LTO, per-function opt overrides, and SIMD-specific flags. Original entry: Diagnosed at `docs/investigations/parallax_perf.md § Findings, 2026-05-10` (`17f63b4`). karac currently sets `OptimizationLevel::Default` on the *target machine* (backend code generation) but runs **zero LLVM mid-end passes** on the IR before emit — `grep -rn PassManager src/` returns no hits. The IR ships to the backend with locals still in alloca'd stack slots; LLVM's `mem2reg` (the foundational SSA-promotion pass) never fires. Disasm evidence: `_busy_loop` in the Parallax bench binary runs 12 instructions per iter through a stack-spill chain (~12-15 cycles/iter at 4 GHz, measured 9.3 ns/iter), where optimal codegen would emit 4 instructions in registers (~1 cycle/iter, ~0.25-0.5 ns/iter). Probe sweep (`docs/investigations/parallax_perf.md § Findings, 2026-05-10`) ruled out runtime + HTTP-layer + auto-par dispatch — the Parallax trampoline ceiling is 108 K req/s; the Kāra row is bound at ~1 K only because of unoptimized integer-loop codegen. Wire `module.run_passes("default<O2>", &target_machine, options)` (inkwell 0.9 + LLVM 18 new pass manager API) in `compile_to_object_with_options` between `compile_program` and `target_machine.write_to_file`. Validation criterion: Parallax bench Kāra row jumps to 20-40 K req/s. **Settled design forks (2026-05-10):** (i) **`default<O2>`**, not `<O3>` or hand-tuned subset — apples-to-apples with Rust's release-profile default; `-O3`'s aggressive vectorization adds compile time without typically moving our IR shape's needle; hand-rolling a subset (just mem2reg + instcombine) would skip easy wins (loop unroll, tail-call elimination, LICM) for no reason. (ii) **Env-var opt-out**: `KARAC_OPT_LEVEL=0|1|2|3|s|z` for debugging fallback + future tuning surface. (iii) **Backend opt level stays in sync** with the pass-pipeline string via a single switch statement so `OptimizationLevel::Default` (target machine) matches `default<O2>` (mid-end passes). **Deferred follow-ups (not in scope of this entry):** profile-guided optimization (LLVM PGO, Phase 8.5 Track 2 territory); LTO across the runtime + user-code modules (separate slice — runtime ships as separate static archive); per-function opt overrides via `#[cold]`/`#[hot]` attributes (no Kāra surface for this yet); SIMD-specific flags (`Vector[T, N]` codegen lands SIMD-aware passes when its tracker entry executes).

- [x] **`match` over a String scrutinee — codegen panic at `expr_ops.rs:1138` shipped 2026-05-21.** Filed and shipped same day. **Root cause discovered during implementation:** the original entry framed this as "match-codegen assumes int-tag scrutinee" needing a String-aware fork in `compile_match`. The actual cause was narrower and lived one level down — `compile_pattern_condition` (in `src/codegen/control_flow_match.rs`) handled `LiteralPattern::String(s)` by emitting *only* the pointer (`build_global_string_ptr(s).as_pointer_value()`), then calling `compile_binop(Eq, scrutinee, pointer)` where `scrutinee` was a String struct `{ptr, len, cap}` and the literal was a bare `*const i8`. The struct-vs-pointer mismatch caused `compile_binop_typed`'s `is_struct_value() && is_struct_value()` check to fail (only LHS was a struct), the float check to fail (no floats), and execution to fall into the int path at `expr_ops.rs:1138 lhs.into_int_value()` — which panicked on the struct LHS. **Fix (12 lines net):** build a full String struct `{ data, len, cap }` for the literal pattern (mirroring `ExprKind::StringLit` codegen at `src/codegen/exprs.rs:39-61`, including `cap = 0` for static-buffer semantics). Both operands now satisfy `is_struct_value() && is_struct_value()`, route through `compile_string_binop`, and use the existing length-check + `memcmp` equality path — the same machinery the `==` operator already used. No new function needed; no scrutinee fork in `compile_match`; the scrutinee-once contract (slice 3 of the original entry) was already satisfied because `compile_match` evaluates `self.compile_expr(scrutinee)?` once before the arm loop. **Tests** (4 new in `tests/codegen.rs` under `Phase 7 § match-on-String codegen`, codegen 696 → 700): `test_e2e_match_on_string_basic` — three inputs route to three arms correctly; `test_ir_match_on_string_uses_memcmp_not_int_cmp` — IR regression guard that `memcmp` appears (would not, if the fix degraded silently); `test_e2e_match_on_string_function_return_scrutinee` — non-identifier scrutinee (`match label_for(n) { ... }`) routes correctly, pins the kata's natural form `match req.path() { ... }`; `test_e2e_match_on_string_routes_to_correct_arm` — independent per-arm assertions catch any all-arms-share-body regression. All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + full `cargo test --features llvm`, zero regressions across all test binaries). **Files:** `src/codegen/control_flow_match.rs` (the 12-line fix in `compile_pattern_condition` + comment cross-referencing the `ExprKind::StringLit` template), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests + section comment documenting the root cause discovered during impl). **What's NOT covered (carry forward if surfaced):** other value-typed scrutinee shapes (`StringSlice`, `Slice[u8]`, tuple, struct, user-enum-with-payloads) — each remains as its own typechecker-rejected or codegen-rejected case until a broader "value-typed scrutinee" consolidation slice surfaces a workload that needs it. The `String` case was carved out because backend katas need it immediately; the consolidation case has no v1 consumer. Cross-references stay the same as the filed entry: `src/codegen/expr_ops.rs:1138` (the panic site, now unreachable for this shape); `src/codegen/expr_ops.rs::compile_string_binop` (the reused equality path); `kara-katas/backend/todo-api/main.kara` (the per-branch workaround pattern lifts once the kata refactors to `match req.path() { ... }`); `/tmp/kara-probes/match_string.kara` + `string_eq_reuse.kara` (probe fixtures, now regression seeds); `wip-todo-api-kata.md § Decisions log 2026-05-21 (later)` (the empirical write-up that surfaced the gap).


- [ ] **`karac_par_run`: post-v1 follow-ups (work-stealing, panic propagation).** Two deferred items from the long-lived-worker-pool entry below (`3953a14` on 2026-05-09), grouped because they live in `runtime/src/lib.rs`'s `karac_par_run` surface and share the same FFI. Both are currently gated on a missing prerequisite — see each sub-slice. **Sequencing:** the work-stealing scheduler is the larger (post-v1, multi-slice); panic-payload propagation is a ~1-slice effort once justified. The third deferred follow-up — "tunable pool size via env var" — graduated into its own ship-soon entry; see "**Auto-par runtime: `KARAC_PAR_WORKERS` env override**" below. Tracked as sub-slices:
  - [ ] **Real work-stealing scheduler** with per-worker deques per `design.md § Runtime Distribution` (line 8933 — explicitly designated as the eventual runtime). The current pool is a hand-rolled MVP with a single `Mutex<VecDeque<Task>>` queue + a `Condvar` — fine for the 4-branch fan-out shape Slice E demonstrates, but a real work-stealing scheduler matters for nested-par or many-branch workloads where queue contention becomes the bottleneck. Likely uses `crossbeam-deque` or hand-rolled (decision deferred). **Blocked on the contention microbench below:** the `crossbeam-deque`-vs-hand-rolled fork can't be picked on evidence, and "queue contention is the bottleneck" stays unproven, until a nested-par / many-branch workload demonstrates it. (post-v1, multi-slice)
    - [ ] **Precursor — nested-par / many-branch contention microbench.** Build a workload that fans out far enough (deep nested `par {}` or a wide many-branch block) to saturate the single global `Mutex<VecDeque<Task>>` and expose lock contention in a profile. Outcome either justifies the work-stealing rewrite above (and informs the `crossbeam-deque`-vs-hand-rolled fork) or confirms the MVP queue is adequate and the scheduler stays deferred. No such workload exists today — the shipped pool has only ever been exercised against Slice E's 4-branch fan-out.
  - [ ] **Panic-payload propagation back to parent.** Current behavior swallows panic payloads via `catch_unwind` inside the worker (`runtime/src/lib.rs::execute_task`); only the cancel flag is signaled to siblings. Richer propagation would stash the first panic payload in `ParCall` and re-raise it on the parent thread when `karac_par_run` returns. **Status (2026-05-28): moot under the shipped panic semantics — there is no Rust panic payload to propagate in any real workload.** Three independent reasons: (1) release builds set `panic = "abort"` (`Cargo.toml` `[profile.release]`), so a worker panic aborts the process — there is no unwinding and the `catch_unwind` never returns `Err`; the Cargo comment calls process-abort "the desired behavior for `par {}` fail-fast semantics anyway". (2) The worker invokes each branch through an `unsafe extern "C"` `func` pointer, and Rust 1.81+ aborts on a panic crossing that non-unwinding FFI boundary (documented at the `test_frame_deregistered_on_panic` note in `runtime/src/lib.rs`). (3) Kāra has its own panic protocol — codegen-emitted branches never unwind into the Rust runtime. **Unblocking** requires first changing the panic ABI (`extern "C-unwind"` on the branch surface + dropping the runtime's release `panic = "abort"`) *and* a test or user-visible diagnostic that actually needs the payload. (~1-slice once that consumer exists.)

- [x] **Auto-par runtime: `KARAC_PAR_WORKERS` env override.** Landed 2026-05-25. New `resolve_pool_workers()` helper in `runtime/src/lib.rs` reads `KARAC_PAR_WORKERS=N` for a valid positive integer (honored exactly, down to 1 — matches `RAYON_NUM_THREADS` / `OMP_NUM_THREADS` / `GOMAXPROCS` / Java's `ForkJoinPool.commonPool.parallelism` posture) and falls back to `available_parallelism()` floored at 2 on missing or unparseable input. Both `pool()` (worker-spawn loop) and `karac_par_reduce` (per-call `pool_workers` lookup that sizes the per-worker slot allocation) now route through the helper, fixing a latent inconsistency where the two sites previously used different `unwrap_or` fallbacks (4 vs 2) on auto-detect failure. Permissive parse posture: 0, negative, empty, and unparseable values silently bypass to auto-detect — same shape as `KARAC_AUTO_PAR` and `KARAC_OPT_LEVEL`. **Validation on kata-71 (auto-par RSS the entry was surfaced by).** Default: 3.6 MiB. `KARAC_PAR_WORKERS=4`: 1.8 MiB (-50%). `KARAC_PAR_WORKERS=2`: 1.5 MiB. `KARAC_PAR_WORKERS=1`: 1.3 MiB — exactly matches the seq lane's RSS, confirming that with 1 worker the `karac_par_reduce` single-worker fast path engages and the worker pool's per-thread libmalloc tcache disappears. Invalid (`bogus`) and `0` both fall back to the 3.6 MiB auto-detect default, confirming the permissive-parse path. **Tests** (3 new in `runtime/src/lib.rs::tests`, serialized on a new `PAR_WORKERS_ENV_LOCK` mutex peer of `FRAME_TRACKING_ENV_LOCK` so cargo-parallel runs don't race the env var): `test_resolve_pool_workers_honors_explicit_count` covers N=4 (typical container-quota override) and N=1 (single-worker fast path); `test_resolve_pool_workers_invalid_value_falls_back_to_auto` covers 0, `bogus`, empty string; `test_resolve_pool_workers_unset_returns_auto_floored` pins the back-compat default. The existing `test_par_reduce_runtime_gate_sentinel_zero_bypasses_gate` was updated to read through `resolve_pool_workers()` instead of duplicating the auto-detect logic — without that, the test would diverge from the runtime's actual chunk count under `KARAC_PAR_WORKERS=N`. **Cross-refs.** Surfaced 2026-05-25 by `kara-katas/leetcode/1-100/71-simplify-path`'s post-fix bench (auto-par RSS 3.8 MiB vs seq 1.3 MiB — steady-state per-thread libmalloc tcache cost scales linearly with worker count); replaced the deferred follow-up listed as item (2) in the `karac_par_run` post-v1 entry above (that entry is now two items: work-stealing and panic-payload propagation).

- [ ] **Auto-par runtime: per-worker scratch buffers in `karac_par_reduce`.** **Status (2026-05-28): gated — do not build yet.** A survey of all 61 `.kara` files in kara-katas found **zero natural-algorithm reductions with allocating bodies**; every instance of the pattern (13 found) is a benchmark-amplification loop — a `K_ITERS` wrapper whose sole purpose is to run an algorithm enough times for measurable wall-time (e.g. kata 71's `while k < 1_000_000 { sum += simplify(inputs[k % 8]).len() }`). So this optimizes *benchmark* RSS, not production code, and fails the optimize-for-production-not-kata gate. **Design gap:** in all 13 instances the per-iter allocations live *inside a callee* (`simplify`, `int_to_roman`, …), behind a function-call boundary — not in the K-loop body. The codegen step below ("auto-detect captures inside the K-loop body") is intraprocedural and would not reach them; capturing them needs interprocedural analysis or a post-inline LLVM-level pass — a materially different and larger mechanism than this entry describes. Blocked on the precursor sub-slice below. **Design (record):** Add an optional per-worker init / finalize hook to the `karac_par_reduce` ABI so workers can allocate scratch once at chunk start, reuse across all iterations in their chunk, and free at chunk end. Today every iteration of the auto-par'd K-loop re-runs the body's per-iter `Vec` / `String` allocations, which on kata 71's allocation-heavy shape (`Vec[char]` snapshot + two `Vec[i64]` stacks + owned String result) is the dominant cost: post-fix kata 71 auto-par RSS is 3.8 MiB (vs 1.3 MiB seq, a +2.5 MiB delta) and per-core efficiency is ~50% (vs kata 65's 94%) because each worker's libmalloc tcache scales with allocation rate. **Why this is the right runtime mechanism, not a kata-source rewrite.** Naïve "just hoist the buffers via `.clear()` reuse" doesn't compose with auto-par: 13 workers each running a chunk of the K-loop in parallel would race on a single shared scratch — undefined output. Per-worker scratch is the only data shape that preserves the K-loop's natural source form *and* gives each worker its own buffer instance. **Implementation surface.** Three coordinated changes: (1) **Runtime ABI extension** — `KaracReduceDescriptor` gains an `init_scratch_fn: extern "C" fn(*mut u8)` and `free_scratch_fn: extern "C" fn(*mut u8)` pair (both nullable for back-compat — descriptors without scratch run today's path). `karac_par_reduce` allocates a per-worker scratch slot of `scratch_size` bytes alongside the existing accumulator slot buffer, calls `init_scratch_fn` once per worker at chunk start, threads the scratch pointer into `worker_fn` as a new param, and calls `free_scratch_fn` once per worker at chunk end. (2) **Codegen lowering** — auto-detect captures inside the K-loop body that are owned `Vec` / `String` allocations created and dropped within each iteration; emit them into the worker's scratch slot with `init_scratch_fn` doing the initial alloc and the body re-`.clear()`-ing instead of dropping. (3) **Language surface** — the auto-detection above is the v1 path (no user-facing syntax); a future opt-in attribute (`#[par_scratch]` on a let-binding inside an auto-par'd loop?) would surface the intent explicitly. **Validation workload.** kata 71's auto-par RSS should drop from 3.8 MiB to ~1.5 MiB (matching kata 65's worker-pool overhead, since per-iter alloc count drops from ~4 to ~0) and per-core efficiency should rise from ~50% toward kata 65's ~94%.
