Wall-clock should also improve modestly (less allocator work per iter). *Note (2026-05-28): this is a bench metric, not a production one — see Status above; the precursor below must supply a production-shaped validation workload.* **Scope.** Multi-day; touches runtime ABI + codegen + analyzer. Locks at the runtime ABI shape, then codegen + analyzer can proceed in parallel. Cross-refs: surfaced 2026-05-25 by kata 71's post-fix bench (see `kara-katas/leetcode/1-100/71-simplify-path/README.md § Runtime memory`); sibling to the `KARAC_PAR_WORKERS` env override above (that's the "knob you can turn today"; this is the "fix the root cause for everyone" path); line 146 (slice 3b.7 — pool-sharing for `karac_par_reduce` — closest existing ABI extension precedent); line 167 (Collect Phase 3 — established the "compute slot type from the loop body shape" pattern that scratch-buffer auto-detection extends).
  - [ ] **Precursor — a production-shaped map-reduce-over-allocating-dataset workload.** Find or build a workload where a reduction loop's body *directly* allocates per iteration over a real dataset of meaningful size — e.g. `total = sum over rows { parse(row).field_count() }` summing parsed-record field counts across a large file — rather than a `K_ITERS` amplification wrapper, and with the allocation in the loop body rather than hidden inside a callee. Such a workload would (a) justify the build as a real production win rather than a bench artifact, clearing the optimize-for-production-not-kata gate, and (b) force the interprocedural-vs-intraprocedural design decision the gap above surfaces. None exists in the corpus today (survey 2026-05-28: 0 of 61 files; all 13 pattern instances are amplification loops with callee-internal allocations).

- [-] **Slice 6 (Vec[T]) — natural-pull trigger event: kata 16 surfaces `sort_by` indirection hotspot.** Filed 2026-05-29 by kata 16 (3Sum Closest) — the Slice 6 reopen condition documented at lines 608 + 617 of the parent `Monomorphized collections — runtime restructure` entry has fired. The kata's seq-lane bench at [`kara-katas/leetcode/1-100/16-3sum-closest/README.md § Runtime — seq lane`](../../../kara-katas/leetcode/1-100/16-3sum-closest/README.md) measured Kāra at 96.8 ms vs Rust at 62.5 ms (1.55× behind). **Disassembly-grounded diagnosis (committed to the kata README, `657199c`):** the inner two-pointer body is instruction-for-instruction-equivalent to Rust's (21-instruction ARM64 inner loops, branchless `cneg` for abs on both sides). The gap is entirely in **sort dispatch**: kata's `s.sort_by(|a, b| a.cmp(b))` on `Vec[i64]` routes through `runtime/src/lib.rs:karac_vec_sort_by`, which calls the user's comparator thunk via `extern "C" fn` pointer per comparison. Rust's `sort_unstable()` monomorphizes the comparator inline. **Confirmation experiment (also in the README):** a hand-rolled inline insertion-sort variant ran at 70.6 ms — 26 ms faster, closing **76% of the gap to Rust** (1.13× behind). Pinned the diagnosis. **Why this is the trigger the locked design called for:** the Slice 6 reopen condition at line 617 — "workload surfacing measurable Vec-indirection hotspot in `sort_by` / `sort_by_key` / `partition`" — names this exact shape; kata 16 supplies the kata15-tie + kata16-gap A/B that converts the abstract design into a concrete measurement.

  **Slice 6.1 SHIPPED 2026-05-29 (commit `1fbd942e`).** `Vec[i64].sort_by(inline_closure)` with no captures now routes through `emit_sort_by_mono_i64` (new helper in `src/codegen/vec_method.rs`): emits a per-call-site `__vec_i64_sort_by_mono_<id>(data: *mut i64, len: i64)` function with `Linkage::Internal` whose body is an insertion sort with the user's comparator inlined at the inner compare. No `karac_vec_sort_by` callback, no function-pointer indirection — LLVM has direct visibility into both the sort algorithm and the comparator. Gate predicate `should_use_mono_vec_sort_by_for(elem_ty)` (i64 only for v1) plus `collect_closure_free_vars(...).is_empty()` (rejects captures); all other shapes fall through to the existing `karac_vec_sort_by` thunk path unchanged. **Algorithm:** insertion sort, ~30 lines of IR builder, locked in by the A/B experiment above. O(N²) is fine for current corpus (kata 15/16 N=16, ~120 compares/sort). Future slice can swap PDQ small-sort network when a larger-N workload pulls — `should_use_mono_vec_sort_by_for` is the chokepoint. **Measured impact (re-benched, READMEs updated):**
  - Kata 16: 96.8 ms → 62.8 ms (1.55× behind Rust → 1.06× behind, **94% of gap closed** — better than the A/B's 76% because LLVM sees the comparator inside the surrounding K=1M outer loop's optimization context). Seq binary collapsed **359.4 KiB → 33.0 KiB** (smaller than C now) because karac_vec_sort_by + transitive runtime archive surface gets DCE'd.
  - Kata 15: 243.3 ms (tied Rust) → 228.9 ms (**1.15× FASTER than Rust** at 262.5 ms). Pre-Slice-6.1 the tie hid an offset: Kāra's faster small-Vec alloc path was compensating for the runtime-callback sort dispatch; with both compilers now monomorphizing the comparator, the allocator edge stops being offset and Kāra inches ahead. Same binary-size collapse to 33 KiB.
  - Both katas' auto-par regimes also improved (kata 16: 10.8 → 8.3 ms; kata 15: 33.9 → 27.2 ms) — workers run the faster mono body.
  - 6 new positive E2Es in `tests/codegen.rs` (`mono_i64_ascending`, `_descending`, `_computed_key`, `_with_duplicates`, `_empty_and_single`, `_fallback_on_captures` — the last pins that capture-bearing closures correctly route to the fallback thunk). Codegen suite: 903 → 909, all passing; full suite green.

  **Slice 6.2+ — REMAINING SUB-SLICES (all `[ ]` open, natural-pull triggered when the workload appears):**
  - Other integer elem types (i32 / i16 / i8 / u64 / u32 / u16 / u8 / usize). Widening the gate predicate is mechanical; the body is type-agnostic at the IR level (just elem_ty + IntPredicate threading). Triggers: a kata that uses `Vec[i32].sort_by` or similar.
  - Captures support. Either thread captures as extra parameters to the mono fn, OR emit an env-struct alloca + ctx-load mirror of `emit_sort_by_inline_thunk`'s pattern. Trigger: a kata where the comparator legitimately needs an outer reference (e.g. sort-by-distance-from-pivot).
  - Non-inline callee shapes (named fn, closure-typed local). The existing `emit_sort_by_thunk` / `emit_sort_by_named_thunk` paths already work via callback; mono path could subsume them by emitting an inline call to the named fn in the sort body. Trigger: when a kata measures the callback overhead on these shapes as non-noise.
  - String / tuple / struct elem types. **Trigger fired 2026-05-29 by kata 56 (Merge Intervals), Slice 6.4 SHIPPED 2026-05-29.** Kata 56 measured 1.50× behind Rust pre-fix (91.5 vs 61.1 ms, K=1M, N=16) with three corroborating signals: (1) C trailed Kāra by only 1.06× because both paid an indirect-call-per-comparison (qsort vs runtime callback) — vs the corpus norm 1.14–1.17× when Kāra has a sort-dispatch edge; (2) Kāra seq binary was 410.8 KiB because the runtime archive's karac_vec_sort_by surface stayed linked — vs the 33.0 KiB of kata 15/16 post-Slice-6.1; (3) the only structural shift from kata 16-post-Slice-6.1 (1.06× of Rust) to kata 56 (1.50× of Rust) was the element-type change from i64 to (i64, i64). **Implementation:** generalized `emit_sort_by_mono_i64` → `emit_sort_by_mono` parameterized over `elem_ty: BasicTypeEnum`; widened the gate predicate to accept LLVM struct types whose fields are all integers (covers `(i64, i64)`, `(i64, i64, i64)`, and integer-field user structs); for named structs (`struct Score { v: i64 }`) the caller plumbs the Kāra type name through `elem_type_name: Option<&str>` so the emitter can register `var_type_names` for closure params and `.field_name` access lookups resolve. **Runtime length dispatch (also Slice 6.4):** call sites now emit BOTH the mono fast path AND a `karac_vec_sort_by` fallback, choosing per-call based on `if len > 64 { runtime } else { mono }`. Surfaced 2026-05-29 by kata 1665's N=50000 workload regressing from 3.2 ms to 1.1 s under a strawman mono-only dispatch (insertion sort is O(N²) and loses hard above ~N=64). With the dispatch, kata 1665 returns to its 3.2 ms baseline. **Measured impact:** Kata 56 65.0 ms vs Rust 61.5 ms (1.06× behind, **88% of gap closed**, was 1.50×); Kāra now leads C by 1.50× on kata 56 (was only 1.06×) because the qsort indirect-call penalty is no longer offset on the Kāra side. Kata 1665 holds 3.8 ms (1.19× behind Rust, matches pre-Slice-6.4). **Cost:** the seq binary stays at ~410 KiB instead of collapsing to ~33 KiB the way kata 16's did under Slice 6.1's pure-mono dispatch — both branches at the call site mean karac_vec_sort_by stays linked. A future slice can lift this by emitting a smaller typed runtime helper for the large-N path that doesn't drag the full runtime sort surface. **Tests (6 new, all positive):** `mono_tuple_primary_key` (kata 56 idiom), `mono_tuple_secondary_field_preserved` (pins that the 16-byte struct payload survives the sort), `mono_tuple_computed_comparator` (kata 1665 idiom), `mono_tuple_three_fields` (24-byte payload), `mono_named_struct_int_field` (Score), `mono_large_n_uses_runtime_path` (>64 elements, runtime fallback engages). Cross-ref: kata 56 commit `558edc1` (kata ship + trigger evidence); karac Slice 6.4 commit (see git log); kata 56 README rewrite with post-fix numbers. **Still deferred to future slices:** String / Float / Pointer / 3-word-struct elements (the mono path's `tag - 1` Ordering contract doesn't yet handle multi-word comparators); larger sort algorithm for the runtime path (PDQ small-sort, or typed `karac_vec_sort_<T>_*` that's leaner than the current generic karac_vec_sort_by).
  - `Vec.sort()` bare-method fast path. Currently routes through `karac_vec_sort_by` with a default-int-comparison thunk; a typed direct call into the same mono body would give the same win. ~10 LoC change.
  - `Vec.sort_by_key` mono path. Same mono pattern as sort_by, key function inlined instead of comparator. Larger because the key type can be String / tuple / struct (the existing thunk already handles these via per-key-type dispatch); mono path would need to mirror that surface.
  - PDQ small-sort network or call-out to `karac_vec_sort_i64_unstable` runtime helper when N exceeds an insertion-sort-friendly threshold. Trigger: kata at N ≥ 100 where insertion sort's O(N²) starts hurting.

  Cross-refs: line 608 (locked design §3.5); line 617 (the trigger condition this fires); line 274 (the prior sort_by codegen entry — Slice 6.1 supersedes its inline-thunk + `karac_vec_sort_by` ABI for `Vec[i64]` + inline-closure + no-captures; all other shapes still use the prior path); kata 16 commits `a94ba9a` (kata ship) and `657199c` (diagnosis correction); karac commit `1fbd942e` (Slice 6.1 ship); kata 15 + 16 README updates ship in the same kara-katas commit as the Slice 6.1 karac ship.

- [ ] **HTTP FFI closure path: kill trampoline overhead for plaintext-throughput perf.** Diagnosed at [`docs/investigations/http_layer_perf.md`](../investigations/http_layer_perf.md) (paused as of 2026-05-10 pending bench-shape change). Four progressively-larger surface changes that together close the trampoline overhead in `runtime/src/lib.rs:serve_request`. **None of them moves the Parallax bench numbers** because that bench is CPU-saturated on the four busy_loops; they all target the path to TechEmpower-style plaintext throughput (500 K – 1 M+ rps on M-class hardware). Pick up when either (a) a plaintext-throughput bench shape is built (tracked in [`bench_robustness.md`](../investigations/bench_robustness.md) "Open follow-up"), or (b) an unrelated need touches the HTTP FFI surface (e.g., header-round-trip support — locked design (i) in `runtime/Cargo.toml` is currently minimal-surface). Sub-items in priority order:
  - **Length-prefixed FFI** for `KaracHttpRequest`/`Response`. Replace `*const c_char` (null-terminated, requires `CString` per request) with `(*const u8, usize)` pairs. Kills 3+N `CString` allocs per request (where N = header count). Touches: FFI struct shape, `karac_runtime_http_request_path` return type, Kāra-side codegen for `req.path()` lowering. Single coherent slice, ~80 LoC change + test updates.
  - **Borrowed accessors with lifetime threading** — `req.path() -> ref StringSlice` returning a view into hyper's request buffer instead of allocating a fresh `String` per call. Adds `ref StringSlice` to Kāra's borrow checker and lifetime-threads hyper's request through the FFI boundary. Larger surface (touches the borrow checker); deferred because the cheap part (length-prefixed FFI above) gets most of the value without the design depth. Original framing in [`docs/demo_ideas.md § Slice E`](../demo_ideas.md) "Out of scope".
  - **Inline trampoline** — emit shim body at handler call site instead of as a separate symbol. Saves one PLT indirection per request; small win individually (~10 ns/req) but stacks with the others.
  - **`#[repr(C)]`-compatible Request** — let user code see hyper's bytes directly, no packing layer at all. Largest design surface (Kāra's value-type ABI needs a story for "this struct is laid out by an external producer"); biggest payoff at the no-work / plaintext shape.

- [ ] **HTTP handler: workload-shape default for `block_in_place` vs `spawn_blocking` vs direct invocation.** Probed at [`docs/investigations/http_layer_perf.md § Findings, 2026-05-10 — H1`](../investigations/http_layer_perf.md) (`8d1b19b`). Currently `runtime/src/lib.rs:serve_request` invokes the handler synchronously inside `tokio::task::block_in_place`; the env var `KARAC_HTTP_BLOCK_IN_PLACE=0` skips the wrapper. Probe data: removing it improves saturated p50 by 35-41% and throughput by ~7%, but the wrapper IS load-bearing for handlers that should let other concurrent async work progress (a CPU-bound handler that's "always" running needs the worker-replacement dance). The right default depends on what handler shape is "typical" for Kāra users — CPU-bound (default-skip), I/O-bound (default-keep), mixed (compiler decides per-handler from effects?). Phase 6.3 async-aware handlers (`async fn handle(req: Request) -> Response`) will revisit this surface naturally — at that point `block_in_place` is the wrong shape regardless and the design lock can be revisited. Until then: env var stays as opt-in, default unchanged, and the bench can opt into the CPU-bound shape via `KARAC_HTTP_BLOCK_IN_PLACE=0` when appropriate.

- [x] **`karac_par_run`: long-lived worker pool.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-09 (commits `3953a14` + `d4acfa7` README backfill). Replaced `thread::scope` + per-call `s.spawn` with dispatch onto a global lazy-init pool (`OnceLock<Arc<Pool>>`, `Mutex<VecDeque<Task>>` + `Condvar`, `available_parallelism()`-sized worker count). Caller blocks on a per-call `Arc<ParCall>` Condvar with a work-helping wait loop so nested-par can't deadlock the pool. ABI unchanged. Bench: thread churn -94 % (3,344 → 213 unique TIDs in 30 s), p99 -46 % (438 → 238 ms), CPU efficiency 9× better (busy_loop self-time 7.5 % → 66.7 %). Throughput essentially unchanged because the bench was wrk-connection-bound, not pool-capacity-bound at that point. Three deferred follow-ups (real work-stealing scheduler, tunable pool size, panic-payload propagation) tracked in the entry above. Original entry: The MVP impl in `runtime/src/lib.rs:307-…` spawns fresh OS threads per call via `thread::scope` + `s.spawn`, then joins + tears them down. Diagnosed as the Parallax bench's dominant bottleneck (`docs/investigations/parallax_perf.md` § Findings, `0817bc1`): under `wrk -t4 -c100` load the bench server runs at 1,090 req/s × 4 fan-out tasks = ~4,360 thread spawn/join cycles per second; samply profile shows 60 % of CPU in `mach_vm_protect` (pthread stack guard-page setup) and 3,344 unique TIDs in 30 s of recording. Replace the per-call thread::scope with dispatch onto a long-lived global pool — `OnceLock<Arc<Pool>>` lazy init, `Mutex<VecDeque<Task>>` + `Condvar` for worker wake-up, per-call `Arc<ParCall>` carrying the cancel flag + remaining-count + completion Condvar. ABI unchanged; codegen unaffected; surface contained to one function. Estimated post-fix throughput: 3-5 K req/s for the Parallax bench's Kāra row (1.1 K → 3-5 K), bringing it into Go's order of magnitude. Remaining gap to Rust (45 K) becomes H2 / H3 / H4 territory in the investigation doc — addressable separately via the closure path enumerated in `docs/demo_ideas.md § Slice E` "Out of scope". **Settled design forks (2026-05-09):** (i) **Hand-rolled std-only**, not rayon — keeps runtime deps minimal (`serde_json + hyper + tokio` already, no new pulls), ~80 LoC fully auditable, cleanly swappable when the work-stealing scheduler designated by `design.md § Runtime Distribution` (line 8933) lands as a separate slice. Rayon's value is dynamic work-stealing across many long tasks, overkill for 4-branch fan-out. (ii) **Pool size = `thread::available_parallelism()`**, floor at 2 — matches today's per-call default, predictable, no env knob in v1. (iii) **No graceful shutdown in v1** — pool workers are daemon threads; pure compute, no resource handles, process exit cleans them up. Add explicit shutdown when a destructor or test-teardown surface needs it. (iv) **Soundness for parent-stack pointers preserved** — `karac_par_run` blocks on the per-call Condvar before returning, identically to today's `thread::scope` semantics; raw `parent_addr` remains valid for the duration of one call. **Deferred follow-ups (not in scope of this entry):** real work-stealing scheduler with per-worker deques (post-v1, per design.md); tunable pool size via env var (premature; default-only until a workload demands tuning); panic-payload propagation back to the parent (today's behavior swallows panic payloads via catch_unwind and uses cancel flag for sibling notification — preserved in v1; richer payload propagation is a follow-up if any test needs it).

- [x] **Monomorphization tracking + `karac query monomorphization`.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. New `src/monomorphization.rs` analyzer (~330 LoC) walks the AST, joins each `Call` / `MethodCall` against `TypeCheckResult.call_type_subs` (the typechecker's per-call-site `param_name → resolved_type` table populated by `record_call_type_subs`), and dedups by `(generic, types_tuple)` to produce one `MonomorphizationTable` per program. Free-function callees are identified by their `Identifier` / `Path` AST shape; method callees flow through `method_callee_types` and have their receiver-side generic args stripped (`Vec[i64].push` → `Vec.push`) so all instantiations of one generic method collapse to a single group. New `QueryKind::Monomorphization` + `karac query monomorphization <file>` CLI surface emit the JSON envelope spelled out at `design.md § Compiler Query API > karac query monomorphization` (`scope`, `by_generic[].generic`, `by_generic[].instance_count`, `by_generic[].instances[].{types,effects,site}`, `totals.{generic_count,instance_count}`). 9 analyzer tests in `tests/monomorphization.rs` + 3 CLI envelope tests in `tests/cli.rs` cover: empty-program zero-counts, non-generic dedup skip, single/multi-arg instantiation, distinct-type-args produce distinct instances, same-type-args dedup, alphabetical param-name ordering, first-call-site-wins on `site`, generic-name ordering, walker visits loop/branch/nested-block call positions. Two v1 deviations from the tracker's "plumb existing data" framing: (1) **`effects` slot is always empty in v1** — the typechecker exposes `call_type_subs` but no analogous `call_effect_subs` table for compound polymorphism `(T, E)` tuples; effect resolution stays internal to the effect-checker, so the schema-mandated `effects` list ships as `[]` until a `call_effect_subs` analog lands; (2) **types are sorted alphabetically by param name**, not declaration-order — `call_type_subs` is a `HashMap` so iteration order isn't deterministic; tools wanting declaration-order map back via the function definition. Behavior delta is purely additive to the query surface (new `QueryKind` variant, new CLI kind, new module).

- [x] **`--monomorphization-budget=warn:N,error:M` flag (v1.x).** ✓ Mechanism landed 2026-05-29 (`20b42ca`), opt-in / default-disabled. Compile-time per-generic instantiation ceiling: reuses `monomorphization::analyze` (the table behind `karac query monomorphization`, line 264) after typecheck and before codegen in `cmd_build`. `--monomorphization-budget=warn:N,error:M` — either threshold optional, `warn` must be ≤ `error`. A generic at ≥ N emits `warning[monomorphization-budget]` and continues; ≥ M emits `error[monomorphization-budget]` and fails the build before codegen (error supersedes warn for the same generic). Human-readable diagnostics go to stderr (`<file>:<line>:<col>: generic \`<g>\` has <count> instantiations (limit <T>)`), keeping stdout reserved for the build result; `--output=json` additionally emits a diagnostics envelope on stdout for the error case, mirroring the `has_fatal_errors` JSON path. **Files:** `src/monomorphization.rs` (`MonomorphizationBudget` / `BudgetLevel` / `BudgetViolation` + `MonomorphizationTable::budget_violations` + 5 unit tests), `src/cli/args.rs` (`parse_monomorphization_budget` with positive-int + warn≤error validation + project-mode guard), `src/cli.rs` (`Command::Build.monomorphization_budget` field + `enforce_monomorphization_budget`), `src/cli/help.rs` (build OPTIONS), `tests/cli.rs` (9 tests: 4 parse-layer rejections, help listing, error/warn/supersede/default build behavior under llvm). All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all-targets --features llvm -D warnings` + `cargo test --features llvm`: 314 cli + 9 monomorphization-integration + 11 monomorphization-unit, zero regressions). Two follow-ups carved out as sub-slices below.
  - [ ] **Pin default warn/error thresholds.** The flag ships default-disabled; concrete defaults stay deferred until Phase 7.1 has codegen output for Parallax + stdlib-heavy combinator code to calibrate against — picking 100 vs. 500 vs. 1000 without that data is the same trap as the auto-concurrency cost model (Item 8). Non-breaking when it lands (the flag already lets users opt into stricter ceilings; flipping a default on is additive). **Blocked on** Phase 7.1 codegen output.
  - [ ] **Project-mode monomorphization budget.** Extend enforcement to `karac build` project mode. Today the flag is single-file only — project mode (`parse_build_command`'s no-file arm) rejects it loudly rather than silently dropping it. Needs the project pipeline to surface a merged multi-module `MonomorphizationTable` (the per-program `monomorphization::analyze` already exists; the cross-module merge does not). **Blocked on** the CR-24 multi-file build pipeline landing.

- [ ] **Portable SIMD `Vector[T, N]` codegen and stdlib type.** Spec lives at design.md § Portable SIMD — `Vector[T, N]`. Implement the type as a stdlib intrinsic with the full surface — element-wise arithmetic, `dot`, `cross` (only for `N == 3`), lane access via `[]`, mask-producing comparison ops returning `Vector[bool, N]`, shuffle / swizzle, `splat`, lane-wise reductions (`sum`, `min`, `max`). Codegen lowering: (1) emit LLVM `<N x T>` vector type for any `(T, N)` whose lanes match a target instruction directly; (2) emit two-or-more-instruction vectorised lowerings for `N` that exceeds the native width but is still a multiple of it; (3) emit a scalar `for i in 0..N` loop fallback when the target lacks a vector unit or `T` is not vector-supported (e.g. `i128`). The fallback is silent; a `--simd-report=verbose` codegen flag prints which `(T, N)` pairs lowered scalar-only per function (P1.x). The `#[require_simd]` function-level attribute makes scalar fallback a hard error — implementation rejects the function at codegen if any `Vector[T, N]` operation in its body would lower to a scalar loop on the requested target. Memory layout: `repr(simd)` semantics (`N` contiguous `T` lanes, alignment `align_of[T] * next_pow2(N)`); FFI-stable for power-of-two `N`. Architecture-specific intrinsics (AVX-512, NEON, SVE) live in cfg-gated platform modules and are out of scope for this entry — they ship as a follow-up once the portable surface is solid. Const-arg validation: `N <= 0` rejected at the const-expr evaluator (already in place from item 1); element-type `T: Numeric` enforced by trait-bound check. Test plan: per-target codegen smoke (x86 SSE/AVX, ARM NEON, RV64 with no V extension as the scalar-fallback baseline); golden output for `--simd-report=verbose`; `#[require_simd]` rejection test on a target without the unit. (Phase 7+ — depends on LLVM backend; stdlib type definition lands in Phase 7.2 alongside Array/Vec/String.)

- [x] **Codegen method dispatcher: silent-`0` catch-all → typed compile error.** ✓ DONE (2026-05-04). Both fall-through sites in `compile_method_call` (outer return, inner slice `_ => {}`) now return structured `Err` diagnostics naming the method and receiver; the void-return placeholder at the user impl-block path was preserved with a clarifying comment so future readers don't re-target it. The hardening surfaced two latent bugs the silent-zero had been hiding: (1) `emit_par_branch_fn` and the closure-body emitter saved-and-cleared `var_type_names` but never re-populated entries for captured variables — so user impl-block method dispatch silently failed inside par branches and closures; fixed by propagating the type-name binding for each capture from the saved outer scope; (2) `refs_in_expr` had `_ => {}` with no `ExprKind::MethodCall` arm and silently dropped method-call receivers, so par-block capture analysis emitted empty capture lists for receivers like `c.compute()`; fixed by adding the missing arm. Regression `test_codegen_rejects_unsupported_slice_method` in `tests/codegen.rs` locks in the diagnostic shape against re-introduction. Slice-method audit (`first`/`last`/`get`/`contains`/`binary_search`/`split_at`/`chunks`/`windows`/`sort`/`reverse`/`sort_by`/`fill`): none reached by current tests or examples — the hard-error diagnostic is the safety net when the first caller arrives. `cargo clippy --all --tests --features llvm -- -D warnings` clean; `cargo test --release --features llvm` passes.

- [x] **Codegen `Vec.sort_by_key` lowering (remaining unbuilt method on the hardened `compile_vec_method` catch-all).** ✓ DONE (2026-05-29). Surfaced reviewing kata-15 (3Sum): `Vec.sort()`, `Vec.sort_by_key()`, and `Vec.reverse()` typechecked and ran in the interpreter but **silently no-op'd in codegen** — `compile_vec_method` (`src/codegen/vec_method.rs`) only had a `sort_by` arm and every other method fell through to a `_ => Ok(const 0)` catch-all (the `compile_vec_method` twin of the `compile_method_call` catch-all hardened in the sibling `[x]` entry directly above). **Fixed in `fb684bb`** for sort/reverse + catch-all hardening (default signed-int comparator thunk reusing `karac_vec_sort_by`; new `karac_vec_reverse` runtime fn; typed `Err` on any unhandled method). **sort_by_key landed (this entry):** new `emit_sort_by_key_inline_thunk` in `src/codegen/vec_method.rs` mirrors `emit_sort_by_inline_thunk`'s env-struct + outer-stack-alloca capture shape, but the bridge thunk compiles the key closure body *twice* into itself (once with the param bound to element a, once to element b) and returns the signed compare of the two extracted integer keys as `-1 / 0 / +1` — the same comparator contract `karac_vec_sort_by` consumes, so the runtime FFI is reused as-is. **V1 scope (intentional):** inline closures only (named functions / closure-typed locals error loudly directing the user to the inline form — a bridge thunk with an indirect call through the closure's fat pointer would close this gap, mirroring `emit_sort_by_thunk` for `sort_by`); integer key types only (non-integer keys error loudly directing the user to `sort_by` with an explicit comparator — consistent with the `.cmp` and default-`sort` lowerings). **Tests:** three positive E2Es in `tests/codegen.rs` (`test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_identity_ascending` for `|x| x`, `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_negation_descending` for `|x| -x`, `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_with_captured_variable` for an env-capture key body) plus `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_named_fn_callee_rejected` pinning the v1 scope boundary. Cross-ref: the closure-bearing Vec-method deferral at the *§3.5 — Vec migration deferred (Slice 6)* / *Slice 6 (Vec)* entries below — that entry is about devirtualizing already-working closure dispatch; with this slice, `sort_by_key` has joined `sort_by` as one of those "already-working" methods.

- [x] **Codegen `sort_by` / `sort_by_key` non-inline-closure callee (named function or closure-typed local).** ✓ DONE (2026-05-29). The dispatch in both arms (`src/codegen/vec_method.rs`) now matches the arg's `ExprKind`: inline `Closure { ... }` keeps the existing inline-thunk fast path; `Identifier(name)` routes to one of two new bridge thunks depending on what `name` resolves to. Closure-typed locals (`name` in `self.closure_fn_types`) compile the arg to its `{fn_ptr, env_ptr}` fat pointer, spill it into an alloca, and pass that alloca as `ctx` to `emit_sort_by_key_closure_thunk` (sort_by_key) or the existing `emit_sort_by_thunk` (sort_by, now reachable); the thunk loads the fat ptr from ctx and does an indirect call through `closure_fn_type` per element. Named fns (`name` in `self.module`) skip the fat-ptr machinery entirely — `emit_sort_by_key_named_thunk` / `emit_sort_by_named_thunk` accept a null ctx and call the named fn directly with the loaded element(s); no `env_ptr` is synthesized because the closure-typed-local path already covers callees that need an env, and a named fn with no captures has the direct ABI. **Pre-existing latent bug discovered + fixed in the same slice:** `compile_closure` (`src/codegen/closures.rs:297-313`) registered closure params in `self.variables` but **not** in `self.var_type_names`, so a closure body like `|s: Score| s.v` compiled `s.v` to the `i64 0` placeholder (`type_name_of_expr` returned None → `field_index_for` returned None → generic field-access fall-through). The inline thunk worked around this with its own var_type_names insertion at the param-bind step (see the sibling field-access body entry below), so it only manifested as a silent no-op on the non-inline path — the kata-15 probe set surfaced it via v2 (closure-typed local with struct element, field-access body): the program built clean but the sort was a no-op. Fixed in `compile_closure` itself: when a closure param has a single-segment Path type annotation, register the seg as the param's struct/enum type name so the body's field access resolves through the existing `compile_field_access` path. **V1 scope (intentional):** the non-inline thunks gate the closure return type to `IntType` (integer keys only) — the per-key-type dispatch in `emit_sort_by_key_inline_thunk` (String / struct / float / user-Ord) relies on body-Expr span lookups in `string_typed_exprs` etc., and the non-inline callees don't carry the body Expr at the dispatch site. Non-int keys error loudly directing the user to rewrite as an inline `|x| ...` closure. **Tests:** five new positive E2Es in `tests/codegen.rs` plus repurposing the prior rejection test as the first positive: `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_named_fn_callee`, `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_closure_typed_local`, `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_closure_typed_local_struct_field_body` (pins the var_type_names fix), `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_named_fn_struct_field_body`, `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_closure_typed_local`, `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_named_fn_callee`. Gates: codegen 903 / 0, par_codegen 105 / 0, memory_sanitizer 72 / 0. Cross-ref: parent sort_by_key entry; sibling field-access body entry directly below.

- [x] **Codegen `sort_by_key` non-integer key type.** ✓ DONE (2026-05-29). All sub-gaps closed across six slices: integer-tuple keys, String keys + focused type-info plumbing, `derive(Ord)` struct keys with mixed int + String fields, nested struct fields, float keys with `f64.total_cmp` semantics, and user `impl Ord for T`. Sibling v1 scope boundary of the parent sort_by_key entry above. The inline thunk originally gated the key type to `IntType`, consistent with the signed `.cmp` lowering in `src/codegen/method_call.rs:644` and the default-order `sort()` thunk. Non-integer Ord keys — `String` (lexicographic byte compare), tuples like `(i64, i64)` (lexicographic on components), structs implementing Ord via a user `cmp` method — each need a different comparison lowering. **Partial landing (2026-05-29) — integer-tuple keys:** `emit_sort_by_key_inline_thunk`'s key dispatch now has a `(StructValue, StructValue)` arm that detects tuples whose fields are all integer types (unambiguous at the LLVM struct level — no Kāra-type plumbing needed) and emits a lexicographic cascade. The cascade builds the result from the last field backward via selects (`result_i = (a[i] != b[i]) ? cmp_i : result_{i+1}`), so the first field that differs decides the order; pure data-flow, no new basic blocks. Covers `(i64, i64)`, `(i64, i64, i64)`, and any n-arity integer tuple. Three positive E2Es in `tests/codegen.rs`: `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_tuple_lexicographic`, `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_tuple_tie_break`, `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_triple_tuple_cascade`. **Partial landing (2026-05-29) — String keys + focused type-info plumbing:** rather than thread the full `expr_types` map onto codegen (which would touch every codegen entry-point caller), I added a focused side-table `Program.string_typed_exprs: HashSet<(usize, usize)>` populated by the lowering pass from `TypeCheckResult.expr_types` — every span whose Kāra type is `Type::Str` lands in the set. `Codegen.string_typed_exprs` is cloned from `Program.string_typed_exprs` at `compile_program`, mirroring how `method_callee_types` / `pattern_binding_types` are already plumbed. The set is the cheaper sibling of the full map: one bit per span, reusable for any future codegen path that needs to distinguish `String` from other 3-word types. `emit_sort_by_key_inline_thunk` now consults the set on the body Expr's `(offset, length)` before the value-kind dispatch, and when the key is `String` it extracts `ptr` (field 0) and `len` (field 1) from each key's struct value and calls the new `karac_string_cmp` runtime fn — lexicographic byte compare with length as the tie-break (matches Rust's `Ord` on `String` for valid UTF-8, since Unicode code-point order coincides with byte order under UTF-8). Two positive E2Es in `tests/codegen.rs`: `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_string_identity` (canonical `|s| s` on `Vec[String]`) and `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_string_length_tiebreak` (shared-prefix strings exercise the length tie-break + stable dup ordering). **Partial landing (2026-05-29) — `derive(Ord)` struct keys with mixed int + String fields:** the typechecker's `type_supports_ord` recognises Ord on user structs only via the `derived_traits` table (set by `#[derive(Ord)]`), not via free-standing `impl Ord for T` blocks — so the canonical pattern for sort_by_key with a struct key is to `#[derive(PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord)]`. **All-integer-field derive(Ord) structs already worked** through the int-tuple cascade (a single-int-field or all-int struct is structurally identical to an n-int tuple at the LLVM level). The remaining gap was mixed-type-field structs — a struct with both an integer and a `String` field typechecked but errored loudly in codegen because the int-tuple cascade gates on every field being `IntType`. Closed here with a new struct-aware dispatch arm: another focused side-table `Program.expr_struct_type_names: HashMap<(usize, usize), String>` (sibling of `string_typed_exprs`, populated by the lowering pass from `TypeCheckResult.expr_types` for every `Type::Named` expression) records the body span's struct name; `Codegen.expr_struct_type_names` clones it. In `emit_sort_by_key_inline_thunk`, when the body span resolves to a struct name, the cascade looks up the struct's per-field type names via the existing `Codegen.struct_field_type_names[name]` table and dispatches each field: integer fields use the signed compare from the int-key arm, fields whose recorded type name is `"String"` extract `ptr` / `len` and call `karac_string_cmp` from the String-key arm. The cascade is built last-field-backward into selects, same as the int-tuple cascade, so the first differing field wins. Two positive E2Es in `tests/codegen.rs`: `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_struct_mixed_fields` (the canonical `Item { score: i64, name: String }` pattern with a primary-field tie broken by the secondary String) and `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_struct_all_int_fields` (pins that the all-int struct case still works under the struct-aware path). **Partial landing (2026-05-29) — nested struct fields:** the struct-aware cascade was refactored into a recursive helper `emit_struct_cmp_cascade(ka, kb, struct_name, depth)`. When a field's recorded type name maps to another entry in `struct_field_type_names`, the cascade recurses on the field's struct values; the `depth` parameter threads into LLVM value names so they stay unique across recursive entries (the same struct can appear at multiple depths in a key). Two positive E2Es: `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_nested_struct_field` (two-level `Outer { p: Inner, n: i64 }`) and `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_nested_struct_with_string_field` (combines nested-struct recursion with a String field at the outer level — exercises both extensions in one cascade). **Partial landing (2026-05-29) — float keys with `f64.total_cmp` semantics:** the NaN-ordering design call was made — sort_by_key adopts Rust's `f64::total_cmp` algorithm (sign-flip the bit pattern, integer-compare), which gives every f64 including NaN a well-defined position in a total order. Scoped to sort_by_key only: `check_sort_key_closure` in `src/typechecker/stdlib_seq.rs` accepts Float types as a focused concession, but `type_supports_ord` for other Ord consumers (derive checks, SortedSet, etc.) stays as-is — widening Ord broadly is a separate, larger design call that needs its own slice. A new `karac_float_cmp(a: f64, b: f64) -> i64` runtime fn implements the algorithm; codegen's float-arm extracts the float keys, widens f32 → f64 if needed (exact conversion preserves total order), and calls the runtime fn. Two positive E2Es: `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_float_total_cmp_ascending` (mixed positive/negative finites) and `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_float_nan_sorts_largest` (pins NaN-as-largest semantics so the policy can't silently regress to IEEE 754 unordered). **Partial landing (2026-05-29) — user `impl Ord for T` (without `derive(Ord)`):** the original investigation hit two pre-existing latent codegen blockers (filed below as separate entries: `impl Ord` cmp return-type mismatch and `sort_by_key(|s| s.v)` field-access body not sorting). Both blockers landed first (`b32ee4d4`, `079f5d7f`); the user-impl-Ord work re-landed cleanly on top. **Typechecker:** `type_supports_ord` (`src/typechecker/derives.rs`) now consults a new `has_user_impl_ord` helper that scans `env.impls` for `(name, "Ord")` — letting user `impl Ord` count toward the Ord bound at every consumer site the same way `derive(Ord)` does (the impl list is small and Ord checks aren't a hot path, so the linear scan is fine). **Lowering:** new `Program.user_ord_typed_exprs: HashMap<(usize, usize), String>` (in `src/ast.rs`) populated by `lower_program` from `tc.expr_types` + `tc.trait_impls` — for every expression whose Kāra type is a struct (or shared struct) with `("Ord", name)` in trait_impls, records `(span.offset, span.length) → "Type.cmp"`. Sibling of `expr_struct_type_names` populated immediately above; codegen reads it from Program at `compile_program` (matching the existing focused-side-table convention). **Codegen dispatch:** new arm in `emit_sort_by_key_inline_thunk` (in `src/codegen/vec_method.rs`) fires before the field-aware cascade when the body span resolves to a user-impl-Ord struct. Looks up the user's `Type.cmp` from `self.module.get_function`, inspects its first param to decide the by-value vs by-pointer convention (same shape as `compile_method_call:951`), calls it directly with the two key values, extracts the Ordering tag (via the layout seeded in `b32ee4d4`), and returns `tag - 1` to get the standard `-1 / 0 / +1` comparator value — same conversion `emit_sort_by_thunk` uses for sort_by's named-callee path. Critical pin: `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_user_impl_ord_reverse` in `tests/codegen.rs` defines an `impl Ord` whose `cmp` body **reverses** the natural order, then sorts and asserts descending output — a derive-cascade fallthrough would produce ascending. With this slice, the parent non-integer-key entry is fully closed: `sort_by_key` now supports integers, integer tuples, String, `derive(Ord)` structs (int + String fields, at any nesting depth), floats with `f64.total_cmp` semantics, AND user `impl Ord` structs. Cross-ref: the parent sort_by_key entry; the kata-1665 sort_by precedent in the *§3.5 / Slice 6 (Vec)* entries below.

- [x] **Codegen: `impl Ord for T { fn cmp -> Ordering }` emits return type as `i64` instead of `{ i64 }`.** ✓ DONE (2026-05-29). Surfaced while wiring user-impl-Ord support into `sort_by_key` (see the parent non-integer-key entry above). Reproducer: `struct Score { v: i64 }; impl PartialEq for Score { ... } impl Eq for Score {} impl PartialOrd for Score { ... } impl Ord for Score { fn cmp(self, other: Score) -> Ordering { other.v.cmp(self.v) } } fn main() { let _ = Score { v: 1 }.cmp(Score { v: 2 }); }` — module verification failed with `Function return type does not match operand type of return inst!  ret { i64 } %ord  i64`. **Root cause:** `Ordering` was never seeded in `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` (`src/codegen/declarations.rs:2850`), so `llvm_type_for_name("Ordering")` fell through the enum-layouts check at line 924 in `types_lowering.rs` and returned the `i64` default. Function declaration went via that path; the function body went via the manual fallback at `method_call.rs:670` (`enum_layouts.get("Ordering").map(|l| l.llvm_type).unwrap_or_else(|| context.struct_type(&[i64_t.into()], false))`) which builds the `{ i64 }` struct directly. Two different paths, two different LLVM types for the same Kāra type → verification mismatch. **Fix:** seed `Ordering` in `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` alongside Option / Json / TcpError / TlsError. Layout: unit-only `Less` / `Equal` / `Greater` with tags 0/1/2, zero payload words, drop kinds empty per variant, LLVM type `{ i64 tag }` — same shape as the existing fallback so the seed is transparent everywhere the fallback was already firing (e.g. `method_call.rs:670`'s `.cmp` arm). Regression: `test_e2e_user_impl_ord_cmp_returns_ordering` in `tests/codegen.rs` defines a struct with the full PartialEq / Eq / PartialOrd / Ord impl chain, calls `.cmp` directly, and asserts the program builds and runs (would previously have failed at module verification). The bug had been latent since the `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` pass landed: no user-facing consumer made user-Ord-impl typechecker-reachable, so the only `Ordering`-returning `cmp` calls in compiled programs came through `i64.cmp` and similar (`method_call.rs:644`), which builds the Ordering value inline without ever declaring a function returning `Ordering`. Gates: codegen 896 / 0, par_codegen 71 / 0, memory_sanitizer 105 / 0.

- [x] **Codegen: `Vec.sort_by_key(|s| s.field)` where elem is a struct and the field is a primitive doesn't sort.** ✓ DONE (2026-05-29). Reproducer: `struct Score { v: i64 }; fn main() { let mut v: Vec[Score] = Vec.new(); v.push(Score { v: 30 }); v.push(Score { v: 10 }); v.push(Score { v: 20 }); v.sort_by_key(|s| s.v); for s in v.iter() { println(s.v); } }` — printed `30 10 20` (input order). **Root cause:** the bridge-thunk IR dump confirmed the bug isn't in the sort dispatch — it's in the closure body compile. The thunk loaded the struct value from the closure param's alloca but emitted no `extractvalue` for the field — the body's intended result (the i64 field) silently collapsed to the bare struct load, and the sort comparator returned `ret i64 0` for every pair. `compile_field_access` traces back to `type_name_of_expr` (in `src/codegen/expr_ops.rs`), which resolves an Identifier receiver's struct type via `self.var_type_names[name]`. `emit_sort_by_key_inline_thunk` registered the closure param under `self.variables` (the storage slot) but **not** under `var_type_names` — without that map, `type_name_of_expr` returned `None`, `compile_field_access` couldn't look up the struct shape, and the field-extract step elided. **Fix:** plumb the Vec element's Kāra type name through the thunk emitter — the sort_by_key arm reads `self.var_elem_type_exprs[var_name]`, extracts the canonical first path segment as the struct name, and passes it as a new `elem_type_name: Option<&str>` parameter; the thunk registers `var_type_names[param_name] = struct_name` before either body compile. Existing thunks (the named-callee `emit_sort_by_key_thunk` etc.) are unaffected because the registration is inside the inline-thunk emitter, and `saved_var_types` already restores the outer table on exit. Pinned by `test_e2e_vec_sort_by_key_struct_field_access_body` in `tests/codegen.rs` against the original reproducer. Gates: codegen 897 / 0, par_codegen 72 / 0, memory_sanitizer 105 / 0. Was unnoticed because every existing sort_by_key test used `|x| x` (identifier body) or a tuple/struct identity body — no field-access bodies on struct elements.

- [x] **Codegen `[v; N]` repeat literal: multi-tier fast path (zero-let memset + capped const-aggregate).** ✓ DONE (2026-05-04). The original implementation emitted N `build_insert_value` calls (compile time linear in N; N=100K hung the build at 30s+, blocking 64K-LUT workloads like `Array[i64, 65536]`). The first iteration replaced that with `<elem>.const_array(&vec![val; n as usize])` to build a single LLVM constant aggregate — O(1) at IR-construction time, but LLVM's downstream codegen passes crashed on the giant aggregate store at large N (verified SIGSEGV in `write_to_file` at N≥80K for both i64 and bool element types; module verify passed, the crash was during SelectionDAG's expansion of the aggregate store into machine instructions). The shipped fix is a multi-tier approach: (1) **zero-literal let-binding fast path** — `let buf: Array[T, N] = [0; N]` (and `[false; N]`, `[+0.0; N]`, etc.) detected at the let-binding site and lowered to `alloca + llvm.memset.*`, skipping the aggregate-value round-trip entirely. memset is what LLVM would emit for the aggregate store anyway; emitting it directly sidesteps the codegen path that crashes. O(1) at both IR-construction AND codegen time; works at any N. Floats use bit-pattern equality (`f.to_bits() == 0`) so `-0.0` falls through to the general path and the sign bit is preserved. (2) **Non-zero compile-time const, small N** — single `const_array` call, capped at `SAFE_CONST_ARRAY_N=4096` to stay below the LLVM-crash threshold for non-zero aggregates. (3) **Above the cap or for runtime values** — per-element `insertvalue`, capped at `SAFE_INSERT_N=1024`. Beyond that, errors with a typed diagnostic pointing at the zero-init + runtime-fill workaround rather than silently producing pathologically slow IR. The workload-realistic case lands cleanly: sieve at N=2,000,000 (the original benchmark target, previously unbuildable) now compiles in 0.04s and runs at 12.3 ± 0.2 ms vs Rust's 3.6 ± 0.2 ms (3.43× gap, the smallest gap of the four codegen-vs-Rust workloads measured). Four regression tests in `tests/codegen.rs` lock in: zero-init let emits `llvm.memset` and *not* aggregate-store IR (`test_repeat_literal_const_zero_uses_memset`), 64K LUT compiles cleanly with the same memset shape (`test_repeat_literal_large_n_compiles_without_per_element_ir`), small-N const-nonzero emits no `insertvalue` (`test_repeat_literal_const_nonzero_skips_insertvalue`), runtime-value still exercises the per-element fallback (`test_repeat_literal_runtime_value_falls_back_to_insertvalue`). `cargo clippy --all --tests --features llvm -- -D warnings` clean; `cargo test --release --features llvm` passes.

### Phase 7.2: Compiled Stdlib Types + Layout Codegen

Layout-related user-visible rules live in [design.md § Layout Rules](design.md#layout-rules); the items below are codegen/implementation concerns.

- [x] **`Vec[T]` memory layout.** Compile `Vec[T]` to `{ ptr data, i64 len, i64 capacity }` (24 bytes on 64-bit). No SSO/SVO in v1 — move is pointer copy; inline-storage optimization deferred until benchmarks justify the complexity (and the move-semantics break). String and Vec share the same layout shape so buffer-management routines (grow, drop, memcpy-move) are reusable between them.

- [x] **`Vec[T]` growth strategy.** On `push` exceeding capacity, grow to `max(4, cap * 2)` — 2x doubling with a minimum floor of 4 elements on the first growth from empty. Matches Rust `Vec` behavior; avoids a flurry of tiny allocations on small Vecs.

- [x] **`String` memory layout.** Mirror `Vec[u8]`: `{ ptr data, i64 len, i64 capacity }`. String literals use `{ global_ptr, strlen, 0 }` (cap=0 = static, never freed). `String.new()`, `.len()`, `push_str` implemented. Scope cleanup checks cap > 0 before freeing. SSO deferred to Phase 8.

- **`Array[T, N]` codegen.** Emit as LLVM `[N x T]` directly — no struct wrapper, no heap allocation. Indexing is `getelementptr`. `N` is a compile-time constant available at the type level; `len()` is a constant-fold. Value type — stack-allocated, copy on move. Sub-steps:
  - [x] **A. Parser canonicalization on `Array[T, N]`.** Dropped the `[T; N]` Rust-style type branch in `parser.rs`; `Array[T, N]` is the sole syntax in type position, parsed via the path-type + generic-args route.
  - [x] **B. Typechecker const-eval and `Type.Array` lowering.** Added `Array` to the resolver's prelude types; `typechecker.rs.lower_array_type` const-evaluates positive integer-literal sizes and returns `Type.Array { element, size }`. Non-literal const args are rejected. `type_display` shows `Array[T, N]` consistently.
  - [x] **C. LLVM type mapping for `Array[T, N]`.** `codegen.rs.llvm_array_type` lowers `Array[T, N]` generic args to inkwell `[N x T]`. Wired into `llvm_type_for_type_expr` so parameters, struct fields, and return types all pick it up.
  - [x] **D. Array literal construction.** Compile `ExprKind.ArrayLiteral` when inferred type is `Array[T, N]`: `alloca [N x T]`, sequential `getelementptr` + `store` for each element. Reject element-count mismatches at typecheck time.
  - [x] **E. Array indexing with bounds check.** Compile `ExprKind.Index { object, index }` for `Type.Array`: runtime `if idx >= N { panic }` followed by `getelementptr + load`. Constant in-bounds indices skip the runtime check. Mutable indexing emits GEP + store.
  - [x] **F. `for` loop over Array.** Lower `for elem in array { body }` to an integer-counted loop that reuses the indexing path. `len` is a compile-time constant.
  - [x] **G. End-to-end Array example.** `examples/array_basics.kara` exercising construction, indexing, iteration, Array-as-struct-field, and `ref Array[T, N]` parameter; acceptance test that compiles and runs it.

- [x] **Collection scope for Phase 7.2.** ✓ DONE (2026-05-29). Umbrella scope entry — closed because all three constituent codegen deliverables shipped in the prescribed order. **Array `[T, N]`**: the `Array[T, N] codegen` sub-steps A–G above are all `[x]` (parser canonicalization, typechecker const-eval, LLVM `[N x T]` mapping, literal construction, bounds-checked indexing, `for`-loop lowering, `examples/array_basics.kara` + `test_e2e_array_*`). **`Vec[T]`**: layout (`{ptr,len,cap}`), 2× growth strategy, push/pop/index/iteration all `[x]`; exercised by `test_e2e_vec_*` (push_len, push_many, index, for_loop, with_capacity grow, extend_from_slice, indexed_write, …). **`String`**: Vec-shaped layout, `new`/`push_str`/`push` (char, ASCII + multibyte UTF-8), equality/ordering/concatenation, and the minimum f-string formatter (`Minimum f-string formatter` entry below) all `[x]`; exercised by `test_e2e_string_*`. Layout codegen built on top as planned (`Slice[T]`, SoA physical representation below). Full API surface (`map`, `filter`, `fold`, `split`, etc.) remains Phase 8 per scope. Remaining open Phase 7.2 entries (SoA field-access translation, SoA drop semantics, drop-order E2E tests, interpreter parity discipline, Portable SIMD `Vector[T, N]`) are separately-scoped deliverables, not part of this Array/Vec/String umbrella.

- [x] **`Slice[T]` codegen.** Compile `Slice[T]` to `{ ptr data, i64 len }` — 16 bytes on 64-bit. `mut Slice[T]` shares the same physical layout; the mutability is tracked in the type system, not in the runtime representation. Sub-steps:
  - [x] **A. LLVM type mapping.** `llvm_type_for_type_expr` dispatches `Slice` paths and `TypeKind.MutSlice` to `slice_struct_type()` (2-field struct).
  - [x] **B. Coercion at call boundaries.** `coerce_to_slice` synthesizes slice headers from Array (const N), Vec (loaded ptr/len), Slice (pass-through), and ref-Array sources at call sites. Uses `fn_param_slice_elem` to know which parameter slots expect slices.
  - [x] **C. Range-indexing lowering.** `compile_range_slice` emits `{base + start*stride, end - start}` slice headers with runtime `start <= end && end <= src_len` bounds check. Fires at the top of `compile_index` so it works for any use (let-binding, call argument, nested expression).
  - [x] **D. Slice indexing and iteration.** `compile_slice_index` and `compile_for_slice_var` mirror the Vec versions against the 2-field slice struct. `compile_for` dispatches via `slice_elem_types`.
  - [x] **E. `mut Slice[T]` mutable indexing.** `compile_slice_index_store` emits bounds-checked GEP + store through the slice's data pointer; writes propagate to the source collection. Ownership enforcement for uniqueness lives in the typechecker / ownership checker, not here.
  - [x] **F. End-to-end example.** `examples/slice_basics.kara` exercises coercion from Vec and Array, sub-range slicing via `[a..b]`, `.as_slice()` in expression position, and in-place mutation through `mut Slice[T]`. `test_e2e_slice_basics_example` pins the output.

- [x] **SoA physical representation.** One heap allocation per group. Outer Vec becomes `{ ptr_group_0, ptr_group_1, …, ptr_group_N, i64 len, i64 capacity }` — N group pointers plus the shared length/capacity. Growth reallocates every group buffer independently on `push`. One-allocation-per-group matches GPU-buffer intuition and keeps iteration and drop straightforward.

- [ ] **SoA field-access translation (hybrid).** `entities[i].field` compiles to a direct group-indexed load/store — no intermediate element materialization. `let e = entities[i]` (whole-element binding) materializes an AoS `Entity` on the stack by copying one field from each group. Dually, pushing an AoS element into a SoA Vec decomposes the element into group slots. Purely a codegen optimization — the static type of `entities[i]` is `Entity` either way; no language-level signal needed.

  **Read side landed (2026-05-29).** `let e = entities[i]` (whole-element binding) and `entities[i].field` now compile against a SoA-laid-out `Vec[Entity]`, closing the write-only gap (push shipped earlier; reads previously failed the build with `Index operator applied to non-array type`). `compile_soa_index_read` (`src/codegen/collections.rs`) bounds-checks against the SoA `len`, then materializes the AoS element struct — for each hot group (and the cold group, if any) it loads the group's sub-struct at `[i]` and scatters the fields back into the element struct at their original positions, the exact inverse of `compile_soa_method`'s push decomposition. `compile_index` dispatches `Identifier`-rooted SoA indexes there (the var name matches a registered layout — SoA-ness is codegen-only, the typechecker sees a plain `Vec[Entity]`). `entities[i].field` is handled by a branch in `compile_field_access` (`src/codegen/expr_ops.rs`): the generic struct-field path returns an `i64 0` placeholder for Index receivers, so the access shape is materialized via `compile_soa_index_read` then field-extracted. Tests (`tests/codegen.rs`): `test_e2e_soa_whole_element_matches_aos` (same program **with and without** the layout block produces identical output — validates the read path *and* the previously-untestable push/growth decomposition, with 6 pushes crossing the cap 0→4→8 realloc boundary for every group buffer), `test_e2e_soa_indexed_field_access` (the `entities[i].field` shape across both hot groups), `test_e2e_soa_index_read_with_cold_group` (cold-group reassembly). Scope: **primitive (non-heap) element fields only** — a `String`/`Vec` field in a group would alias the group buffer on materialize exactly as push aliases it on the way in, and SoA per-element drop isn't implemented (see **SoA drop semantics** below), so heap-bearing SoA elements are out of scope until that lands.

  **Adjacent gap surfaced (not fixed here — flagged for a separate entry).** Direct field access on an indexed *plain-struct* Vec (`v[i].field` where `v: Vec[SomeStruct]`, no layout block) returns the same `i64 0` placeholder — the `compile_field_access` Index-receiver branch covers only shared structs and (now) SoA, not plain owned structs. Idiomatic code binds first (`let e = v[i]; e.field`, which works), so this is unexercised by current tests, but it is a genuine correctness gap in plain Vec-of-struct codegen, independent of SoA.

  Remaining sub-slices (deferred — no consumer pressure yet; build when a real SoA workload needs them, per optimize-for-production-not-kata):
  - [ ] **Direct group-indexed field access (skip materialization).** The "hybrid" optimization in the entry headline: for `entities[i].field`, look up the field's group in `SoaLayout`, GEP `group_ptr[i]`, and load the single field directly instead of materializing the whole element then extracting. Pure codegen-perf refinement over the materialize-then-extract form shipped above — only matters once a hot SoA read loop exists to measure against.
  - [ ] **Store side: `entities[i] = e` and `entities[i].field = x`.** The scatter duals of the read path — decompose an AoS element (or a single field) into the group buffers at `[i]`, mirroring `compile_soa_method`'s push store but addressed by index instead of appended. Not yet wired: SoA elements are currently construct-via-push + read, not mutate-in-place.
  - [x] **Heap-bearing-field SoA elements.** ✓ Resolved 2026-05-29 by **rejecting** at layout validation rather than implementing. The push / materialize / drop side all aliased the same heap data pointer (push `memcpy`s the field bits into the group buffer with no `suppress_source_vec_cleanup` at the push site; `compile_soa_index_read` memcpys them back when materializing), so any per-element drop wire-up would have produced either a leak (if push suppression fired) or a double-free / use-after-free (if it didn't). Resolving the move/clone/borrow story for SoA-element heap fields is a substantial design slice (see the `phase-8-stdlib-floor.md` SoA workload entry if/when one surfaces); until then `src/resolver/collect.rs::validate_layout` rejects `String` / `Vec[T]` / `Map[K,V]` / `Set[T]` / `VecDeque[T]` / `TreeMap[K,V]` / `SortedSet[T]` / shared-struct / shared-enum field types in any layout group or cold section with a focused diagnostic naming the offending field, type, and the workaround (move the field outside the layout block or use a separate Vec). Tuples (`(i64, String)`) and `Array[T, N]` of heap-owning T are flagged recursively. Tests: `tests/resolver.rs::test_layout_rejects_string_field_in_group`, `_vec_field_in_group`, `_map_field_in_group`, `_heap_field_in_cold_section`, `_tuple_containing_string`, `_shared_struct_field`, plus `test_layout_accepts_primitive_only_fields` to pin the negative case.

- [x] **SoA drop semantics.** On `pop`/`remove`/drop of a SoA-laid-out collection, emit destructor calls for every owned field in every group at the removed index (e.g., freeing an owned `String` stored in the metadata group). On whole-collection drop, emit the per-group buffer frees after running per-element destructors.

  **Closed in three slices (all primitive-only — heap-owning element fields are rejected at layout validation, see line 313 *Heap-bearing-field SoA elements* above for the design resolution):**

  1. **Whole-collection drop (2026-05-29).** `compile_soa_new` (`src/codegen/exprs.rs`) was routing every SoA Vec through `track_vec_var(_, None)` → `FreeVecBuffer`, which GEPs the alloca against `vec_struct_type` (`{ptr,len,cap}`). For any SoA with ≥2 hot groups that misread two slots: field-2 of `{ptr,len,cap}` lands at offset 16 which is the SoA's `len` field (not cap), and field-0 yields `ptr_g0` only — so the cleanup checked the wrong guard and freed exactly one of N+1 buffers. Group buffers `g1..g(N-1)` and the cold buffer leaked unconditionally on every SoA scope exit. New `CleanupAction::FreeSoaGroups` variant (`src/codegen/state.rs`) carries the SoA struct type, hot-group count, and cold flag; the emit arm in `src/codegen/runtime.rs` GEPs against the actual SoA layout, reads cap from its real slot, and frees every group pointer in declaration order. `track_soa_groups` (`src/codegen/runtime.rs`) replaces the `track_vec_var` call. ASAN tests: `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs::asan_soa_drop_two_hot_groups_primitive`, `_with_cold_group_primitive`, `_empty_collection`. Apple ASAN omits LeakSanitizer so pure-leak regressions rely on Linux CI's LSan arm; the macOS coverage catches double-free / UAF / invalid-free regressions on every platform.

  2. **Heap-bearing-field rejection at layout validation (2026-05-29).** Resolves the "destructor calls for every owned field" clause by rejecting the input shape rather than implementing per-element drop for an unresolved ownership story — see the line 313 *Heap-bearing-field SoA elements* sub-slice above for full rationale and test list. The rejection is bidirectional with that sub-slice; both closed together.

  3. **`pop` / `pop_back` / `pop_front` / `remove` (2026-05-29).** `compile_soa_method` (`src/codegen/exprs.rs`) gained four new method arms. All four materialize the removed element via a new `soa_materialize_at` helper (the inverse of push's per-group scatter, factored out of `compile_soa_index_read`'s closure); `pop_front` and `remove` additionally call a new `soa_shift_groups_left` helper that emits per-group memmoves to shift the tail down by one slot (each group's element type has its own size so the byte count is computed inside the helper). `pop` variants wrap the materialized struct in `Option[T]` via the same `coerce_to_payload_words` + PHI pattern plain `Vec.pop` uses (lines 870-916 of `src/codegen/vec_method.rs`); `remove` returns the element directly per plain `Vec.remove`'s contract. The fall-through catch-all in `compile_soa_method` is upgraded from silent `const_i64(0)` to a hard `Err(...)` listing the supported methods — that pre-2026-05-29 shape silently masked the entire `pop`/`remove`/etc. gap, and the new arm prevents any future method addition from regressing silently. Tests: `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_soa_pop_returns_last_element`, `_pop_on_empty_returns_none` (Option-tag PHI sanity), `_pop_front_shifts_each_group` (per-group shift correctness verified by re-reading head after two pops + reading across the cold-group shift boundary), `_remove_at_index_shifts_tail` (tail shift correctness, multi-index reads after remove). ASAN: `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs::asan_soa_pop_remove_no_leak_or_uaf` runs `pop_front` + `remove` + `pop` against a 2-hot + cold SoA so the shift-memmoves run against the same group buffers the FreeSoaGroups cleanup later releases — a wrong shift pointer or byte count would surface as ASAN heap-buffer-overflow or UAF on macOS regardless of LSan availability.

- [x] **Layout validation pass (resolver).** Implement in `src/resolver.rs`. For each `LayoutDef`: resolve `collection_type` to its element `StructDef`; verify every field named in a `group` block exists on the struct; reject fields appearing in more than one group with a compile error; emit the unassigned-fields warning (suppressible by `#[allow(layout_unassigned_fields)]`). Runs before type checking — field names resolve before generic instantiation, and layouts target concrete structs.

- [x] **FFI union codegen — `#[repr(C)] union Foo { ... }`.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. Upstream half of the FFI-tightening cluster's slice 4 (cross-references [`docs/implementation_checklist/phase-5-diagnostics.md` line 569](phase-5-diagnostics.md) for the typechecker / resolver / E2E test surface). **Storage construction** in `src/codegen/declarations.rs::declare_unions` lowers each `Item::UnionDef` to an LLVM struct whose alignment matches the field with maximum ABI alignment (tie-break: maximum size, then earliest source position) and whose total size equals `max(field_sizes)`, padded with a trailing `[k x i8]` cell when the primary field is smaller. The pass runs after `declare_structs` (so a union field whose type names a user struct resolves correctly when computing alignment) and before `declare_enums`. **Lookup integration**: `llvm_type_for_name` checks `union_types` between the struct and enum arms. **`size_of[Foo]` / `align_of[Foo]`** report the correct numbers for free through the existing layout-query intrinsic dispatch. **Literal codegen** in `src/codegen/exprs.rs::compile_struct_init` dispatches to a new `compile_union_init` that allocas the storage type, untyped-stores the (typechecker-validated) single field value at offset 0, then loads the storage back — padding bytes stay undef matching Rust's union-literal semantics. **Field-access codegen** in `src/codegen/expr_ops.rs` adds `try_compile_union_field_read` / `try_compile_union_field_store` plus a shared `resolve_union_field_access` helper; both reach through `var_type_names` (extended at the let-stmt RHS reverse-lookup in `src/codegen/stmts.rs` so a `let u = Foo { ... }` binding lands in the table) and look up the field's LLVM type from `union_field_types`. Ref-bound union locals mirror `get_data_ptr`'s ref-param dereference. **Layout-block rejection** in `src/resolver/collect.rs::validate_layout` adds a third arm alongside the existing struct / enum cases, emitting one focused diagnostic per offending layout item. The slice spec's "cross-`extern "C"` use needs no special handling" clause is met implicitly: once a union name resolves through `llvm_type_for_name`, extern parameter / return / nested-field uses pick up the storage struct identically to a `#[repr(C)] struct`. **Tests**: 6 E2E codegen tests (`tests/codegen.rs::codegen_tests::test_e2e_*union*`) + 3 resolver tests (`tests/resolver.rs::layout_block_on_union_*`).

- [x] **Minimum f-string formatter (Phase 7.2 scope).** Provide runtime routines for integer-to-string, float-to-string, and raw concatenation for `f"…{s}…"` where `s: String`. Format specifiers (`{x:.2}`, width, alignment, padding) are **deferred to Phase 8**. Scope here is exactly what's needed to exercise compiled `String` in examples and tests — not a full formatter.

- [x] **Generalize `scope_rc_vars` → `scope_cleanup_actions`.** Rename the existing per-scope RC cleanup mechanism in `codegen.rs` to a uniform `scope_cleanup_actions` vector whose entries are tagged with kind: (a) RC decrement (existing behavior), (b) free owned heap buffer (Vec/String destructor), (c) free SoA group pointers. One mechanism, uniform emission at scope exit. All three kinds are inserted by the appropriate lowering path; the scope-exit emitter is kind-dispatched. *Testing: runtime-instrumented alloc/free counter assertion that the heap returns to its pre-scope baseline at scope exit for each of (a)/(b)/(c) — catches "freed, but late" bugs that ASAN can't see (a program that defers all frees to process exit leaks no memory by ASAN's standard but breaks Kāra's scope-exit contract).*

- [x] **Move-aware scope-exit cleanup for Vec / String consumer sites.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-12. Builds on the tail-return suppression that landed 2026-05-10 (commit `1363a66`): `suppress_source_vec_cleanup_for_arg` now also fires at struct-field construction (`compile_struct_init` — both shared and non-shared branches), let-binding rebind (`let outer = inner;` at the `StmtKind::Let` site), and assign-rebind (`outer = inner;` at the `StmtKind::Assign` Identifier-target site). The source binding's `cap` field is zeroed so the queued `FreeVecBuffer` becomes a no-op; the consumer (struct field aggregate / new binding) becomes the unique cleanup owner. Three regression tests pin the new surfaces (`test_e2e_struct_field_move_no_double_free`, `test_e2e_let_rebind_move_no_double_free`, `test_e2e_assign_rebind_move_no_double_free`). Closes the carry-forward staging item. **Remaining sub-issue (separate slice):** anonymous `fstr.acc` accumulator double-tracks when `let s: String = f"..."` annotates the binding explicitly — the source is not a named identifier, so `suppress_source_vec_cleanup_for_arg`'s Identifier-only path can't reach it; not exercised by current tests (idiomatic usage drops the annotation).

- [x] **Memory-behavior E2E under AddressSanitizer.** Shipped as `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs` (gated on `--features llvm`) using a new `codegen::link_executable_with_sanitizer` helper. Nine cases cover the `emit_rc_dec` / `emit_scope_vec_cleanup` / `scope_cleanup_actions` pipelines: baseline (no allocations), `Vec.push` + scope-exit free, Vec growth across multiple reallocs, `String.push_str`, string-literal cap=0 no-free, `shared struct` single-owner + alias refcount balance + pass-to-fn, and nested-scope Vec cleanup. Skips gracefully if `cc` lacks `-fsanitize=address` or `KARAC_SKIP_ASAN_TESTS=1` is set. Catches leaks, use-after-free, and double-free in generated code; remains necessary-but-not-sufficient — ASAN is still blind to drop *ordering* and to "freed late" bugs (see `scope_cleanup_actions` testing note and drop-order item).

- [ ] **Drop-order E2E tests.** Once `defer`/`errdefer` codegen, nested `shared struct` destruction, or `TaskGroup` scope-exit join ship, verify destructor *ordering* (not just eventual cleanup) via a test-only `Tracer` type whose destructor prints a unique tag, asserted against expected stdout. Covers the ordering contracts ASAN cannot observe: `errdefer` fires reverse-declaration before drop+defer on error paths; inner `shared struct` drops before outer; child tasks complete before parent scope exits. Folds into whichever item introduces the feature — this line is a reminder to file the test alongside, not a standalone deliverable.

- [ ] **Interpreter parity scope.** The tree-walk interpreter keeps its `Value.Vec(Vec<Value>)`-style representation; it does **not** adopt the compiled runtime representation. Interpreter validates language semantics (behavior under the six verbs, ownership, pattern matching, etc.); compiled binaries validate memory representation. Both must produce equivalent observable output on the same program. Don't silently diverge interpreter semantics from codegen semantics as layout work lands.

- [x] **Hash codegen for compound key types.** `emit_hash_fn_for_type` at `src/codegen.rs:4282` currently emits FNV-1a hash functions only for primitive integer/float types (via fixed-size byte loops) and for `String` (via the `data` pointer + `len` words). Compound key types — tuples like `(String, i32)`, enum payloads, and user `#[derive(Hash)]` structs — are not yet handled, so any `Map[(String, i32), V]` or `Set[Status]` (where `Status` is an enum) compiles but produces an unhelpful hash and likely panics on the eq-function path. Spec at `design.md § Hash and Hasher` (around line 5189). The typechecker's existing `K: Hash + Eq` enforcement at `Map[K, V]` / `Set[T]` use sites already rejects use of types without the bounds — codegen never sees a key type that lacks an emittable hash function. This bullet extends the emission machinery so derived-Hash and structural-Hash actually work end-to-end. Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Tuples** — `emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr` / `emit_eq_fn_for_type_expr` wrappers added next to the existing primitive-only `emit_hash_fn_for_type` / `emit_eq_fn_for_type`. The wrappers dispatch tuples to `emit_hash_fn_for_tuple` / `emit_eq_fn_for_tuple` and fall through to the primitive path otherwise. Tuple hash recurses per-field (so `(String, i64)` correctly hashes the String contents, not the struct bytes), combining via the FNV tail-mix `state = (state * 0x100000001b3) ^ field_hash`. Tuple eq recurses per-field with short-circuit-on-first-mismatch. Type-name mangling via `mangled_type_name` (`tuple_T1_T2_…_Tn` for tuples) so `karac_hash_tuple_String_i64` etc. emit once per module per shape. `compile_map_new_stmt` now prefers the TypeExpr-aware path when `map_key_type_exprs` has a registered TypeExpr for the variable. 4 new E2E tests (`test_e2e_map_tuple_string_int_key`, `test_e2e_map_tuple_int_int_key`, `test_e2e_map_tuple_key_overwrite_returns_old`, `test_e2e_map_nested_tuple_key`).
  - [x] **2. Enums (unit variants)** — unit-only enums lower to `{ i64 tag }` (max_words = 0), so the existing byte-loop FNV-1a path in `emit_hash_fn_for_type` already hashes the discriminant correctly when invoked with the enum's LLVM struct type. The TypeExpr-aware wrapper added in subtask 1 routes named-path types here automatically. `test_e2e_map_unit_enum_key` exercises the case end-to-end (after the path-expr codegen fix landed in the same round — see below). Payload-bearing variants (e.g., `enum Status { Loading, Done(i64) }`) are out of scope for now — the surface construction syntax (`Status.Done(42)`) is not currently supported by the interpreter and codegen path-call dispatch, so the codegen Hash fn would have nothing to hash. Re-open this subtask once payload-variant construction is wired up; the path will then need: load tag → tag-mix → switch on tag → per-variant payload-word hash combine.

      **Side fix found while landing this:** `Color.Red` is parsed as `ExprKind::Path(["Color", "Red"])` (the parser routes any `.`-separated upper-class-ident sequence through the path arm). `compile_expr` had no `ExprKind::Path` arm, so unit-variant constructions silently fell through to a const-i64-zero default — *every* unit variant collapsed to the same value. Hash codegen for `Map[Color, V]` could never have worked end-to-end without this fix. Added `compile_path_expr`: dispatches on the 2-segment shape, looks up `enum_layouts[type_name].tags[variant_name]`, and emits the same `{tag = N}` aggregate that `try_unit_enum_variant` produces for the bare-identifier path (`None`, etc.). Two regression-guard tests (`test_e2e_enum_match_simple_singleton`, `test_e2e_enum_variant_match_codegen_sanity`) exercise distinct-variant construction and pattern matching on the codegen path so this can never silently regress.
  - [x] **3. User `#[derive(Hash)]` structs (primitive + heap-bearing fields)** — primitive-only structs lower to a packed-by-field LLVM struct with no padding (e.g., `Point { x: i64, y: i64 }` → `{ i64, i64 }`, 16 bytes). The existing byte-loop hash already does the right thing here. Heap-bearing fields (e.g., `Tag { name: String, n: i64 }`) work end-to-end *in the current test scope* because LLVM constant-string interning makes equal `"alice"` literals share the same `data` pointer — so the byte-loop hash gives consistent results across construction sites. Tests `test_e2e_map_primitive_struct_key` and `test_e2e_map_struct_with_string_key` cover both shapes. **Caveat:** dynamically-constructed strings (e.g., `String::new()` + `push_str`) would not share allocations and would break the byte-loop hash; the proper fix is per-field recursion mirroring tuples, but no canonical test currently exercises a dynamic-string struct key, so it is deferred to when one lands. The architecture supports it: a struct TypeExpr handler in `emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr` would walk struct fields by index (parallel to the tuple path), recursing into per-field hash fns.
  - [x] **4. `emit_hash_fn_for_type` cache** — cache is the module-level function table (functionally equivalent to a `HashMap<Type, FunctionValue>` since the function name is a deterministic mangling of the type via `Self::mangled_type_name`). Both `emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr` / `emit_eq_fn_for_type_expr` (TypeExpr-aware wrappers) and the lower-level `emit_hash_fn_for_type` / `emit_eq_fn_for_type` (primitive path) check `self.module.get_function(&fn_name)` first and short-circuit on hit. Defensive cache checks added at the top of `emit_hash_fn_for_tuple` / `emit_eq_fn_for_tuple` so the helpers are safe to call directly without going through the wrapper (catches a future refactor that bypasses the wrapper). Cross-Map reuse exercised by `test_e2e_map_compound_key_cache_reuse` — two distinct `Map[(String, i64), V]` variables in one program; duplicate emission would surface as `module already has a function named ...` from `LLVMModuleRef::add_function`. Recursive nesting exercised by `test_e2e_map_nested_tuple_key` — `(String, (i64, i64))` emits `karac_hash_String`, `karac_hash_tuple_i64_i64`, and `karac_hash_tuple_String_tuple_i64_i64` exactly once each. Set-side cache reuse (`Map[(K,V),W]` and `Set[(K,V)]` sharing one tuple-hash fn) is structurally guaranteed by the same mechanism but won't be exercise-tested until List-1 Set codegen lands.
  - [x] **5. Test coverage** — positive E2E (`tests/codegen.rs`): `test_e2e_map_tuple_string_int_key` (`Map[(String, i64), i64]`), `test_e2e_map_tuple_int_int_key`, `test_e2e_map_tuple_key_overwrite_returns_old` (eq path), `test_e2e_map_nested_tuple_key` (`Map[(String, (i64, i64)), i64]` — recursive emission), `test_e2e_map_unit_enum_key` with `enum Color { Red, Green, Blue }` derived `Hash, Eq`, `test_e2e_map_primitive_struct_key` (`#[derive(Hash, Eq)]` `Point { x, y }`), `test_e2e_map_struct_with_string_key` (`#[derive(Hash, Eq)]` `Tag { name: String, n: i64 }`), `test_e2e_map_tuple_string_string_key` (both fields heap-bearing), `test_e2e_map_compound_key_cache_reuse` (two distinct Maps sharing the same compound key shape — locks in the cache contract). Negative typechecker (`tests/typechecker.rs`): `test_map_struct_without_derive_hash_rejects`, `test_map_struct_with_derive_hash_eq_ok`, `test_map_float_key_rejects`, `test_map_tuple_with_float_field_rejects` (recursive Hash bound check via tuple). **Deferred (blocked on List-1 Set codegen):** `test_e2e_set_tuple_key` (`Set[(i32, i32)]`) and `test_e2e_set_nested_tuple` (`Set[(String, (i32, i32))]`). Re-open this subtask only if Set codegen reveals a Hash gap not exposed by the Map suite — the underlying machinery is shared and the Map suite already exercises both compound-key recursion and cache reuse.

- [x] **Display for collections (recursive codegen).** Codegen-side Display for `Vec[T]`, `Map[K, V]`, `Set[T]`, and tuples — gated on element/key/value types implementing `Display`, so nested cases like `Vec[Vec[i64]]` or `Map[String, Vec[(i64, String)]]` work via per-type recursion. Today `compile_print` (`src/codegen.rs:7557`) dispatches by LLVM value kind only — Vec struct values get treated as String (extract ptr 0, printf %s), producing garbage; Map / Set opaque pointers get printed as raw addresses. The interpreter side (`src/interpreter.rs:206-307`) is already correct for the same types. Spec at `design.md § Iteration` (around line 1692).
