Split out from the closed `Map codegen gap closure` umbrella because recursive codegen is its own scope. `SortedSet[T]`, `TreeMap[K, V]`, `VecDeque[T]` Display lands when those types' codegen ships. Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Per-type Display function emission machinery** — `emit_display_fn_for_type(type_name, ty) -> FunctionValue` added in `src/codegen.rs` with `display_fn_cache: HashMap<String, FunctionValue>`. Pattern parallels `emit_hash_fn_for_type` / `emit_eq_fn_for_type`. Function signature is uniform `void karac_display_<type_name>(ptr)` so callers don't need per-type calling conventions. Cache lookup + module lookup before emit so each type emits at most once per module. `#[allow(dead_code)]` annotation present until subtask 7 wires the dispatch — flip when subtask 7 lands. Commit `8123a8e`.
  - [x] **2. Primitive Display fns** — primitive cases implemented in `emit_display_fn_for_type`: `i8`/`i16`/`i32`/`i64`/`isize` sign-extend to i64 + `printf("%lld")`; `u8`/`u16`/`u32`/`u64`/`usize` zero-extend + `printf("%llu")`; `f32` widens to f64; `f64` uses `printf("%g")`; `bool` selects `"true"`/`"false"` static strings; `char` uses `printf("%c")` (ASCII; UTF-8 refinement deferred); `String`/`str` extracts data ptr + len fields and uses `printf("%.*s", len, ptr)` to handle non-NUL-terminated strings. Compound types panic with "not yet supported"; subtasks 3-6 extend the match. Commit `8123a8e`.
  - [x] **3. `Vec[T]` Display fn** — `Vec_*` arm in `emit_display_fn_for_type` dispatches to a new `emit_vec_display_body` helper that loads `data`/`len` from the 24-byte Vec struct, prints `"["`, walks elements with `", "` separators, and per-iteration GEPs `data + i * sizeof(T)` (i8 stride) before recursing into `emit_display_fn_for_type(T)`. Element-name → `BasicTypeEnum` resolution goes through a new `resolve_ty_for_display_name` helper covering primitives + nested `Vec_*` (Map/Set/Tuple to be added in subtasks 4-6). Nested cases like `Vec[Vec[i64]]` work via the recursive call landing on the inner `Vec_i64` Display fn. `#[allow(dead_code)]` retained on both helpers until subtask 7 wires `compile_print`. Round commit pending.
  - [x] **4. `Map[K, V]` Display fn** — typed entry point `emit_map_display_fn(key_name, key_ty, val_name, val_ty)` added (Map's two type parameters can't round-trip through a single mangled name string, so the recovery-by-string-split pattern Vec uses doesn't compose; the catch-all `Map_*` arm in `emit_display_fn_for_type` panics with a "use the typed entry point" message). Body factored into `emit_map_display_body`: prints `"{"`, loads handle from the slot, drives `karac_map_iter_new` / `karac_map_iter_next` (mirroring `compile_for_map_var` at `src/codegen.rs:8038`), tracks first-pair via an `is_first` i1 alloca (no scalar counter like Vec's `i == 0`), per-iteration recurses into `emit_display_fn_for_type` for K and V with `": "` between key/value and `", "` between pairs, frees the iterator in the exit block, prints `"}"`. `resolve_ty_for_display_name` extended with `Map_*` → `ptr_ty` (the map slot is a `ptr` to the opaque handle). `#[allow(dead_code)]` retained until subtask 7 wires `compile_print`. Iteration order is unspecified per `design.md` line 1588 — tests must not assert order.
  - [x] **5. `Set[T]` Display fn** — typed entry `emit_set_display_fn(elem_te)` mirrors `emit_map_display_fn` minus the value-side Display. Cache key `Set_<elem_mangled>`; the catch-all `Set_*` arm in `emit_display_fn_for_type` panics on cache miss steering callers to the typed entry point. Body loads the opaque set/map handle, prints `Set{`, drives `karac_map_iter_*` per element with the value out-slot replaced by a single shared `i8` alloca (Set lowers to `Map[T, ()]` so the runtime stores zero bytes — content discarded), recurses via `emit_display_fn_for_type_expr` for each element, prints `}`. Format `Set{a, b, c}` matches the interpreter's `Display for Value::Set` at `src/interpreter.rs:292`. Iteration order is unspecified — tests assert on single-entry sets only.
  - [x] **6. Tuple Display fn** — typed entry `emit_tuple_display_fn(elems: &[TypeExpr])` added next to `emit_map_display_fn`. Cache key is the `mangled_type_name`-derived `tuple_T1_T2_..._Tn` shared with the generic `display_fn_cache`; the catch-all `tuple_*` arm in `emit_display_fn_for_type` panics on cache miss steering callers to the typed entry point (parallel to the `Map_*` panic redirect). Body GEPs each field through the tuple's LLVM struct type, recurses into per-field Display via the new TypeExpr-aware dispatcher (subtask 7) so nested compound shapes (`((i64, i64), String)`, `(String, Vec[i64])`) compose correctly. Format `(field0, field1, ...)` matches the interpreter at `src/interpreter.rs:215`.
  - [x] **7. `compile_print` integration** — landed alongside a refactor that introduces `emit_display_fn_for_type_expr(te)` as the canonical TypeExpr-aware dispatcher. `compile_print` recognizes bare-identifier args (`ExprKind::Identifier`) whose surface type registers in the side-tables: Vec — both `vec_elem_types[var]` and `var_elem_type_exprs[var]` set (`vec_elem_types` alone holds for String); Map — both `map_key_type_exprs[var]` and `var_elem_type_exprs[var]` (which is overloaded as the Map-value `TypeExpr`); Set — `set_elem_type_exprs[var]`. Vec dispatch goes through `emit_vec_display_fn_te(elem_te)`, Map through `emit_map_display_fn(key_te, val_te)`, Set through `emit_set_display_fn(elem_te)`. Trailing `\n` is conditionally emitted for `println`. Non-identifier and non-collection args keep the existing `is_int_value` / `is_struct_value` / `is_pointer_value` / `is_float_value` fallbacks. Same refactor: `emit_vec_display_body` / `emit_map_display_fn` / `emit_map_display_body` signatures changed from `(name, ty)` pairs to `TypeExpr`s — recursion now flows via the dispatcher; the `Vec_*` / `Map_*` / `Set_*` / `tuple_*` arms in `emit_display_fn_for_type` were converted to panic redirects with the TypeExpr-API guidance; the now-dead `resolve_ty_for_display_name` helper was deleted; `display_mangle_te` (deeper than `mangled_type_name`, walks generic args) provides the cache-key mangling.
  - [x] **8. Test coverage** — 13 codegen E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs` (search `test_e2e_display_`): Vec — `vec_i64`, `vec_empty`, `vec_string`, `vec_nested` (`Vec[Vec[i64]]`); Map — `map_string_i64_singleton`, `map_i64_i64_singleton`, `map_empty`, `map_with_vec_value_singleton` (`Map[String, Vec[i64]]`); Tuple — `vec_tuple_i64_i64` (Vec of tuple via `Map.entries()`), `vec_tuple_i64_string` (heap-bearing tuple field); Set — `set_i64_singleton`, `set_string_singleton`, `set_empty`. Multi-entry Map / Set output is order-dependent (runtime walks bucket array) — `design.md` line 1588 declares iteration order unspecified — so all multi-entry tests use single entries; multi-entry coverage lives on the interpreter side where iteration is over an ordered Vec.

- [x] **For-loop bindings don't propagate Vec/String/Slice element type for method dispatch.** ✓ DONE (2026-05-04). The original write-up suggested threading a `bound_elem_type` enum through `bind_pattern`, but the existing side-table architecture already encodes the same information per-variable (`vec_elem_types`, `slice_elem_types`, `map_*_types`) — the missing piece was a `TypeExpr` companion table so for-loop bindings can re-derive their registrations from the source's element type. Implementation:
  - [x] **1. Element-`TypeExpr` side-tables.** Added `var_elem_type_exprs: HashMap<String, TypeExpr>` (element of Vec/Slice, value-side of Map) and `map_key_type_exprs` (key-side of Map). Necessary because LLVM types alone can't disambiguate `Vec[String]` from `Vec[Vec[T]]` (both store `vec_struct_type` as the element LLVM type) — the bound name's registration at iteration time needs to know which.
  - [x] **2. Populate at let / param sites.** Extended the let-statement site and the function-parameter site to fill the new tables alongside the existing `vec_elem_types` / `slice_elem_types` / `map_*_types` registrations. Param-site also gained the previously-missing Map-by-value handling so `fn iter_map(m: Map[K, V]) { for (k, v) in m {...} }` works.
  - [x] **3. `register_var_from_type_expr` helper.** New `&mut self` method that, given a variable name and `TypeExpr`, registers all the appropriate side-tables — extracted so the for-loop site can re-use the same logic the let-site uses without duplication.
  - [x] **4. `register_for_loop_bindings` + wiring at three for-loop sites.** New helper called immediately after `bind_pattern` in `compile_for_vec_var`, `compile_for_slice_var`, and `compile_for_map_var`. Handles `PatternKind::Binding(name)` (single binding gets the element TypeExpr) and `PatternKind::Tuple` of length 2 (Map iteration's `(k, v)` — each side gets its respective TypeExpr). `compile_for_array_var` would need its caller to thread the source var name through; deferred (no canonical test exercises array iteration with a heap-bearing element type).
  - [x] **5. Test coverage.** Added the four bullet-named tests in `tests/codegen.rs`: `test_e2e_for_in_vec_string_calls_len`, `test_e2e_for_in_vec_vec_inner_push`, `test_e2e_for_in_map_string_keys_use_len`, `test_e2e_for_in_slice_string_calls_len`. All four asserted `["0", "0"]` (silent fall-through) before the fix; all assert correct element-method results after. Also updated the comment in `test_e2e_map_keys_string_keys_len` (which previously documented the bug as a known limitation).
  - [x] **6. Interpreter parity.** Verified the tree-walk interpreter doesn't have the bug — it dispatches off runtime-tagged `Value::String` / `Value::Vec` / etc. variants which carry the type at runtime, so for-loop bindings already route correctly. Added `test_for_in_vec_string_calls_len_interp` in `tests/interpreter.rs` as a regression guard.
  - [x] **7. Tuple / struct / enum-variant pattern recursion.** Subtask 3 of the original write-up asked for recursive destructuring (e.g. `for (a, b) in vec_of_tuples`). Deferred — no canonical test exercises this. The architecture supports adding it later by extending `register_for_loop_bindings`'s `Tuple` arm.

- [x] **Compound-payload enum codegen (Slice F predecessor).** `coerce_to_i64` (`src/codegen.rs:12118-12131`) explicitly returns `i64.const_int(0)` for any payload value that doesn't fit a single i64 word — the catch-all at line 12131 silently zeroes multi-field aggregate payloads. As a result, `enum E { V(String) }` / `enum E { V(Vec[T]) }` / `enum E { V(SomeStruct) }` constructions silently round-trip as zero bytes, and pattern-match destructure produces uninitialized aggregates because there's no single-i64 word that reconstructs the 3-word String/Vec aggregate. The gap is masked today by the absence of e2e tests for the existing `IoError.Other(String)` placeholder variant (verified via `grep -rn 'IoError.Other' tests/`: zero hits). Surfaced 2026-05-08 during the [`std.json`](phase-8-stdlib-floor.md) Slice F delegation when `Json.String(String)` / `Json.Array(Vec[Json])` / `Json.Object(Vec[(String, Json)])` round-trips were expected to work but produced zero bytes; Slice F was demoted to staging awaiting this predecessor.

- [x] **Compound-payload enum follow-up: pattern-bound element-type registration.** Closes the gap surfaced by CP slice's *Out of scope, still open* (line 380 above): direct method dispatch on a pattern-bound `Vec[T]` / `String` / `Slice[T]` payload (e.g. `xs.len()` where `xs` is the binding for a `V(Vec[i64])` payload) currently routes through a generic fallback that doesn't know the payload's parameterized inner type. The CP slice's own test 2 (`test_compound_enum_vec_payload_round_trip`) had to route the bound `xs` through a `ref Vec[i64]` function parameter (`fn use_vec(xs: ref Vec[i64]) { ... xs.len() ... }`) instead of calling `xs.len()` directly on the bound name — function-arg routing is the work-around because `pattern_binding_types`'s `HashMap<SpanKey, String>` value carries only the canonical type *name* (`"Vec"`), not the parameterized inner type (`Vec[i64]`'s element). The codegen-side `vec_elem_types` / `slice_elem_types` registries need the LLVM element type to drive method-dispatch routing through `compile_method_call`'s Vec/Slice arms; without it, `.len()` / `.is_empty()` / index-read / `.push()` on a pattern binding all silently fall through to the generic path and either produce wrong codegen or fail with cryptic diagnostics.

- [x] **Compound-payload enum follow-up: drop-path `track_enum_var` + `emit_enum_drop_switch` implementation.** Closes the second half of CP slice's *Out of scope, still open* (line 380): the original CP plan's sub-step (f) — drop / scope-exit reinterpretation — was scoped to the narrow case the regression gate requires. v1 ships move-only correctness via the existing String/Vec scope cleanup on extracted bindings (constructed enum binding in scope ⇒ payload's source binding is in `Moved` state, no double-free); broader drop coverage requires variant-conditional destructor invocation at scope exit (tag-switch, per-variant payload-word reinterpretation, heap-bearing field cleanup). Without this, an enum binding that goes out of scope without being moved into a downstream consumer leaks its heap-bearing payload (e.g., `let _ = Status.Done(make_string());` followed by scope exit leaks the `String`'s data buffer). The CP slice's "Out of scope, still open" calls out the full implementation as Phase 7.2's binary-size + GC-style cleanup territory; this slice is that work.

- [x] **HTTP handler ABI trampoline (`Server.serve(handler)` end-to-end).** ✓ Landed 2026-05-09 (commit `5f4cbcc`). Per-handler `extern "C"` shim adapts hyper's FFI signature to the user value-typed `fn(Request) -> Response`; `Request` lowers as opaque pointer; `Request.path()` / `.method()` round-trip through runtime externs returning fresh owned Strings; shim cached per-handler-fn. Smoke test un-ignored.

  *Settled design forks (2026-05-09).*
  - **F1 — Handler panic semantics.** Shim does nothing special. Kāra's `emit_panic` (`src/codegen.rs:2164`) is `printf + exit(1)` — no unwinding — so handler panics terminate the server process. The runtime's existing `catch_unwind` at `runtime/src/lib.rs:2127` catches Rust-side panics from runtime helpers but cannot intercept Kāra's `exit(1)` path. Recovery requires `std.panic` (referenced as future work at `src/codegen.rs:559`); not in this slice's scope. Document the v1 limitation in `Server.serve`'s doc comment.
  - **F2 — `Request` value shape.** Lower `Request` to an opaque heap pointer — same precedent as `Map[K, V]` (`runtime/stdlib/map.kara:10` is `struct Map[K, V] { }`, codegen treats it as opaque ptr). Methods lazy-FFI to existing runtime externs (`karac_runtime_http_request_path` at `runtime/src/lib.rs:1828`, `_method` at line 1845) and copy bytes into a fresh Kāra `String` per call. Re-allocates per call — fine for v1's `GET /dashboard/:id` shape. Shim collapses to ~30 lines (packs `req_ptr` into the opaque Request, calls user fn, decomposes returned `Response`). Eager-copy and borrow-from-shim alternatives rejected: opaque-ptr mirrors existing precedent and keeps the shim trivial.
  - **F3 — `Request` method surface.** Ship `path()` + `method()` only. Both runtime externs already in place. `body()`, `query()`, `header()`, `headers()` deferred — additive when a real consumer needs them; none blocks the demo.

  *Out of scope (deferred to follow-ups).*
  - Closures-with-captures handlers — `E_CLOSURE_AS_FN_PTR_NOT_YET` keeps firing at `src/codegen.rs:17383`. Closure `{fn_ptr, env_ptr}` ABI doesn't fit a single-ptr slot regardless of trampoline approach.
  - `Server.serve(addr, handler)` 2-arg form. ✓ Closed 2026-05-12. Addr lifts to the user surface; codegen mirrors `serve_static`'s `String → null-terminated C string` packing pattern.
  - Per-request `headers` round-trip — v1 hardcodes `content-type: application/json` (`runtime/src/lib.rs:2187`).
  - Structured panic recovery on the handler path — gated on `std.panic` (separate Phase 8 item).

- [x] **Codegen `Index store on non-array type` for `Vec[T]` indexed writes.** ✓ Landed (tracker bookkeeping flip 2026-05-29 — implementation shipped earlier; entry stayed `[ ]` until verified during a tracker walk). `compile_vec_index_store` (`src/codegen/collections.rs:1283`) was added per the slice plan below, mirroring `compile_vec_index`'s shape and routed from a new `Identifier`-keyed dispatch arm at the top of `compile_index_store`. Bounds-check uses `len` (not `cap`) so `v[len]` panics rather than silently writing into reserved capacity. All five planned tests live in `tests/codegen.rs`: `test_e2e_vec_indexed_write_basic` (round-trip through both write and read), `test_e2e_vec_indexed_write_oob_panics` (panic message matches the read-path's `"vec index out of bounds"`), `test_e2e_vec_indexed_write_after_push` (write path reads `len`, not initial cap), `test_e2e_vec_indexed_write_through_mut_ref_param` (`mut ref Vec[T]` parameter shape via `get_data_ptr`), `test_e2e_vec_indexed_write_string_element` (element-type-agnostic store for heap-bearing element types). Original deferred concern about overwrite-drop semantics for heap-bearing elements (a `v[i] = new_string` leaks the prior `String`) remains pre-existing behavior shared with Array indexed writes — documented in the *Out of scope* section below.

  Original entry (kept for the historical slice plan + out-of-scope notes the close-out references):

  `compile_index_store` (`src/codegen.rs:11675`) bails for every receiver shape that isn't `BasicTypeEnum::ArrayType` with `Err("Index store on non-array type".to_string())` (line 11740). Slice and Map writes already route through dedicated paths at the top of the function (lines 11685-11698); **Vec writes have no equivalent dispatch**, so `vec[i] = val` for `Vec[T]` fails codegen even though indexed *reads* on Vec already work via `compile_vec_index` (`src/codegen.rs:11499-11556`). Surfaced 2026-05-09 by the LeetCode 3629 kata while scaffolding `bfs_sieve.kara`. Also blocks the bottom-up section of `examples/leetcode/coin_change.kara`.

  *Slice plan (drafted 2026-05-09) — Codegen Vec[T] indexed write.*

  Add a `Vec[T]` dispatch in `compile_index_store` mirroring the existing `compile_vec_index` read-path's shape: keyed by `self.vec_elem_types.contains_key(name.as_str())`, route to a new `compile_vec_index_store` helper that loads `len`, bounds-checks against `len` (not `cap`), GEPs `data[i]` and stores. **No design forks** — the read-path's machinery (`get_data_ptr`, `vec_elem_type_for_var`, `vec_struct_type`, `emit_panic`) is the established pattern; the write-path is a structural mirror.

  *Sub-steps.*
  - **(a)** Codegen: add a new dispatch arm at the top of `compile_index_store` (sibling to the existing slice/map dispatches at `src/codegen.rs:11685-11698`):
    ```rust
    if let ExprKind::Identifier(name) = &object.kind {
        if self.vec_elem_types.contains_key(name.as_str()) {
            return self.compile_vec_index_store(name, index, val);
        }
    }
    ```
    Insert immediately after the Map dispatch and before the alloca-fast-path code (~5 lines).
  - **(b)** Codegen: add `compile_vec_index_store(&mut self, name: &str, index: &Expr, val: BasicValueEnum<'ctx>) -> Result<(), String>` helper as a sibling of `compile_vec_index` (`src/codegen.rs:11499`). Body mirrors the read-path verbatim through the bounds-check, then GEPs `data[i]` and emits `build_store(elem_ptr, val)` instead of `build_load`. Reuse `get_data_ptr(name)` for the struct-base pointer (handles both owned Vec and `ref Vec[T]` parameter shapes), `vec_elem_type_for_var(name)` for the element LLVM type, `vec_struct_type()` for the `{ptr, len, cap}` layout, and `emit_panic("vec index out of bounds")` for the OOB diagnostic (matching the existing read-path's panic message). Bounds-check uses `len` (field index 1), NOT `cap` — overwriting at index `i ∈ [len, cap)` is bounds-error per spec, even though the underlying allocation has room. ~50 lines.
  - **(c)** Verify the OOB-write panic message string matches (or is intentionally distinct from) the read-path's `"vec index out of bounds"` — recommend keeping them identical so users see one stable diagnostic regardless of read-vs-write.
  - **(d)** Tests under `// ── Vec indexed write ──` in `tests/codegen.rs`:
    1. `test_vec_index_store_basic` — `let mut v = Vec.filled(4, 0i64); v[2] = 99; assert_eq!(v[2], 99);` (round-trip through both write and read paths).
    2. `test_vec_index_store_oob_panics` — `let mut v = Vec.filled(2, 0i64); v[5] = 99;` exits non-zero with stderr matching `vec index out of bounds`.
    3. `test_vec_index_store_after_push` — `let mut v: Vec[i64] = Vec.new(); v.push(0); v.push(0); v[1] = 42;` then read-back → 42. Pins that the write path correctly reads `len` (post-push) rather than the initial cap.
    4. `test_vec_index_store_through_ref_param` — function `fn write_at(mut v: ref Vec[i64], i: i64, val: i64) { v[i] = val; }` writes through a `mut ref Vec[T]` parameter; caller reads back. Pins the `get_data_ptr`-mediated dispatch for the ref-param shape.
    5. `test_vec_index_store_string_elem` — `let mut v = Vec.filled(3, String.new()); v[1] = "hello".to_string();` then read-back. Pins the element-type-agnostic store path for heap-bearing element types. **Cross-check critical:** the slot's existing String value must not double-free with the overwrite — verify or scope to skip if the underlying `String` overwrite leaks the original (acceptable v1 behavior; pre-existing concern not introduced by this slice).

  *Files expected to change.* `src/codegen.rs` — new dispatch arm in `compile_index_store` (~5 lines), new `compile_vec_index_store` helper (~55 lines). `tests/codegen.rs` — 5 new tests (~150 lines including link/run scaffolding). This doc — flip status to `[x]` and add a "What landed" close-out paragraph. Total ~210 LoC.

  *Out of scope.*
  - **`Vec[T]` push-through-index ergonomic** — `v[len] = x` (writing one past the end to grow) is rejected per spec; users push through `v.push(x)`. The bounds-check using `len` not `cap` enforces this directly.
  - **Drop-of-overwritten-value semantics for heap-bearing element types.** When `v[i] = new_string` overwrites an existing `String`, the previous element's heap buffer leaks in v1. This matches the pre-existing behavior for Array indexed writes and isn't unique to this slice — full move/drop semantics for Vec elements are deferred to the same broader cleanup work that the compound-payload drop-path slice opens. **Mention in close-out.**
  - **Vec method dispatch on indexed receivers** — `v[i].push(...)` and `v[i].len()` go through `compile_method_call`, not `compile_index_store`; that's sub-item (c) of three Vec runtime gaps and ships as a separate slice.
  - **Slice / Array / Map indexed writes** — already work via existing dispatches at `src/codegen.rs:11685-11698`. This slice is Vec-only.

  *Hard-stop triggers.*
  - **`get_data_ptr` doesn't handle the index-store call site uniformly.** The read-path's caller threads `name` into `get_data_ptr(name)`; if the helper has any read-path-specific assumptions (e.g., assumes the binding is positionally before a read-only use), the write path breaks. Verify by inspection — `get_data_ptr` is used by both read and other Vec mutation paths (verify via grep `get_data_ptr`). **Default fallback:** mirror the read-path's exact call shape; if it doesn't compose, scope this slice to the owned-Vec case and file the ref-param case as a separate hard-stop.
  - **The bounds-check off-by-one direction matters.** Write at index `i ∈ [0, len)` is OK; write at `i == len` should panic per spec (use `push`). Verify the read-path uses `UGE` (`>= len`) for the panic comparison — if so, mirror exactly. **Default fallback:** mirror the read-path verbatim; if read-path is wrong, the read-path is wrong, not this slice.
  - **`Vec.filled(n, val)` doesn't compile cleanly today** for the test fixture. Verify by writing the test program directly first; if `Vec.filled` is broken, fall back to `let mut v: Vec[i64] = Vec.new(); v.push(0); v.push(0); ...` to construct the test fixture, but flag the `Vec.filled` gap as an out-of-scope side-finding.
  - **Cleanup interaction with the parent's `track_vec_var` cleanup.** The slot's `cap` tracking is unaffected by element overwrites; but if the slot is a `mut ref Vec[T]` parameter, the parent owns the buffer and the function's local cleanup must not fire. Mirror the read-path's `get_data_ptr`-based dispatch (no extra cleanup logic). **Default fallback:** the read-path doesn't trigger any cleanup; the write-path mirrors it; cleanup is a non-issue.

  State: **plan drafted to autonomous-friendly bar 2026-05-09.** No prerequisites — `compile_vec_index` (read-path) at `src/codegen.rs:11499-11556`, `get_data_ptr`, `vec_elem_type_for_var`, `vec_struct_type`, `emit_panic` are all in place. Pure codegen work; no parser, typechecker, resolver, lowering, ast, or interpreter changes. Estimated time: 30-45 min.

  **Phase target.** Phase 7.2 — Vec runtime codegen surface. Sub-item (b) of three Vec runtime gaps surfaced by the LeetCode 3629 kata; (a) interpreter `Vec.new` dispatch lives in `phase-4-interpreter.md`, (c) method dispatch on indexed receivers is the next bullet below this one. Lights up `vec[i] = val` end-to-end and unblocks the bottom-up section of `examples/leetcode/coin_change.kara` as a side effect.

- [x] **Codegen method dispatch on indexed (non-identifier) receivers.** ✓ Landed (tracker bookkeeping flip 2026-05-29 — implementation shipped earlier; entry stayed `[ ]` until verified during a tracker walk). `compile_indexed_receiver_method` (`src/codegen/calls.rs:38`) implements the slice plan below: when `compile_method_call` sees an `ExprKind::Index { object, index }` receiver, it routes via a leading guard at `src/codegen/method_call.rs:523` that lowers the index through the per-container path (Vec / Slice / Array) and re-dispatches the method on the element pointer. Read-only (`ref self` / `self`) methods lower through Index; mutating (`mut ref self`) methods lower through IndexMut, so `factors[i].push(x)` on a `Vec[Vec[T]]` writes through to the outer Vec. Single-level chains are supported; multi-level chains (`a[i][j].method()`) are explicitly rejected with a focused diagnostic per `test_e2e_indexed_receiver_chained_rejected`. All six planned tests live in `tests/codegen.rs`: `test_e2e_indexed_receiver_inner_vec_len`, `_inner_vec_is_empty`, `_inner_vec_push`, `_slice_path_len`, `_chained_rejected`, `_user_struct_method`.

  Original entry (kept for the historical slice plan + MR1-5 design notes):

  `compile_method_call` (`src/codegen.rs:6345`) only dispatches methods when the receiver is an identifier; for indexed-access receivers like `factors[i].is_empty()` or `factors[j].push(i)` it falls through with the self-describing diagnostic at `src/codegen.rs:6610-6615`: `codegen: no handler for method '<name>' on non-identifier receiver (method dispatch fell through; this is a codegen bug — add a dispatcher arm in 'compile_method_call' or mark the test '#[ignore]' if the method is genuinely deferred)`. Surfaced 2026-05-09 by the LeetCode 3629 kata while scaffolding `bfs_sieve.kara` (specifically `factors[j].push(i)` and `factors[i].is_empty()` on the merged-factors `Vec[Vec[i64]]` table). The design fully specifies this through `Index` / `IndexMut` (`design.md:5165` — `index_mut(mut ref self, idx) -> mut ref Self.Output`); the gap is purely a missing codegen dispatcher arm.

  *Slice plan (drafted 2026-05-09) — Codegen method dispatch on indexed receivers.*

  At the method-call site, when the receiver expression is a `Subscript` (or `Index`-shaped expression), lower the receiver via the existing Index / IndexMut lowering to obtain the element pointer, then dispatch the method through that pointer — same shape as the existing identifier-receiver path with one extra lowering step. **Locked design choices (2026-05-09):** (i) **MR1: receiver-shape early dispatch.** At the top of `compile_method_call` (after the existing identifier-receiver paths and shared-state extraction at `src/codegen.rs:6345`-ish; verify exact line via grep), add a leading guard that handles `ExprKind::Subscript { object, index }` receivers by recursing through Vec/Slice/Array index lowering and re-dispatching the method on the element pointer. **Rejected:** moving the dispatch deeper into the existing receiver-resolution path — the indexed receiver doesn't have a `name` to key registries by, so existing identifier-keyed paths can't be reused without inventing fake names. (ii) **MR2: route by container shape, not by method name.** When the receiver `object` resolves to `Vec[T]` / `Slice[T]` / `Array[T, N]`, use the same per-container path the existing identifier-keyed dispatch would have taken — i.e., compute the element pointer via `compile_vec_index`-equivalent logic for Vec, `compile_slice_index`-equivalent for Slice — and dispatch the method on the element. The element type drives method resolution (`is_empty` / `push` / `len` on the inner Vec, etc.). **Rejected:** dispatching by method name (whitelist) — too many methods to enumerate; the per-container shape captures the right invariant. (iii) **MR3: read-only methods (`ref self` / `self`) lower through `Index`; mutating methods (`mut ref self`) lower through `IndexMut`.** Determined by the resolved method's receiver mode (already known to the typechecker; pulled through whatever method-resolution machinery `compile_method_call` already consults — verify the existing identifier-path's pull and mirror it). **For nested `Vec[Vec[T]]`** — `factors[i].push(x)` requires `IndexMut` on the outer Vec to yield a `mut ref Vec[T]` element, then `push` dispatches on that. (iv) **MR4: register the element binding in the appropriate per-call-site registry** so the inner method dispatch finds the right element type. Specifically, when computing the element pointer, populate a temporary entry in `vec_elem_types` / `slice_elem_types` keyed by a synthesized name (`__indexed_elem_<spawn_id>`) that the inner dispatch uses, then drop the entry after the call. **Alternative considered:** thread the element type through the call directly without a registry — heavier refactor of the existing identifier-keyed dispatch; the synth-name approach is a smaller diff. (v) **MR5: out-of-scope is the chained case `a[i][j].method()`** — that requires recursive lowering through two levels of Subscript, which composes naturally if the dispatch is recursive but adds a test surface. Single-level `a[i].method()` is the v1 target; multi-level chains are a follow-up if the pattern surfaces in a real workload.

  *Sub-steps.*
  - **(a)** Codegen: at `compile_method_call`'s entry (`src/codegen.rs:6345`), add an early guard that matches `ExprKind::Subscript { object, index }` (or whatever the indexed-access AST shape is — verify via grep `ExprKind::Subscript` / `ExprKind::Index`). Skip if the object is itself another Subscript (out-of-scope per MR5). ~3 lines.
  - **(b)** Codegen: add `compile_method_call_on_indexed_receiver(&mut self, object: &Expr, index: &Expr, method: &str, args: &[Argument]) -> Result<BasicValueEnum<'ctx>, String>` helper. Body:
    1. Resolve the container shape from `object`. If `object` is an identifier whose name is in `self.vec_elem_types` → Vec path. If in `self.slice_elem_types` → Slice path. Otherwise — fall through to the existing diagnostic (no support yet for non-identifier outer objects; that's the chained case in MR5).
    2. For the Vec path, mirror the lead of `compile_vec_index` (data-ptr load + bounds-check + element-pointer GEP) but **don't load** — keep the pointer.
    3. The element type comes from `vec_elem_type_for_var(name)`. Pull the element's surface type name (canonical: `"Vec"` / `"Slice"` / a struct name) from `var_type_names` or the inner Vec's element registry; for nested `Vec[Vec[T]]`, the inner element's surface name is `"Vec"`.
    4. Synthesize a temporary identifier name `__indexed_elem_<counter>`, register it in `self.variables` (or whichever map the existing identifier-receiver path consults) with the element pointer + element LLVM type, AND populate `vec_elem_types` / `slice_elem_types` if the element is itself a Vec/Slice (so inner method calls dispatch correctly).
    5. Re-call `compile_method_call` (or directly invoke the appropriate per-container method dispatcher like `compile_vec_method` at `src/codegen.rs:6629`) with a synthesized `Identifier(synth_name)` receiver expression.
    6. Drop the temporary registrations after the call returns. ~80 lines.
  - **(c)** Tests under `// ── Method dispatch on indexed receivers ──` in `tests/codegen.rs`:
    1. `test_method_dispatch_on_indexed_vec_of_vec_len` (read-only, ref self) — `let grid: Vec[Vec[i64]] = ...; let n = grid[0].len();` resolves to the inner Vec's `len()`. Pin the canonical 2D-array minimal repro per the staging entry text.
    2. `test_method_dispatch_on_indexed_vec_of_vec_is_empty` (read-only, `ref self`) — same shape with `.is_empty()`.
    3. `test_method_dispatch_on_indexed_vec_of_vec_push` (mutating, `mut ref self`) — `let mut grid: Vec[Vec[i64]] = ...; grid[0].push(42); assert_eq!(grid[0][0], 42);`. **The headline regression gate** — closes the LeetCode 3629 kata's primary blocker (`factors[j].push(i)`).
    4. `test_method_dispatch_on_indexed_slice_method` (slice receiver) — `let s: Slice[Vec[i64]] = ...; let n = s[0].len();` — verify the Slice path mirrors Vec.
    5. `test_method_dispatch_on_indexed_chained_rejected_with_diagnostic` (negative test, MR5 boundary) — `let g: Vec[Vec[Vec[i64]]] = ...; g[0][0].len();` falls through to the existing diagnostic (or a new specialized one); pin that the chained case is rejected at codegen time, not silently miscompiling. **Mark `#[ignore]` if `g[0][0]` would correctly panic earlier in the lowering — the test exists to pin the boundary.**
    6. `test_method_dispatch_on_indexed_user_struct_method` — `let v: Vec[Foo] = ...; v[0].compute();` where `Foo` has a user-defined `compute()` method. Pin that user-defined method dispatch through the indexed receiver works, not just builtin Vec/Slice methods.

  *Files expected to change.* `src/codegen.rs` — early guard in `compile_method_call` (~3 lines), new `compile_method_call_on_indexed_receiver` helper (~80 lines), per-container shape resolution + temp-name synthesis (incorporated into the helper). `tests/codegen.rs` — 6 new tests (~280 lines including link/run scaffolding). This doc — flip status to `[x]` and add a "What landed" close-out paragraph. Total ~290 LoC.

  *Out of scope.*
  - **Chained indexed-receiver dispatch** (`a[i][j].method()` — MR5 boundary). Recursive composition of the lowering would close it, but adds test-surface complexity and isn't a clean single-slice win; defer to a follow-up if a real workload surfaces it.
  - **Field-projection-of-indexed receivers** (`a[i].field.method()`). The `.field` projection is a FieldAccess in the AST; the indexed-receiver guard wouldn't fire on a FieldAccess receiver. Composes naturally if the FieldAccess receiver path is patched analogously, but that's a separate codegen surface.
  - **Method dispatch on Map index** (`m[k].method()`). Map index returns a value (with a per-call hash + lookup), not a pointer; mutating methods on a Map-indexed receiver would need a get-mut-or-insert path that doesn't exist yet. File-and-fix when surfaced.
  - **Method dispatch on tuple index** (`t.0.method()`). Tuple-index lowering is via FieldAccess (`.0`), not Subscript; falls under the FieldAccess-receiver case above.
  - **`Vec.filled(...)` / `Vec.new(...)` constructor reliability for the test fixtures.** Tests exercise either the existing (working) Vec construction surface or the patterns landed by sub-item (a) — sub-item (b)'s indexed write must already be in place for the mutating push/index-write tests to round-trip cleanly. Cross-check during implementation: sub-item (b) is a soft prerequisite for the headline mutating test to pass without scaffolding; if (b) hasn't shipped, the mutating tests use `push`-only construction.

  *Hard-stop triggers.*
  - **The receiver-mode (ref / mut ref / owned self) propagation through `compile_method_call` is opaque** — the existing identifier-receiver path may rely on per-method receiver-mode tables that don't surface cleanly. Verify by reading `compile_method_call`'s body for receiver-mode branching. **Default fallback:** if receiver-mode resolution requires a typechecker round-trip the codegen doesn't have, scope this slice to the read-only case (`ref self` / owned `self`) and file mutating dispatch (`mut ref self`) as a separate hard-stop. The headline `factors[j].push(i)` test requires mutating; without it, the slice closes only the read-only half of the gap.
  - **The existing `compile_vec_method` / `compile_slice_method` paths are keyed by identifier-name in ways that resist synthesis.** If the synthesized name approach (MR4) doesn't compose because the per-container methods read from `var_type_names` / `vec_elem_types` and there's no clean way to inject + cleanup, fall back to extracting the per-container method-dispatch logic into a name-agnostic helper that takes a `(ptr, elem_ty)` pair. Heavier refactor; halt and triage if it cascades. **Default fallback:** scope the slice to a single concrete container (e.g., Vec[Vec[T]] only); other containers ship in a follow-up.
  - **The temporary registry entries leak to peer expressions in the same scope.** If `self.variables` / `vec_elem_types` registry entries persist across the method call and pollute downstream lookups, file as inline-fix (`pop` after the call) or scope to a builder-RAII guard. **Default fallback:** explicit pop after `compile_method_call` returns; no RAII layer needed.
  - **Sub-item (b)'s `compile_vec_index_store` hasn't landed yet at execution time.** Test 3 (`test_method_dispatch_on_indexed_vec_of_vec_push`) requires write-back through `push`, which doesn't go through `compile_index_store` — it goes through the inner Vec's `push` method directly via the registered element pointer. Should be unblocked by this slice alone. Cross-check: write a minimal repro before delegating; if the test depends on (b), wait for (b) to land first or scope to read-only tests only.

  State: **plan drafted to autonomous-friendly bar 2026-05-09.** No hard prerequisites; sub-item (b) is a soft prerequisite for the mutating-test surface but NOT for the slice's main delivery (read-only dispatch + the canonical `factors[j].push(i)` shape works through inner-Vec method registration, not through `compile_index_store`). Pure codegen work; no parser, typechecker, resolver, lowering, ast, or interpreter changes. Estimated time: 60-90 min.

  **Phase target.** Phase 7.2 — Vec runtime codegen surface. Sub-item (c) of three Vec runtime gaps surfaced by the LeetCode 3629 kata; (a) interpreter `Vec.new` dispatch lives in `phase-4-interpreter.md`, (b) is the previous bullet above. Lights up the canonical 2D-array minimal repro (`grid[0].push(42)`) and unblocks any Kāra program that uses indexed-receiver method dispatch — DP tables, adjacency lists, factor tables, the canonical CS-101 algorithm shapes.

- [x] **Codegen fn-pointer-as-free-fn-arg + `Server.serve(handler)` dispatch (Slice B follow-up).** ✓ Landed 2026-05-09 (commit `60ce3a4`). Codegen-only slice: free-fn-name-as-value path in `compile_expr` (sub-step b), `Server.serve(handler)` dispatcher mirroring `serve_static`'s shape against `karac_runtime_serve_http` (sub-step c), and structured `E_CLOSURE_AS_FN_PTR_NOT_YET` rejection for closure handlers (sub-step d); `runtime/stdlib/http.kara` declares `effect resource Network;` and the `Server.serve(handler: Fn(Request) -> Response) -> Result[Unit, HttpError] with sends(Network) receives(Network)` placeholder. Runtime-side handler-ABI trampoline (translating between the Kāra `Request`/`Response` value types and the FFI `*const KaracHttpRequest` / `*mut KaracHttpResponse` pointers) remains a separate codegen track — `tests/http_server.rs::test_server_serve_handler_smoke` ships `#[ignore]`'d as documentation of the gap; the codegen path is verified by `tests/codegen.rs::test_server_serve_with_free_fn_handler_compiles` + `_rejects_closure_handler` + `test_free_fn_as_value_emits_fn_ptr`, plus `tests/typechecker.rs::test_server_serve_signature_typechecks`.

- [x] **Primitive-type associated constants.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-10 (Theme 7 commit `7587995`). The canonical `let max = i64.MAX;` / `let inf = f64.INFINITY;` / `let n = usize.MAX;` forms now run end-to-end through both `karac run` and `karac build`. Surfaced 2026-05-09 from a user question.

  *Locked design choices (2026-05-10).* Plan-time PC1/PC2/PC3 shipped as drafted; PC4/PC5 revised after probing the parse + dispatch surface:
  - **PC1 — single shared table.** `pub static PRIMITIVE_CONSTS: &[(&str, &str, ConstValue)]` in `src/prelude.rs` consumed by typechecker, interpreter, and codegen via `lookup_primitive_const(type_name, const_name)`. Same one-table-with-N-readers shape as `STDLIB_SOURCES`.
  - **PC2 — float constants via const Rust literals.** Stored as `f32::INFINITY` / `f64::NAN` etc. directly in the static table — these are `const` since Rust 1.83 (well within MSRV) so no `LazyLock` / `from_bits` workaround needed. Bit patterns survive the round-trip through codegen's `const_float` (which accepts an f64; for f32 widths the f64→f32 narrowing is exact for the values we emit).
  - **PC3 — `usize.MAX = u64::MAX` for v1.** v1 is 64-bit only; when 32-bit targets land, `lookup_primitive_const` grows a target-conditional swap on the `Usize` arm.
  - **PC4 (revised) — only `i64.MAX` parses; `i64::MAX` is a parser error.** Original plan claimed both forms produce `ExprKind::Path { segments: ["i64", "MAX"] }`. Probe disproved: `i64.MAX` parses as `FieldAccess(Identifier("i64"), "MAX")` (NOT `Path`), and `i64::MAX` doesn't parse at all (`Expected Semicolon, found Colon`). Dispatch keys on the FieldAccess shape — `Identifier(name).field` where `(name, field)` lives in `PRIMITIVE_CONSTS`.
  - **PC5 (revised) — dispatch at the FieldAccess intercept, not via synthetic env.functions entries.** Typechecker's `infer_field_access` early-intercepts before calling `infer_expr(object)` (which would silently return `Type::Error` for the bare primitive identifier). Same intercept shape on interpreter and codegen sides. Cleaner than a synthetic `env.functions` registration because the typechecker stays pure and the dispatch site is structurally aligned across the three consumers.

  *Out of scope (deferred to follow-ups).*
  - **Per-target `usize` width.** v1 is 64-bit only; PC3 hardcodes `usize.MAX = u64::MAX`. Refactor when 32-bit targets land.
  - **`isize` constants.** Parallel surface to `usize`; add when `isize` joins the prelude.
  - **`bool.TRUE` / `bool.FALSE`.** Redundant with the `true` / `false` keywords; intentionally absent.
  - **`char.MAX_VALUE` / `char.MIN_VALUE`.** Char surface shape (UTF-8 vs Unicode-scalar-value) is undefined; add when the broader char story lands.
  - **Tightened diagnostic on unknown primitive const.** `i64.NONEXISTENT` falls through silently today (returns `Type::Error` from the second leg of `infer_field_access`). Tightening into a structured "unknown constant on primitive" diagnostic would give better error messages but is independent of this slice.
  - **Cross-side stdout parity.** Interpreter and codegen render some constants differently — `u64.MAX` → `-1` (interp, signed Display) vs `-1` (codegen, signed printf) match by coincidence; `f64.NAN` → `NaN` (interp) vs `nan` (codegen, C printf) differ. The bit patterns are identical; surface formatter parity is a separate runtime / interp printer alignment concern.

  **Phase target.** Phase 7.2 — primitive-type runtime surface. Closes the staging carry-forward sub-item (i) of "Slice surface gaps + primitive-type associated constants". Cross-ref [`phase-4-interpreter.md`](phase-4-interpreter.md) for the interpreter-half tracking pointer (flips in lockstep).

- [x] **Compound-payload tuple-payload destructure.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-10 (Theme 5 commit `242173d`). The pattern `match e { V((xs, n)) => xs.len() + n }` — variant carrying a tuple payload — now lights up end-to-end through `karac run` and `karac build`; un-ignored `test_pattern_bound_nested_tuple_vec_payload` plus 4 new codegen tests + 1 ASAN test cover the primitive×primitive, heap×primitive, nested-tuple, and 3-element shapes.

  *Locked design choices (2026-05-10).* Five forks settled at plan time; the implementation kept (i)/(ii)/(v) as drafted, replaced (iii)/(iv) with a more direct shape after surveying the construction side:
  - **TP1 — tuple destructure reuses let-pattern machinery.** The new `PatternKind::Tuple` arm in `bind_pattern_values` mirrors `bind_pattern`'s let-pattern arm: `build_extract_value` per element + recursive call. Rejected duplicating logic via a separate path.
  - **TP2 — `reconstruct_payload_value` returns a per-element value-tree.** New Tuple branch packs per-element reconstructed values into a synthesized tuple struct via `build_insert_value`. Rejected keeping single-value return.
  - **TP3 (revised) — per-element word counts via pattern shape lookup.** Construction's `field_word_offsets` records ONE entry per source field (the whole tuple as a single multi-word payload); destructure derives per-element word counts on the fly via the new `pattern_payload_word_count` helper, which mirrors `payload_word_count_for_type_expr` (Vec/String=3, Slice=2, registered struct=N, primitive/wildcard=1, tuple=sum) using `pattern_binding_types` instead of the source-level `TypeExpr`. Rejected (and necessarily) the original "use field_word_offsets per-element" plan because that table is keyed at the source-field level, not per-tuple-element.
  - **TP4 (revised) — typechecker registers `Type::Str` as `"String"` in `pattern_binding_types`.** Required so the new `pattern_payload_word_count` helper can distinguish String (3 words) from primitives (1 word). Mirrors the existing `Type::Named { name: "Vec" }` → `"Vec"` registration; landed in both `bind_pattern_types` AND `check_pattern_against` Binding arms (the latter is the path actually used for match-arm patterns; the former didn't surface in the failing test). Small drift past the original "pure codegen" framing — in scope.
  - **TP5 — recursive-tuple support via pattern recursion.** Nested tuples like `match e { V(((a, b), c)) => ... }` work automatically through the recursive `reconstruct_payload_value` / `bind_pattern_values` Tuple branches. Confirmed by `test_compound_tuple_payload_nested`.

  *Out of scope (deferred to follow-ups).*
  - **Tuple destructure with `..` rest pattern** (`V((a, .., z))`). Not in v1's pattern surface; defer until rest-pattern lands broadly.
  - **Struct-payload destructure with field renaming** (`V(MyStruct { x, y })`). The `PatternKind::Struct` arm in `bind_pattern_values` is a separate gap; this slice covers tuple-only.
  - **Move-semantics for tuple-element bindings.** ASAN test 3 confirms heap-bearing String elements round-trip cleanly (no double-free) — the existing scope-exit cleanup machinery handles tuple-extracted bindings the same way it handles single-aggregate payloads.
  - **Variant payload that's a single tuple type** (`V((T,))` — one-element tuple). Today users write `V(T)` instead; one-tuples remain syntactic noise.

  **Phase target.** Phase 7.2 — compound-payload enum codegen. Closes the staging carry-forward "Compound-payload tuple-payload destructure" entry.

- [x] **Multi-file project-mode codegen.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-10 (Theme 4 commit `dc8bfbd`). `cmd_build_project` now drives codegen + link end-to-end. Surfaced 2026-05-09 by the Parallax demo path; CR-24 shipped resolver + typechecker per-module, this slice closes the codegen + link orchestration.

  *Locked design choices (2026-05-10).* MF2/MF3/MF4 shipped as drafted. MF1/MF5 revised after probing the existing pipeline:
  - **MF1 (revised) — concat super-program + cross-module name-collision detection (mangling deferred to v2).** Original plan called for `kara_<module_path>_<item>` symbol mangling at every declaration site. Implementation revealed that codegen has ~14 `module.get_function(name)` call sites (concrete declarations + monomorphizations + path-call dispatches + traits + run-time intrinsics) plus the typechecker / resolver name resolution that would need to mangle in lockstep — touches at least three subsystems and breaks the LLVM `main` entry-point convention without careful special-casing. Replaced with a simpler shape: concatenate all module items (in topological order, dropping `import` declarations + the synthetic prelude) into a single super-program, then drive it through the existing single-file pipeline. Cross-module function-name collisions surface as resolve-time errors against the merged super-program (clear diagnostic naming the colliding identifier; pinned by `test_build_project_codegen_cross_module_collision_diagnostic`). v2 follow-up: full mangling for true private-namespace isolation.
  - **MF2 — prelude / baked-stdlib emits ONCE.** Inherent to the super-program approach — one Codegen instance, one `compile_program` call, one prelude emission. No guard plumbing needed.
  - **MF3 — manifest `name` field becomes binary name.** Output path is `<project_root>/<mf.name>`; pinned by `test_build_project_codegen_manifest_name_becomes_binary_name`.
  - **MF4 — single LLVM module for v1.** Inherent to the super-program approach.
  - **MF5 — topological emission order via `module::emission_order`.** Iterative DFS reverse-postorder over `tree.graph.edges` rooted at `tree.root`, with disconnected modules visited from their own roots so files no other module imports still appear in the output. Dependencies emit before dependents — pinned by `test_build_project_codegen_three_module_chain_runs` (main → db → db.users).
  - **NEW — post-typecheck phases run on the super-program (not per-module).** Concurrency analysis depends on knowing imported callees' effects; a per-module concurrency pass would lose cross-module visibility. Per-module wrapping for these phases would require a separate "shared effect map" infrastructure that doesn't exist today. Trade-off: late-phase diagnostics (effect / ownership / concurrency / codegen) lose per-file context; the spans still carry line:col but not file paths. Per-module diagnostics for parse / cycles / resolve / typecheck still fire upstream of codegen via the existing CR-24 path.

  *Out of scope (deferred to follow-ups).*
  - **Symbol mangling for true private-namespace isolation (v2).** Original MF1; replaced with collision-detection + concat-super-program for v1. Real-world projects rarely have cross-module pub-fn collisions; when they do, the diagnostic clearly names the collision so the user can rename. v2 follow-up promotes this to per-module mangled namespaces (`kara_<module_path>_<item>`) so collisions become structurally impossible.
  - [x] **Per-module file context in late-phase diagnostics.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-12. At concat time the new `src/span_visitor.rs` module walks every appended item with `visit_item_spans` and registers a `(offset, length, line, col) → module_index` entry in a `ModuleSpanTable`; `format_pipeline_errors` consults the table for each error span and prefixes `file:line:col` when the span maps to exactly one module. Spans absent from the table (synthesized post-concat) or shared by two modules (rare — only when distinct files have identical leading bytes) degrade gracefully to bare `line:col`. The cross-module shared-map question raised in the staging entry (per-module wrappers for effect / ownership / concurrency) remains out of scope and post-v1; this slice keeps the super-program shape.
  - **Multi-object compilation.** Per MF4, v1 ships single-LLVM-module emission. Per-module object files + link-time aggregation is a v2 perf win.
  - **Incremental rebuild.** `karac build` re-emits the whole tree every invocation. Incremental codegen is post-v1.
  - **Multi-package builds.** v1 is single-package only.
  - **Parallax example end-to-end.** ✓ Closed 2026-05-10 in the same slate as Theme 4. Three sub-fixes shipped alongside the Theme 4 close-out: (a) `providers` lexer keyword demoted to a contextual identifier (parser dispatches on `Identifier("providers") + {` for the providers-block expression form), freeing the bareword for module names + functions + bindings; (b) per-module typecheck extended via `collect_import_origins` to register imported structs / enums / traits in the local env so `infer_struct_literal` recognises them (closes the `E0207 NotAStruct` cross-module gap); (c) `examples/parallax/src/{traits,resources,providers}.kara` gained the missing `import` declarations + the README retired the `cat ... > /tmp/parallax.kara` workaround. `karac build` from `examples/parallax/` now produces a working binary that fans out four resources concurrently and joins.

  **Phase target.** Phase 7 — codegen pipeline orchestration. Closes the staging carry-forward "Multi-file project-mode codegen" entry.

---

## v62 Brainstorm Outcomes (2026-05-06)

The items below land from the v62 brainstorm on interpreter perf and binary size. See `design.md § Execution Model and Compilation Targets`, `§ Generics and Monomorphization Strategy`, `§ Bounds-Check Elision and the get_unchecked Escape Hatch`, and `§ Build-profile linker flags` for the design locks; entries here track the implementation work.

- [x] **Always-JIT execution backend via LLJIT.** ✓ **DONE 2026-06-03 (tracker bookkeeping flip — all three steps shipped earlier).** Step (a) MCJIT prototype (2026-05-29), (b) `llvm-sys::orc2`/LLJIT wrap (the entry below), and (c) the JIT-default flip + documented cold-start bench (L599 / L606) all landed by 2026-06-01. The only remaining `[ ]` items in this cluster — ambient-method codegen (L626), unified provider dispatch (L632), the L640 harness flake, and REPL aggregate snapshots (L642) — are non-blocking follow-ons tracked as their own entries, none part of the core backend/flip. Original sequencing note follows. Wire `karac repl` and `karac test` to compile each user-defined function via LLJIT on first call rather than executing through the tree-walk interpreter. Same compiler pipeline as `karac build`; codegen output loaded into an in-process LLJIT engine instead of written to an object file. Tree-walk interpreter retained as a dev/debug tool only — see `design.md § Tree-walk interpreter (dev / debug only)`. P0 v1. Sequencing: (a) MCJIT sanity-check prototype (~3 days, validates LLVM-JIT viability on representative Karac modules; not a shipping vehicle), (b) wrap `llvm-sys::orc2` and integrate LLJIT (see entry below), (c) ship v1 with documented cold-start as the perf headline.

  *Sub-step (a) complete 2026-05-29.* MCJIT prototype landed under the `mcjit_prototype` cargo feature (`src/codegen.rs` `jit_run_main`, `tests/mcjit_prototype.rs`). Empirical finding: inkwell 0.9 + LLVM 18 + macOS arm64 MCJIT runs pure-internal modules (arithmetic, control flow, helper-fn calls) correctly but hangs at PC=0 the moment a JITted module calls any external symbol — libc (`@malloc`, `@free`, `@printf`, `@snprintf`) or karac runtime — across both `engine.get_function` and direct `transmute` of `get_function_address`'s return, and across `add_global_mapping`-bound libc fns. Sample confirms the JITted code itself jumps to address 0; `get_function_address` returns a valid non-null address before the call. This is the L558 → (b) transition signal: orc2/LLJIT is structurally necessary on the user's primary dev platform (Apple M5 Pro), not just "preferred per the design lock". MCJIT is not a viable fallback on Apple Silicon. The (b) entry's W1 acceptance criterion is correspondingly strengthened — see the next entry. The prototype tests live as a pre-baked regression battery the orc2 wrap re-enables one-by-one as each W milestone lands.

- [x] **Wrap `llvm-sys::orc2` for LLJIT integration.** ✓ **DONE 2026-06-03 (tracker bookkeeping flip — milestones shipped earlier).** W1–W2 (2026-05-29), W3–W4 full codegen-E2E-via-JIT (closed at the coro-correctness-pass entry below, 2026-05-31), and W5 (2026-05-31) all green; no W6 was defined. Original detail follows. `inkwell` does not expose ORC v2 / LLJIT; the JIT subset bypasses `inkwell` and calls `llvm-sys::orc2` directly. The C API surface is ~30 functions; the hard parts are ORC's lifetime/threading invariants. Effort estimate 2–4 weeks initial. Milestones (W1–W6 from v62 lock):
  - **W1:** skeleton wrapper compiles and runs a hello-world IR module via LLJIT. **Acceptance strengthened per L558 (a) finding (2026-05-29):** "hello-world" must include at least one libc external call (a `printf("hello\n")` round-trip is sufficient) and must execute on macOS arm64. This is the exact code shape that exposed MCJIT's failure mode; if LLJIT/jitlink also hangs here, halt and revisit the v2 Cranelift question before W2 rather than accumulating effort. ✓ **W1 closed 2026-05-29.** `src/codegen/lljit.rs` ships the `LLJITEngine` wrapper (~140 LOC over `llvm-sys::orc2`); `tests/lljit_prototype.rs` round-trips `print(42)` through the JIT on macOS arm64 (Apple M5 Pro), `42` arrives on stdout, exit code 0. Load-bearing piece is `LLVMOrcCreateDynamicLibrarySearchGeneratorForProcess`: it adds the process-symbol-search generator to the main JITDylib so libc / runtime symbols resolve via the process symbol table, sidestepping the MCJIT/RuntimeDyld arm64-Mach-O relocation issue. Post-W1 probe (informational): Vec.push (the exact program that hung MCJIT at PC=0), control-flow while, f-string snprintf, internal-fn call — all 4 pass. 7/7 LLJIT tests green; the prototype tests stay around as a pre-W2 regression battery.
  - **W2:** lifetime / ownership story stable; multiple modules co-existing without leaks. ✓ **W2 closed 2026-05-29.** `ResourceTracker<'engine>` ships in `src/codegen/lljit.rs` — RAII handle binding lifetime to the engine, exposing `.remove()` for explicit teardown plus `Drop` for refcount release (mirrors LLVM's `LLVMOrcResourceTrackerRemove` vs `LLVMOrcReleaseResourceTracker` split). `LLJITEngine::add_ir_module_with_tracker` installs each module under its own tracker. Lifetime hygiene validated by two 100-iteration stress tests (engine new/drop cycle and tracker add/remove cycle on a single engine), neither leaks. **Finding (pinned by `lljit_w2_finding_same_jd_collides_on_runtime_globals`):** direct multi-module coexistence in *one* JITDylib fails — every karac-compiled module emits the same Debugger-Contract globals (`KARAC_SPAWN_SITES*`, `karac_jit_template_manifest`, `kara.string_table`), and LLJIT correctly rejects the duplicates. Two v1 paths: (1) REPL cell shadowing via tracker-cycle (the load-bearing v1 use case, working today), (2) per-module JITDylib isolation (W3+ work — requires dropping below `LLVMOrcLLJITLookup` to `ExecutionSession::lookup` since LLJIT C API only exposes main-JD lookup).
  - **W3–W4:** full integration — every test in `tests/codegen.rs` E2E passes through the JIT execution path. ✓ **W3.1 (de-risk slice) closed 2026-05-29.** Built the JIT-based E2E test harness — `tests/lljit_e2e.rs::jit_run_program(src) -> Option<String>` mirrors the AOT `run_program`'s signature, routing through `LLJITEngine` with dup2-based stdout capture (fd 1 → `mkstemp`+`unlink` tempfile around the JIT call, restore on return). Required prerequisites: `karac-runtime` promoted to `["staticlib", "rlib"]` crate-type so it's consumable as a Rust dev-dep on `karac`; `pub fn __preserve_no_mangle_symbols()` added to `runtime/src/lib.rs` to keep the `karac_*` exports alive against rlib-level DCE (the LLJIT process-symbol-search generator resolves them via `dlsym(RTLD_DEFAULT)` at JIT-link time, which requires them in the test binary's symbol table). Representative subset of 10 tests across `println` (i64/bool/i32), arithmetic, fn call, while loop, Vec push+iterate, Map insert+get, f-string interpolation. **10/10 pass** with stdout matching the AOT path exactly. W3.2+ scope: par-block thread lifecycle (the engine-Drop interaction), `?`-bearing Result flows, exit-code-asserting tests, and the remaining ~1,500 codegen tests' scale-up. ✓ **W3.2 (surface-unknowns slice) closed 2026-05-29.** par-block / `?` / exit-code surfaces all round-trip cleanly. **Finding:** `karac_runtime_*` Debugger-Contract introspection symbols reference `extern KARAC_SPAWN_SITES*` (runtime/src/lib.rs L1059, cfg(not(test))-gated); AOT codegen satisfies these per-binary, but in JIT each module's defs live inside its own JITDylib only, so the test binary's static link needs neutral stand-ins. Added in `tests/lljit_e2e.rs` (zero-initialized, 8-aligned, `#[no_mangle]`); JITted code reads its own module-local defs at runtime, so the stand-ins only satisfy the test binary's link, not user-program semantics. par-block thread lifecycle is non-issue: the join happens inside `karac_par_run`, synchronous from main's perspective. 14/14 LLJIT E2E tests green. **What's left for the W3-W4 ship gate is mechanical** — bulk migration of the existing ~1,500 codegen tests onto `jit_run_program` with per-batch growth of the runtime-symbol force-link list. No more structural unknowns; that's W3.3+.
  - **W5:** error handling + threading edge cases. ✓ **W5 closed 2026-05-31.** Two hardening changes in `src/codegen/lljit.rs` + a regression battery in `tests/lljit_prototype.rs`. (1) **Threading:** `LLJITEngine::new`'s `Target::initialize_native` mutates LLVM's global target registry and is unsafe to call concurrently; funnelled it through a process-wide `OnceLock` (`ensure_native_target_initialized`) so N threads each building their own engine race only the first init, which `get_or_init` serializes (later callers clone the cached result). Documented that the engine is intentionally `!Send + !Sync` (it holds raw LLVM pointers) — the supported concurrency model is one engine per thread; JIT'd code may itself spawn worker threads (`par {}`) independent of engine ownership because workers run compiled fn pointers and never touch the engine handle. (2) **Error handling:** `Drop` now surfaces `LLVMOrcDisposeLLJIT` teardown failures on stderr (was silently discarded — the one place W1's "log in W2" intent had stayed deferred). **Tests (4 new, 15/15 green in the file):** `lljit_w5_malformed_ir_returns_err` (garbage IR → clean `Err`, no abort/panic), `lljit_w5_lookup_missing_symbol_returns_err` (missing symbol → `Err`, not a 0 address that would null-deref when transmuted + called), `lljit_w5_engine_usable_after_parse_error` (a failed parse doesn't poison the shared context — a subsequent valid module still installs, looks up, and runs), `lljit_w5_concurrent_engines_across_threads` (8 threads × engine build/run/drop concurrently — the `OnceLock` regression guard). The **"wrapping done" criterion** (full codegen E2E via JIT + Level 2 DWARF) has its dependencies cleared as of 2026-05-31: the JIT-path coro-pass seam closed, and the Level 2 entry shipped in full (part 1 panic location + part 2 DWARF `DIBuilder` emission). What remains for "wrapping done" is wiring those into the LLJIT path itself (route the DWARF + coro passes through `LLJITEngine` and run the full codegen E2E suite via JIT) — tracked by the L577 always-JIT backend entry, not by missing Level 2 / coro infrastructure.
  - **Tripwire (W6):** if W3 has not landed by W6, halt and re-evaluate (likely revisits the v2 Cranelift question).
  - **"Wrapping done" criterion:** full codegen E2E suite passes via JIT path with Level 2 DWARF preserved (per crash-diagnostics lock).

  *W3.3+ progress.* `tests/codegen.rs::run_program_capturing_inner` env-routes via `KARAC_TEST_JIT=1` to a `karac_jit_runner` subprocess (`src/bin/karac_jit_runner.rs`) so panics + atexit-stderr stay isolated per test. All ~960 codegen tests pass through this single point under `--features lljit_prototype`. The cutover into the user-facing `karac` CLI surfaces (`repl` + `test`) ships as the two slices directly below — separate from L581 because they're per-tool integration on top of the engine wrap, not new orc2 plumbing.

- [x] **JIT execution path must run the coro correctness passes before `add_ir_module` (gates the L581 "full codegen E2E via JIT" criterion).** ✓ **Closed 2026-05-31.** The JIT path (`LLJITEngine::add_ir_module` / `karac_jit_runner`) hands karac-emitted IR straight to LLJIT — it never runs `src/codegen/driver.rs::apply_optimization_passes`, which is where the AOT path runs `coro-early,coro-split,coro-cleanup` **unconditionally** (a correctness pass even at `-O0`; see `docs/spikes/network-async-coroutine-transform.md` §8). So a coroutine-compiled program (the A2 network-async transform, gated behind `Codegen::set_coro_enabled`) run through the JIT would emit **un-split coroutines** — the `llvm.coro.*` intrinsics left unlowered → a no-op task, the exact bug-C failure class relocated to the JIT path. **No live collision yet, but the margin narrowed 2026-05-31:** `3eda2b06` flipped coroutines *on by default* — but **only on the AOT object path** (`compile_to_object_with_hot_swap(…, coro_enabled=true)`, reached by `karac build`/`run`), which runs `apply_optimization_passes` and is therefore correct. The JIT/IR entry points (`compile_to_ir` and every `compile_to_ir_*` variant used by `karac test` / `repl` / the JIT E2E harness) still **do not** call `set_coro_enabled`, so JIT-compiled programs carry no `llvm.coro.*` and the gap was harmless in practice — but the seam is closed proactively so flipping the JIT path to `coro_enabled=true` (or routing `tests/coro_e2e.rs` through the JIT) is safe by construction rather than a latent footgun.

  **Fix shipped:** `LLJITEngine::run_coro_passes` (`src/codegen/lljit.rs`) runs `coro-early,coro-split,coro-cleanup` via raw `llvm_sys::transforms::pass_builder::LLVMRunPasses` on the parsed module inside `parse_ir_into_tsm`, *after* the data-layout/triple stamp and *before* the `LLVMOrcCreateNewThreadSafeModule` wrap — so **both** `add_ir_module` and `add_ir_module_with_tracker` (every JIT install path) get it. `LLVMRunPasses` needs a non-null `TargetMachine` and the LLJIT does not expose its internal one through the C API, so the pass run builds a throwaway generic machine from the engine's own triple (coro lowering is target-independent; PIC/Default mirror the AOT reloc/code-model) and disposes it before returning. A pass-run failure is a hard `Err` (the failure mode is otherwise silent). For the non-coroutine modules that are everything today this is a pure no-op — the coro passes only touch `presplitcoroutine` functions. **Regression guard:** `tests/lljit_prototype.rs::lljit_coro_split_runs_on_jit_path` installs a hand-written `presplitcoroutine` ramp (LLVM-18 opaque-pointer coro ABI) and asserts `lookup_address` materializes it to a non-null handle. Negative control (call `#[cfg(any())]`'d out) reproduces the exact failure — `LLVM ERROR: Cannot select: intrinsic %llvm.coro.begin`, SIGABRT — confirming the test is a real guard, not a vacuous pass. 16/16 `lljit_prototype` tests green; fmt + clippy (`--all-targets --features lljit_prototype`) clean. This clears one of the two open dependencies of the L581 "wrapping done" criterion (the other being L601 Level 2 DWARF).

Four sub-slices: **c.1** lowered `assert*` / `assert_eq` / `assert_ne` to a structured-stderr bridge via new `karac_test_record_failure` runtime fns; **c.2** synthesized per-test `main` wrappers (no-fixture core in c.2a, fixture-prologue / -epilogue in c.2b); **c.3** wired `cmd_test` to dispatch each test through `karac_jit_runner` as a subprocess and parse JSONL outcomes from stderr; **c.4** added per-test watchdog deadlines, ran the AOT regression sweep, and measured cold-start overhead. The subprocess-per-test contract bounds blast radius (a panicking test's exit doesn't take out the test runner) and gives natural cancellation via SIGTERM. Surface in code: `src/cli.rs::cmd_test` (env-gated dispatch path); `src/bin/karac_jit_runner.rs` (the runner binary); `runtime/src/lib.rs` (`karac_test_record_failure*` family).

- [x] **`karac repl` JIT cutover (slice B / c-repl).** ✓ Shipped 2026-05-30 behind `KARAC_REPL_JIT=1`. Closes the "Wire `karac repl` to compile via LLJIT" half of the L577 sequencing. Architecture: a persistent `karac_jit_runner --repl-mode` subprocess per session (lazy spawn on first cell, re-spawned after panic) installs each cell's IR as its own LLJIT module + resource tracker so cross-cell symbol amortization (declare-only re-emission for previously-installed fns) works without re-codegen. Sub-slices: **B.A** the subprocess protocol (length-prefixed cell IR in, length-prefixed stdout + status JSON out); **B.B** session-side dispatch + banner + the runner-died re-spawn flow; **B.4** cross-cell symbol amortization via `jit_installed_fns`; **B.5.1** value-snapshot for primitive `let` bindings (per-binding LLVM global as cross-cell side channel — `__karac_repl_snapshot_<name>`); **B.5.2** extended to `String`; **B.5.3a** to `Vec[primitive]`; **B.5.3b** to `Map[primitive, primitive]` (single opaque handle; registration-site suppression of `track_map_var` in `compile_map_new_stmt`); **B.5.3c** to `Set[primitive]` (same handle mechanism, reuses Map runtime). Also surfaced + shipped: declare-only linkage fix (External vs Internal for cross-cell fn refs); Map tail-return cleanup suppression (`suppress_map_cleanup_for_tail_identifier` in `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` — also covers `Set`, lowers to `Map[T, ()]`). Surface in code: `src/repl.rs` (session integration); `src/repl/jit_runner_client.rs` (client protocol); `src/codegen.rs::SnapshotPrimKind` + `src/codegen/stmts.rs` (capture/replay mechanism); `tests/repl_jit.rs` (22 integration tests).

- [x] **JIT-default flip for `karac repl` + `karac test` (closes L577 step (c)).** ✓ **DONE 2026-06-01** — both halves flipped: `karac repl` (`e06d877a`, 2026-05-31) and `karac test` (this slice). `KARAC_REPL_JIT=0` / `KARAC_TEST_JIT=0` are the regression-bisect escape hatches; the dispatch blocks are `#[cfg(feature = "lljit_prototype")]`'d so non-feature / `--features llvm` production builds are unaffected.
