  - [x] **`karac test` JIT-default flip — codegen-path gaps ALL CLOSED 2026-06-01; flip + cold-start bench DONE (split out from the parent flip 2026-05-31).** Gaps (a)+(b)+(c)+(d) all FIXED; fixing (a) advanced the provider-fixture cli tests 1/7 → 5/7 under JIT and surfaced (c)+(d), now also closed. The flip itself shipped this slice (see the `[x]` sub-item below): `src/cli.rs` default inverted, one cli test pinned `KARAC_TEST_JIT=0`, cold-start measured (~15 ms/test). All verified via AOT codegen (`karac build`) + the JIT cli suite, not just in-process.
    - **(a) Ambient `with_provider` overrides across a function-call boundary.** ✓ **FIXED 2026-06-01** (unified runtime ambient-provider dispatch). The ambient override path was lexically-scoped static monomorphization (`c65cf2b4`): `Clock.now()` inside the `with_provider[Clock]` body saw the override, but across a fn-call boundary did not (AOT printed `0`) — and `test_main_synth` wraps a *call* to the test fn, so test-body ambient calls are always cross-boundary. Fix: ambient resources now push onto the **same runtime provider stack** as user resources. `compile_with_provider` guard keys on `!provider_resource_traits.contains_key` (ambient/trait-less resources route to the ambient path); codegen mints stable resource IDs for `PRELUDE_EFFECT_RESOURCES` (`prelude::AMBIENT_RESOURCE_METHODS` gives the canonical method order); `compile_with_provider_ambient` lazily emits an override vtable (eagerly pre-emitted by `emit_ambient_provider_vtables`, mirroring `emit_provider_vtables`, so a cross-boundary call compiled before the `with_provider` site still sees it) and `karac_provider_push`/`pop`s it; `compile_ambient_resource_method` emits a runtime `karac_provider_lookup` + null-branch (override indirect call vs builtin FFI default, i64 phi). The old compile-time `ambient_provider_overrides` path + `try_compile_ambient_override` were removed. No new runtime FFI. Gates: AOT codegen 1004/1004, memory_sanitizer 73/73, repl_jit 23/23, the canonical `test_with_provider_overrides_builtin_primitive_clock` passes under JIT.
    - **(b) Contract-fault category not propagated through the JIT runner subprocess.** ✓ **FIXED 2026-06-01** (`79f1d531`). `emit_panic` prints to **stdout** (printf), not the `KARAC_TEST_FAILURE` stderr marker, so contract faults reached `map_exit_to_outcome` with no marker → generic outcome. `map_exit_to_outcome` now scans the runner's captured stdout for the `panic at … : <msg>` line and recovers the message + span; the shared `contract_fault_category` (cli.rs) then tags `contract_violated` / `contract_predicate_panicked` identically to the interpreter. No runtime change.
    - **(c) Trait-less *user* resource `with_provider` dispatch (`effect resource R;` with no `: T`).** ✓ **FIXED 2026-06-01** (generalized the runtime ambient-provider path to ALL trait-less resources). `test_multiple_with_provider_attributes_all_active_in_body` declares `effect resource AuditLog;` (trait-less, NOT in `PRELUDE`) and overrides it; `AuditLog.count()` errored `resource 'AuditLog' has no provider trait`. **Reproduction note** ([[feedback_reproduce_before_trusting_bug_diagnosis]]): the *test* (attribute form) already passed under JIT after the (a) fix — the live failure was the **expression form** `with_provider[R](U {…}, || …)` on the AOT/codegen path (`karac build` errored; `karac run` printed correctly). Fix routes trait-less resources to `compile_with_provider_ambient` by **trait-absence alone** (the `compile_with_provider` guard dropped its `PRELUDE_EFFECT_RESOURCES.contains` clause). Since a trait-less user resource has no trait to pin a canonical method order, codegen derives it from the override type's inherent-impl methods (`collect_inherent_methods`), recorded in a new `Codegen::user_ambient_resource_methods` map (resource-keyed, since the call site `R.method` knows R but not the override type U) during the eager vtable pre-pass (`emit_ambient_provider_vtables`); `emit_ambient_vtable` reads the order from there for user resources and from `AMBIENT_RESOURCE_METHODS` for prelude ones. The call site `try_compile_provider_dispatch` now handles the trait-less case: it indexes into that recorded order and dispatches **unconditionally** through the active override (no FFI default — the effect checker guarantees R is in scope), reusing the existing `karac_provider_lookup` + vtable-GEP + indirect-call machinery (the `(U, R)` vtable uses the resource name as its trait key). Prelude ambient resources stay on the FFI-default `compile_ambient_resource_method` path (NOT recorded in `user_ambient_resource_methods` → `try_compile_provider_dispatch` returns `None` for them). No new runtime FFI/ABI. **Verified via AOT `karac build` (not just in-process):** trait-less override prints correct values, multi-method vtable indexing + cross-fn-boundary dispatch + nested prelude-ambient all match `karac run`; the canonical cli test passes under both interpreter and `KARAC_TEST_JIT=1`. New E2E `test_e2e_with_provider_trait_less_user_resource`. Gates: codegen 1005/1005, memory_sanitizer 73/73, provider_escape 54/54, par_codegen 105/105, cli 330/330, repl_jit 23/23, lljit_prototype 16/16, fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs) clean.
    - **(d) `unreachable()` (and other never-returning tails) in a struct-returning fn emit invalid IR.** ✓ **FIXED 2026-06-01** (`compile_diverge` + diverging-branch merge). `test_with_provider_constructor_failure_emits_structured_fail` uses `fn boom() -> FakeClock { unreachable() }` as the fixture ctor; codegen emitted `ret i64 0` for a `{ i64 }`-returning fn → `Module verification failed`. **Root cause:** `unreachable()` / `todo()` (type `!`) had *no* codegen lowering — they fell through to the unknown-callee fallback and produced an `i64 0` placeholder, so the fn-tail `ret` emitted `ret i64 0` against the real return type. **Fix:** lower both in `compile_call` via new `compile_diverge` → `emit_panic(<msg>)` + `build_unreachable()` (messages mirror the interpreter's `eval_builtin_diverge`: `"not yet implemented"` / `"entered unreachable code"`, with a string-literal arg folded in as `"<default>: <lit>"`; a runtime-valued arg degrades to the default since `emit_panic` takes a compile-time `&str`). The `unreachable` terminator makes the existing terminator guards (`compile_function`'s tail `ret`, `compile_block` between statements) correctly skip the follow-on instruction. **Also fixed the latent sibling bug** in `if` / `if let` / `match` value merges: when exactly one branch diverged, the merge collapsed to the const-0 placeholder instead of the live branch's value (`if c { v } else { unreachable() }` evaluated to `0`). Now a single diverging branch → the live branch's value flows through (single live predecessor dominates the merge); all branches diverge → terminate the unreachable merge block (so an all-diverging tail in a struct-returning fn doesn't re-hit the `ret`-mismatch). The `match` path already excluded diverging arms from its phi (one live arm = one-incoming phi); only the all-arms-diverge case needed the merge terminator. **Verified via AOT `karac build`:** the gap-d repro compiles + runs (panics, exit 1); `if`/`match` diverging-arm programs print the live value matching `karac run`. New regression tests in `tests/codegen.rs`: `test_ir_diverge_unreachable_tail_emits_unreachable_not_ret` (IR pin — body has `unreachable`, no `ret i64`), `test_e2e_diverge_if_branch_yields_live_value`, `test_e2e_diverge_match_arm_in_struct_returning_fn`. With `boom()` now *compiling* + panicking at runtime, `test_with_provider_constructor_failure_emits_structured_fail` no longer hits a codegen error. **Correction (surfaced by the flip slice below):** an earlier draft of this entry claimed the fix "restored the `provider_construction_failed` distinction" under JIT — that is **wrong** ([[feedback_reproduce_before_trusting_bug_diagnosis]]). The gap-d verification run used `--features llvm` (NOT `lljit_prototype`), which cfg's out the JIT dispatch, so it silently exercised the *interpreter*. Under real JIT the synthesized main calls the ctor inline, so a panicking fixture is indistinguishable from a panicking body — the runner surfaces a generic `test_fail` with the panic message, NOT the `provider_construction_failed` *reason*. That distinction stays an interpreter-only behaviour (the cli test is now pinned `KARAC_TEST_JIT=0` in the flip slice); preserving it under JIT is its own follow-up. Surface: `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (`compile_diverge`), `src/codegen/control_flow.rs` (if + if-let merges), `src/codegen/control_flow_match.rs` (all-diverge merge). Gates: codegen 1007/1007, par_codegen 105/105, provider_escape 54/54, memory_sanitizer 73/73, cli 330/330, repl_jit 23/23, lljit_prototype 16/16, fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs) clean.
    - [x] **Flip + cold-start bench.** ✓ **DONE 2026-06-01.** `src/cli.rs` `cmd_test` JIT-dispatch guard flipped `== Ok("1")` → `!= Ok("0")` (symmetric with the `karac repl` flip `e06d877a`); `KARAC_TEST_JIT=0` is the regression-bisect escape hatch. Like the repl flip, the dispatch block is `#[cfg(feature = "lljit_prototype")]`'d, so a non-feature build (incl. the `--features llvm` production install) is unaffected — JIT-default is observable only under `lljit_prototype`. **Test fallout: exactly one cli test needed pinning.** Running the full cli suite under `cargo test --release --features lljit_prototype --test cli` (no env set, so the new default applies) was **333/334**, the sole failure being `test_with_provider_constructor_failure_emits_structured_fail` — under JIT a panicking fixture ctor is indistinguishable from a panicking body, so it surfaces a generic `test_fail` with the panic message instead of the `provider_construction_failed` *reason* (a documented JIT limitation; see the gap-d correction above). Pinned that one test `KARAC_TEST_JIT=0` (it genuinely asserts interpreter-only behaviour) → **334/334** under JIT-default, **330/330** on the plain `--features llvm` interpreter lane (4 tests are lljit-gated). No `tests/repl.rs`-style mass pinning was needed — the `karac test` cli tests pass identically under JIT once the codegen gaps closed. design.md § Execution Model already documents JIT as the test/repl backend, so no spec change. **Cold-start measured (M5 Pro, release):** the JIT path spawns one `karac_jit_runner` subprocess per test, each re-initializing LLVM + JIT-compiling a synthesized main. Marginal **~15 ms/test** (1-test run 19.8 ms vs interpreter 8.8 ms; 20-test run 301.9 ms vs interpreter 12.8 ms → (301.9−19.8)/19 ≈ 14.8 ms/test). The tree-walk interpreter is near-flat (~9–13 ms total regardless of count). So JIT cold-start is **linear in test count (~15 ms × N)**; for a large suite the per-test LLVM re-init dominates. This is the documented v1 cold-start headline (design.md § Crash diagnostics / Execution Model); the per-test-subprocess LLVM-init cost is the obvious optimization target — a persistent runner (as the repl already uses) would amortize it — tracked as the follow-up below.

  - [x] **(follow-on) Amortize `karac test` JIT cold-start with a persistent runner.** ✓ **DONE 2026-06-01.** The flip's one-shot path spawned a fresh `karac_jit_runner` per test (~15 ms/test, dominated by per-process LLVM target init), so cost was linear ~15 ms × N. Replaced with a **persistent batch runner**: a new `karac_jit_runner --test-batch <prefix>` mode (one engine for the whole suite, LLVM init paid ONCE) + a parent-side `TestBatchRunner` (`src/test_jit_dispatch.rs`) that `cmd_test` creates once and drives per test via `dispatch(...)`. **Re-spawn-on-death** (mirroring the repl client): a failing test lowers to `emit_panic` → `exit(1)`, killing the shared runner, so the runner redirects each test's stdout/stderr to **parent-known** tempfiles (`<prefix>.<id>.{out,err}`) — the `KARAC_TEST_FAILURE` marker survives the death — and the parent reaps the exit code, maps the outcome, and lazily re-spawns for the next test. Each test's module is installed under its own resource tracker and **removed** after the run (unlike repl mode, which keeps cells alive) so test N+1's identical `main`/items don't collide. Per-test watchdog (kill-on-timeout, disambiguated from test-exit via the killed flag) preserves the c.4 deadline semantics. The one-shot `run_test_via_jit` + helpers were deleted (fully superseded). **Measured (M5 Pro, all-passing):** 20 tests 302 ms → **106 ms** (2.85×), 40 tests 600 ms → **239 ms** (2.5×); marginal **~5.6 ms/test** (was ~14.8 ms), 1-test ~tied (~20 ms; a Drop-shutdown poll at 1 ms granularity keeps the exit tail low). Mostly-passing suites — the common case — pay one engine init + one more per *failing* test. **No silent fallback:** under JIT-default a missing runner surfaces as a per-test `test_fail` ("binary not found"), not an interpreter downgrade. Regression test `test_jit_batch_runner_continues_after_failing_tests` (tests/cli.rs) pins the re-spawn contract (interleaved pass/fail/panic all report). Gates: cli 335/335 (lljit batch) + 331/331 (interp lane), repl_jit 23/23, lljit_prototype 16/16, fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs) clean. **Deeper follow-on — DONE 2026-06-01 (shared-module cache):** the residual per-test cost was the runner re-JIT-compiling the *whole* module per test (the per-test IR redefined every user fn). Now the suite's module is codegen'd + JIT-compiled **once** and referenced declare-only by each per-test `main`. New runner `module <ir_len>` command installs a persistent shared module (kept alive); per-test `main` modules emit the module's fns / `Type.method`s as `declare`s (`compile_to_ir_for_repl_cell` with `declare_only` = the module's concrete symbols) under a non-`main` entry symbol (`TEST_MAIN_SYMBOL` — a literal `main` collides with the process `_main`), Debugger-Contract globals suppressed (they live in the persistent module). New codegen `compile_to_ir_for_test_module` + a `force_external_linkage` flag emit the persistent module's fns as `External` (the pub/FFI-vs-`Internal` split would hide private fns from cross-module JIT linking, so the per-test declares wouldn't resolve). **Ambient-resource caveat (gated):** a module whose tests override an **ambient prelude resource** (`Clock`/`Env`/…) via `with_provider` runs in "full mode" (self-contained per-test module, no persistent install) — ambient override dispatch is decided per module at compile time (the `R.method()` call site emits a runtime branch only if a `with_provider` vtable for that resource exists *in the same module*), so splitting the `with_provider` site from the call site silently drops the override. User-resource (trait-ful / trait-less) fixtures are unaffected (their vtable comes from the impl blocks in the persistent module); only prelude-ambient fixtures trigger the per-module full-mode fallback (`TestBatchRunner::cache_module`, gated in `cmd_test` via `PRELUDE_EFFECT_RESOURCES`). **Measured (M5 Pro):** module-size sensitivity **~0.085 → ~0.017 ms/fn/test (~5×)** — 200 fns × 10 tests **240 ms → 82 ms (2.9×)**; per-test marginal **~5.6 → ~2.8 ms** (small module). The win compounds at scale (large module × many tests). Gates: cli 335/335 (lljit batch) + 331/331 (interp lane), codegen 1008/1008, repl_jit 23/23, repl 134/134, lljit_prototype 16/16, fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs) clean. **Third follow-on — DONE 2026-06-01 (signature-only skeleton):** the residual per-test cost was parent-side: `build_test_main_ir` cloned + resolved + typechecked + lowered the *whole* module per test (profiled on a 200-fn module: typecheck **~1.64 ms** of ~3.0 ms parent-side, ~54% — re-checking the 200 helper-fn bodies that are identical across tests and never emitted, since module fns are declare-only). Codegen does its *own* inference over the lowered AST and never consumes `TypeCheckResult`, so the per-test resolve/typecheck/lower exist *only* to lower the tiny synth `main` — yet they reprocessed every body. Now the runner caches a **signature-only skeleton** (`build_skeleton`, `src/test_jit_dispatch.rs`): the module's items with every concrete (non-generic) free-fn / impl-method body replaced by `{ unreachable() }` (contracts cleared; stub reuses the original body span so its span-keyed typecheck entries don't collide with the synth `main`'s all-`(0,0)` spans). Each **no-fixture** test clones + resolves + typechecks + lowers the skeleton instead of the real module — stub bodies process trivially while every signature the synth `main` needs stays in scope. **Soundness — why no-fixture only:** no stubbed body is ever emitted (concrete fns are declare-only → linked to the persistent module's real definitions; generic fns are emitted only on instantiation). A no-fixture synth `main` is just `{ test_fn(); }` — one call to the concrete, declare-only test fn — so it triggers **zero** local generic instantiation; a *fixture* `main` evaluates arbitrary constructor exprs that could instantiate a generic locally (emitted from the stub → wrong IR), so fixture tests keep the full module (`dispatch` gates on `fixtures.is_empty()`; ambient-fixture modules are already full-mode). Generic items keep real bodies in the skeleton (rare; correctness over the last µs). **Measured (M5 Pro, best-of-3 full-suite wall, skeleton on vs off):** 200 fns × 20 tests **160 → 120 ms (25%)**, 200 × 80 **500 → 360 ms (28%)**, 400 × 40 **400 → 270 ms (33%)**, 50 × 100 **420 → 340 ms (19%)** — the win grows with module_size × test_count. Per-test parent-side profile: typecheck **1.64 → 0.82 ms**, resolve **0.41 → 0.20 ms**, lower **0.21 → 0.01 ms**. Tests: `build_skeleton_stubs_concrete_bodies_only` (unit — stubs concretes, leaves generics/type-defs/signatures, preserves span, clears contracts) + `test_jit_skeleton_path_links_real_bodies_not_stubs` (cli E2E — free-fn / method / enum-match bodies all compute real results across item kinds, proving declare-only linkage to the persistent module's real bodies rather than the `unreachable()` stub; a leaked stub would abort, not return). Gates: cli 336/336 (lljit) + 331/331 (interp lane), lib 596/596, codegen 1008/1008, repl_jit 23/23, repl 134/134, lljit_prototype 16/16, lljit_e2e 15/15, karac_jit_runner_repl 3/3, fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs) clean. **Next lever — DONE 2026-06-02:** the parent-side floor was the per-test env build over the module's signatures (~0.82 ms typecheck + ~0.20 ms resolve on 200 fns); it's now *eliminated* for no-fixture tests by skipping the per-test resolve + typecheck entirely (the no-fixture synth `main` lowers to nothing, so it needs no typecheck result at all). See the `[x]` "Incremental module-env reuse for `karac test` JIT" entry below.

  - [x] **(follow-on, non-blocking) Incremental module-env reuse for `karac test` JIT.** ✓ **DONE 2026-06-02 — and the lever turned out simpler + stronger than "incremental check."** After the signature-only skeleton (third follow-on above), the per-test parent-side floor was the resolve + typecheck *env build* over the module's signatures — even with stubbed bodies it ran **~0.20 ms (resolve) + ~0.82 ms (typecheck) per test** on a 200-fn module, paid once per test though the module is identical across the whole suite. The entry originally proposed *incremental* reuse: build the module env once, then per test resolve+typecheck **only the synth `main`** against it and merge its `expr_types` / `call_type_subs` / `pattern_binding_types` into the cached result. **Reproducing the floor surfaced a better answer ([[feedback_reproduce_before_trusting_bug_diagnosis]]): for a no-fixture test the synth `main` needs no typecheck at all, so we skip the per-test resolve + typecheck *entirely*** — eliminating the whole ~1 ms/test floor instead of shrinking it, with no resolver/typechecker public-API surgery (the prerequisite that made the incremental version "the bulk of the work"). **Why sound — the no-fixture synth `main` is degenerate.** Lowering is the *only* consumer of the typecheck result in the per-test path (`compile_to_ir_for_repl_cell` takes just `&Program`; codegen does its own inference — the same fact the skeleton rests on). A no-fixture synth `main` is mechanically `{ test_fn(); }`: one call to the concrete, declare-only test fn, with no operators / method calls / patterns / `?` / `let` for the lowerer's `try_rewrite` to touch and no span-keyed side-tables it reads. So lowering it against a `TypeCheckResult::default()` (all-empty) is byte-identical to lowering it against the full module's result — minus the env build. The "incremental check" the entry proposed would have produced only empty/inert tables for this degenerate main anyway. **Scope = exactly the skeleton's no-fixture gate.** `build_test_main_ir` takes a `skip_typecheck` flag set by `dispatch` on the same `(fixtures.is_empty(), skeleton cached)` condition that selects the skeleton source; a *fixture* main has `let`-bound providers whose lowering genuinely needs typecheck (`var_type_names` for `infer_provider_type_name`), so it keeps the full pass. `TypeCheckResult` gained `#[derive(Default)]` (every field is a `HashMap` / `Vec` / `HashSet`). **Measured (M5 Pro, best-of-3 full-suite wall, skip on vs off — isolated by toggling the flag, same binary otherwise):** 200 fns × 20 tests **120 → 80 ms (~33%, ~2.0 ms/test)**, 400 fns × 40 tests **260 → 160 ms (~38%, ~2.5 ms/test)** — on top of the skeleton's win (the 200×20 "off" number, 120 ms, matches the skeleton-on baseline above), and compounding with module_size × test_count as predicted. Both synthetic suites pass 20/20 + 40/40 under the skip path (real computed results through the declare-only persistent module — a dropped/mislowered main would fail or abort, not return). Correctness covered by the existing `test_jit_skeleton_path_links_real_bodies_not_stubs` (cli E2E — every no-fixture test in the suite now routes through skip-typecheck; free-fn / method / enum-match bodies all compute real results). Surface: `src/test_jit_dispatch.rs` (`build_test_main_ir` `skip_typecheck` arm + `dispatch` gate), `src/typechecker.rs` (`TypeCheckResult` derive). Gates: cli 336/336 (lljit) + 331/331 (interp lane), lib 596/596, codegen 1008/1008, repl_jit 23/23, repl 134/134, lljit_prototype 16/16, lljit_e2e 15/15, karac_jit_runner_repl 3/3, fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs) clean.

  - [x] **(follow-on, non-blocking) Preserve the `provider_construction_failed` outcome distinction under JIT.** ✓ **DONE 2026-06-02.** Under the interpreter, a `with_provider` fixture ctor that faults surfaces as `provider_construction_failed` (the frame is never pushed, the body never runs, `duration_ms` is 0). Under JIT the synthesized main calls the ctor inline, so a faulting ctor *was* indistinguishable from a faulting body — the runner reported a generic `test_fail`, and `test_with_provider_constructor_failure_emits_structured_fail` was pinned `KARAC_TEST_JIT=0`. **Fix — per-ctor checkpoint markers (no `errdefer`/IR-level split needed):** `append_test_main` now emits `println("<PROVIDER_CTOR_MARKER>")` (`test_main_synth::PROVIDER_CTOR_MARKER`) immediately *after* each fixture's ctor `let`, so a marker prints only if that ctor constructed cleanly. On a fault the runner counts the markers in the test's captured stdout (`provider_ctor_fault_index`): fewer markers than fixtures means the (count)-th ctor faulted before the body ran, and `count` is the source-order index of the failing fixture. `dispatch` returns `JitTestResult::Completed { provider_ctor_failed: Some(idx), .. }`; `cmd_test` maps it to `test_fail_provider_construction_fields(t, &t.with_providers[idx].resource_path, msg)` — the *same* event the interpreter path emits (resource named, `duration_ms` 0). **Why stdout `println` markers:** `eprintln` / explicit `stderr.*` don't lower in codegen yet (interpreter-only — the "remaining ambient built-in resource methods" entry above), but `println` does; the runner redirects each test's stdout to a parent-known tempfile it reads for panic parsing then deletes, so markers are never surfaced, and only fixture tests (full codegen path, not the no-fixture skeleton fast-path) emit them. The stale c.3 comment in `src/cli.rs` that wrongly claimed gap-d had already restored this is corrected. `test_with_provider_constructor_failure_emits_structured_fail` is **un-pinned** — it now runs JIT-default under `lljit_prototype` (and interpreter under plain `--features llvm`), asserting identical `reason`/`resource`/`duration_ms` in both lanes. Multi-fixture index logic (count→fixture) unit-tested via `provider_ctor_fault_index_maps_marker_count_to_fixture` (count 0/1/2, pass, interleaved stdout) since the 2-fixture *E2E* path hits a separate pre-existing codegen gap (tracked in the new entry below). Surface: `src/test_main_synth.rs` (`PROVIDER_CTOR_MARKER` + per-ctor marker injection), `src/test_jit_dispatch.rs` (`provider_ctor_fault_index` + `JitTestResult::Completed.provider_ctor_failed`), `src/cli.rs` (`Completed`-arm mapping + comment fix). Gates: cli 336/336 (lljit) + 331/331 (interp lane), lib 597/597, codegen 1008/1008, repl_jit 23/23, lljit_prototype 16/16, lljit_e2e 15/15, fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs) clean.

  - [x] **(bug) Trait-less user-resource `with_provider` fixtures mis-codegen — three distinct root causes.** ✓ **FIXED 2026-06-03.** Surfaced 2026-06-02 while testing the `provider_construction_failed` slice above ([[feedback_surfaced_bugs_tracked_or_fixed]]). **Reproduction corrected the diagnosis on every axis** ([[feedback_reproduce_before_trusting_bug_diagnosis]]): it is NOT "multiple fixtures" (a *single* trait-less user-resource fixture fails), NOT JIT-only (two of the three causes reproduce in plain AOT `karac build`), and NOT "the pre-pass records only one resource per module" (that hypothesis was wrong). Trait-less user resources (`effect resource R;`, no provider trait) compile + run correctly under the interpreter but were broken under codegen for three independent reasons:
    1. **Split-module under the JIT test cache (JIT-only).** Trait-less dispatch is module-local: with no trait there is no canonical method order, so codegen derives it per module from the override type's inherent impl *at the `with_provider` site*, and the `R.method()` call site can only dispatch when the `with_provider` is in the SAME module. The persistent-module cache splits them (the `with_provider` lands in the per-test `main`, the call site in the shared module) → the call site found no order and returned `0`. This is the exact module-locality constraint the persistent-runner entry already documented for prelude-ambient resources, but the full-mode gate (`ambient_fixture_modules`) only covered *prelude* names. **Fix:** the gate (now `full_mode_fixture_modules`, `src/cli.rs`) routes a test to full mode if any fixture resource is NOT a trait-ful user resource — i.e. prelude ambient OR trait-less user. Trait-ful user resources (`effect resource R: T;`) stay on the cache: their vtable comes from the impl blocks in the persistent module and the trait pins a canonical order the call site shares (verified: trait-ful fixture passes on the cache path).
    2. **Call-ctor type inference in the eager pre-pass (AOT + JIT).** `emit_ambient_provider_vtables` inferred the override type only from `let p = StructLiteral` / inline struct-literal providers; a provider bound to a *constructor call* (`let p = make_foo();`, `Type.new()`) couldn't be typed, so the vtable + method order were never recorded → `with_provider[R]: no method order for resource`, even for a single fixture, even in plain `karac build`. (The *real* `with_provider` lowering already handles call-bound providers via `var_type_names`; only the pre-pass didn't.) **Fix:** `collect_ctor_return_types` (`src/codegen/provider.rs`) maps free-fn / inherent-method callee keys → return-type name; `ambient_provider_type` resolves a `Call` provider through it.
    3. **Nested-block binding reset (AOT + JIT).** `scan_block_for_ambient_overrides` reset its `bindings` map per block, so a nested `with_provider[B](pb, …)` inside a block-bodied closure couldn't resolve `pb` when it was bound in the *outer* block → inner override dropped. **Fix:** thread inherited provider bindings into the nested-block scan.
    All three reproduce-confirmed before + after. Tests: `test_e2e_with_provider_trait_less_call_ctor` + `test_e2e_with_provider_nested_block_closures_two_resources` (codegen E2E, AOT — causes 2 & 3); `test_with_provider_trait_less_user_resource_fixture_dispatches` (cli, two trait-less fixtures, struct-lit + call ctor — cause 1) + `test_with_provider_second_constructor_failure_names_that_resource` (cli, 2nd ctor faults → `provider_construction_failed` names the *second* resource, exercising causes 1+2 and the prior slice's marker-count→index recovery end-to-end). Surface: `src/cli.rs` (full-mode gate), `src/codegen/provider.rs` (`collect_ctor_return_types` + `ctor_call_key` + call-arm in `ambient_provider_type` + inherited-bindings threading). Gates: cli 338/338 (lljit) + 333/333 (interp lane), lib 597/597, codegen 1014/1014, repl_jit 23/23, lljit_prototype 16/16, lljit_e2e 15/15, fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs) clean.

  **⚠ Both named gates cleared 2026-05-31, but a flip attempt broke tests and was reverted — a THIRD blocker surfaced (sub-item below).** L581 W5 closed and L601 Level 2 DWARF (both parts) landed, so on paper this was unblocked. The flip shipped as `2edff685` (the `src/repl.rs` half only — the symmetric `src/cli.rs` edit + tracker edit were lost to tool-output corruption that session, so it landed as an inconsistent *half*-flip). It broke **40 of 134 `tests/repl.rs` cases under `cargo test --features lljit_prototype --test repl`**; plain `cargo test` stayed green because the JIT dispatch in `eval_cell` is `#[cfg(feature = "lljit_prototype")]`'d out, so a non-feature CI lane would NOT catch this. Reverted as `e9fd5b1d`; main is back to the env-gated opt-in (`== Ok("1")`) and feature-gated repl tests are 134/134. Do NOT re-attempt the flip until the blocker below clears.

  **↻ Diagnosis corrected 2026-05-31 (reproduction-backed).** An earlier version of this block claimed the 40 failures meant "cross-cell redeclaration, provider scopes, and meta-commands are interpreter-only." **That was a hypothesis shipped as fact and it is wrong.** Reproduction: `KARAC_REPL_JIT=1 cargo test --features lljit_prototype --test repl` naively shows 40 fails, but **25 are a pure test-harness artifact** — `tests/repl.rs` never sets `KARAC_JIT_RUNNER` (unlike `tests/repl_jit.rs`), so cell-running tests die with "karac_jit_runner binary not found." Build the runner (`cargo build --features lljit_prototype --bin karac_jit_runner`) and export `KARAC_JIT_RUNNER=<path>`; failures drop to **15**. Redeclaration was never broken — `redeclaring_{item,struct,enum,const}_across_cells`, `item_definition_persists`, `struct_definition_persists`, `statement_cell_*` all PASS under JIT with the runner wired.   - [x] **`env.set` + `clock.now` not handled in codegen.** ✓ **Fixed 2026-05-31** (`6eac2803`). REAL user-facing — and the "JIT REPL bug" framing was itself too narrow: **this was never JIT-specific.** AOT `karac build` of `env.set("x","y")` failed identically (`codegen: no handler for method 'set' on variable 'env'`). The entire ambient built-in *resource-method-call* family (the interpreter's BuiltinDefault dispatch in `src/interpreter/resource_method.rs`) had **zero** codegen lowering; the JIT-REPL `cell_effect_*` tests merely surfaced it first. The 3 failing `cell_effect` tests asserted on `r.effect_footer` / `cell_effect_history()`, both computed by *static* analysis from cell source — they failed only because the cell errored out at codegen, so unblocking codegen flips them green with no footer-path changes. Fix: codegen counterpart of the BuiltinDefault path — runtime FFIs `karac_runtime_env_set` / `karac_runtime_clock_now` (`runtime/src/lib.rs`) + `compile_ambient_resource_method` / `ambient_resource_for_alias` (`src/codegen/method_call.rs`), reached as the last resort before the dispatch-fail error so a user `with_provider` override still wins first (via `try_compile_provider_dispatch`); guards on `self.variables` so a local named `env` shadows the ambient resource; `extract_string_ptr_len` bumped to `pub(super)`. **Surfaced + fixed mid-slice:** the LLJIT path's `dlsym` symbol-search generator couldn't resolve the new FFIs (they weren't in `__preserve_no_mangle_symbols`), which **hung the runner subprocess** rather than erroring — added both to the keep-list. Took the JIT-REPL `cell_effect_*` tests **3→0** failing (15→12 real repl failures); AOT compiles+runs both. New E2E test `test_e2e_ambient_resource_clock_now_and_env_set` (codegen 1001/1001, memory_sanitizer 73/73, interpreter repl 134/134). **Scope deliberately narrow:** only `env.set` + `clock.now` (what the tests need); sibling ambient methods get their own entry below.

  - [ ] **Lower the remaining ambient built-in resource methods in codegen (`env.var` / `env.args`, `rand`, `stdin`, `fs.*`, explicit `stdout/stderr.*`).** Surfaced by the `env.set` fix above (`6eac2803`): the BuiltinDefault dispatch family is interpreter-only across the board, not just `env.set`. `compile_ambient_resource_method` currently returns a precise `"ambient resource method '<R>.<m>' is not yet lowered (interpreter-only)"` error for every pair except `Env.set` / `Clock.now`, so any AOT/JIT program calling e.g. `env.var(name)` or `rand.next_u64()` fails to compile. Each needs a runtime FFI + an arm + a keep-list entry; the harder ones return aggregates (`env.var → Result[String, VarError]`, `stdin.read_line → Result[String, IoError]`) so they pull in enum-layout construction from a runtime-returned C string, unlike the scalar `clock.now` / void `env.set`. Not a v1 blocker unless a workload needs them — the interpreter path covers `karac run`. Mirror the interpreter arms in `src/interpreter/resource_method.rs` and the alias table in `ambient_resource_for_alias`.

  - [x] **JIT REPL bug — duplicate-symbol on impl-method re-install across cells.** ✓ **Fixed 2026-05-31** (`09c04d90`). REAL user-facing. **Tracker had conflated two distinct tests under one description — reproduction split them.** Only `binding_outside_provider_scope_survives_end_provide` actually hit `add_ir_module: Duplicate definition of symbol 'FakeClock.now'`: slice B.4's declare-only dedup (`jit_installed_fns`) tracked only free functions (`Item::Function`), never impl methods, so each cell re-emitted the method body on top of the prior install. Fix: impl methods install under the LLVM symbol `Type.method` (same keyspace `declare_only_fns` already uses), so (a) codegen `compile_program` skips impl-method body emission when the qualified name is in `declare_only_fns` (no-op for AOT — set always empty there); (b) `run_cell_via_jit` records each non-generic impl method under its `Type.method` key after a clean cell; (c) new `pub(crate)` `impl_target_name_for_repl` (gated on `lljit_prototype`) keeps the two key computations in lockstep. JIT repl 12→11 failing; codegen E2E 1001/1001 (no AOT regression), repl_jit 22/22, interpreter repl 134/134. **The OTHER test the old description named — `run_time_wraps_cell_body_when_provider_active` — fails on a different root cause, split out below.**

  - [x] **`with_provider` override of an ambient prelude resource (`Clock`/`Env`/…) by a statically-typed provider.** ✓ **Fixed 2026-05-31** (`5d9b13a6`). REAL user-facing; **never JIT-specific** — AOT `karac build` failed identically with `with_provider: unknown effect resource 'Clock' (no resource ID assigned)`. design.md §4344/§6409 specify built-in `with_provider` override as a first-class v1 feature for deterministic-replay testing. The gap was two-sided: (a) the `with_provider[Clock]` site couldn't be lowered (ambient `PRELUDE_EFFECT_RESOURCES` get no codegen resource ID / provider trait / vtable — only explicit `effect resource R: T` do), and (b) ambient method call sites (`Clock.now()`) never consulted any provider. **Chose Plan approach B/C (static monomorphization)** after a design pass + user scope decision: when the override's concrete type is statically known at the `with_provider` site (struct literal / typed binding — the same shapes `infer_provider_type_name` already requires for *user* resources), the override is entirely compile-time — no runtime provider-stack push/pop, no synthesized vtable. New `Codegen::ambient_provider_overrides` (LIFO compile-time `resource → (type, data ptr)` scope frames); `compile_with_provider_ambient` pushes/compiles-body/pops; `try_compile_ambient_override` lowers an in-scope ambient call to a direct `@Type.method` call, wired into both the lowercase (`compile_ambient_resource_method`) and capitalized (`call_dispatch`, before the generic assoc-call fall-through that previously yielded const-0) paths. Runtime-typed providers (fn-return) get a precise error — a deliberate v1 non-goal that **matches the user-resource path's identical restriction**, so expressiveness is symmetric (design.md-faithful "works identically to user-declared resources"), no new runtime FFI/ABI. **Why B not A:** A (full runtime vtable dispatch for ambient only) would have made built-in primitives *more* capable than user resources — inverting the design promise — for runtime-typed providers no test/example exercises; full runtime parity, if ever needed, is a separate *unified* user+ambient slice with B as its devirt fast-path (tracked below). Closes the AOT gap (verified `karac build` repro prints 42 = `karac run`) and **5** repl tests (JIT repl 11→6): the 3 named blockers (`run_time_wraps_cell_body_when_provider_active`, `nested_close_prunes_only_inner_scope_bindings`, `reference_after_end_provide_surfaces_notebook_aware_tail`) + 2 export tests depending on provider scopes. New E2E `test_e2e_with_provider_ambient_override`; codegen 1004/1004, memory_sanitizer 73/73, repl_jit 22/22, interpreter repl 134/134.

  - [ ] **(deferred, non-blocking) Unify codegen provider dispatch with the interpreter's full runtime semantics (runtime-typed providers, user + ambient).** Both the user-resource vtable path and the new ambient static-monomorphization path (`5d9b13a6`) are **static-shape-only**: the provider's concrete type must be inferable at the `with_provider` site (`infer_provider_type_name` — struct literal / typed binding). A runtime-chosen provider (e.g. `with_provider[Clock](pick_clock(), ...)` where `pick_clock()` returns one of two types) compiles in the interpreter but errors on the codegen path. No test or design example exercises this today, and the static subset is design.md-faithful (§4344/§6409 "works identically to user-declared resources" — true, since *both* paths are static-only). When/if a real DI-style runtime-typed-provider workload surfaces, the right slice is **unified** runtime-stack dispatch for user + ambient resources together (emit vtables, runtime `karac_provider_lookup` + indirect call at each site), keeping the current static path as the devirtualization fast-path when the type is statically known. NOT a v1 blocker; the interpreter path covers `karac run`.

  - [x] **JIT-path stdout capture dropped per-line newlines.** ✓ **Fixed 2026-05-31** (`49ac8130`). REAL user-facing — found while reproducing the "6 remaining re-gating" bucket, which was itself a mis-diagnosis ([[feedback_reproduce_before_trusting_bug_diagnosis]] again). The interpreter's `captured_output` retains each line's trailing `\n` (`write_stdout` pushes `format!("{s}\n")`) because the sole consumer rebuilds the raw stream with `stdout.join("")`. The JIT runner's `bytes_to_stdout_lines` split on `\n` and *dropped* the newline, so `join("")` glued adjacent prints — two `println`s collapsed to `"78"` instead of `"7\n8\n"`. Switched to `split_inclusive('\n')` (round-trips through `join("")` for newline-terminated / bare-`print` / interior-blank / empty shapes; unit test `bytes_to_stdout_lines_round_trips_all_shapes`). **Why it hid so long:** every `repl_jit.rs` assertion uses `.stdout.trim()`, masking a missing-newline-*between*-prints defect; it surfaced only in the two `tests/repl.rs` cases asserting exact multi-line output (`let_value_snapshot_chains_across_three_cells`, `export_reproduces_observable_behavior`), both now green under JIT. JIT repl 6→4 failing; interpreter repl 134/134, repl_jit 22/22, fmt + clippy ×3 cfgs clean.

  - [x] **JIT REPL test re-gating — snapshot-inspector introspection surface.** ✓ **Done 2026-05-31** (`test(repl): gate 4 snapshot-inspector tests…` commit). Decision (user-confirmed long-term-lens call): **gate to the interpreter path, do NOT build a JIT-side inspector.** The 4 `let_value_snapshot_{records_cached_value,rebinding_drops_stale_entry,reset_clears_cache,unused_binding_still_visible}` tests assert against `Session::let_snapshots()`, an interpreter-path value cache the JIT path deliberately replaces with runner-side globals (so the inspector is empty under JIT). Exposing JIT state through the inspector would mean marshalling each binding's typed value back across the subprocess boundary and reconstructing an interpreter `Value` per-type — a parallel, introspection-only copy of the runner-side store that already does the real work, plus a two-stores-must-agree sync obligation. That inverts the cost: the durable architectural fact is that interpreter and JIT have *legitimately different* internal value representations; gating *encodes* that ("this probe inspects the interpreter cache; JIT's equivalent is verified behaviorally in `repl_jit.rs`"), the inspector-unify option papers over it. **Verify-then-gate discipline applied:** cross-checked all 4 against `repl_jit.rs` behavioral coverage first — `records_cached_value`→`repl_jit_runs_let_bindings`/`_let_rhs_is_not_re_evaluated`, `reset_clears_cache`→`repl_jit_reset_clears_snapshot_state`, `unused_binding_still_visible`→`repl_jit_runs_let_bindings` (read-in-next-cell, same shape); the one gap was **cross-type rebind** (the i64→String type-confusion guard `rebinding_drops_stale_entry` exists for — JIT shadow tests only covered same-type), filled with new `repl_jit_cross_type_rebind_uses_new_value` (passes — the shadow-drop evicts the stale i64 snapshot global). Implementation: scoped per-test `pin_interpreter(&mut s)` helper (`#[cfg(feature="lljit_prototype")] set_jit_enabled_for_tests(false)`, no-op without the feature) — explicitly NOT a blanket suite-wide disable. **JIT-repl failures now 0** (full `tests/repl` passes 134/134 under `KARAC_REPL_JIT=1`); `repl_jit` 23/23; plain `repl` 134/134; fmt + clippy ×3 cfgs clean.

  - [x] **`karac test` JIT default — analogous audit.** ✓ **Done 2026-05-31.** Ran the symmetric reproduction: the full codegen E2E corpus under `KARAC_TEST_JIT=1` (routes ~1004 programs through the LLJIT compile + `karac_jit_runner` subprocess path, the same runner the `karac test` command uses). **Found one real codegen/linkage gap of the env.set class** → ✅ **FIXED** (`fix(runtime): preserve contract predicate FFIs…` commit, `037ce290`): `karac_runtime_enter_predicate` / `_exit_predicate` / `_panic_prefix` were missing from `__preserve_no_mangle_symbols`, so any contract (`requires`/`ensures`/`invariant`) program — or one reaching the `panic_prefix`-bearing panic/bounds path — failed to materialize `main` under the runner (`Symbols not found: [_karac_runtime_*]`). Corpus 119 failures → 1; confirmed on the actual `karac test` command (a contract test flipped test_fail → test_pass). **[[feedback_reproduce_before_trusting_bug_diagnosis]] near-miss:** ~98 of the 119 presented only as empty stdout (`left:""`) because their assertions printed stdout but not the symbol-bearing stderr — I nearly bucketed them as a harness artifact; reproduction (the fix cleared all 98) proved they were the same `panic_prefix` omission. The remaining **1** is a separate, non-blocking harness flake → own sub-entry below. **W5 + Level 2 DWARF already cleared (2026-05-31), so this was the last codegen/linkage prerequisite — the flip entry above is now unblocked** (remaining = the mechanical flip slice itself). (remaining-ambient-methods and the unified-runtime-dispatch item are separate non-blocking follow-ons.)

  - [ ] **(non-blocking) Codegen E2E suite flakes under `KARAC_TEST_JIT=1` — shifting-identity failure over the full 1004-program run.** After the predicate-FFI fix (`037ce290`) the corpus under `KARAC_TEST_JIT=1` is 1003/1004, but the single failing test's *identity shifts* run-to-run (observed: `test_e2e_mut_ref_map_param_method_dispatch`, `test_enum_variant_name_collision_with_seeded_other_is_deterministic`) — each passes in isolation under JIT and consistently on AOT (committed gate 1004/1004), and fails only inside the full sequential/parallel JIT-dispatch run. Shifting identity + isolation-clean + AOT-clean over 1004 sequential `karac_jit_runner` subprocess spawns points at a test-harness resource/ordering flake (subprocess spawn/flush variance, `/tmp` IR churn, or process-global codegen state accumulated across compiles), NOT a runner codegen/linkage gap. **Crucially NOT a flip blocker:** the `karac test` *command* spawns one runner per test in its own subprocess with no cross-test accumulation, so it doesn't share this harness's failure mode (verified: contract + array tests pass per-test on the command). Root-cause before trusting `KARAC_TEST_JIT=1 cargo test --test codegen` as a clean gate signal; until then, treat that harness mode as 1003/1004-with-one-known-flake.

- [ ] **REPL value-snapshot for non-primitive aggregates (B.5.3d).** Extends the B.5.1 / B.5.2 / B.5.3a-c snapshot port to `struct` / `enum` / tuple / `Option` / `Rc` / `Arc` / closure / `SortedSet` `let` bindings. Each carries its own ownership story (RC inc/dec, drop-fn dispatch, slice lifetimes, closure capture environment) that needs its own design pass — the shallow shape transfers that work for Vec/Map/Set primitive containers don't generalize to types that own heap pointers behind a refcount or a drop fn. SortedSet is the closest adjacent shape but distinct from Map/Set at runtime (B-tree-backed, not `karac_map_*`), so it can't piggyback on the B.5.3b/c handle story and needs its own treatment. Until any of these lands, the v1 source-replay fallback gives correct (re-evaluating) semantics — the let RHS re-runs on each cell rather than reading from a snapshot global. Deferred until a concrete REPL workload surfaces friction; ordering when prioritized: `Option` and shared (`Rc`/`Arc`) types are the most REPL-relevant because they're common in interactive exploration, followed by struct/enum payload types; closures last (the capture environment opens questions the snapshot mechanism wasn't designed for).

- [x] **Crash diagnostics — Level 2 (DWARF instruction-level).** ✓ **Closed 2026-05-31.** P0 v1. ~3–6 weeks estimated. Shipped in two parts; **both landed 2026-05-31** — part 1 (the user-facing headline) and part 2 (the DWARF-emission *bonus*), each tracked below.

  **✓ Part 1 — panic location (`panic at <file>:<line>:<col> in <fn>`). Shipped 2026-05-31.** Delivers the design's stated user-facing outcome (design.md § Crash diagnostics: "users see `panic at file:line:col in fn_name`"). `Codegen` gained `current_span: Option<Span>`, set at the top of `compile_expr`; `emit_panic` (`src/codegen/runtime.rs`) reads it together with `source_filename` + `current_fn_name` and emits the location as **compile-time-constant** `printf` operands. **Deliberate deviation from this entry's original "runtime panic handler walks the stack … via DWARF" wording:** there is NO runtime DWARF walk and NO runtime symbolizer. The panic path is reachable from every program (bounds checks), so a DWARF symbolizer there would re-add the ~57 KiB gimli/addr2line/object tree that the **Phase 3 binary-size fix deliberately dead-strips** (see the Phase 3 entry below) onto *every* binary. Constant operands give the identical user-facing string at **zero** binary-size cost, and are more reliable than address symbolization. Gated on `source_filename` (the CLI build/run path threads it; bare-IR tests/dumps don't), mirroring the sibling `?`-error-return-trace, so every existing no-filename panic test stays green. Verified end-to-end: a CLI-built binary (`karac build crash.kara`) prints `panic at ./crash.kara:3:16 in main: vec index out of bounds`, exit 1 (captured byte-for-byte). Tests: 3 new in `tests/codegen.rs` (`test_e2e_panic_location_vec_oob`, `_has_line_col` pinning source line 4, `_bare_form_without_filename` guarding the gate); full codegen suite 997/997; fmt + clippy clean.

  - [x] **Part 2 — DWARF debug-info emission via `DIBuilder` (the gdb/lldb *bonus*).** ✓ **Shipped 2026-05-31** (`50d0dd8e`, new module `src/codegen/debug_info.rs`; fmt cleanup `136b2d42`). Checkbox synced to the on-main code 2026-05-31 — the parent (603) was flipped `[x]` at part-2 ship but this sub-box was left stale. Emit `DICompileUnit` / `DIFile` / `DISubprogram` per function and `DILocation` per instruction (the `current_span` plumbing from part 1 already supplies line/col at every site, so wiring `builder.set_current_debug_location` is the mechanical remainder), set the `"Debug Info Version"` module flag, and `dibuilder.finalize()` before codegen. inkwell 0.9 exposes the full surface (`Module::create_debug_info_builder` → `(DebugInfoBuilder, DICompileUnit)`, `create_file` / `create_function` / `create_subroutine_type` / `create_debug_location` / `finalize`; `DWARFSourceLanguage`/`DWARFEmissionKind` enums). Value is purely the design's stated *bonus*: `gdb`/`lldb` symbolic backtraces — most relevant on the **JIT path** (REPL/test, in-process via ORC's GDB JIT interface) where binary size is moot. **Must be gated** (a `-g`/`--debug-info` build flag, default **off**) so AOT release binaries don't carry `.debug_*` sections and regress the Phase 1–3 size floor (on macOS Mach-O, DWARF stays in `.o`/`.dSYM` and `strip -x` drops the debug map, so the gate is mostly a Linux-ELF concern — but it must be explicit, not incidental). Closes the literal "DWARF instruction-level" name and the L581 "wrapping done" criterion's "Level 2 DWARF preserved" clause. Deferred from the 2026-05-31 part-1 ship: it is a separable bonus, not the headline, and warrants the gating design pass above rather than being rushed in behind part 1.

- [ ] **Crash diagnostics — Level 3 (rustc-style snippets).** Builds on Level 2's DWARF + a diagnostic-formatter integration: panics print snippets with caret pointers and AST-node-aware messages (e.g., `this index operation panicked` rather than `panicked at <addr>`). P1, ships as a v1 patch release. ~3–4 additional weeks.

- [x] **Phase 1 binary-size optimization: `strip -x` + `panic = "abort"` in runtime release profile.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-07. P0 v1. Single PR. Two changes: (1) add `strip -x <output>` after the `cc` invocation in `link_executable` (`src/codegen.rs` ~line 121) — verified -18% on a representative binary (1.4 MB → 1.18 MB); (2) set `panic = "abort"` in `runtime/Cargo.toml`'s `[profile.release]` — drops `__eh_frame` + `__unwind_info` (~114 KB on a representative binary). Ship `panic = "abort"` unconditionally for v1 — `catch_panic` (currently P1 deferred) lands its own build-profile gate (kernel/embedded → abort, default → unwind) when it ships, not pre-built here. Combined estimated effect: 1.4 MB → ~900 KB.

- [x] **Phase 2 binary-size optimization: cross-archive LTO + DCE flags.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-12. P0 v1. Two changes: (1) add `-Wl,-dead_strip` (macOS) / `-Wl,--gc-sections` (Linux) to the `cc` invocation in `link_executable_impl` (`src/codegen.rs:240`) — skipped under sanitizer flags so ASAN's interceptor globals survive; (2) set `lto = "thin"` in the workspace root's `[profile.release]` (Cargo rejected per-package `lto` with the same error as per-package `panic`, so this applies to every workspace member's release build — modest compile-time cost on the compiler crate is acceptable for the runtime-archive size win on every Kāra program). Linux Mach-O note moot here — macOS subsections-via-symbols is always-on; Linux ELF gets `-ffunction-sections -fdata-sections` from rustc's default codegen-units behavior under thin LTO. **Measured on the LeetCode #1665 sort-heavy bench:** 2,667,576 B → 383,944 B (−85.6%, 2.5 MB → 375 KB), now ~21% **smaller** than the equivalent `rustc -O` binary (483,448 B). Top symbol `karac_vec_sort_by` shrank 161 KB → 23 KB (unused fast-path closures inlined and DCE'd); the full tokio / hyper / h2 / serde_json subgraph dropped to zero bytes because this program imports no http / json modules. Text-symbol count fell from 3,759 to 220. **E2E gate:** `cargo test --features llvm` clean on macOS (one flaky http_server smoke test from a parallel-port race, pre-existing and unrelated; passes under `--test-threads=1`). **Keep-list re-audit** — see `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` updated 2026-05-12: 37 `#[no_mangle]` exports total (was 19 at original sweep; new entries since 2026-05-07: 6 `karac_provider_*`, 3 `karac_runtime_for_each_active_frame` / `_get_current_frame` / `_has_debug_metadata`, `karac_runtime_list_par_blocks_into`, 4 `karac_runtime_http_*` getters/setters, 2 `karac_runtime_serve_http*`, 4 `karac_runtime_json_*`, `karac_vec_sort_by`), still zero `#[used]` / `#[link_section]` / `#[ctor]` / `#[dtor]` attributes. All reachable via direct codegen-emitted call sites, so DCE preserves them through entry-point reachability without needing explicit `#[used]`.

- [x] **Pre-flight runtime symbol sweep (gates Phase 2 LTO/DCE).** ✓ Landed 2026-05-07 (bundled with Phase 1 binary-size slice). Sweep audit lives at `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md`: 19 `#[no_mangle]` exports documented (`karac_par_run`, `karac_error_trace_*`, `karac_string_clone`, 15 `karac_map_*`), 1 libc `extern "C"` import (`atexit`), 1 private `extern "C"` callback (`print_trace_at_exit`), zero `#[used]` / `#[link_section]` / `#[ctor]` / `#[dtor]` attributes. Phase 2 LTO/DCE PR re-runs the audit + uses the file as its keep-list reference. Original entry: grep `runtime/src/` for `#[used]`, `#[link_section]`, `#[ctor]`, `#[dtor]`, `#[no_mangle]`, and `extern "C"` declarations before enabling LTO. Document any findings in the Phase 2 PR's checklist as a keep-list — symbols DCE would strip incorrectly otherwise. The runtime is 726 LOC across 2 files; this is a 5-minute task, not a design question. Phase 2 PR's checklist: (1) sweep done, (2) flagged symbols documented as keep-list, (3) LTO enabled, (4) E2E tests pass, (5) measured size delta reported.

  *Bundled into Phase 1 binary-size slice.* See entry above (`Phase 1 binary-size optimization`) — the symbol sweep is sub-step (a) of that slice's plan, since the audit pairs naturally with the build-config changes.

- [x] **Phase 3 binary-size regression fix: don't co-emit the runtime `rlib` in the production staticlib build.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-30 (`b41c42f6`). The auto-par binary floor had silently regressed 295.7 KiB → 417.7 KiB (+41%) at `712d8f4d`, which added `rlib` to `runtime/Cargo.toml`'s `[lib] crate-type = ["staticlib", "rlib"]` so the opt-in `lljit_prototype` test path could consume the runtime as a Rust dep. **Root cause:** under `lto = "fat"`, emitting both `staticlib` and `rlib` in one `cargo build` invocation defeats the staticlib's cross-module DCE — the linker can no longer prove std's panic / alloc-error default hooks unreachable, so the full DWARF backtrace symbolizer (gimli + addr2line + object + rustc_demangle, ~57 KiB) survives `-dead_strip` into *every* AOT binary, even pure-compute programs. Bisected with clean rebuilds (the first bisect attempt was contaminated by incremental builds — it falsely fingered a test-only commit; `cargo clean -p karac-runtime` between steps was required) over a C stub referencing `karac_par_reduce` linked against the archive with `-dead_strip`; `-Wl,-why_live` traced two anchor paths (`resolve_pool_workers → env::var → panic → default_hook → symbolize` and `par_reduce → handle_alloc_error → default_alloc_error_hook → symbolize`), both gone once the symbolizer is dead-strippable. **Fix:** build the production staticlib with `cargo rustc -p karac-runtime --release --crate-type staticlib` (emits only the staticlib → fat-LTO + `-dead_strip` strip the symbolizer). `rlib` stays declared in the manifest; it's only materialized by `cargo {build,test} --features lljit_prototype`. Updated CLAUDE.md, `resolve_runtime_path`'s error message, and the `crate-type` comment (which had wrongly claimed AOT builds were unaffected). Verified: count.kara (par) 417.7 → 360.4 KiB, two-sum hash_map.kara 393.9 → 343.2 KiB, both sinks byte-identical; archive 45 MB → 9.6 MB. Surfaced by the kara-katas JSON-bench sweep (`kara-katas/BENCH_JSON.md` + `scripts/bench-compare.py`) comparing fresh #1/#204 numbers against their committed README baselines.

- [x] **Phase 4 binary-size: gate the runtime's TLS / networking surface so compute-only binaries don't link it (residual ~+45 KiB).** ✓ DONE 2026-05-30 (Part A `a3c689f1` + Part B, both sub-slices below). The auto-par floor for compute-only programs is back to **295.7 KiB** (the pre-regression baseline); a `karac build` of a TLS-using program transparently links the full archive. Root cause turned out to be rustls/ring alone (not "HTTP/tokio" broadly — tokio/hyper/mio/serde_json are DCE-clean), gated behind a runtime `tls` cargo feature and selected per-program by scanning the emitted object's symbols. Historical analysis retained below. After the Phase 3 fix above, the auto-par floor sat at ~360 KiB — still ~+65 KiB over the 295.7 KiB pre-regression baseline. Bisected (clean rebuilds, same C-stub harness) to `fcb1f905` (rustls server-side TLS FFI, +~49 KiB) plus a smaller follow-on bump from the same dep-bulk era (~+16 KiB). `bloaty` attributes the dominant chunk to `_rust_eh_personality` (+45.5 KiB) — libstd **unwinding** machinery. Mechanism: `fcb1f905` added only a new `runtime/src/tls.rs` module + `rustls`/`ring` deps (one `pub mod tls;` line, no changes to the par/shared path), and **no TLS/rustls/tokio symbols are reachable** in a par binary (all dead-stripped — verified 0). But pulling rustls/ring into the crate drags in unwinding-aware instantiations of *shared* std code (io/alloc error paths) that `par_reduce` also touches; once those carry unwind landing pads, `-dead_strip` can't drop the eh machinery from the compute path. This is the **"feature-gate HTTP/tokio/TLS in karac-runtime"** item flagged as a "big potential win, real refactor" in the line-595 Phase 2 entry's tokio/hyper note. **Fix direction (each a real slice, none quick):** (a) feature-gate the runtime's TLS/networking/HTTP surface behind a cargo feature so `karac build` of a compute-only program links a `tls`-less archive — blocked on the runtime not being one monolithic module surface (tokio reactor + hyper acceptor live alongside the simple primitives, same constraint noted at line 595/281); (b) `-Z build-std` with `panic_immediate_abort` to drop libstd's precompiled unwind paths wholesale — nightly-only, not v1-viable. **Regression guard now in place:** `kara-katas/scripts/bench-compare.py` flags deterministic binary-size deltas vs a committed baseline, so any further floor creep fails loudly on the next bench sweep. Not a v1 blocker (compute binaries still ship; the cost is footprint, not correctness), but the path back toward 295.7 KiB runs through (a).

  **Scoping validated 2026-05-30 (synthetic isolation experiment, `/tmp/szexp`).** Built minimal staticlib crates (compute-only export + a dead-stripped networking export referencing a candidate dep) under the same profile (`lto="fat"`, `panic="abort"`, `opt-level=3`, `codegen-units=1`) and linked a C `main` calling only the compute export with `-Wl,-dead_strip`. Results: (1) a **referenced-but-dead-stripped** `rustls`-using export adds **+48.5 KiB** to the compute binary (278.3 → 326.8 KiB) even though `nm` shows 0 of its symbols survive — `_rust_eh_personality` + `__Unwind_Backtrace` stay because the compute path's own panic/alloc landing pads share the unwind machinery rustls drags in from libstd. `-dead_strip` provably cannot recover this; the code must be **compiled out**. (2) An **unreferenced** dep is fully DCE'd — 0 inflation. (3) Crucially, a referenced-but-dead-stripped **tokio+hyper** export adds **only 16 bytes** — tokio/hyper/mio/socket2/serde_json are unwind-clean, which is exactly why the 295.7 KiB baseline was lean *despite* already shipping them. **So the residual is rustls/ring alone, and the fix is far narrower than "gate all networking": gate only the TLS surface** — the `rustls` / `rustls-pemfile` / `tokio-rustls` / `webpki-roots` / `ureq`(tls) deps plus the code that references them: `runtime/src/tls.rs` (whole module), the WS-over-TLS path in `event_loop.rs` (`ws_accept_tls` / `ws_handshake_conn_tls` + the `tls::lookup_session(fd)` branches in `ws_send`/`ws_recv`), and in `lib.rs` `karac_runtime_serve_https` + the `ureq`-backed HTTP client (`http_client_agent`, `read_response_body_bytes`, `capture_response_headers`, the `_client_get`/`_post`/`_send`/`_builder_send` FFI) + the `tls::*`/`serve_https`/`ws_accept_tls` entries in `__preserve_no_mangle_symbols`. tokio/hyper/tcp/plain-http-server/plain-ws/json all stay in the lean archive. **Two-part plan:** (A) **runtime** — `tls` cargo feature (`default = ["tls"]`), the 5 deps made `optional`, the surface above `#[cfg(feature = "tls")]`-gated; verify both `--features tls` and `--no-default-features` compile + test, and that the `--no-default-features` archive measures ~48 KiB lighter on a compute binary. The lean archive loses HTTPS-serve + the HTTP client (ureq pulls rustls); plain-HTTP serve + TCP + WS + JSON remain. (B) **karac** — build/install both archives (`libkarac_runtime.a` full + `libkarac_runtime_min.a` lean), and in `link_executable`/`resolve_runtime_path` select the lean archive when codegen emitted no TLS/https/http-client symbol reference (default lean, escalate to full on TLS-symbol use; fall back to full if min is absent — always correct, just bigger). Each part is its own tracked slice below.

  - [x] **Phase 4 Part A — runtime `tls` cargo feature (compile the rustls surface out of the lean archive).** ✓ Landed 2026-05-30. Added `tls` feature (`default = ["tls"]`); made `rustls`, `rustls-pemfile`, `tokio-rustls`, `webpki-roots`, `ureq` `optional = true` and pulled in by the feature; `#[cfg(feature = "tls")]`-gated `pub mod tls`, the WS-over-TLS path in `event_loop.rs` (`TlsConnIo` + its Read/Write impls, `ws_handshake_conn_tls`, `ws_handshake_worker`, `ws_handshake_pool_for`, `karac_runtime_ws_accept_tls`, the `WsHandshakePool`/`HandshakeStats`/`HandshakeStep`/`ws_stats_reporter`/`WS_HANDSHAKE_POOLS`/`ws_handshake_thread_count`/`ws_drive_upgrade_handshake` handshake-pool cluster, the `AtomicU64` import, and the two `lookup_session(fd)` dispatch branches in `ws_send`/`ws_recv`), `karac_runtime_serve_https` + the entire ureq HTTP-client + request-builder FFI in `lib.rs` (`http_client_agent`, `read_response_body_bytes`, `capture_response_headers`, `HTTP_RESPONSE_HEADERS_NEXT_ID`, `write_owned_bytes_into_out_params`, `malloc`/`free` externs, `kara_str_to_str`, `slice_to_owned_string`/`_bytes`, `HttpBuilderState`/`HTTP_BUILDERS`/`HTTP_BUILDER_NEXT_ID`, `_client_get`/`_post`/`_send`, `_builder_new`/`_add_header`/`_set_body`/`_set_timeout`/`_free`/`_send`), the matching `__preserve_no_mangle_symbols` entries, and the 14 http-client unit tests + their 5 helpers. **Gates:** `cargo build`/`clippy --all-targets`/`test -p karac-runtime` clean in BOTH `--features tls` (default, 151 pass + 1 ignored) and `--no-default-features` (124 pass — 28 TLS/client tests correctly excluded); `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + workspace `clippy --all --all-targets` clean. **Measured (C-stub referencing `karac_par_reduce`+`karac_par_run`, `-dead_strip`+`strip -x`):** compute binary against the FULL archive = 360.1 KiB; against the LEAN (`--no-default-features`) archive = **295.4 KiB — back to the 295.7 KiB pre-regression baseline, recovering 64.7 KiB** (the full residual, even more than the 48.5 KiB rustls-only synthetic, because the lean archive drops the whole client+TLS+ws-tls surface). Archive itself: 9.66 MB full → 6.81 MB lean. **Behavior-neutral for karac today:** `default = ["tls"]` means the production `cargo rustc --crate-type staticlib` build still emits the full archive; the lean one only materializes under `--no-default-features`. Unblocks Part B (which wires karac to build + select it). `rcgen` left as an ungated dev-dep — it only compiles for tests, never the staticlib, and the `tls.rs` tests that use it are gated out under `--no-default-features` (unused dev-deps don't warn).
  - [x] **Phase 4 Part B — karac dual-archive build + TLS-aware selection.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-30. `src/codegen/driver.rs`: `object_references_tls(obj_path)` scans the just-emitted object's symbol table (via `nm`) for any TLS-only runtime marker (`karac_runtime_tls_` / `_serve_https` / `_http_client_` / `_http_builder_` / `_ws_accept_tls` — substring match, prefix-agnostic for Mach-O's `_`; the `_https` suffix + `_client_`/`_builder_` infixes are what discriminate from the plain-HTTP `_serve_http`/`_http_request_*`/`_http_response_*` symbols that stay in BOTH archives). `link_executable_impl` computes `prefer_min = !object_references_tls(obj)` and `resolve_runtime_path(prefer_min)` prefers `libkarac_runtime_min.a` at each tier (KARAC_RUNTIME override → installed `<bin>/../lib` → dev `target/release`), deriving a `_min` sibling next to an explicit `KARAC_RUNTIME` override and falling back to the full archive when no lean one exists (always correct). Reading the object's referenced symbols is ground truth — decoupled from codegen internals, and robust to the unconditional FFI `declare` pass (an unreferenced `declare` emits no undefined symbol, verified). Conservative on `nm` failure (→ full). Escape hatch `KARAC_FORCE_FULL_RUNTIME=1`. **Pure marker-matcher unit-tested** (`symbol_listing_references_tls`: flags client/tls/https/ws symbols, does NOT flag par/map/string/serve_http/http_request/http_response/tcp/json/ws_accept). **E2E proof via the `karac build` CLI:** a `par { }` program links the lean archive at **295.7 KiB** (the pre-regression baseline) vs **360.4 KiB** forced-full = **−64.7 KiB recovered**, both run identically; a `Client.get(...)` program auto-selects the full archive (1.62 MiB, links + runs), and forcing it onto the min archive fails to link with undefined rustls symbols (proving detection is load-bearing + the lean archive genuinely omits the surface). **Gates:** `cargo test --features llvm` across codegen (954, now linking the lean archive), par_codegen (73), memory_sanitizer (105, ASAN clean), parallax (6), tls_codegen (12), http_client_codegen (21), http_server (17) all pass; clippy `--features llvm --all-targets` + fmt clean. CLAUDE.md build recipe updated to the lean-then-full two-archive flow; [[karac-install-path]] updated to install both archives. **Closes Phase 4 — the auto-par floor is back to 295.7 KiB for compute-only programs.**

- [x] **`emit_drop_fn_for_type_expr` framework (prereq for monomorphized collections, Slice 0.c).** ✓ Landed 2026-05-15 (uncommitted; in-tree). Per-type-expr drop fn framework mirroring `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr` (`src/codegen.rs:13378`). Dispatcher + per-shape sub-emitters (primitive, string, vec, tuple, plus Map/Set placeholders delegating to existing `karac_map_free*` runtime) at `src/codegen.rs:13985+`. New `drop_fn_cache: HashMap<String, FunctionValue<'ctx>>` field cache-keyed on `display_mangle_te(te)`. All emit_*_drop_fn methods + the cache field carry `#[allow(dead_code)]` until Slice 1 lands the first production consumer; full test suite green (417 codegen tests + 910 typechecker tests + 570 interpreter tests), clippy clean, fmt clean.

  *Settled design forks (2026-05-15).*
  - **F1 — Map/Set sub-emitters as placeholders, not specializations.** Map and Set drop fns delegate to existing `karac_map_free` runtime (preserving today's behavior). Per-K/V specialization happens in Slice 1+ alongside the monomorphized Map layout. Rationale: this slice ships the framework as foundation; pre-designing Map drop bodies against today's erased layout would be thrown-away work.
  - **F2 — Vec drop strictly recursive.** `emit_vec_drop_fn` calls `emit_drop_fn_for_type_expr` per element, so `Vec[Vec[Vec[T]]]` correctly drops every level — improvement over the existing `CleanupAction::FreeVecBuffer` cleanup which is documented as one-level only.
  - **F3 — Tests deferred to first consumer slice.** End-to-end tests need a production consumer to exercise the framework; that consumer (monomorphized `Map[i64, i64]` drop) lands in Slice 1. The framework ships as foundation; tests land alongside the first consumer to avoid building test-only public hooks just to exercise a foundation that has a planned natural consumer.

  *Out of scope (deferred to follow-ups).*
  - **Migrating existing scope-exit cleanup to consult the framework.** The existing `track_vec_var` / `track_map_var` / `CleanupAction::FreeVecBuffer` machinery keeps working as-is. Migration would replace those with `emit_drop_fn_for_type_expr` calls — a follow-up slice once the framework has at least one production consumer to validate against.
  - **Per-K/V Map drop body.** Designed in Slice 1 alongside the monomorphized Map layout. This slice's `emit_map_drop_fn` placeholder is replaced then.
  - **User-`impl Drop` trait dispatch.** When the `Drop` trait lands, the framework is the natural extension point — sub-emitters consult a user-`Drop` impl if one exists for the type.
  - **Drop ordering guarantees** (last-field-first vs source order for tuples) — design.md doesn't pin this today; leaf sub-emitters iterate fields in source order. One-line reverse if a different order is mandated later.

- [x] **Generic-arg propagation audit for monomorphized collections.** ✓ Audit completed 2026-05-15 (read-only investigation, no commit). Verified all Map/Set method codegen sites carry concrete K/V/T types at the call site as `BasicTypeEnum` via `map_key_types` / `map_val_types` / `set_elem_types` — which is exactly what `mangle_mono_name` (`src/codegen.rs:21951`) takes. 19 methods audited (10 Map at `compile_map_method` `src/codegen.rs:13092–13354`; 9 Set at `compile_set_method` `src/codegen.rs:14403–14630`); 19/19 ready. Dispatch is identifier-only-receiver-gated at `src/codegen.rs:8610` — consistent with how other codegen dispatches (Vec, etc.) work; not a new constraint. **Verdict: ready for monomorphization, no K/V plumbing prereq slice needed.** One follow-up surface to verify in Slice 1: `Map[char, i64]` and `Map[i32, i64]` mangle identically (both K's lower to LLVM i32 via `llvm_type_to_mangle_str` at `src/codegen.rs:21983`); semantically distinct but codegen-identical — confirm Hash dispatch behaves correctly for both. Tracked as a Slice 1 verification gate in [`wip-monomorphized-collections.md`](wip-monomorphized-collections.md) § Slice 1.

- [-] **Monomorphized collections — runtime restructure.** P1 (post-v1, P0 design-property). Replace today's type-erased C runtime (`runtime/src/map.rs` and any future erased collections) with monomorphizable per-K/V LLVM symbols compiled into the user crate. `Map[K, V]`, `Set[T]`, `Vec[T]`, future `BTreeMap[K, V]` get one specialized implementation per concrete type tuple — direct hash/eq calls, full inlining, no function-pointer indirection, no byte-blob storage.

  *Shipped (2026-05-15).* Slice 1 (Map[i64, i64]) — sub-slices 1a (scaffolding + len wrapper, commit `3d5e487`), 1b.1 (runtime `#[repr(C)]` + direct-field len, commit `537e5d2`), 1b.2a (mono insert_old symbol + dispatch, commit `c73169b`), 1b.2b (inline fast-path probe loop, commit `f956d72`), 1b.3 (mono get + inline probe, commit `80f7400`), 1b.4 (bench refresh, doc-only). Slice 2 (Map[char, i64]) — sub-slices 2.0 (`llvm_type_for_name "char"` arm fixes latent `key_size = 8` bug, commit `c8983a9`) and 2.1 (generalized emit helpers over (K, V), gate predicate accepts (i32, i64), `Map[char, i64]` routes through `karac_map_i32_i64_*` mono symbols shared with `Map[i32, i64]`, commit `48e4963`). 426 codegen tests; full suite green.

  *Bench evidence (post-Slice-2 + FxHash + O(1) chars decode).* Map[i64, i64] microbench (1M insert+get, hyperfine 8 runs): karac mono **21.7 ms** vs Rust std::HashMap **42.4 ms** → karac mono runs **1.95× faster than std**. Map[char, i64] microbench (1M isolated gets, tiny 26-entry table): karac mono **5.2 ms** vs Rust std::HashMap **2.3 ms** → karac mono runs **2.27× slower than std** (small-table case dominated by Option-match codegen). LeetCode #3 kata (Map[char, i64]-heavy, 104K-char input × 20 iter): karac **8.1 ms** vs Rust **16.7 ms** → karac runs **2.06× faster than Rust**. The original kata baseline was 98× SLOWER than Rust; we closed the gap and inverted it by combining three compounding optimizations (mono Map dispatch + FxHash + O(1) chars decode).

  *Headline-metric finding (history).* The Slice 1 / Slice 2 work alone did NOT close the kata gap — kata was still 95.7× of Rust after both shipped. The mono Map work captured the "function-pointer indirection tax" for primitive K types but the kata bottleneck turned out to be elsewhere. Two follow-up workstreams from the Slice 2 finding (`bench/hash_quality/` investigation → FxHash swap; chars-iter investigation → runtime O(1) decode fix) closed the remaining gap. The compounding is the key — none of the three optimizations individually moved the kata more than ~2%, but together they delivered a 196× karac-side speedup (1587 ms → 8.1 ms).

  *Settled design (locked 2026-05-15).*
  - **§3.1 — User-impl `Hash` C-ABI wrapper deleted in Slice 5** (atomic-cleanup). Mono inlines the hash; the wrapper has no consumer. Reopens if `dyn Hash` / reflection / FFI consumer lands.
  - **§3.2 — `Linkage::LinkOnceODR` on every monomorphized collection symbol.** Cross-crate/cross-TU dedup at link time. ~5 LoC. Reopens if post-link `nm` shows duplicate symbols.
  - **§3.3 — Drop semantics via `emit_drop_fn_for_type_expr` framework.** Shipped 2026-05-15 (separate tracker entry above). Map/Set sub-emitters delegate to the existing `karac_map_free*` runtime as placeholders; per-K/V drop specialization happens alongside each Map slice that ships.
  - **§3.4 — `Set[T]` rides on `Map[T, ()]`.** Already the codebase precedent (`emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr` delegates Set to Map). Slice 4 just adds the same delegation for the mono path. Reopens if `V = ()` lowering wastes per-cell padding.
  - **§3.5 — Vec migration deferred (Slice 6).** Vec's hot path (indexed read/write, iteration, push) is already direct. Remaining indirected ops are closure-bearing (`sort_by`, `sort_by_key`, `partition`, future `map/filter/fold`) and call-rare in current benches. Out of scope unless a workload surfaces a Vec-indirection hotspot — natural-pull trigger.
  - **§3.6 — Coexist during Slices 1-4, atomic delete in Slice 5.** Each call site dispatches to mono if the K/V tuple's specialization exists, falls back to the erased `karac_map_*` runtime otherwise. Slice 5's delete is gated on `grep karac_map_ src/codegen.rs` empty AND full Map suite still green.

  *Path-B deviation (locked 2026-05-15).* The wip plan called for "dispatch through `compile_generic_call`" — i.e., bake a generic `Map[K, V]` in Kāra stdlib source and route through the user-fn generic infrastructure. Investigation showed this is blocked behind a much larger precursor: Kāra has no raw-allocator API in source today (no `malloc`/`free`/`alloc`/`Box::leak` equivalent; `runtime/stdlib/map.kara` is a type-shape stub `struct Map[K, V] { }` only). Path B (hand-emit per-K/V LLVM functions via parallel codegen helpers — `MapMonoMethods` cache, `mono_map_cache_key`, `should_use_mono_map_for`, `get_or_emit_map_mono_methods`, `emit_mono_map_insert_old_body`, `emit_mono_map_get_body`) was adopted instead. The user-fn generic infra (`generic_fns`, `generated_monos`, `compile_generic_call`) is sidelined for runtime collections — they share the *design pattern* (compile-on-demand, content-addressed mangling, `linkonce_odr` dedup) but not the *literal functions*. See `design.md § Generics and Monomorphization Strategy`.

  *Dormant — pending workload pull (Slices 3, 4, 5, 6).* The bench evidence above means Slices 3-5 (`Map[String, *]` family / `Set[T]` / atomic erased-fallback delete) and Slice 6 (Vec[T] indirected-method migration) all share the same natural-pull trigger: a real workload that surfaces hotspot for the corresponding shape. The architecture is validated and the design is locked — execution is mechanical when the trigger fires. Specific reopen conditions:
  - **Slice 3 (Map[String, V])** — real user code surfacing String-key Map performance as a bottleneck. Heap-bearing K exercises the §3.3 drop framework in production.
  - **Slice 4 (Set[T])** — Set-heavy workload surfacing the erased-Set tax. Per §3.4 rides on Slice 3 in ~50 LoC.
  - **Slice 5 (atomic delete of `karac_map_*`)** — operational pressure to shrink `libkarac_runtime.a` and remove ~558 lines of unsafe Rust runtime, OR a future Map K/V tuple that needs `karac_map_*` extended in a way that's only justifiable post-monomorphization.
  - **Slice 6 (Vec)** — workload surfacing measurable Vec-indirection hotspot in `sort_by` / `sort_by_key` / `partition` / future closure-bearing iter methods. **Trigger fired 2026-05-29 by kata 16 (3Sum Closest); Slice 6.1 (Vec[i64] sort_by inline-closure no-captures) SHIPPED 2026-05-29 in `1fbd942e`** — see the standalone `Slice 6 (Vec[T]) — natural-pull trigger event` entry above for measurements, the shipped sub-slice's scope, and the remaining 6.2+ sub-slices.

  *Validation artifacts.* `bench/indirection_cost/` (standalone Cargo project) — three configs (std::HashMap, hand-rolled Rust mono, FFI to karac runtime) for predicting the gap to close. Re-run when slicing resumes to refresh the baseline.

- [x] **`karac_string_decode_char` runtime — O(n)-per-call → O(1)-per-call.** ✓ Shipped 2026-05-15. Investigation under `wip-chars-inline.md` (deleted on closeout) was originally framed as "is inline LLVM UTF-8 decode in the for-loop body worth the codegen complexity?" but the bench revealed the bottleneck wasn't the FFI crossing — it was the runtime helper's *body*. Prior implementation called `std::str::from_utf8(slice)` on the **whole remaining string** every call, making each per-char decode O(remaining_bytes). For an N-character iteration that's O(N²) total validation work; for the 104K-char LeetCode #3 kata × 20 iter, total bytes re-validated was ~108B even though only 2.08M chars were actually consumed. Fix is mechanical: single-char UTF-8 decoder in `runtime/src/clone.rs` — lead-byte width classification (ASCII fast path + 2/3/4-byte handling), continuation-byte validation, overlong / surrogate / out-of-range rejection. ~40 lines. Output parity with prior version is exact for well-formed UTF-8; malformed input emits U+FFFD and advances 1 byte (standard WHATWG decoder recovery rule). Inline LLVM decode is now **dormant** — the residual FFI crossing cost is ~5-20ns/call, but the runtime fix already brought karac competitive with Rust on chars-heavy workloads, so the marginal win of also inlining the decode is small relative to the codegen complexity. Reopens if a workload surfaces a chars-iter hotspot the runtime fix didn't address. **Measured delta:**
  - Pure chars-iter bench (104K chars × 20 iter, no Map ops): 1614ms → 3.8ms (**425× speedup**). Karac is now 1.77× slower than Rust on pure iter; the residual gap is FFI crossing overhead + for-loop machinery.
