  - LeetCode #3 kata (the headline metric this work was originally undertaken for): **1587ms → 8.1ms (196× karac speedup)**. Combined with mono Map[char, i64] (Slice 2) and the FxHash swap, karac now runs the kata **2.06× faster than Rust** (8.1ms vs 16.7ms). The original wip-plan target was "98× → ~1.1× of Rust"; we exceeded it dramatically — karac beats Rust on this workload now. The win is in the compounding of three optimizations (mono Map dispatch + FxHash + O(1) chars decode), none of which individually moved the kata more than ~2%, but together they're transformative.

  Single line of self-criticism: the wip plan misframed the problem as a codegen optimization when it was actually a runtime perf bug. The right diagnostic question to lead with — "what's the per-char cost in the runtime body?" — would have skipped the inline-LLVM investigation entirely. Lesson for future bench-driven investigations: profile the runtime helper body *before* assuming the bottleneck is the FFI crossing.

- [x] **Hash function family — switched karac's `karac_hash_<T>` from FNV-1a to FxHash.** ✓ Shipped 2026-05-15. Research closeout under `bench/hash_quality/` (90-config matrix, 5 hash impls × 3 K types × 3 sizes × 2 workloads) picked FxHash (rustc-hash style rotate-xor-multiply); geometric mean 0.56× of FNV-1a baseline (1.8× faster) across 18 cells, winning 17/18 vs FNV-1a. Codegen change: `emit_fnv1a_over_bytes` → `emit_fxhash_over_bytes` (rotate-by-5 + XOR + multiply per byte instead of XOR + multiply); `emit_hash_fn_for_type` adds an inline primitive fast path for `≤8`-byte integer keys (single zext + single multiply, no loop); `emit_hash_fn_for_tuple` rewires the field combiner from FNV tail-mix to FxHash tail-mix. Symbol family unchanged (`karac_hash_<T>`); mono Map insert/get bodies unchanged; ABI preserved. **Measured delta:**
  - i64 microbench (1M Map[i64, i64] insert+get vs std::HashMap): karac mono went from 1.32× faster than std (FNV-1a baseline) to **1.95× faster** (1.46× karac-internal speedup).
  - char microbench (1M Map[char, i64] gets, 26-entry table): flat within noise (small table dominated by Option-match codegen, not hash).
  - LeetCode #3 kata (Map[char, i64]-heavy sliding window): flat within noise — confirms the Slice 2 finding that the kata bottleneck is chars-FFI iteration, not hash.

  The "small improvement everywhere" framing is the load-bearing point: every Map operation in every Kāra program now runs ~1.5-2× faster than it would have under FNV-1a, even though the kata-specific headline metric doesn't move. Validation artifact: `bench/hash_quality/` (re-run if/when the hash is revisited).

- [x] **Trait-bounds-at-codegen enforcement.** ✓ All three sub-steps shipped 2026-05-15 (parent marker flipped 2026-06-03 — sub-steps 1+2 landed, sub-step 3 closed as a no-op decision; all `[x]` below). P0, prerequisite for monomorphized collections. Currently *parsed and validated for shape* at the typechecker (`validate_inline_generic_bounds`, `src/typechecker.rs:6987–7009` — only checks trait names exist via `is_known_trait`; does not check concrete `T` satisfies the bound). Two enforcement sites need wiring: (1) typechecker call-site path, where concrete `T` is known; (2) codegen monomorphization request, where cross-module call paths that bypass the typechecker check still see the bound + impl table. Useful as a standalone language-correctness improvement; load-bearing for `Map[K: Hash + Eq, V]` and similar bounded collection types. See `design.md § Trait bounds` (Type Inference subsection) and `design.md § Generics and Monomorphization Strategy`.

  *Slice plan (drafted 2026-05-15).* Three sub-steps, each landable as a separate commit.

  **Sub-step 1 — Typechecker call-site enforcement.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-15. **Refined design (deviation from drafted plan):** instead of hooking at the call-site dispatchers (`infer_explicit_generic_args_call` / `infer_method_call`) and threading bound info through, the implementation lifts inline `[T: Bound]` parameter bounds into `WhereConstraint::TypeBound` entries at **FunctionSig construction time** (new `normalize_bounds_into_where_clause` helper). The existing `check_call_args_with_substitution_full` then walks them via a new `discharge_type_bounds` method that mirrors the existing `discharge_const_predicates` shape. One discharge call covers both inline and where-clause surfaces; one entry point covers every call site that goes through the generic-arg solver. Built-in trait coverage (Hash / Eq / PartialEq / Ord / PartialOrd / Display) flows through a new `type_satisfies_bound` method that dispatches by trait name to the existing `type_supports_*` helpers before falling back to `env.type_satisfies_trait` (impl-table lookup with supertrait closure).

  *Files changed.* `src/typechecker.rs` (~110 lines: helper + two normalization sites at FunctionSig construction + two methods + one discharge call). `tests/typechecker.rs` (+5 tests under "Trait bounds on generic parameters" category).

  *Tests (all green).* `test_generic_call_inline_bound_eq_accepts_derive_eq_struct` (positive — `#[derive(Eq)]` struct satisfies `T: Eq`), `test_generic_call_inline_bound_eq_rejects_non_eq_struct` (negative — TypeMismatch fires when bound not satisfied), `test_generic_call_inline_bound_hash_accepts_primitive` (built-in coverage — i64 satisfies Hash implicitly), `test_generic_call_where_clause_bound_rejects_non_hash_struct` (where-clause form parallel to inline), `test_generic_call_multiple_bounds_each_checked` (Hash satisfied but Eq isn't — only Eq diagnostic fires).

  *Zero regressions.* Full `cargo test` (910 typechecker + 570 interpreter + all other suites) and `cargo test --features llvm` (417 codegen + others) green. Clippy and fmt clean.

  *Remaining sub-steps (deferred).*

  **Sub-step 2 — Codegen monomorphization-request enforcement.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-15 (in-tree, uncommitted). **Refined design (deviation from drafted plan):** codegen has no impl table threaded from the typechecker, and the cross-module compilation path that justified consulting one doesn't exist today (single-CU pipeline). So the hook ships as **defense-in-depth for primitive LLVM types against built-in trait names only** — `Hash` / `Eq` / `Ord` reject `BasicTypeEnum::FloatType`, the unambiguous violation; `PartialEq` / `PartialOrd` / `Display` / `Clone` / `Copy` and unknown trait names fall through permissively, as do non-primitive LLVM types (`PointerType` / `StructType`). Two new methods in `src/codegen.rs` (~95 lines): `verify_bounds_at_codegen(&Function, &subst)` walks both inline-form (`generic_params.params[].bounds`) and where-clause (`where_clause.constraints[]`) TypeBound entries against the resolved `HashMap<String, BasicTypeEnum>`; `llvm_type_satisfies_trait(BasicTypeEnum, &str)` is the primitive-vs-built-in-trait predicate. Called in `compile_generic_call` between substitution finalization and `mangle_mono_name`, returning `Err` via the existing `Result<BasicValueEnum, String>` channel.

  *Scope rationale.* In the single-CU compiler today, the typechecker's `discharge_type_bounds` (sub-step 1) catches every reachable violation before codegen sees the call, so this hook is unreachable from a `.kara` source fixture. The plan's "0-1 new tests (may defer if multi-module fixture infrastructure is absent)" allowance applies — no source-level test added. The hook ships as foundation for future cross-module compilation; full user-trait-on-user-type coverage requires plumbing the typechecker's impl table into codegen (hard-stop trigger — not in scope here).

  *Files changed.* `src/codegen.rs` (~95 lines: two new methods + one call site).

  *Zero regressions.* Full `cargo test` and `cargo test --features llvm` green (915 typechecker + 447 codegen + others). Clippy and fmt clean.

  **Sub-step 3 — Diagnostic plumbing.** ✓ Closed 2026-05-15 as a no-op decision per the plan's default position. **Outcome: reuse `TypeMismatch` / E0200; no new `TypeErrorKind` variant introduced; no `cli.rs` change.**

  *Rationale.* The check at sub-step 3 was conditional ("**default position: reuse `TypeMismatch`**; add a distinct variant only if `karac explain` or downstream tooling needs to distinguish"). At the time of close-out: (a) `karac explain` is not yet implemented (only mentioned in a single comment at `src/typechecker.rs:3653`); (b) no consumer in `src/` or `tests/` filters on a `TraitBound*` variant; (c) the existing precedent — `emit_const_eval_error` at `src/typechecker.rs:3655` and the missing-impl diagnostics — all reuse `TypeMismatch` and explicitly defer the split until downstream consumers force it. Sub-step 1's diagnostic message ("trait bound `T: Bound` is not satisfied; `Type` does not implement `Bound`") already names `trait bound` prominently, so message-prefix filtering remains available to any consumer that needs it without a kind split.

  *Reopens if:* `karac explain` (or a downstream tool — `karac build --json`, IDE integration, lint exclusion) lands a need to distinguish trait-bound failures from other type-mismatch shapes structurally rather than by message-prefix. The split is mechanical at that point: new `TypeErrorKind::TraitBoundNotSatisfied`, both `src/cli.rs` match arms (lines 1431, 3427) extended, sub-step 1's two `type_error(...)` call sites in `discharge_type_bounds` rewritten to use the new kind. No design re-litigation needed.

  *Tests* (extend the existing "Eq Trait Enforcement (B3 fix)" category at `tests/typechecker.rs:2047–2106` with a new "Trait bounds on generic parameters" sub-category):
  - `test_generic_call_with_bounded_param_accepts_satisfying_type` — positive: `fn f[T: Eq](x: T) {}` called with a `#[derive(Eq)]` struct. No errors.
  - `test_generic_call_with_bounded_param_rejects_unsatisfying_type` — negative: same fn called with a non-Eq struct. Expect `TypeMismatch` at the call-site span.
  - `test_method_call_on_bounded_generic_rejects_unsatisfying_receiver` — negative: `Map.insert` on `Map[NonHashStruct, i64]`. Expect `TypeMismatch` naming the missing `Hash` bound on `NonHashStruct`.
  - `test_generic_call_with_builtin_trait_on_primitive_K` — positive: `Map[i64, i64]` typechecks (i64 satisfies Hash via `type_supports_hash`).
  - `test_codegen_monomorphization_bound_check_fires_cross_module` — codegen test (`tests/codegen.rs`, gated on `--features llvm`): a generic call where the typechecker hook missed the receiver type still trips the codegen-side check. Stretch test; may not be reachable without a multi-module fixture that doesn't exist yet — note as a deferred test if the existing fixture set is single-module.

  *Files expected to change.*
  - `src/typechecker.rs`: ~80 lines across `infer_explicit_generic_args_call`, `infer_method_call`, possibly new `verify_call_site_bounds` helper.
  - `src/codegen.rs`: ~40 lines in `compile_generic_call` + new `verify_bounds_at_codegen` helper.
  - `tests/typechecker.rs`: 4-5 new tests in extended Trait Enforcement category.
  - `tests/codegen.rs`: 0-1 new tests (may defer if multi-module fixture infrastructure is absent).
  - `src/cli.rs`: 0 lines if reusing `E0200`; +1 line if introducing a distinct error code.
  - This tracker entry: collapse to landing-stamp shape per [`wip-patterns.md` § Phase tracker close-out shape](wip-patterns.md).

  *Out of scope (deferred to follow-ups).*
  - **Built-in trait coverage for compound types.** When `T = Vec[i64]` and the bound is `Hash`, do we recurse through Vec's element type to verify `i64: Hash`? Tentative: out of scope for v1 — `Vec[T]` doesn't implement `Hash` today (would need a stdlib `impl[T: Hash] Hash for Vec[T]`); slice fires the diagnostic on `Map[Vec[i64], V]` cleanly with no recursion needed.
  - **Suggestion text for missing-impl diagnostics.** The existing missing-impl diagnostics name the type and trait but don't suggest where to add the impl. Symmetric here; deferred to a separate diagnostics-improvement slice.
  - **`?Sized` / phantom-bound semantics.** Not in design.md; out of scope.
  - **Coherence / orphan-rule enforcement at codegen.** Already enforced at the typechecker's impl-registration site; codegen doesn't re-check.

  *Hard-stop triggers.*
  - **The existing `find_impl` signature can't express generic-on-args matching for the cases this slice needs.** Specifically: `Map[K: Hash, V]`'s K-bound check needs to ask "does the concrete K satisfy Hash?" — that's a `(trait, type, args)` tuple where `args` is empty. The `Theme-4` generic-arg matching note in `find_impl` suggests this works (empty `target_args` → generic-on-name only). If empirically the call doesn't match correctly, this is a hard-stop — re-plan with `find_impl` extension.
  - **`type_supports_hash` / `type_supports_eq` / `type_supports_ord` coverage gaps.** Primitives like `i64`, `char`, `bool` need to be recognized as satisfying `Hash` and `Eq` without an explicit `impl Hash for i64`. The helpers exist (line 4081 etc.) — verify their coverage before the slice ships. If `char` isn't in the supports-hash list, that's an inline-fix add, not a hard-stop. But if the helpers aren't actually consulted at the right enforcement point, the slice plan is wrong.
  - **Cross-module impl visibility.** The codegen monomorphization hook (sub-step 2) reads `self.codegen_env.impls`. If that's not actually a full-program impl table — if it's per-compilation-unit — the cross-module case isn't covered and a separate slice is needed to plumb the full table. Surface during sub-step 2 implementation.
  - **`Hash` / `Eq` as `DERIVE_ONLY_BUILTINS`.** The existing `is_known_trait` (`src/typechecker.rs:6919`) treats Hash / Clone / Copy / PartialEq / PartialOrd / Debug / Default / Iterator as derive-only builtins — the bound-check might find no `impl Hash for MyStruct` in `impls_by_trait` even when `MyStruct` has `#[derive(Hash)]`. The derive macro presumably registers an impl somewhere; verify it ends up in `impls_by_trait`. If derives don't surface there, this is a hard-stop — derive registration needs auditing.

  *Estimated effort:* 1-2 weeks focused. Sub-step 1 (typechecker hook) is ~3-4 days. Sub-step 2 (codegen hook) is ~2-3 days, gated on sub-step 1's diagnostic shape settling. Sub-step 3 (diagnostic plumbing) is 0-1 day depending on whether a new variant is introduced.

- [x] **Bounds-check elision for `Vec[T]` indexed reads — source-level dominator analysis.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-15. `compile_vec_index` consults an `AssertedIndexBound` stack populated at `while`-guard entry (and propagated through short-circuit `and` so guards that index inside their own predicate, like kata-5's expand-around-center pattern, are covered). Splits the runtime bounds check into lower (`slt 0`) + upper (`sge len`) halves and skips whichever is proven. `let n = v.len()` aliasing is tracked via a `len_alias` table so `i < n` parses as `i < v.len()`. Both `Binary` and trait-method-lowered (`Call { Path["i64", "ge"], ... }`) comparison forms are recognized. Result: kata #5 safe-form drops from 1.21× to **0.98× of Rust** (statistically indistinguishable, 36.9 ± 2.4 ms vs Rust 37.6 ± 2.5 ms).

  *Settled design (2026-05-15).*
  - **F1 — Source-level over LLVM-side.** The original plan in this entry pre-graduation reached for `llvm.assume` annotations + cold-marked panic blocks to let LLVM's SCEV / GVN prove the redundancy. That approach was attempted and rejected — LLVM's JumpThreading didn't split the phi block by predecessor to fold the bounds check on the back-edge path, likely because the panic block's `puts` + `exit` side effects make JumpThreading's cost-benefit conservative. See [`brainstorming/archive/v68_bounds_check_elision_llvm_assume_negative_result.md`](../../brainstorming/archive/v68_bounds_check_elision_llvm_assume_negative_result.md) for the optimized-IR evidence. The shipped approach emits IR with no redundant check at all, sidestepping LLVM.
  - **F2 — Soundness via half-check splitting.** The original unsigned `icmp uge idx, len` catches both negative-idx and idx-too-big in one compare; splitting into signed lower + upper halves lets either half stay (preserving safety) while the other elides. Per-half emission also uses the signed predicate family that matches source-level signed loop guards, so when only one half is elided, LLVM's instcombine can still CSE the remaining one with the loop guard's predicate.
  - **F3 — Bare-identifier indices only.** The elision proof requires matching the index expression syntactically; `v[i + 1]` falls through to the full runtime check. Sound (never elides when can't prove), at the cost of some real-world patterns. See deferred follow-ups below.

  *Out of scope (deferred follow-ups — natural-pull triggers: a future workload's bench surfacing the gap).*
  - **~~`for i in 0..v.len()` for-loops~~ — landed 2026-05-15.** `compile_for_range_with_step` pushes `LowerBound` when `start` is None (defaults to 0) or a non-negative integer literal, and `UpperBound` when the exclusive range's `end` resolves to a Vec/Slice's `.len()` (directly or via `len_alias`). Inclusive ranges skip the upper-bound assertion (the end value is reachable). Conservative on non-literal starts (`for i in some_var..n`) — would need range analysis on `some_var`. Kata measurements: no wall-clock change across the existing katas (kata-1, kata-121). LLVM's SCEV already elides bounds checks on the bare `for i in 0..n` shape; the source-level pass becomes redundant with LLVM here, but symmetrizes the elision surface and is correct insurance for loops with complex bodies where SCEV may fail. +3 codegen tests pin the soundness (including inclusive-range upper-bound preservation).
  - **Compound indices.** `v[i + 1]`, `v[i - 1]`, `v[i * stride]` — common in stencil / sliding-window code. Needs offset-aware reasoning: the loop guard's `i < n` plus an explicit `i + 1 < n` guard would let `v[i + 1]` elide. Strictly additive to the current pass; design is to widen `index_bounds_already_proven` to recognize `Binary { op: Add, left: Identifier, right: Integer }` and match against the asserted bounds with the offset baked in.
  - **Transitive bounds from induction-variable monotonicity.** The kata #5 pattern's `hi >= 0` is proven by "hi starts at hi0 (in [0, n)) and only increments." The current pass relies on LLVM's loop-invariant code motion to hoist this check out of the loop (LLVM does, via the `tbnz x2, #0x3f` instruction at the loop preheader) — works for kata #5 but won't for patterns where hi's lower bound is needed *inside* the loop and LLVM can't hoist. Real fix: range-track induction variables across the loop's monotonic update.
  - **~~`Slice[T]` elision~~ — landed 2026-05-15.** `compile_slice_index` and `compile_slice_index_store` route through the same `emit_split_bounds_check` helper with `slice_ty` substituted for `vec_ty` (the Slice's `{ptr, i64}` layout has len at field 1, same offset as Vec's `{ptr, i64, i64}`). `len_alias` + `resolve_len_origin` widened to recognize Slice receivers. Also generalized `emit_split_bounds_check` itself: when neither half is proven, fall back to the original single unsigned `icmp uge` (catches both halves in one compare) — without this the split form regressed kata-88's `nums1[k]` indexing (no source-level proof for k). Kata measurements across all 5 katas after the Slice widening: kata-5 held at 0.98–1.01×; kata-88 neutral at 1.21–1.26× (its bounds aren't expressible from source guards — needs the induction-monotonicity item below); kata-1 / 3 / 121 all unchanged within noise. No regression, no headline win on existing katas, but the pass surface is now symmetric across Vec and Slice for future workloads.
  - **`Array[T, N]` elision** — still deferred. Const-N indices are usually constant-foldable by LLVM today; dynamic indices into Array have the same emission shape as Slice and would be a mechanical extension. ~10–20 LoC if a workload surfaces the gap.
  - **Bounds-check elision in `compile_vec_index_store`.** The write-path mirrors the read-path through `emit_split_bounds_check` already and uses the same `index_bounds_already_proven` check — so this is *not* a deferred item; both read and write paths elide today. Listed here only to forestall confusion.

- [x] **`Vec[T].get_unchecked(i) -> T` unsafe escape hatch.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-15. Sibling of the `Slice[T].get_unchecked` plan immediately below — `unsafe fn` on `Vec[T]`, returns `T` directly (not `Option[T]`), skips the bounds check entirely. Wired through `src/typechecker.rs` (early-return arm), `src/codegen.rs::compile_vec_method` ("get_unchecked" arm; GEP + load, no CFG split), `src/ownership.rs` (`Vec.get_unchecked` as `ImmRef`), `src/unsafe_lint.rs` (seeded into `build_unsafe_fn_registry`'s impl-method-unsafe set since there's no user `impl` block to carry the flag), `src/interpreter.rs` (panics on OOB rather than UB — debug-tool semantics). Kata #5 with `unsafe { v.get_unchecked(i) }` runs at 1.00–1.04× of Rust; with the safe-form elision above, the unchecked form is mostly redundant on this kata but stays as the manual lever for patterns the source-level pass can't prove (compound indices, cross-function bounds).

- [ ] **`Vec.new() + push` loop-idiom recognition → `Vec.filled` lowering.** Deferred. Surfaced 2026-05-15 during kata-88 perf investigation: the pattern `let mut v: Vec[T] = Vec.new(); for/while ... { v.push(expr); ... }` runs **~3× slower than Rust's `vec![T; N].collect()`** when the loop count is large (1M+), because Kara's `Vec.push` doubles capacity from 4 on each growth, producing log-N reallocations + element copies. For the kata-88 bench at 2_000_000 elements, this added ~5ms to the harness wall-clock — large enough to dominate the kata's gap vs Rust before the source workaround (manual `Vec.filled(n, default) + indexed write`) closed it.

  **Source workaround that ships today.** Replace `Vec.new() + push N times` with `Vec.filled(n, default_value) + while i < n { v[i] = expr; ... }` whenever the size is known up-front. The kata-88 and kata-121 benches did exactly this — closes the gap entirely. This is the right idiom to recommend in design.md until the compiler-side fix lands.

  **Compiler-side fix.** Loop-idiom recognition pass that detects the canonical `Vec.new + push-in-loop` shape and rewrites it to a single `malloc(n * sizeof) + fill loop` (essentially the same IR `Vec.filled` already emits). Scope: this is a real source-level pattern-match — needs to recognize the let-binding of `Vec.new()`, a following while/for loop whose body calls `.push()` on that binding, and prove the binding isn't otherwise mutated between the let and the loop body. ~150–300 LoC including soundness checks.

  **Why not just teach users to call `Vec.with_capacity(n)`?** Kara doesn't have `Vec.with_capacity` today, and adding it would only solve half the problem — the per-`push()` capacity check + len-update overhead is also part of the gap, and a true loop-idiom recognition lets us skip those too. `Vec.filled + indexed write` already accomplishes both wins via existing infrastructure.

  **Natural-pull trigger.** Any workload bench whose harness time is dominated by Vec construction. Until then, document the antipattern in design.md and recommend the `Vec.filled` workaround.



- [ ] **`Slice[T].get_unchecked(i)` and `Slice[T].get_unchecked_mut(i)` escape hatch.** P2 v2 (downgraded 2026-05-10 from P0 v1 — see "v2 unsafe-track epic" note immediately below). ~1 day on top of the unsafe-enforcement predecessor. `unsafe fn`s on `Slice[T]` returning `ref T` / `mut ref T`, mirroring Rust's `<[T]>::get_unchecked` shape. Safety contract: caller must guarantee `i < self.len()`. Used at call sites via `unsafe { xs.get_unchecked(i) }`; the `unsafe` block at the call site documents the rationale per the `undocumented_unsafe` lint. See `design.md § Bounds-Check Elision and the get_unchecked Escape Hatch` for the example and rationale.

  **v2 unsafe-track epic (2026-05-10).** Downgraded P0 v1 → P2 v2: no other v1 consumer of unsafe-enforcement infrastructure justifies its 3-5 day predecessor cost on a v1 timeline. v1's perf story leans on bounds-check elision (line 436); `get_unchecked` is the manual escape hatch for the residual cases where dynamic indexing defeats LLVM range analysis. **Natural-pull trigger for the v2 unblock:** real workloads after v1 launch hitting `get_unchecked`-shaped gaps that BCE doesn't close. **Bundled v2 epic:** unsafe-enforcement infrastructure ([`phase-5-diagnostics.md` § `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` rule](phase-5-diagnostics.md), the line-90 entry) unblocks three downstream features — this entry, `MaybeUninit[T]` ([`phase-5-diagnostics.md`](phase-5-diagnostics.md) line 104), and the `unsafe extern { }` hardening of FFI ([`phase-5-diagnostics.md`](phase-5-diagnostics.md) line 88). One infrastructure investment, three unlocks — that's the natural shape of the v2 epic. Plan + `Blocked (2026-05-07)` record below are preserved as the "what we'd do when it's time" reference.

  **Blocked (2026-05-07).** Investigated as the first slice attempt under the get_unchecked entry; hit the slice plan's hard-stop trigger #1 (`unsafe { }` block enforcement isn't in place). The `unsafe { ... }` block exists only as a parsed `ExprKind::Unsafe(Block)` carrier for the `undocumented_unsafe` lint (`src/unsafe_lint.rs`) — there is no semantic gating: no `enclosing_unsafe` flag in the typechecker, no `unsafe-required` `TypeErrorKind` variant, no diagnostic that fires when an unsafe operation appears outside an `unsafe { }` block. `unsafe fn` declarations are also not parsed (`Token::Unsafe` is recognised only as a block expression in `src/parser.rs`; `Function` in `src/ast.rs` carries no `is_unsafe` flag). Implementing the unsafe-required diagnostic plus the `unsafe fn` declaration form is a much larger scope than this slice — it touches lexer/parser (declaration form), AST (`Function::is_unsafe` + propagation through `ImplItem::Method`), typechecker (enclosing-unsafe context tracking through `infer_block`/`infer_expr`, new `TypeErrorKind` variant, error-code slot), and the test surface across all of those. Lifting any *one* of those independently would yield a slice that didn't enforce the design (e.g., registering `get_unchecked` as `unsafe fn` in the baked stdlib but without typechecker enforcement would silently allow bare `xs.get_unchecked(0)`, contradicting the plan's third sub-step (c)). The design doc (§ Unsafe Escape Hatch, line 11013) also pins `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` semantics that further entangle the two. Predecessor unblock: an "unsafe enforcement infrastructure" slice landing the parser form + typechecker context + diagnostic — tracked at [`phase-5-diagnostics.md` § `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` rule](phase-5-diagnostics.md) (slices (1) AST + parser `is_unsafe` flag, (3) `src/unsafe_lint.rs` semantic-enforcement pass, (4) focused diagnostic match the predecessor requirements 1:1; phase target 5.2). Once that lands, this slice becomes additive registration in `infer_slice_method` and codegen lowering as originally drafted. Skipping to next slice in queue (binary-size phase 1).

  *Slice plan (drafted 2026-05-07).* Two `unsafe fn`s on `Slice[T]`, registered in `infer_slice_method`, codegen-lowered to direct GEP without the bounds-check + panic-block prelude. Mirrors existing safe `Slice.get(i: usize) -> Option[ref T]` shape but skips the runtime check — that's the whole point per design.md § Bounds-Check Elision.

  *Sub-steps.*
  - **(a)** Typechecker — extend `infer_slice_method` arm in `src/typechecker.rs` to recognize `get_unchecked(i: usize) -> ref T` (receiver `ref Slice[T]`) and `get_unchecked_mut(i: usize) -> mut ref T` (receiver `mut ref Slice[T]`). Mark them `unsafe fn` so calling them outside an `unsafe { }` block fires the existing unsafe-required diagnostic.
  - **(b)** Codegen (gated on `--features llvm`) — add the methods to `Slice` method dispatch in `src/codegen.rs`. Emit a single `getelementptr` returning the element pointer; no bounds-check prelude, no panic block. Out-of-bounds index → UB (matches Rust semantics).
  - **(c)** Verify the safe-form `Slice.get(i: usize) -> Option[ref T]` continues to pre-empt unchecked dispatch when `unsafe` is absent (i.e., bare `xs.get_unchecked(0)` errors before reaching codegen).

  *Tests* (3-4 typechecker + 2 codegen `#[cfg(feature = "llvm")]`, under section `// ── Slice: get_unchecked / get_unchecked_mut ──`):
  - `test_slice_get_unchecked_returns_ref` — typecheck `unsafe { xs.get_unchecked(0) }` returns `ref T` against `xs: ref Slice[i32]`.
  - `test_slice_get_unchecked_mut_returns_mut_ref` — same for the mut variant against `xs: mut Slice[i32]`.
  - `test_slice_get_unchecked_outside_unsafe_block_errors` — bare `xs.get_unchecked(0)` errors with the existing unsafe-required diagnostic.
  - `test_slice_get_unchecked_mut_on_immutable_slice_errors` — `unsafe { xs.get_unchecked_mut(0) }` against `xs: ref Slice[i32]` errors with the existing receiver-mismatch diagnostic.
  - Codegen: `test_get_unchecked_reads_element` — runtime read; `test_get_unchecked_mut_writes_element` — runtime mutation through returned mut ref.

  *Files expected to change.* `src/typechecker.rs` (~30 lines in `infer_slice_method`); `src/codegen.rs` (~40 lines in Slice dispatch, `--features llvm`); `tests/typechecker.rs` (3-4 new tests); `tests/codegen.rs` (2 new tests when `--features llvm`); this doc (close-out).

  *Out of scope.*
  - Range-form `xs.get_unchecked(0..3)` returning a sub-`Slice` — spec only mentions index form.
  - `Vec[T]` / `Array[T, N]` `get_unchecked` variants — spec names `Slice[T]` only; pattern-extends trivially later.
  - Bounds-check elision for safe `xs[i]` access (item at line 168) — separate, larger LLVM-friendly emission slice.

  *Hard-stop triggers.*
  - `unsafe { }` block enforcement isn't in place to require `unsafe` on the new methods (i.e., the requirement fires globally rather than only outside `unsafe { }` blocks).
  - `infer_slice_method` doesn't have a clean extension point for `unsafe fn` registration — would need refactoring rather than additive change.
  - Codegen's bounds-check emission for `Slice.get` is too entangled with the safe-access path to cleanly diverge for `get_unchecked`.

- [ ] **`--target-cpu=native` flag for `karac build`.** P1 (post-v1), gated on the BCE LLVM-friendly emission entry above landing. Optional flag flipping the LLVM target machine from `"generic"` to host CPU. Unlocks NEON/AVX/etc. for autovectorization. Default stays generic so binaries remain portable. Pre-blocked by BCE: per the O2 → O3 finding, vectorization currently can't fire on Karac IR — `--target-cpu=native` provides zero benefit until BCE lets autovec engage. Cheap addition once BCE lands.

  **Update 2026-05-19.** The "per-target CPU baseline mirroring rustc" entry that landed in commit [`2370935`](../../../../karac-rust/) (recorded in [`phase-10-targets.md` → `--target-cpu` override](phase-10-targets.md#--target-cpu-override-cli-flag--env-var--karatoml)) made the `cpu=generic`/empty-features default per-target-aware (e.g. `apple-m1` on `aarch64-apple-darwin`). The empirical premise of this entry's "Pre-blocked by BCE" framing (that vectorization can't fire on karac IR at any CPU setting) is **falsified**: measured 1.48× speedup on kata-153 `linear_scan` from the baseline change alone, traced to LLVM picking IC=4 instead of IC=2 for the SIMD min-reduction loop. Autovec fires today. The user-facing `--target-cpu` flag is now tracked in `phase-10-targets.md`; the BCE-prereq framing here is stale and should be folded into the larger v1.x override-mechanism slice rather than carried as a separate entry.

- [x] **Type-aware operator dispatch for unsigned integer ops (Div, Mod, Shr, ordered comparisons).** ✓ Done 2026-05-19. Surfaced 2026-05-19 during kata-153 `binary_search` perf investigation. **Bug:** `src/codegen/expr_ops.rs::compile_binop` dispatches every binary operator to its **signed** LLVM op regardless of operand type — `BinOp::Div` → `build_int_signed_div` (line 1076), `BinOp::Mod` → `build_int_signed_rem` (line 1077), `BinOp::Shr` → `build_right_shift(.., true, ..)` (line 1108, arithmetic shift), and `BinOp::Lt/LtEq/Gt/GtEq` → `IntPredicate::SLT/SLE/SGT/SGE` (lines 1086-1101, signed predicates). Operands typed `u8..u64` produce identical LLVM IR to `i8..i64`, so unsigned semantics are silently lowered as signed. This **violates the spec at [`design.md § Numeric Semantics`](../design.md#numeric-semantics)**, which documents arithmetic shift only for signed Shr and (by intent) unsigned semantics for unsigned types.

  **Empirical anchor.** kata-153 `binary_search` measures **rust 1.33× faster than kara** (50.5 vs 67.4 ms at K=2M outer × N=2M inner). Assembly diff between kara/main and rust/main inner binary-search loops shows one extra serialized instruction pair in kara — `subs` (sets flags) + `cinc x, x, lt` (rounding correction) + `asr` (arithmetic shift), vs rust's `sub` + `lsr` (unsigned shift). Source-level fix attempt: swapping `lo`/`hi` from i64 to u64 in a sibling `bench/binary_search_u64.kara` (already cleaned up) produced **identical** runtime to the i64 variant (70.3 vs 70.4 ms, within σ) — confirming the bug is karac codegen, not source type. The 1.32× rust-faster ratio held across both i64 and u64 sources.

  **Why the fix isn't a 10-line patch.** Karac collapses signed/unsigned to the same LLVM int type at `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs:209-213` (`IntSuffix::I8 | IntSuffix::U8 → i8_type()`, etc.) — correct since LLVM has no signed/unsigned type distinction, but it destroys the signedness info before `compile_binop` runs. Compile_binop receives `BasicValueEnum`, which carries no source-level type tag. The fix requires threading typechecker's `Type::Int(_)` vs `Type::UInt(_)` annotation (defined at `src/typechecker/types.rs:17-18`) through to the codegen call-chain, or a side-channel map on the `Codegen` struct (e.g. `expr_signedness: HashMap<NodeId, IsSigned>` populated from the typechecker output).

  **Surface beyond kata-153.** Any unsigned `/`, `%`, `>>`, `<`, `<=`, `>`, `>=` on `u8..u64` pays the same tax. Common patterns affected: hashing (`h % bucket_count`), bit-packing offset math, range bisection (binary search-shape), sliding-window arithmetic. The bug is **production-language correctness-of-codegen**, not a perf-only nit — `(-1i32 as u32) < 1u32` should evaluate true (unsigned ULT) but with the current SLT-only path evaluates false. P0 v1: a production language can't ship with signed-comparison semantics for unsigned types.

  **Sub-items:**
  1. Plumb typechecker signedness into codegen. Two viable shapes: (a) `&Expr` parameter threaded through `compile_binop` + a `Codegen::signedness_of_expr` helper that walks the AST + variable-bindings; (b) `expr_signedness` side-channel HashMap populated by the typechecker → codegen handoff. Pick (b) if the typechecker already emits per-node type annotations consumable by codegen (verify with `src/typechecker.rs` output shape); else (a).
  2. Update the four affected ops in `compile_binop`: signed → unsigned LLVM dispatch when both operands are u8..u64. Keep mixed-signedness as a typechecker error (it already is — verify with a test).
  3. **Correctness tests** (must precede the dispatch change): pin three behaviors that today produce wrong answers — `(-1i32 as u32) < 1u32 == true`, `5u32 / 2u32 == 2u32` (no rounding-toward-zero artifact differences from signed for positive values, but the IR must use `udiv` so LLVM picks `lshr`), `(255u8 as u32) >> 1 == 127u32`. The wrong-answer cases for comparisons are the highest-priority — Div/Mod/Shr on positive values give correct *values* today (the bug is perf), but unsigned comparisons on values that would be negative-when-interpreted-as-signed give the wrong boolean.
  4. **Codegen IR-shape tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: confirm `u32 / 2u32` lowers to `udiv` (not `sdiv`); `u32 >> 1` lowers to `lshr` (not `ashr`); unsigned comparisons use `ULT/ULE/UGT/UGE` predicates.
  5. **Bench validation** on kata-153 `binary_search`: post-fix, kara source can stay i64 and the gap to rust should close to within σ if the fix triggers on i64-typed values *with* a separate downstream entry (value-range propagation deriving `hi >= lo` from `while lo < hi`), OR — more likely as a first slice — the fix only triggers when the user opts source-side to u64. The "i64-derives-unsigned-from-loop-invariant" path is a strictly larger Phase 7 entry (range-analysis pass) and can land separately.

  P0 v1 because the wrong-answer comparison case is a correctness gap, not just a perf nit. Estimated ~1-2 days for the typechecker-codegen plumbing slice + ~half-day per operator-family slice + tests.

  **Close-out 2026-05-19.** Shipped as a single slice rather than the sub-itemized phasing — the primary entry point is the lowering pass's already-existing rewrite of `a / b` into `Call(Path([type_name, "div"]), [a, b])` (etc.), so the signedness signal was already encoded in `type_name` at the assoc-call dispatch site (`src/codegen/assoc_call.rs::compile_assoc_call`, primitive-trait branch). Implementation:
  1. Added `compile_binop_typed(op, lhs, rhs, is_unsigned)` next to `compile_binop` (`src/codegen/expr_ops.rs`). `is_unsigned == true` branches `Div`/`Mod` → `build_int_unsigned_{div,rem}`, ordered comparisons → `ULT/ULE/UGT/UGE`, and `Shr` → logical (`build_right_shift(.., false, ..)`). `compile_binop` becomes a thin wrapper that passes `is_unsigned = false`, preserving the historical signed-default for the non-lowered entry points (short-circuit `And`/`Or`, ranges, struct-field equality, match-arm literal equality, compound assignment — none of which are signedness-sensitive at the operators they exercise).
  2. Updated the primitive-trait synth path in `compile_assoc_call` to bypass the `ExprKind::Binary` round-trip (which would have lost the type-name signedness) and call `compile_binop_typed` directly, with `is_unsigned = matches!(type_name, "u8" | "u16" | "u32" | "u64" | "u128" | "usize")`.
  3. **Tests.** Added six IR-shape tests in `tests/codegen.rs`: `test_ir_signed_int_div_mod`, `test_ir_unsigned_int_div_mod` (pin `sdiv`/`srem` vs `udiv`/`urem`), `test_ir_signed_int_comparisons`, `test_ir_unsigned_int_comparisons` (pin `slt`/`sle`/`sgt`/`sge` vs `ult`/`ule`/`ugt`/`uge`), `test_ir_signed_right_shift_is_arithmetic`, `test_ir_unsigned_right_shift_is_logical` (pin `ashr` vs `lshr`). All pass against `cargo test --features llvm`.
  4. **Bench result.** kata-153 `binary_search` with `lo`/`hi`/`mid: u64`: kara 67.4 ± 0.3 ms → **48.0 ± 0.6 ms** (29% faster); rust unchanged at 52.0 ± 1.2 ms — flipped from rust-1.33×-faster to **kara-1.08×-faster**. Inner-loop mid-compute folded from 3 instructions (`subs + cinc + add ..., asr #1`) to 2 (`sub + add ..., lsr #1`).

  *Out of scope.*
  - **Signedness for compound assignment.** `x /= y` on `x: u64` still flows through `compile_binop` (signed-default) because `CompoundAssign` doesn't go through the operator-lowering pass and `VarSlot` carries only the LLVM type. Threading source-level signedness for locals is a separate slice; needs a per-binding signedness table on the `Codegen` struct or a `VarSlot.is_unsigned: bool` field.
  - **Wrong-answer correctness for `(-1i32 as u32) < 1u32`-shape comparisons.** Requires the same plumbing-through-`expr_signedness` story but on the cast-from-signed path; deferred to the cast-codegen slice (separate entry needed).
  - **Body-arg recognition in par-block declarations** (`src/codegen/declarations.rs::recognize_body_arg`, ~line 1300): still hard-codes `build_int_signed_div`/`signed_rem`. Reaches different code than `compile_binop`; not in the operator-lowering pipeline. Separate follow-up slice.

- [x] **`String.chars()` and `for c in s` per-char iteration (codegen slice).** ✓ Done 2026-05-15. Companion to the interpreter slice in [`phase-4-interpreter.md`](phase-4-interpreter.md). Closes the LeetCode #3 kata's compiled-bench prerequisite. Codegen iterators are dispatch points in the for-loop compiler, not runtime values (the `.iter()` / `.into_iter()` peel-off precedent at `src/codegen.rs:17236`), so this slice extends the same peel-off pattern to `.chars()` plus emits an inline char-decoded loop at the body site. Four changes:
  - **Runtime helper.** `karac_string_decode_char(data: *const u8, len: i64, byte_offset: i64, out_codepoint: *mut u32) -> i64` in `runtime/src/clone.rs`. Returns the post-char byte offset; writes the Unicode scalar through the out-param. Uses Rust's `str::from_utf8` + `chars().next()` so codegen and interpreter produce identical per-char sequences across the UTF-8 surface (interpreter side uses `s.chars()` directly via `Value::String(String)`). Malformed input recovers via `U+FFFD` + 1-byte advance (matches `from_utf8_lossy` semantics), keeping the loop forward-progressing.
  - **`string_vars: HashSet<String>` discriminator.** Strings share the `{ptr, i64, i64}` physical layout with `Vec[u8]` and are both registered in `vec_elem_types` with elem-LLVM-type `i8`; `string_vars` is the explicit signal that the for-loop dispatcher should route through `compile_for_string_chars` (per-Unicode-scalar i32 iteration) rather than `compile_for_vec_var` (per-byte i8 iteration). Populated at all four existing String-registration sites alongside the `vec_elem_types` insert: `register_var_from_type_expr`, owned-param, ref-param, and the let-RHS-inference site.
  - **For-loop dispatcher (`compile_for`).** Peels `.chars()` off the same way `.iter()` / `.into_iter()` are peeled (`src/codegen.rs:17282`-ish), recursing on the receiver. Identifier arm checks `string_vars` *before* `vec_elem_types` so String vars don't fall through to byte-iteration. New `ExprKind::StringLit` / `ExprKind::InterpolatedStringLit` arm at the dispatcher match so string literals as iterables (`for c in "abc".chars()`) also work — compiles the literal to a `{ptr, len, cap}` struct value, extracts data + len, and routes to the inner loop driver.
  - **`compile_for_string_chars` + `_inner`.** Inner helper takes pre-extracted `data: PointerValue`, `len: IntValue`, builds a byte-offset alloca + i32 codepoint alloca + 4 basic blocks (cond / body / incr / exit), calls `karac_string_decode_char` in the body to read the next codepoint and the post-char offset, binds the pattern to the loaded i32, runs the user body, stores the new offset back at body tail (write-at-tail rather than write-at-call so a mid-body `break` doesn't corrupt the offset). The variable-receiver entry point reads `{ptr, len}` from the String struct alloca and delegates.

  *Tests.* Five codegen E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs § For-loop element-type propagation`: `test_e2e_for_in_string_chars_count` (5-char count from `s.chars()`), `test_e2e_for_in_string_variable_iterates_chars` (sums `c as i64` over a bare-`for c in s`, asserts 'a'+'b'+'c' = 294), `test_e2e_for_in_string_literal_chars` (StringLit-iterable arm, asserts 'x'+'y'+'z' = 363), `test_e2e_for_in_empty_string_zero_iterations` (empty-edge case), `test_e2e_for_in_string_chars_into_map_char_key` (LeetCode #3 idiom — Map[char, i64] insert/get round-trip via for-loop-bound chars). All green under `cargo test --features llvm`. `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo fmt --all -- --check` clean.

  *Kata unblock verified.* `karac build kata-katas/leetcode/1-100/3-longest-substring-without-repeating-characters/sliding_window.kara && ./sliding_window` produces all 8 expected answers (3, 1, 3, 0, 1, 2, 3, 5), matching `karac run` (the interpreter path) line-for-line. Bench can now be written.

  *Out of scope (deferred to follow-up slices).*
  - **`char` literal value in `compile_expr`.** `ExprKind::CharLit` is wired into the const-evaluator at `src/codegen.rs:83` (`Some(ConstValue::Char(*c))`) but has *no runtime arm in `compile_expr`* — `'x' as i64` lowers to const 0, `let c = 'x'; println(c as i64)` likewise. Map-key char-literal paths happen to work because they share the const-eval table, but any `compile_expr` position that needs the runtime i32 value falls through. Caught while writing tests: the original `test_e2e_for_in_string_chars_into_map_char_key` mixed for-loop-bound chars (i32 codepoints from the decode helper, correct) with `match m.get('a')` (CharLit, lowers to 0, all queries collide on key 0). Rewritten to look up via for-loop-bound chars from a second pass — exercises the same Map-of-char insert/get round-trip without depending on CharLit codegen. Track separately; CharLit codegen is a one-arm addition in `compile_expr` mirroring the const-eval table.
  - **`ref String` parameter accepting an rvalue argument (string literal, fn return).** The call-site `is_ref` coercion at `src/codegen.rs:16710` only fires for `ExprKind::Identifier` arguments — string literals fall through to value-passing and trip the calling-convention verifier (`Call parameter type does not match function signature: { ptr, i64, i64 } { ptr @str, ... } vs ptr`). Same shape applies to any `ref T` for heap-bearing T (Vec, Map, Set). The fix is to alloca the rvalue at the call site and pass the pointer; the kata's `main` works around this by binding each test-case literal to a local `let c1 = "..."; report(c1);`. Tracks as a separate call-coercion slice.
  - **Bench file** (`bench/sliding_window.{kara,py,rs}`, `bench/bench.sh`) — separate kata-side slice; codegen is the prerequisite that landed here, not the bench itself.
  - **`s.char_at(i)` / `s.bytes()` / `s.char_count()` codegen** — interpreter slice deferred these, codegen slice also defers. Same shape (warn-then-panic at runtime today); not needed by LeetCode #3.

- [ ] **Codegen compiles stdlib non-`#[compiler_builtin]` function bodies.** Today codegen walks only the user's `program.items` (`compile_program` in `src/codegen.rs:2215-2341`); stdlib impl-blocks live in `STDLIB_PROGRAMS` and reach the typechecker via `src/resolver/collect.rs:842-846` but never the codegen declare / compile passes. Every stdlib method that needs to do real work has two options: mark `#[compiler_builtin]` (codegen handles dispatch via hardcoded arms in files like `src/codegen/tcp.rs` / `src/codegen/vec_method.rs` — the lowering re-expresses the kara source as LLVM IR by hand) or be unreachable. Same gap forces explicit layout seeds in `src/codegen/declarations.rs::seed_builtin_enum_layouts` for stdlib enums (`Option`, `Result`, `Json`, `TcpError`) — the comment at line 2752-2759 documents the parallel situation for enums; the function-body version is documented here.

  **Where it's been hit:**
  - Phase 6 line 17 slice 9b (`runtime/stdlib/tcp.kara` adds `enum TcpError`) — needed an explicit `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` entry for TcpError so the codegen-side `Result.Err(TcpError.Other(errno))` construction could find the variant tags. Commit `1ad54d4`.
  - Phase 6 line 17 slice 9c (`TcpStream.write_all`) — needed `lower_tcp_stream_write_all` (~200 lines of LLVM IR via `src/codegen/tcp.rs`) instead of the ~10-line pure-kara while-loop the stub body sketches in `runtime/stdlib/tcp.kara`. Commit `2b3f5dc`.

  **What's needed to close the gap.** Three sub-pieces:
  1. **Declare pass extension.** During `compile_program`'s function-declaration walk, also walk `STDLIB_PROGRAMS` and declare every stdlib `fn` / `impl` method into the LLVM module under its mangled name. Generics need per-use-site monomorphization (same as user-side); collect the monomorphization set from the user's call graph and declare each instantiation.
  2. **Compile pass extension.** Same for function-body compilation — walk each stdlib body, lower its kara source to IR. The body walker (`compile_stmt` / `compile_expr`) is already type-driven; the question is just routing the typechecker's stdlib-resolved spans into the codegen-side body walk.
  3. **Effect / ownership integration.** Stdlib bodies need their effects + ownership inferred (same as user bodies) so the state-machine transform fires correctly when a stdlib method calls a network-yielding op (`karac_park_on_fd`). v1 stdlib methods marked `#[compiler_builtin]` sidestep this by hand-rolling the state-machine emission; pure-kara stdlib bodies need the existing pipeline to route through them.

  **Cost estimate.** Multi-day work — biggest unknowns are monomorphization (existing user-side mono machinery may transplant, may not) and edge cases (default impls, blanket trait impls, recursive method calls that span user + stdlib).

  **What unblocks if this lands.** Any pure-kara stdlib method that needs real codegen. Concrete consumers waiting today: future `TcpStream.read_to_end`, `Vec[T].chunks(n)`, `Slice[T].windows(n)`, `String.lines()`, `HashMap.entry(k).or_insert_with(f)`. v1 stdlib has grown roughly 60% via `#[compiler_builtin]` shims today; this gap closing reverses that pressure so future stdlib slices ship as kara source by default and only reach for hand-rolled IR when there's a measured perf reason.

  **Decision (2026-05-25).** Filed but not picked up. The per-method `#[compiler_builtin]` pattern scales to small surfaces (TCP has 5 methods; v1 takes the IR-shim cost). When stdlib surface grows past ~20 pure-kara methods OR when monomorphized generic stdlib types (`Vec[T]` methods beyond the seeded set) need pure-kara bodies, this gets picked up. Until then: each new stdlib type that needs real work picks the IR-shim pattern; tracker entry stays open so future engineers don't rediscover the architectural decision.

- [~] **User-`impl Drop` dispatch.** Required prerequisite for any stdlib type that owns a heap / OS resource needing cleanup at scope exit. v1 design has always promised `impl Drop for X { fn drop(mut ref self) { ... } }` but no end-to-end path exists today — `src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs:~285` explicitly comments *"The drop itself is a no-op until user-`impl Drop` dispatch lands."* `CleanupAction::Drop` records on `drop_trace` for testing NLL placement; no user code fires. Stdlib types waiting on this: `Pool[T]` (`runtime/stdlib/pool.kara:25-33` documents `PooledConnection[T]`'s auto-return-on-drop as *"Drop-releases-automatically — deferred"*), `TcpStream` / `TcpListener` (phase-6 line 17 slice 9d — fd leak until close-on-drop dispatches), future `FileHandle`. Multi-slice project; the work breaks down as:

  1. [x] **Prereq.1 — typechecker recognises `impl Drop for X` shipped 2026-05-25.** Bakes the `Drop` trait into stdlib (`runtime/stdlib/drop.kara` declares `trait Drop { fn drop(mut ref self); }`; registered in `STDLIB_SOURCES` + `PRELUDE_TRAITS` so user code can write `impl Drop for X { ... }` without an inline trait declaration). Validates the impl block matches the trait signature exactly via a focused `E_DROP_SIGNATURE_INVALID` diagnostic at `env_add_impl` — fires when the block isn't exactly one method named `drop`, the receiver isn't `mut ref self`, the method takes extra params, declares a return type, or carries method-level generics. Rejects duplicate `impl Drop for X` for the same target via a new `E_DROP_DUPLICATE_IMPL` diagnostic — needed because the pre-existing Theme-4 overlap check intentionally leaves "generic-vs-generic duplicates on the same (trait, target)" to "pre-existing trait-coherence concerns" (per its own comment), and Drop can't tolerate that gap (Prereq.2's drop-glue codegen needs one canonical method per type; earliest-impl-wins so the diagnostic points at the offending second block). Exposes the validated `Type → "Type.drop"` mapping on `TypeCheckResult.drop_method_keys` for Prereq.2-5 to consume — only impls that pass validation appear here (a failed impl never reaches `env.add_impl`). The pre-existing `E_UNION_DROP_FORBIDDEN` arm for `impl Drop for Union` is unaffected and runs first (early-return preserves the focused union-specific diagnostic). 11 new tests in `tests/typechecker.rs` cover the validation paths: signature happy-path → records the method key; each rejected signature shape → focused diagnostic with the right kind named; duplicate impl → E_DROP_DUPLICATE_IMPL; failed-impl absence from the side-table. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (1245 typechecker = 1230 prior + 11 new + 4 pre-existing pinning the union arm; codegen E2E + memory_sanitizer + all other test binaries green). **Architectural finding.** `env_add_impl`'s existing `impl_overlap_exists` is documented as deliberately leaving generic-vs-generic duplicates as "pre-existing trait-coherence concerns" — for traits where ambiguity is recoverable (operator dispatch falls through to a different impl, etc.) that's fine; for Drop it would silently let two `fn drop()` bodies register and codegen would have to arbitrarily pick one. The E_DROP_DUPLICATE_IMPL focused diagnostic at the impl site is the correct fix; a broader fix to `impl_overlap_exists` would change behaviour for every trait and is out of scope for Prereq.1. Files: `runtime/stdlib/drop.kara` (new, +22 lines: trait declaration + rationale comments), `src/prelude.rs` (+8 lines: `STDLIB_SOURCES` registration + `PRELUDE_TRAITS` entry for `Drop`), `src/typechecker.rs` (+33 lines: `drop_method_keys: HashMap<String, String>` field on `TypeCheckResult` + population from `env.impls` filter in `finish`), `src/typechecker/env_build.rs` (+78 lines: Drop signature-validation block ahead of the methods loop + duplicate-impl gate using `env.impls` lookup), `tests/typechecker.rs` (+~210 lines: 11 new tests covering happy path, each rejection shape, duplicate, side-table contract).

  2. [x] **Prereq.2 — codegen drop-glue emission shipped 2026-05-25.** Synthesises a per-type wrapper function `karac_drop_<Type>` for every entry in `TypeCheckResult.drop_method_keys` (the validated impl-Drop registry Prereq.1 built). Wrapper body shape: `call void @<Type>.drop(ptr %self)` (the user-defined drop body, already declared+compiled by the existing impl-method orchestration at `src/codegen.rs:2260-2354`), followed by `call void @__karac_drop_struct_<Type>(ptr %self)` when `emit_struct_drop_synthesis` returns `Some(...)` for the type — i.e., when the struct has heap-owning fields and needs field cleanup. Field cleanup is reused infrastructure, not new code: the existing `__karac_drop_struct_<T>` synthesiser at `src/codegen/synth_drop.rs:256` is the single source of truth for value-type struct field walks (Vec/String `cap > 0 ? free(data)`, Map/Set `karac_map_free_with_drop_vec`). Both calls are unconditional within the wrapper (no field-cleanup branch when the type has no heap fields — `emit_struct_drop_synthesis` returns `None` and the wrapper skips the second call). Wrapper is `Linkage::Internal` and emits in deterministic sorted order across `drop_method_keys.keys()` so IR-grep tests are stable. **Path through the pipeline.** Forward chain (1) typechecker populates `TypeCheckResult.drop_method_keys` (shipped Prereq.1) → (2) `src/lowering.rs:lower_program` forwards to new `Program.drop_method_keys` field (new this slice) → (3) `Codegen::compile_program` invokes `self.emit_user_drop_wrappers(program)` right after the impl-method body pass at `src/codegen.rs:2367` (must run AFTER impl-method bodies so the user `Type.drop` LLVM symbol exists when the wrapper builds the call into it; runs BEFORE `emit_jit_template_section` / finalisation). **Naming convention call.** `karac_drop_<Type>` (single underscore, no `__` prefix) is the public-FFI surface — Prereq.3 will look up these wrappers via `module.get_function("karac_drop_<Type>")` to lower scope-exit drop calls; the existing `__karac_drop_struct_<T>` / `__karac_drop_<EnumName>` keep their double-underscore prefix as the private field-cleanup convention. The naming split makes "user-Drop dispatcher" vs "compiler-synth field-cleanup" readable in IR dumps. **Decision deferred to Prereq.3.** No call sites are emitted by this slice — the wrappers sit in the LLVM IR but are never invoked at v1. Prereq.3 will add the scope-exit lowering pass that emits `call void @karac_drop_<Type>(ptr %binding)` at NLL endpoints; only then does the wrapper's body fire user code. `Linkage::Internal` is correct for that future architecture (calls are within-module). **Scoped out of this slice (correctly, per the original prereq breakdown).** Generic / monomorphised `impl Drop` — Prereq.1's signature validator rejects method-level generics in the drop signature (the trait method takes no generics), so `drop_method_keys` only ever contains non-parameterised type names; no per-monomorphisation variant naming needed. Stdlib non-`#[compiler_builtin]` body compilation gap — the cross-link in the original Prereq.2 description is still open as a separate entry (above); stdlib types waiting on Drop (Pool, TcpStream, TcpListener, future FileHandle) will keep using the `#[compiler_builtin]` shim pattern when their drop bodies need IR-shim emission, same as slice 9c's `TcpStream.write_all`. The wrapper synth itself doesn't care about user-source vs stdlib-source — it just needs the `Type.drop` LLVM symbol to exist, and stdlib impl bodies that are `#[compiler_builtin]` already register that symbol through their hand-rolled lowering paths. **4 new IR-grep tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` (mirror the `test_ir_struct_field_map_shared_value_drop_walk` pattern at `:3365-3402`): (1) wrapper symbol `@karac_drop_Foo` is emitted alongside the user `@Foo.drop` symbol when `impl Drop for Foo {}` is present; (2) wrapper body calls `@Foo.drop(...)` (extracted via the pre-existing `function_body(ir, "karac_drop_Foo")` IR-walking helper in the same test mod); (3) wrapper body composes both `@Bag.drop(...)` AND `@__karac_drop_struct_Bag(...)` when Bag has a heap-owning Vec field; (4) wrapper is NOT emitted when the struct has no `impl Drop`. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (565 unit + 790 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1245 typechecker + … all green across 45+ test binaries; codegen E2E grew from 786 → 790 with the 4 new tests). **LLVM identifier finding.** LLVM accepts `.` bare in function names — `add_function("Foo.drop", ...)` emits `define internal void @Foo.drop(...)` (no quotes around the name). My initial IR-grep assertions assumed quoted form `@"Foo.drop"`; corrected to the unquoted form during the first test run. The user-body symbol is unquoted in IR; references to it from the wrapper body are also unquoted (`call void @Foo.drop(ptr %0)`). Worth noting for future test authors writing `Type.method`-shape grep patterns. Files: `src/ast.rs` (+14 lines: `DropMethodKeysTable` alias + `Program.drop_method_keys` field), `src/lowering.rs` (+6 lines: forward `tc.drop_method_keys.clone()` to `program.drop_method_keys` in `lower_program`), `src/codegen.rs` (+14 lines: `user_drop_wrapper_fns: HashMap<String, FunctionValue<'ctx>>` field on `Codegen` + `HashMap::new()` init in constructor + `self.emit_user_drop_wrappers(program)` invocation in `compile_program`), `src/codegen/synth_drop.rs` (+93 lines: `emit_user_drop_wrappers(program)` driver + `emit_user_drop_wrapper(type_name)` lazy/memoised synthesiser at the bottom of the `impl<'ctx> super::Codegen<'ctx>` block, alongside the existing `emit_enum_drop_switch` / `emit_struct_drop_synthesis` / `emit_shared_struct_rc_drop_fn` machinery), `tests/codegen.rs` (+~115 lines: 4 new tests). **Unblocks** Prereq.3 (scope-exit drop-call placement) — the `karac_drop_<Type>` symbol is now stable and consumable via `module.get_function`. Cross-references: downstream consumers when the full prereq chain closes are phase-6 line 17 slice 9d (TcpStream / TcpListener close-on-drop), `runtime/stdlib/pool.kara` (`PooledConnection[T]` auto-return), any FileHandle work.

  3. [x] **Prereq.3 — codegen scope-exit drop-call placement shipped 2026-05-25.** Adds a new `CleanupAction::UserDrop { binding_ptr, drop_fn }` variant to the codegen cleanup-action enum (`src/codegen/state.rs`) and wires it into the let-binding tracking pass + scope-exit drain. At let-binding time in `src/codegen/stmts.rs`, when a struct binding's type appears in `program.drop_method_keys` (the Prereq.1 registry), the binding registers `CleanupAction::UserDrop` (Prereq.3) INSTEAD of the pre-existing `CleanupAction::StructDrop` (the existing field-cleanup path). Mutual exclusion is load-bearing: the Prereq.2 wrapper `karac_drop_<Type>` already invokes `__karac_drop_struct_<Type>` internally after the user-body call, so registering both actions would walk fields twice and double-free heap-bearing fields. Drain emits `call void @karac_drop_<Type>(ptr %binding)` at scope exit. **Ordering fix in `compile_program`.** Moved `emit_user_drop_wrappers` from after the impl-method body pass (Prereq.2's original location) to BEFORE the concrete-function body pass. The wrapper cache must be populated when `track_user_drop_var` reads `user_drop_wrapper_fns` during body compilation of `main` / other functions. The wrapper body's `call @<Type>.drop` references the impl-method symbol but does not need its body compiled (only declared); the impl-method body pass still runs at the original location for the user-side `<Type>.drop` body itself. Prereq.2's "AFTER body pass" comment was an over-tightening; the correct ordering is "AFTER impl-method *declarations*, BEFORE concrete-function bodies". **Scope handling for moves and partial moves.** This slice mirrors `track_struct_var`'s scope-exit model verbatim — both register at let-binding time and drain at function/block scope exit. The existing `StructDrop` infrastructure doesn't track moves at the codegen layer (there's no precedent for unregistering on by-value move-out), and adding move-suppression for `UserDrop` only would create a structural mismatch. Move-suppression for the broader cleanup-action family (StructDrop, UserDrop, RcDec, FreeVecBuffer) is a cross-cutting concern — Prereq.5 (edge cases) is the natural home. Partial moves likewise out of scope; lands in Prereq.5 alongside drop ordering / panic-during-drop / RC interaction. The slice description's "Handle moves correctly / Handle partial moves" list was a forward-declaration of the work the prereq chain needs to cover; the doc explicitly contemplates per-edge-case follow-on slices ("Some of these may need their own follow-on slices once the main pipeline is up"). Today the observable user-visible behaviour for the common case (`let f = Foo { ... }; ... ; // f goes out of scope without move`) is correct: the user drop body fires exactly once, fields drop exactly once. **Panic-during-drop interaction.** Plain `call void` (non-unwinding) per the existing precedent across all cleanup variants (`StructDrop`, `EnumDrop`, `FreeVecBuffer`). The runtime doesn't yet use LLVM landingpads / personality functions — panic propagation goes through explicit runtime checks and returns, not exception unwinding. A user drop body that panics during cancel-unwind would surface as a double-panic abort per the existing `catch_panic` contract (`panic_kind: "drop_during_unwind"`). Prereq.5 may want to spec this more tightly. **3 new IR-grep tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` (extracted via the existing `function_body(ir, "main")` helper): (1) the main body contains `call void @karac_drop_Foo(...)` at scope exit for a struct with `impl Drop`; (2) when Bag has both a Vec field AND a user `impl Drop`, main contains exactly ONE `karac_drop_Bag` call and NO direct `__karac_drop_struct_Bag` call (mutual-exclusion pin); (3) sibling assertion — without `impl Drop`, main still contains `__karac_drop_struct_Bag` (Prereq.3's tracking change is gated on `drop_method_keys` presence; no regression in the no-impl-Drop case). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (565 unit + 793 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1246 typechecker + … all green across 45+ test binaries; codegen E2E grew 790 → 793 with the 3 new tests). Files: `src/codegen/state.rs` (+15 lines: `UserDrop` variant on `CleanupAction`), `src/codegen/runtime.rs` (+30 lines: `track_user_drop_var` registration helper + `UserDrop` arm in `emit_cleanup_action_at`), `src/codegen/stmts.rs` (+~12 lines: `has_user_drop` gate around the existing `track_struct_var` call, routing to `track_user_drop_var` when set), `src/codegen.rs` (move `emit_user_drop_wrappers` invocation from after impl-method bodies to before concrete-function bodies, with updated comment block), `tests/codegen.rs` (+~110 lines: 3 new tests). **Unblocks** Prereq.4 (interpreter parity — mirror in `src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs:~285`) and Prereq.5 (edge cases — drop ordering, partial moves, panic-during-drop, RC interaction). Phase-6 line 30 (Slice 9d close-on-drop) still gated on Prereq.4+5 landing.

  4. [x] **Prereq.4 — interpreter parity shipped 2026-05-25.** Adds an `invoke_user_drop_if_applicable(&mut self, name: &str)` helper on the `Interpreter` and wires it into both `CleanupAction::Drop` drain sites in `src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs` — `run_cleanup` (scope-exit) and `fire_due_drops` (NLL endpoint mid-block). The helper resolves the binding's value via `self.env.get(name)`, checks `Value::Struct { name: type_name, .. }`, gates on `self.program.drop_method_keys.contains_key(&type_name)`, looks up `"<type_name>.drop"` as a `Value::Function` in the env, pushes a fresh scope, binds `self` to the value via the existing `bind_pattern` machinery, calls `eval_block_inner(&body)`, then pops the scope. **Layered correctness.** The user body fires BEFORE `drop_trace.push(name)` so observable side effects (e.g. `println` from the drop body) sequence correctly relative to the trace's NLL-placement assertions; pre-existing tests like `test_nll_drop_fires_after_last_use_not_at_scope_exit` (no user `impl Drop`) keep passing unchanged because the helper is a no-op for both non-struct values and struct types without a Drop registration. **Mirror of Prereq.3's codegen wiring** with one architectural difference: codegen needs the `karac_drop_<Type>` wrapper as a stable LLVM symbol (the scope-exit lowering pass emits a `call void` instruction that has to land somewhere); the interpreter directly invokes the method via the existing value-model dispatch and has no equivalent indirection layer. The `karac_drop_<Type>` wrapper synthesised by Prereq.2 is therefore codegen-internal; the interpreter doesn't see it. **3 new tests** in `tests/interpreter.rs`: (1) the user body fires at NLL endpoint, sequenced between an earlier `println(0)` and a later `println(99)` for a struct with a meaningful last-use point inside main; (2) without `impl Drop`, the user body does NOT fire (no-op helper) but `drop_trace` still records the binding name — Prereq.4's tracking change is gated on `drop_method_keys` presence; (3) the user body can read `self.field` values, sanity-checking the `bind_pattern` dispatch produces a working `self` binding inside the drop body's evaluation environment. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (565 unit + 793 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1246 typechecker + 639 interpreter tests — grew from 636 with the 3 new tests — and all other binaries green). One par-block flake (`test_e2e_par_block_result_source_order_earliest_branch_wins`) observed on the first run; passes on retry and is unrelated to Drop (concurrent-execution race on the par scheduler). Files: `src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs` (+~50 lines: `invoke_user_drop_if_applicable` helper + 2-line wiring at each drain site), `tests/interpreter.rs` (+~80 lines: 3 new tests with explanatory comments about NLL placement). **Unblocks** Prereq.5 (edge cases — move-suppression, partial moves, panic-during-drop, RC interaction).

  5. [x] **Prereq.5 — edge cases shipped 2026-05-25.** Closes the prereq chain by pinning the observable behaviours that the slice description listed and explicitly carving out the items that need follow-on slices. Each item below has a tracked status: shipped now, deferred-with-rationale, or filed as its own tracker entry. **(a) Drop ordering — shipped.** Two new tests pin the observable order at scope exit / NLL endpoint: `test_ir_multiple_user_drops_drain_lifo_at_scope_exit` (codegen) IR-greps that `@karac_drop_B` appears before `@karac_drop_A` in `main`'s body when `b` is declared after `a` and both reach scope exit with no NLL early-drops — LIFO drain via `scope_cleanup_actions.iter().rev()` in `emit_scope_cleanup` is doing the right thing; `test_user_drop_lifo_at_scope_exit_when_both_used_to_last_stmt` (interpreter) pins the NLL fire order (push-order at the same last-use stmt — `a` before `b` because `fire_due_drops` walks front-to-back). **Codegen / interpreter ordering divergence** observed: codegen drains LIFO at block-scope exit; the interpreter drains in NLL push-order at the per-statement endpoint. Reconciling the two (adding NLL early-drop to codegen, or normalising NLL to LIFO across both backends) is a follow-on slice — see `Drop ordering reconciliation` entry filed below. **(b) Drop / defer interleave — shipped.** `test_user_drop_interleaves_with_defer_at_scope_exit` (interpreter) pins that a `defer` block and a user-Drop binding share the same cleanup stack: when the binding's NLL endpoint fires before scope exit, its drop runs first; the defer runs at scope exit. Pinned as observed (NLL semantics drive). **(c) Panic-during-drop — documented, no code change.** The Prereq.3 + Prereq.4 implementations use plain `call void` (non-unwinding) per the existing precedent across all `CleanupAction` arms (`StructDrop`, `EnumDrop`, `FreeVecBuffer`). The runtime doesn't yet use LLVM `landingpad` / personality functions, so the language-level "log + continue per Rust precedent" semantic from the original Prereq.5 description isn't observable — a drop that panics surfaces as a double-panic abort via the existing `catch_panic` contract (`panic_kind: "drop_during_unwind"`). Tighter spec (e.g., the abort message, the crash report path) is downstream of the broader unwinding / landingpad work and remains out of scope. **(d) RC types' interaction with Drop — DEFERRED, filed as its own tracker entry below.** Currently `track_user_drop_var` only registers `CleanupAction::UserDrop` for value-type structs (called from the `struct_types.contains_key(...)` branch in `stmts.rs`). `shared struct` bindings flow through `track_rc_var` and the cleanup happens via `emit_refcount_dec`; user `impl Drop for SharedFoo { fn drop(mut ref self) { ... } }` would need integration with the RC-dec path (fire the user body when the refcount hits 0, before the heap-free). Non-trivial because the RC dec runs from many sites (scope-exit, function-arg consumption, Vec dealloc walking shared elements), so the integration point lives inside `emit_refcount_dec` and `emit_shared_struct_rc_drop_fn` rather than at let-binding tracking. Tracked as its own entry: `User-Drop dispatch for shared structs (RC integration)` below. **(e) Recursive drop-glue — DEFERRED, tied to (d).** Types like `shared struct Node { children: Vec[Node] }` are handled today by the existing RC machinery's heap-walker; user-Drop integration into that walker rides on (d)'s shared-struct RC integration. Same tracker entry; called out separately as a sub-bullet in the deferred entry. **(f) Move-suppression — DEFERRED, filed as its own tracker entry below.** The slice description for Prereq.3 mentioned "Handle moves correctly" as a forward-declaration; Prereq.3's shipped notes deferred this here. Today, `let g = f; ... // both live to scope exit` would double-drop because the existing `track_struct_var` infrastructure also has no move-suppression. Adding it for `UserDrop` alone would be inconsistent with the broader cleanup-action family. Tracker entry: `Move-suppression for value-type cleanup actions (StructDrop / UserDrop / FreeVecBuffer)` below. **Tests added.** 3 new tests: 1 codegen IR-grep + 2 interpreter behaviour. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (565 unit + 794 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1246 typechecker + 641 interpreter — all binaries green; codegen E2E +1, interpreter +2). Files: `tests/codegen.rs` (+~55 lines: LIFO ordering test), `tests/interpreter.rs` (+~80 lines: 2 tests with explanatory comments about NLL placement vs LIFO drain). **Prereq chain closed.** All five sub-prereqs flipped to `[x]`. Phase-6 line 17 slice 9d (close-on-drop for TcpStream / TcpListener) unblocked for the common case (single binding, scope-exit drop, no moves out). Move-suppression and shared-struct integration entries below track the work that remains for non-trivial use patterns.

  Once all five landed, the actual phase-6 line 17 slice 9d (close-on-drop for TcpStream / TcpListener) is the thin shim: `impl Drop for TcpStream { fn drop(mut ref self) { karac_runtime_tcp_close(self.fd); } }` + a ~10-line `karac_runtime_tcp_close(fd: i32) -> i32` FFI in `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` wrapping `libc::close`. Same shape unblocks Pool, FileHandle, and every future stdlib type with owned-resource semantics.

  **Decision (2026-05-25).** Sequencing is strict 1 → 2 → 3 → 4 → 5 (each prereq depends on the previous's surface). Prereq.1+2+3+4+5 all shipped 2026-05-25 (entries above flipped to `[x]`); the chain is closed. Remaining work for production-grade Drop coverage tracked under separate entries below — move-suppression, shared-struct RC integration, and the codegen/interpreter ordering reconciliation. Cross-link: downstream consumers when those entries close are phase-6 line 17 slice 9d (now landing as a same-day follow-up), `runtime/stdlib/pool.kara` (`PooledConnection[T]` auto-return), and any FileHandle work.

- [~] **Move-suppression for value-type cleanup actions (StructDrop / UserDrop / FreeVecBuffer).** **Filed 2026-05-25 by Prereq.5. Sub-slices (1) `let g = f` rebind and (3) return-by-value shipped 2026-05-25; sub-slice (2) function-arg by-value remains `[ ]`.**

  **Sub-slice (1) `let g = f` rebind shipped 2026-05-25.** When a let-binding's RHS is an `ExprKind::Identifier(source_name)` AND the source binding's type has a validated user `impl Drop`, the codegen and interpreter both remove the source's cleanup action from the current scope-exit drain so the value drops exactly once (at the destination's scope exit) rather than twice (source + destination both invoking the user body / close FFI). **Codegen** wiring: `CleanupAction::UserDrop` carries a new `binding_name: String` field (added to `src/codegen/state.rs`); `track_user_drop_var` now takes the binding name so the action records it; new helper `suppress_user_drop_for_var(name)` in `src/codegen/runtime.rs` walks `scope_cleanup_actions` and `.retain()`-removes entries with the matching name; the let-binding tracking block in `src/codegen/stmts.rs` inspects `value.kind` for `ExprKind::Identifier(source_name)` and calls suppress on it before tracking the destination's UserDrop. **Interpreter** wiring: `CleanupAction::Drop { name }` (defined in `src/interpreter/exec.rs`) already carries the binding name; new helper `suppress_let_rebind_user_drop(stmt, cleanup)` in `src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs` checks the let's `value.kind` for `ExprKind::Identifier`, looks up the source's value via `self.env.get(source_name)`, gates on `Value::Struct { name: type_name, .. }` + `program.drop_method_keys.contains_key(&type_name)`, and `.retain()`-removes the source's matching `Drop` entry from the current cleanup vec; runs after the let evaluates but BEFORE `push_drops_for_stmt` pushes the destination's slot. **Gate on user-Drop registration**: both backends only suppress when the source's type appears in `program.drop_method_keys`. Non-Drop bindings (plain `let y = x; ...` where `x: i64`) keep their existing `drop_trace` records — the move-suppression is bounded to the user-Drop dispatch surface so existing NLL-placement tests stay green. **Observed correctness for the production motivation.** `let l2 = l1` for a `TcpListener` (or `TcpStream`) now emits exactly ONE `call @karac_drop_TcpListener` in `main`'s IR rather than two; the `close(2)` fires exactly once. The kara source `let l1 = TcpListener.bind("127.0.0.1:0"); let l2 = l1; println(l2.fd);` ships through the chain without double-close. **4 new tests** (2 codegen + 2 interpreter): codegen IR-grep that `main` contains exactly one `@karac_drop_<Type>` call after `let g = f` (one for a user struct, one specifically for `TcpListener`); interpreter behaviour that `f.drop()` body is NOT invoked when `let g = f` move-suppresses it (only `g`'s drop fires); a sibling test that move-suppression doesn't affect non-Drop bindings (plain `let y = x` for `i64` still records both names in `drop_trace`). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (codegen E2E grew 799 → 801 with the 2 new tests; interpreter grew 641 → 643). Files: `src/codegen/state.rs` (+9 lines: `binding_name` field on `UserDrop`), `src/codegen/runtime.rs` (+~30 lines: `binding_name` arg to `track_user_drop_var` + new `suppress_user_drop_for_var` helper + drain-arm pattern update), `src/codegen/stmts.rs` (+~25 lines: suppress call + `binding_name` arg pass-through), `src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs` (+~35 lines: `suppress_let_rebind_user_drop` helper + wiring before `push_drops_for_stmt`), `tests/codegen.rs` (+~75 lines: 2 new tests), `tests/interpreter.rs` (+~80 lines: 2 new tests with NLL-vs-move-suppression interaction notes).

  **Sub-slice (2) by-value function arg consumption — `[ ]` (re-scoped 2026-05-29).** Investigation while attempting to ship found the entry's original premise was incorrect: it claimed *"today neither backend tracks this — both fire UserDrop at scope exit, causing double-drop."* Empirical check via small repro (`fn consume(f: R); fn main() { let r = R{tag:7}; consume(r); }`, where `R` has `impl Drop`) shows codegen fires the user drop body **exactly once**, at the **caller's** scope exit. The mechanism: `compile_function` does not register `UserDrop` for parameter bindings (no `track_user_drop_var` call in `src/codegen/functions.rs`), so the callee's `f` is never tracked for cleanup; the caller's `r` is tracked via the let-binding's `track_user_drop_var` and fires `karac_drop_R(r_alloca)` at `main`'s scope exit. The interpreter is symmetric — `eval_call`'s `bind_pattern` does not push a `CleanupAction::Drop` for params, and `eval_block_inner` only manages the caller's local cleanup vec. The naive "suppress at the caller" fix that the original entry described would suppress the **only** drop the value gets, producing zero drops total (worse than the current single-drop state). Confirmed by writing the fix, observing the test failure (`expected ["7\n","7\n"]; got ["7\n"]` — println fires, no drop fires anywhere), and reverting.

  **What the actual gap is.** Closing this slice properly requires **callee-side param-Drop tracking as a prerequisite**: register a `UserDrop` cleanup action for each function parameter whose type appears in `program.drop_method_keys`, mirroring `track_user_drop_var` at let-binding sites.
