The codegen wiring point would be `src/codegen/functions.rs::compile_function`'s parameter-init loop (after each param's alloca is materialised + the value is stored); the interpreter wiring point would be `src/interpreter/eval_call.rs` immediately after `bind_pattern` in the `Value::Function` arm. **Then** the caller-side suppression as originally drafted becomes the correct second half — without it, the double-drop premise becomes true (callee drops via the new param tracking + caller drops via the existing let tracking).

  **Scope sequencing if this is picked up.** Prereq slice: callee-side param-Drop tracking (both backends). Then: caller-side by-value-arg suppression (codegen + interpreter), which the original entry already drafted. Tests must verify both halves together — testing the prereq alone (param tracking without suppression) would surface the double-drop the original entry described; testing the suppression alone (as I attempted) breaks the current single-drop behaviour. The two slices commute on the wire but the test surface needs both landing before the observable behaviour is correct.

  **Blocked by:** nothing structural, but the prereq + suppression pair is a larger slice than the original entry implied. **Production impact:** none for v1's current stdlib types — `TcpListener` / `TcpStream` aren't consumed by-value by any v1 stdlib function (`bind` / `accept` / `connect` produce them, no `consume(s: TcpStream)` shapes exist). The current single-drop-at-caller-scope semantics close the fd correctly, just at the caller's scope exit rather than the callee's — semantically equivalent for resource cleanup. Defer the prereq + suppression pair until a workload surfaces where caller-vs-callee scope timing matters (e.g., a Pool consumer that takes a `TcpStream` by value and the caller's scope outlives the value for many milliseconds; fds would stay open longer than intended).

  **Sub-slice (3) return-by-value of a local binding shipped 2026-05-25.** Closes the `fn make() -> T { let l = T::new(); l }` and `return l;` gap. **Codegen** wiring: extended the pre-existing `suppress_cleanup_for_tail_return(&mut self, body)` in `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (was previously `&self` for Vec suppression only — converted to `&mut self` to call `suppress_user_drop_for_var`) to also suppress user-Drop bindings when the trailing expression OR the last statement's `return expr` value is an `ExprKind::Identifier`. The existing call from `compile_function:404` runs this BEFORE `emit_scope_cleanup`, so the source's UserDrop action is removed from `scope_cleanup_actions` before the drain walks it. Added a sibling suppression call in `src/codegen/exprs.rs::compile_expr`'s `ExprKind::Return` arm (line ~270) — same pattern as the existing `suppress_source_vec_cleanup_for_arg`, but for UserDrop. **Interpreter** wiring: added two helpers in `src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs` — `suppress_tail_expr_user_drop(expr, cleanup)` (called from `eval_block_inner` immediately before evaluating `block.final_expr`) and `suppress_return_stmt_user_drop(stmt, cleanup)` (called from the statement-iteration loop before `eval_stmt_cf`). Both helpers check the expression for `ExprKind::Identifier`, gate on `Value::Struct` + `program.drop_method_keys`, and `.retain()`-remove the matching `Drop` entry. Pre-statement suppression for explicit `return expr;` works because the source binding is still alive in env at the iteration point — the value is moved at evaluation time, but the cleanup-vec entry is gone before any `run_cleanup` triggered by `ControlFlow::Return` fires. **Observed correctness.** `fn make() -> Foo { let f = Foo {...}; f }` now emits ZERO `@karac_drop_Foo` calls in `make`'s IR (and the caller drops exactly once via its own scope exit). Same for explicit `return f;`. **5 new tests** (3 codegen IR-grep + 2 interpreter behaviour): trailing-expression suppression for user struct; explicit `return f;` suppression; interpreter trailing-expression observable single-drop (one `println` from drop body, not two); interpreter explicit-return observable single-drop; `make` body absent `@karac_drop_<Type>` while caller's `main` body present (caller-keeps-ownership invariant). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (codegen E2E grew 801 → 803 with 2 of the 3 codegen tests landing as passing; the third TcpListener-return test was held back because TcpListener-as-function-return-type currently fails LLVM module verification, a separate stdlib struct-return ABI gap noted inline). Interpreter grew 643 → 645. Files: `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (+~15 lines: signature change + UserDrop suppress call), `src/codegen/exprs.rs` (+~13 lines: UserDrop suppress in Return arm), `src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs` (+~50 lines: two new helpers + wiring at both block-trailing-expr and statement-iteration sites), `tests/codegen.rs` (+~75 lines: 2 new tests + comment about deferred TcpListener case), `tests/interpreter.rs` (+~80 lines: 2 new tests). **Note on stdlib-struct-return ABI gap.** The motivating production case `fn make_listener() -> TcpListener { let l = TcpListener.bind(...); l }` is correctly suppressed at the IR level by the changes shipped here, but currently fails LLVM module verification with "Function return type does not match operand type of return inst!" because the codegen's struct-return ABI lowering doesn't yet handle the stdlib's `{ i32 fd }` shape through a function's return slot. User-defined struct returns (e.g., `fn make() -> Foo` for a user `struct Foo { x: i64 }`) work and exercise the same move-suppression mechanism — so once the stdlib return-ABI gap closes, the TcpListener case will compile and the move-suppression machinery already wired here will make it correct without further changes.

  **Cross-link to Phase 6 line 30.** Slice 9d's "What still leaks" section explicitly named return-by-value of TcpListener as the remaining gap; sub-slice (3) closes the IR-level move-suppression for that. The full TcpListener-specific case will be observable when the orthogonal stdlib-struct-return ABI gap closes (filed in sub-slice (3)'s notes above). Sub-slice (1) closed the `let l2 = l1` rebind gap. Sub-slice (2) (by-value function-arg consumption) remains outstanding and may bite production when a TcpListener / TcpStream is passed by value to a callee that takes ownership — the symptom would be double-close at caller scope + callee scope. Current stdlib types (no `bind` / `accept` consumers in v1) don't trigger it.

- [x] **User-Drop dispatch for shared structs (RC integration).** ✓ **DONE 2026-06-03.** Codegen fires the user `impl Drop` body at refcount→0, fully recursively (each link/child of a `shared struct Node { next: Option[Node] }` chain fires as its own refcount hits 0). Implementation — all in `emit_shared_struct_rc_drop_fn` (`src/codegen/synth_drop.rs`): (1) gate on `program_snapshot.drop_method_keys`; (2) synth an RC drop fn even for a primitive-only shared struct when a user Drop exists (so the body fires before the plain `free`); (3) emit the user `@<T>.drop` call at the top of the drop fn, *before* the field walk + free — wrapping the heap pointer in a temp slot because shared-struct `mut ref self`/`ref self` methods receive `self` as a pointer-to-the-binding-slot (ptr-to-heap-ptr) per `get_data_ptr`, not the heap pointer directly; (4) disable the iterative self-chain fast path when a user Drop exists, so each link routes through the drop fn and fires. No change needed to `emit_rc_dec`/`emit_arc_dec` — both already dispatch through `rc_drop_fns`. Also fixed a double-fire + crash: the let-stmt flow (`src/codegen/stmts.rs`) registered the *value-type* `track_user_drop_var` for shared structs too, so the body ran twice and the value path passed `alloca` (ptr-to-ptr) → `self.field` dereferenced garbage; now gated `&& !shared_types.contains_key`. Interpreter (`invoke_user_drop_if_applicable`, `src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs` + new `Environment::drop_target`, `src/interpreter/exec.rs`): fires for the **single-owner** case via a non-cloning `Arc` strong-count==1 check at the drain point. **Aliased / recursive / field-held shared structs are NOT fired on the interpreter path** (the lingering-Arc-in-`env` limitation) — codegen handles them correctly; interpreter parity is folded into the "Drop ordering reconciliation across backends" item below. Tests: `test_ir_shared_struct_user_drop_synth_fn_calls_body`, `test_e2e_shared_struct_user_drop_fires`, `test_e2e_shared_struct_user_drop_recursive_chain_each_node_fires` (codegen), `asan_shared_struct_user_drop_recursive_chain_leak_free` (memory_sanitizer — leak-free + no double-free), `test_user_drop_shared_struct_fires_once` (interpreter). **Original filing follows.** Today `track_user_drop_var` (Prereq.3) only registers `CleanupAction::UserDrop` for value-type structs (`struct Foo {...}`). `shared struct` bindings route through `track_rc_var` and cleanup via `emit_refcount_dec` — when the last reference drops the refcount to 0, the heap layout is freed. User `impl Drop for SharedFoo` should fire the user body at that moment, BEFORE the heap is freed. **Integration point.** The user-body invocation belongs inside `emit_refcount_dec` (codegen) and the interpreter's RC-dec path, gated on `program.drop_method_keys.contains_key(&shared_type_name)` — when the dec brings the refcount to 0 and a user impl exists, the user body runs first, then field cleanup (heap walk), then the heap free. **Recursive drop-glue sub-item.** Types like `shared struct Node { children: Vec[Node] }` ride the same heap walker today; user-Drop integration into the walker is the same hook (run user body of inner Node when its refcount → 0 during the parent's drop). **Blocked by:** nothing — the RC machinery is in place. **Blocks:** any future stdlib `shared struct` type that needs RAII cleanup (e.g. a `shared struct AsyncResource { handle: i32 }` with a finaliser); also `Pool[T]` if its design ever moves to `shared` semantics (currently value-typed per `runtime/stdlib/pool.kara`). Not on the critical path for v1 Slice 9d (TcpListener / TcpStream are value-type structs).

- [ ] **Drop ordering reconciliation across codegen and interpreter backends.** **Filed 2026-05-25 by Prereq.5.** ↻ **Reframed 2026-06-04 (design.md finding):** design.md § "Drop ordering within a branch" (lines 866 / 2582) is authoritative — destructors fire at each binding's **live-range end (NLL), NOT at lexical scope end**, and it's correctness-relevant (MutexGuard early-unlock, lines 2506-2538). So the **interpreter's NLL early-drop is canonical** and **codegen's LIFO-at-scope-exit drain is the conformance gap** — the original (a)/(b)/(c) choice is superseded: (a) [codegen→NLL early-drop] is the canonical fix; (b) [interpreter→LIFO] and (c) [document-only] would entrench a design.md violation. Status is split into the three sub-items at the end of this entry. **ORIGINAL ANALYSIS:** Codegen drains `CleanupAction::UserDrop` LIFO at block-scope exit; the interpreter fires `CleanupAction::Drop` at per-statement NLL endpoints (push-order at each endpoint). When multiple bindings have user Drop AND a shared NLL endpoint, the two backends produce different observable drop orders. **Scope.** Pick one: (a) add NLL early-drop to codegen (matches interpreter; harder to implement at IR layer since each binding's last-use stmt is known statically but the cleanup-action push site is the let-binding); (b) make the interpreter respect block-scope LIFO drain (simpler implementation; loses NLL early-drop's memory-economy benefit); (c) document the divergence as known and require user Drop bodies to be order-independent (the existing tests cover this implicitly by avoiding ordering-dependent assertions; would need a doc-update). **Blocked by:** nothing — both backends work, just differently. **Blocks:** any user code that relies on a specific multi-binding Drop order across both backends (`karac test` interprets, release binaries codegen — divergence here is a test-vs-prod parity issue). Not on the critical path for v1 Slice 9d. **Cross-references:** `test_ir_multiple_user_drops_drain_lifo_at_scope_exit` (codegen test pinning LIFO at scope exit), `test_user_drop_lifo_at_scope_exit_when_both_used_to_last_stmt` (interpreter test pinning push-order at NLL endpoint).
  - [x] **Interpreter shared-struct user-Drop — ALIASED case.** ✓ **DONE 2026-06-04.** `let r2 = r` (Arc-clone aliases) now fire the body exactly once, at the last holder's drain. New `Environment::remove_local` (`src/interpreter/exec.rs`) releases a shared binding's `Arc` from `env` when its `CleanupAction::Drop` drains (NLL endpoint or scope exit — the slot is dead there), so a later alias's drain observes the decremented `strong_count` and the final holder reaches 1. Wired into `invoke_user_drop_if_applicable` (`src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs`), gated on `drop_method_keys` to bound blast radius; body-firing extracted to `run_user_drop_body`. Tail-escape (return-value clone) keeps the count > 1, so no premature fire. Test `test_user_drop_shared_struct_alias_fires_once_at_last_ref`. Completes the interpreter side of the 938 shared-struct user-Drop slice for the common cases (single-owner + alias).
  - [ ] **Interpreter shared-struct user-Drop — RECURSIVE / field-held case.** Deferred. An inner shared struct held inside another shared struct's *field* (`Node { next: Some(child) }`) is never an `env` binding, so it never reaches a `CleanupAction::Drop` drain and env-release-on-drain can't see it — its user body never fires on the interpreter path. Needs an `Arc`-drop hook: a `SharedStructInner` `Drop` impl that calls back into the interpreter (awkward in Rust — `Drop::drop` has no interpreter handle; would need a thread-local interpreter pointer or a deferred-drop queue). **Not v1-blocking:** the interpreter is dev/debug-only (design.md), and codegen fires these correctly (refcount→0; covered by the recursive-chain codegen + ASAN tests from the 938 slice). **Trigger:** a real `karac run` workload whose correctness depends on recursive/field-held shared-Drop side effects.
  - [ ] **Codegen NLL early-drop — the design.md-canonical fix for the value-Drop ordering divergence.** Deferred. Codegen has no liveness/last-use info today; it drains user-Drop / RC cleanup actions LIFO at scope exit. The design.md-conformant behavior drops each binding at its live-range end (NLL). Needs the ownership/NLL last-use analysis threaded into codegen and the cleanup-action drain restructured from scope-exit to per-last-use — drop/free correctness-critical (mistakes → UAF or leaks), multi-day. **Impact gated on a not-yet-built feature:** the motivating user-observable case is Drop-based RAII guards (`MutexGuard` early-unlock, design.md 2506-2538), which are "slice 2 spec" (future, per `runtime/stdlib/pool.kara:77`) — not in v1. So today the divergence is parity/conformance only, no active bug. **Trigger:** MutexGuard / RAII guards land (when scope-exit-drop becomes a real lock-held-too-long bug). Until then, v1 Drop bodies should be order/timing-independent on the codegen backend. **Cross-references:** `test_ir_multiple_user_drops_drain_lifo_at_scope_exit` (codegen — pins current LIFO-at-scope-exit), `test_user_drop_lifo_at_scope_exit_when_both_used_to_last_stmt` (interpreter — pins NLL push-order).

- [x] **`karac test` per-test timeout (P0 — v1).** **Filed 2026-05-25; all four sub-steps shipped (1 + 4 landed 2026-05-29; 2 + 3 landed 2026-06-03).** Defensive guardrail against a hung user test hanging the whole `karac test` suite. Today `karac test` runs each `_test.kara` block sequentially through the interpreter (per [phase-4 CR-24 follow-up line ~320](phase-4-interpreter.md)); without a per-test timeout, a runaway loop or deadlock in one test would leave the runner blocked indefinitely with no recovery short of SIGINT. The motivating incident was symmetric on the karac-rust side: `cargo test --features llvm --test codegen` hung 30+ min on one flaky concurrent-`Command::output()` before the user manually interrupted (resolved via `tests/codegen.rs::output_with_hang_watchdog`, commit `62af025`). The same defense now lives at the `karac test` surface.

  **Shape.**
  1. [x] **Default timeout: 30 s per test.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-29. New `ControlFlow::TimedOut` variant (`src/interpreter/exec.rs`) classifies as `ExitPath::Normal` so user `errdefer` blocks don't fire on the runner-side guardrail. `Interpreter` gains `test_deadline: Option<Instant>` + `timed_out: bool` fields and a `set_test_deadline(Option<Instant>)` setter. `eval_block_inner` polls the deadline at every statement boundary (alongside the existing `observed_cancellation()` check, both at the iteration head AND before evaluating `block.final_expr`); first observation past the deadline sets `timed_out = true` and raises `ControlFlow::TimedOut`. `run_test_function` reads `self.timed_out` ahead of `runtime_errors` / `ExitUnwind` checks so a deadline observed during user-error recovery still surfaces as a timeout rather than a misleading "test failed" with cleanup-time error.
  2. [x] **`kara.toml` package-level override.** ✓ Landed 2026-06-03. `[test] timeout_seconds = N` (numeric, no unit suffix, must be a positive integer) sets the package-wide per-test default. Parsed by `src/manifest.rs::parse_test_timeout_seconds` into the new `Manifest.test_timeout_seconds: Option<u64>` field (sits under the same `[test]` table as `[test.resources]`, parsed independently so the two coexist); wrong shapes (non-integer, `<= 0`, `[test]` not a table) are hard `InvalidFieldType` errors keyed `test.timeout_seconds`, matching the `[test.resources]` strictness so a manifest typo surfaces immediately rather than silently falling back to the default. `cmd_test` lifts `mf.test_timeout_seconds` once before the per-test loop. 5 unit tests in `src/manifest.rs::tests::{no_test_timeout_seconds_is_none, test_timeout_seconds_parses, _coexists_with_test_resources, _rejects_non_integer, _rejects_zero}`.
  3. [x] **Per-test attribute override.** ✓ Landed 2026-06-03. `#[test(timeout_seconds = N)]` on a test block is read at discovery by `extract_timeout_seconds` (`src/cli.rs`, mirroring `extract_requires`) into the new `DiscoveredTest.timeout_seconds: Option<u64>` field; a non-positive / non-integer value is ignored (the lower-precedence chain applies), matching `extract_requires`' tolerant stance toward unknown `#[test(...)]` arg shapes (`test` is a recognized attribute name and its args aren't allowlisted, so the new key needs no validator change). **Precedence wired** (sub-steps 2+3 together): a new `resolve_test_timeout(per_test, manifest_default, env_default) -> Duration` applies the full chain — per-test attr > kara.toml `[test].timeout_seconds` > `KARAC_TEST_TIMEOUT_SECS` env var > 30 s default — at *both* timeout sites in `cmd_test` (the `lljit_prototype` JIT-batch dispatch and the interpreter loop), replacing the prior env-var-only reads. 2 cli E2E tests: `tests/cli.rs::test_test_kara_toml_timeout_applies` (kara.toml `timeout_seconds = 1`, no env var → runaway killed at 1 s, `test_timeout` event `timeout_s:1`) + `test_test_per_test_attribute_timeout_overrides_manifest` (`#[test(timeout_seconds = 1)]` beats a kara.toml `timeout_seconds = 30` → killed at 1 s, proving attribute precedence). Existing `test_test_per_test_timeout_kills_runaway_loop` (env-var path, no kara.toml timeout) stays green — env wins when no higher layer is set. **Note:** precedence is kara.toml > env var per design (the structured per-package value is the deliberate setting; the env var is the ad-hoc fallback/CI knob for projects without a committed value). Surface: `src/manifest.rs`, `src/cli.rs`, `src/dep_graph.rs` + `src/dep_resolver.rs` (test-helper Manifest construction). Gates: lib 597+/manifest 77, full non-codegen suite (62 binaries) green; fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs, `--all-targets`) clean.
  4. [x] **Test-runner integration.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-29 alongside sub-step 1. `cmd_test` (`src/cli.rs`) reads `KARAC_TEST_TIMEOUT_SECS` for the suite-wide timeout (default 30 s), computes a per-test `deadline = Instant::now() + timeout` before each test, calls `interp.set_test_deadline(Some(deadline))`, runs the test, then captures `interp.timed_out` before clearing the deadline. On timeout, emits a new `test_timeout` JSONL event of shape `{"type":"test_timeout","test":"…","timeout_s":N,"elapsed_ms":M}` (distinct from `test_fail` so downstream tooling can distinguish a guardrail timeout from an assertion failure) and counts the timeout as a failure in the summary. Suite continues regardless. Tests: `tests/cli.rs::test_test_per_test_timeout_kills_runaway_loop` (1-s env-var override on a `while true {}` fixture; asserts the wall-clock is under 12 s, the `test_timeout` event shape, and the summary's `failed:1` count) + `_normal_completion_under_timeout_passes` (5-s budget + a fast `assert(1+1==2)`; asserts `test_pass` fires and no `test_timeout` does). `jsonl_lines` helper extended to accept the new event type — sub-step 1's empirical pre-existing whitelist would have silently dropped any future event type from test inspection, fixed alongside.

  **Why this is P0 for v1.** Every mature test runner ships per-test timeouts (Rust's libtest via `--ensure-time`, Go's `-timeout`, pytest's `pytest-timeout`); v1 launching without one would be a conspicuous regression. Cost is small — ~50 LOC plus the tokio plumbing already in the runtime.

  **Out of scope.** Distinguishing "test is genuinely slow" from "test is hung" without false positives. The per-test override is the escape hatch.

  **Cross-link.** Pairs with `karac run --timeout` (entry below) and `KARAC_DEADLOCK_CHECK` (entry below) — same family (hang prevention), different scope (test-runner vs CLI vs runtime).

- [~] **`karac run --timeout DURATION` CLI flag (P0 — v1).** **Filed 2026-05-25; interpreter-mode flag + parser + exit code shipped 2026-05-29 (sub-steps 1 + 2 + 4); compiled-mode subprocess-timeout (sub-step 3) deferred until `karac run --binary` ships.** Opt-in wall-clock cap for ad-hoc `karac run` invocations. **No default** — `karac run` legitimately targets long-running services (web servers, daemons, REPLs, batch jobs) where any default timeout would be paternalistic and silently break real workloads. The flag covers the orthogonal case: "I expect this to finish in N seconds; fail loudly if it doesn't" (CI smoke tests, scripted invocations, exploratory `karac run examples/foo.kara` where forgetting about a runaway costs real laptop battery).

  **Shape.**
  1. [x] **Flag parsing.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-29. `--timeout 60s` / `--timeout 5m` / `--timeout 100ms` / `--timeout=60` accepted via a hand-rolled duration parser in `src/cli/args.rs::parse_timeout_arg`. Suffixes recognised: `ms`, `s`, `m`, `h`. Bare integer = seconds (GNU `timeout(1)` convention). Rejects empty / zero / unparseable with focused CLI diagnostics (tests pin the diagnostic shapes). Both `--timeout=VALUE` and space-separated `--timeout VALUE` forms work, matching the existing `--manifest` pattern. Avoided pulling in `humantime` as a v1 dep — the hand-rolled parser is ~30 LOC and covers the suffix surface the entry called out.
  2. [x] **Timeout enforcement (interpreter mode).** ✓ Landed 2026-05-29. Reuses the per-test deadline mechanism shipped under the line 847 entry (`Interpreter.test_deadline` + `eval_block_inner` polling at every statement boundary, raises `ControlFlow::TimedOut` on first observation past the deadline). `cmd_run` calls `interp.set_test_deadline(Some(Instant::now() + d))` before `interp.run()` when `timeout` is `Some`; observes `interp.timed_out` after. The same poll cadence the per-test guardrail uses (every statement, plus before each block's `final_expr`) means a `while true {}` surfaces within milliseconds of the deadline. The original design proposed a `tokio::time::timeout` wrapper, but reusing the existing in-process polling mechanism is simpler (no tokio runtime needed) and structurally identical to the per-test surface — one mechanism, two CLI entry points.
  3. [ ] **Timeout enforcement (compiled mode, post-v1 if `karac run --binary` ships).** Spawn the binary as subprocess; watchdog SIGTERM at deadline, SIGKILL 15 s later if still alive. Not on the v1 path — `karac run` is interpreter-only today and the compiled-binary path is itself post-v1.
  4. [x] **Exit code.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-29. On timeout, `cmd_run` prints `karac: timed out after Ns` to stderr and calls `process::exit(124)` matching GNU `timeout(1)` so existing shell pipelines compose. Tests (`tests/cli.rs`): `test_run_timeout_kills_infinite_loop` (1s timeout on `while true {}`; asserts exit 124, wall-clock < 12s, stderr message), `test_run_no_timeout_default_runs_to_completion` (no flag → no cap, regression guard against accidentally adding a default), `test_run_timeout_rejects_zero_value` (`--timeout=0` → exit 1 with "greater than zero" message), `test_run_timeout_rejects_unparseable_value` (`--timeout=fast` → exit 1 with "not a valid duration" message), `test_run_timeout_accepts_bare_integer_as_seconds` (`--timeout=60` parses as 60s). `karac run --help` updated with the flag + usage examples.

  **Cost.** Small — under 100 LOC including parser + tests + interpreter integration. Mostly CLI plumbing.

  **Out of scope.** SIGTERM grace period configuration (always 15 s for v1, matches GNU). Per-thread timeouts inside the user's kara program (use `defer` + an atomic deadline if needed).

  **Cross-link.** Pairs with `karac test` per-test timeout (entry above) and `KARAC_DEADLOCK_CHECK` (entry below).

- [ ] **`KARAC_DEADLOCK_CHECK` opt-in runtime deadlock detector (P1 — v1.x is fine).** **Filed 2026-05-25.** Runtime-side "all workers asleep" detection, modeled on Go's `panic: all goroutines are asleep - deadlock!`. Off by default — a long-blocked HTTP handler is not a deadlock — but on by default under `karac test` and recommended in CI. When enabled, the runtime spawns a watchdog thread that samples worker states periodically; if **all** workers are blocked on locks/channels AND the scheduler ready queue has been empty for K consecutive samples, dump per-worker backtraces and abort with `runtime: deadlock detected — N workers parked, no progress for K×N ms`.

  **Shape.**
  1. [ ] **Env-var gating.** `KARAC_DEADLOCK_CHECK=1` at process startup spawns the watchdog. Unset / `0` / absent → no watchdog, zero overhead in the hot path. Symmetric with `KARAC_PAR_WORKERS` (commit `d33b389`) and `KARAC_AUTO_PAR` conventions.
  2. [ ] **Watchdog mechanism.** Single dedicated OS thread. Reads worker-state atomics every N ms (default 100 ms). Each worker maintains a small state enum — `Running`, `ParkedOnMutex(id)`, `ParkedOnChannel(id)`, `ParkedOnFd(fd)`, `Idle` — already partially tracked by the auto-par scheduler. If for K consecutive ticks (default 50 = 5 s wall) every worker is in a `Parked*` state AND the scheduler ready queue is empty, fire the dump+abort path.
  3. [ ] **Backtrace dump.** Walk each worker's call stack via the `backtrace` crate (already an indirect dep) and write to stderr in a structured envelope (JSONL when `KARAC_OUTPUT=jsonl`, plain otherwise). Include the resource each parked worker is waiting on (mutex id, channel id, fd) and the source span of the wait site where the runtime can recover it.
  4. [ ] **Abort semantics.** Exit code **134** (SIGABRT) to match standard "process aborted by runtime" convention. The runtime's existing atexit error-trace printer (`KARAC_ERROR_TRACE_FORMAT`, commit `42c0e8d`) catches the abort path so the dump composes with existing JSON/JSONL output modes.
  5. [ ] **`karac test` default-on.** `cmd_test` in `src/cli.rs` sets `KARAC_DEADLOCK_CHECK=1` in the child env unless explicitly overridden — same default-on-but-overridable shape as Go's testing runtime. This is the load-bearing default; explicit `karac run` invocations stay off-by-default so production binaries don't pay even the (small) opt-in overhead unintentionally.

  **Cost when disabled.** Zero — no atomic increments, no hot-path instrumentation, no allocator overhead. The state atomics already exist for auto-par scheduling.

  **Cost when enabled.** One OS thread + one atomic-load-per-worker per sample tick. At 100 ms sampling with 18 workers (Apple M5 Pro reference target), that's 180 atomic loads/sec — well below noise.

  **Why P1, not P0.** Reasonable people can ship v1 without this if `karac test` per-test timeout covers the test-side hang surface and `karac run --timeout` covers the dev-side surface. Production users running long-lived services don't hit this gap until they actually have a deadlock — at which point they SIGINT, reproduce in dev with `KARAC_DEADLOCK_CHECK=1`, and get the dump. Shipping in v1.x rather than v1 is acceptable.

  **Out of scope.** Lock-order violation detection (TSAN territory; a separate slice). Detecting livelock (workers running but making no observable progress) — much harder, requires program-counter sampling.

  **Cross-link.** Pairs with `karac test` per-test timeout and `karac run --timeout` (entries above) — same family, different scope.

- [x] **Investigate the concurrent `Command::output()` deadlock in `tests/codegen.rs` parallel runs.** ✓ Resolved 2026-05-25 (`bdbaadd`). Root cause was *not* a process / pipe / FD / libtest race — it was a karac codegen bug whose downstream symptom *manifested* under parallel cargo-test load because libtest's spawn pattern surfaced it more often. Four codegen call sites looked up the enum that owns a given variant name by iterating `self.enum_layouts` (HashMap, non-deterministic order) with only a hard-coded `Option`/`Result` carve-out for the user-vs-seed preference. When a user enum's variant name collided with a *seeded* built-in not in the carve-out — specifically `MyIoErr.Other` (test source) colliding with `TcpError.Other` (seeded via `seed_builtin_enum_layouts`) — HashMap iteration order non-deterministically picked the seeded layout, producing a wrong-shape enum value at construction and the wrong tag at match dispatch. The compiler emitted `unreachable` mid-`main` for the wrong-arm dispatch (LLVM lowers `unreachable` to `brk #0x1` on macOS arm64); under cargo test's parallel spawn pattern the brk-trapped child looped forever instead of terminating, because the libtest parent task intercepts `EXC_BREAKPOINT` Mach exceptions and prevents kernel-default `SIGTRAP` delivery to the child.

  **Investigation chain that led to the root cause:**
  1. 5 consecutive suite runs → 1/5 hung → confirmed real, intermittent (~20%/run).
  2. `lsof` + `sample` on a hung child: child spinning at `main+24` at 57% CPU, single frame, no pipe drain in progress — NOT a process/pipe issue.
  3. Disassembled hung binary: `main` ends in `brk #0x1` (LLVM's `unreachable`), missing the entire `mov w0,#0 / ldp / add sp / ret` epilogue. Standalone `karac build` for the same source produces a correct `ret`-terminated `main`.
  4. Tight repro: compile `MyIoErr.Other("disk full")` 20 times sequentially in-process; 54% produce a 9471-byte IR (wrong TcpError layout), 46% produce a 10132-byte IR (correct MyIoErr layout). Bimodal output from the same input on the same thread.
  5. Bisect: hashed the IR per call → exactly TWO distinct shapes (`03264…` vs `ea8b…`). One-bit-of-state nondeterminism. Diffed the two IRs → enum layout diverges: `{ i64, i64 }` vs `{ i64, i64, i64, i64 }`; tag for `Other` is 1 vs 2.
  6. Located the iteration: `try_compile_enum_variant` at `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs:689` iterates `enum_layouts` HashMap to find which enum owns variant `Other`. Workaround comment in-place for `Option`/`Result` collisions; missed `Json` and `TcpError`.

  **Fix:** `bdbaadd` introduces `seeded_enum_names: HashSet<String>` populated by `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` and applies the user-vs-seed preference at all four lossy lookup sites:
  - `try_compile_enum_variant` (variant constructor with payload)
  - `try_unit_enum_variant` (unit-variant constructor)
  - `enum_tag_for_variant` + `enum_type_for_variant` (match-dispatch tag/type)
  - `infer_enum_from_value` (RHS-typing when an enum is bound to a tracked var)
  - `bind_pattern_values` (offset-lookup fallback when scrutinee-type match misses)

  Regression test in `tests/codegen.rs::test_enum_variant_name_collision_with_seeded_other_is_deterministic` compiles the collision program 20 times and asserts every IR is byte-identical. Verification: 5 consecutive parallel codegen-suite runs post-fix, all 786 tests pass, 0 hangs, 0 failures (pre-fix this same pattern produced ~20% suite hangs and ~60% `test_io_error` "wrong variant" failures).

  **Belt-and-suspenders:** The 62af025 watchdog (`output_with_hang_watchdog`) stays in place. If a future codegen regression emits `unreachable` mid-function, it'll surface as one test failing with the hang panic message instead of hanging the whole suite.

  **Cross-link.** Commit `62af025` (defensive watchdog), `bdbaadd` (root-cause fix). Entry below ("Mirror watchdog into …") is independent and still open — the watchdog mirror is a defensive measure orthogonal to this fix.

- [ ] **Mirror `output_with_hang_watchdog` into `par_codegen.rs`, `parallax.rs`, `parallax_lite.rs`, `cli.rs`.** **Filed 2026-05-25.** Companion to commit `62af025`. The codegen suite shipped a per-spawn hang watchdog (`tests/codegen.rs::output_with_hang_watchdog`), but four other test files still call `Command::new(exe).output()` directly and have identical exposure to the same concurrent-spawn deadlock:

  - `tests/par_codegen.rs` — parallel codegen end-to-end tests (highest exposure; intentionally runs heavy par workloads)
  - `tests/parallax.rs` — parallax runtime tests
  - `tests/parallax_lite.rs` — parallax-lite runtime tests
  - `tests/cli.rs` — CLI end-to-end tests

  **Shape.** Lift `output_with_hang_watchdog` into a shared helper module under `tests/common/spawn.rs` (Rust's integration-test layout requires the `mod common;` workaround; precedent in the codebase if any exists, otherwise establish one). Each test file's spawn sites route through it. Per-file timeout configurability is the only twist: par_codegen tests legitimately run for 5–15 s of real workload, so they need a longer default (60 s) than the 15 s codegen default; CLI tests are short and can match codegen's 15 s.

  **Why not bundled into `62af025`.** Scope discipline — that commit was for the surface that *observably* hung. Each of the four files needs its own per-file timeout calibration; bundling would have ballooned both the diff and the review surface without surfacing any new design decision. Tracked here so the lesson doesn't get lost.

  **Priority.** Medium — the codegen suite was the one observed to hang, but the other four are structurally similar and one of them will eventually hang under enough load. Land before any large refactor that touches the test harness so the mirror is a one-shot, not a one-per-file scattershot.

  **Cross-link.** Commit `62af025`. Entry above (root-cause investigation) is the parent of this work in spirit but doesn't gate it — the watchdog mirror is defensive, root-causing is investigative.

- [->] **`match`-on-literals: emit LLVM `switch` instead of an `icmp`-chain.** **Filed 2026-05-27.** `compile_pattern_condition` lowers each literal arm to `icmp eq + br` and chains them. For all-arms-literal, no-guard matches an LLVM `switch` would let the backend pick a jump-table / balanced tree by case density.

  **Why deferred (impact nil today).** Measured on a 7-way byte classifier (kata 13 `value()`): LLVM's `SimplifyCFG` already reconstructs a balanced binary-search tree from the `icmp`-chain, so the `switch` form compiles to *byte-identical* machine code on sparse fan-ins. Wall-time delta if-chain vs `match`: 1.06× ± 0.12× — sub-noise. See [`docs/investigations/roman_kata_codegen.md`](../investigations/roman_kata_codegen.md) § match lowering.

  **Reopen trigger.** A real workload (kata or production) where a *dense* literal dispatch — roughly ≥16-way over a contiguous-ish integer/byte domain (tokenizer keyword table, 256-way byte state machine, opcode dispatch) — shows up as a hot path AND profiling shows LLVM's chain-recognizer gave up (no jump-table in the disassembly). At that point emit `switch` for the all-literal-arms/no-guard subset and validate against that benchmark.

  **Scope note.** A `switch` only applies when every arm is an integer/char/byte literal with no guard; mixed arms (bindings, ranges, guards) keep the uniform chain. So this is a special-case fast path, not a rewrite — don't add the branching complexity until the trigger fires.

- [->] **Loop-invariant code motion / partial eval across pure calls.** **Filed 2026-05-27.** karac does not hoist or fold a pure function call whose arguments are loop-invariant. A fixed-input parse loop (`roman_to_int(stake)` ×10M on one input) ran 10M times (99 ms) where clang folded the whole loop to one multiply (1.9 ms).

  **Why deferred.** (1) The only observed "impact" was a synthetic fixed-input microbench — real code rarely calls a pure fn with a fully loop-invariant arg 10M times and discards the variation; per [[optimize-for-production-not-kata]] this is a kata artifact, not a production signal. (2) High effort + risk: needs interprocedural purity analysis + LICM/partial-eval across call boundaries, a large surface with real miscompile exposure. Cost/benefit is poor.

  **Reopen trigger.** A production-shaped workload where a provably-pure call with loop-invariant args is a measured hot path that LLVM doesn't already hoist (verify via disassembly first — LLVM's own LICM handles many cases once the callee is inlined). See [`docs/investigations/roman_kata_codegen.md`](../investigations/roman_kata_codegen.md) § parse-only diagnostic.

- [x] **`Option[shared T]` branch-buried return: per-branch (flow-sensitive) refcount compensation for MIXED tails.** **Filed 2026-05-30. DONE 2026-05-30.** A function whose tail is an `if` / `if let` / `match` that MIXES a bare-arg `Option[shared]` return (`l1` / `l2` — needs a compensating inner inc, because returning the param moves it out while its scope-exit `RcDecOption` still fires) with a `Some(<alias>)` return (needs NO inc — `try_compile_enum_variant` already inc'd the payload) cannot be balanced by a single merge-block result-inc. The canonical case is the idiomatic recursive **merge-two-sorted-lists** (LeetCode #21):

  ```
  fn merge(l1, l2) -> Option[ListNode] {
      if let Some(n1) = l1 {
          if let Some(n2) = l2 {
              if n1.val <= n2.val { n1.next = merge(n1.next, l2); Some(n1) }   // Some-tail: no inc
              else { n2.next = merge(l1, n2.next); Some(n2) }
          } else { l1 }                                                        // bare-arg tail: needs inc
      } else { l2 }                                                            // bare-arg tail: needs inc
  }
  ```

  A single exit-block inc serves all leaves: it over-counts the `Some` leaves (→ leak) or, if suppressed, under-counts the bare-arg leaves (→ UAF).

  **The fix (per-branch, flow-sensitive).** A `tail_ret_inner: Option<StructType>` context field carries the return inner-heap type from `compile_function` → `compile_block` (final expr) → `compile_if_let` / `compile_if` / `compile_match` (each branch's final expr). It is CLEARED while compiling block statements (so a non-tail `if let` in statement position never picks it up) and re-armed only for branch finals. `compile_tail_final_expr` does the dispatch: a bare `Option[shared]` binding leaf (`l1`) is inc'd via `share_option_shared_ref_for_arg` IN ITS OWN branch block (only the taken arm pays); `if`/`if let`/`match`/block constructs propagate; `Some(...)` / call move-out / `var.field` get no inc (the constructor already inc'd a `Some` payload; `var.field` is handled by `suppress_tail_field_option_dec`). This subsumes the old single merge-block inc (`inc_branch_buried_option_arg_return` + `option_tail_classify`, both removed) AND the direct-Identifier tail inc that `suppress_cleanup_for_tail_return` used to emit (moved to `compile_tail_final_expr`, so it fires uniformly for direct and branch-buried tails without double-counting). The auto-par emission path parks the context past the statement loop and re-applies it to the final expr.

  **Verified.** `KARAC_RC_TRACE` refcount tracing on `merge([1,2,4],[1,3,4])`; 500k-iter RSS stress on the recursive merge holds flat at 1.80 MB (was 308 MB under the broad-inc variant); `pick` / katas 2 / 19 / 21 all leak-free; `cargo test --features llvm` 6554 passed / 0 failed. `kara-katas/leetcode/1-100/21-merge-two-sorted-lists/recursive.kara` is now `karac build`-correct (codegen == interp == python). The sibling let-site shape (`let x = if c { l1 } else { l2 };`) is NOT exercised by this — only the function-return-tail position is compensated (the let-bound result is not a move-out, so it must not be inc'd); a future kata that needs it would extend the same `tail_ret_inner` threading to the let-RHS.

- [x] **Nested enum-payload bind + discriminate through `Result` / `Option` — fixed 2026-05-30.** Surfaced during phase-8 line-74. A match arm matching an enum nested inside a `Result` / `Option` variant — `match r { Result.Err(E.A(c)) => ... }` where `enum E { A(i64), B }` — was broken two ways: (1) **binding** — `reconstruct_payload_value` had no variant arm, so the inner `E.A(c)` reconstructed as a raw word and the inner binding `c` never got a value (`Undefined variable 'c'`, didn't compile); (2) **discrimination** (latent, exposed once binding compiled) — `compile_pattern_condition`'s `TupleVariant` arm checked only the *outer* tag (`Result.Err`), never the inner `E.A` tag, so a `Result.Err(E.B)` value wrongly took the `Result.Err(E.A(c))` arm (and bound `c` to garbage), and a network `Err(TcpError.Other(-1))` wrongly took an earlier `Err(TcpError.AddrInUse)` arm. **Fix (both in `src/codegen/control_flow_match.rs`):** (a) `reconstruct_payload_value` gained a variant arm that rebuilds the inner enum's tagged-union aggregate `{tag, payload...}` from the payload words (via the new `enum_layout_type_for_variant_pattern`, which resolves the inner enum from a `TupleVariant` / `Struct` *or* a fieldless `Binding`-variant pattern, preferring a qualified `Enum.Variant` path segment); (b) `compile_pattern_condition`'s `TupleVariant` arm now AND-s in `and_in_nested_variant_conditions`, which for each variant sub-pattern extracts its payload words, rebuilds the inner value, and recurses `compile_pattern_condition` on it (so the inner tag — and arbitrarily deeper nesting — is checked). Non-variant sub-patterns and top-level matches are unchanged; shared (pointer) enum nested-variant *conditions* and struct-variant nested conditions are explicit follow-ups (binding for those already works; the field-by-name struct-variant extraction differs from the positional tuple path). Tests: `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_nested_enum_payload_bind_and_discriminate` (binding `E.A(c)→42`, discrimination `E.B`→its own arm not `E.A(c)`, multi-payload `P.Two(a,b)`, and `Option.Some(E…)` / `Result.Ok(E…)` carriers). This also makes `Result.Err(TcpError.Other(c))` / `.Protocol(c)` bind the raw code the line-74 work referenced. Full gate green (fmt, clippy `--all-targets --features llvm`, full non-llvm + codegen + memory_sanitizer).

- [x] **`return;` in `main` fails codegen — `ret void` vs main's `i32` exit-code ABI. Fixed 2026-05-30.** Surfaced by the `supervised_echo` kata (kara-katas). **Minimal repro:** `fn main() { return; }` failed with `Module verification failed: "Function return type does not match operand type of return inst! ret void / i32"`. `main` lowers to a C-ABI `i32 main()` (the process exit code), but a bare `return;` statement emitted `ret void` instead of `ret i32 0`. Any `return;` reachable in `main` tripped it — directly, or nested in an `if` / `while` / `match` arm. Non-`main` void functions were unaffected (their `return;` emits `ret void` matching their `void` LLVM type — the kata's `pick_port` helper uses early `return` freely). **Fix:** the `ExprKind::Return(None)` arm in `src/codegen/exprs.rs` now checks `self.current_fn_name == "main"` and emits `ret i32 0` (mirroring `compile_function`'s implicit end-of-`main` return-zero) rather than `ret void`. The implicit end-of-`main` fall-through already did the right thing; this closed only the *explicit* `return;` path. Tests: `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_explicit_return_in_main_exits_zero` (a `return` nested in `while`+`if` early-exits and stops execution) + `test_ir_explicit_return_in_main_is_ret_i32_zero` (IR pin: `ret i32 0`, no `ret void`). The sibling network-call-in-a-helper bug stays tracked in [`phase-6-runtime.md`](phase-6-runtime.md).
